Title: Digital Markets, Competition and Consumers Act 2024
Date: 2024-07-26
Publisher: Statute Law Database
Identifier: http://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2024/13

## Digital Markets, Competition and Consumers Act 2024

      B e it enacted  by the King’s most Excellent Majesty, by and with the
advice and consent of the Lords Spiritual and Temporal, and Commons, in this
present Parliament assembled, and by the authority of the same, as follows:—

### Digital Markets

#### Overview

##### Overview

1

1.1

This Part —

1.1.a

confers functions on the CMA in relation to the regulation of competition in
digital markets, and

1.1.b

makes related provision.

1.2

Chapter 2  makes provision about the designation of undertakings as having
strategic market status in respect of a digital activity.

1.3

Chapter 3  provides for the CMA to be able to impose conduct requirements on a
designated undertaking.

1.4

Chapter 4  provides for the CMA to take steps to promote competition where it
considers that activities of a designated undertaking are having an adverse
effect on competition.

1.5

Chapter 5  makes provision about a duty to report certain possible mergers
involving a designated undertaking.

1.6

Chapter 6  makes provision about investigatory powers and compliance reports
in relation to a designated undertaking.

1.7

Chapter 7  makes provision about enforcement and appeals in relation to
functions of the CMA under  this Part .

1.8

Chapter 8  makes provision about administration and other matters in relation
to functions of the CMA under  this Part .

#### Strategic Market Status

##### Power to designate undertaking as having SMS

###### Designation of undertaking

2

2.1

The CMA may designate an undertaking as having strategic market status (“ SMS
”) in respect of a digital activity carried out by the undertaking where the
CMA considers that—

2.1.a

the digital activity is linked to the United Kingdom (see section  4 ), and

2.1.b

the undertaking meets the SMS conditions in respect of the digital activity.

2.2

The SMS conditions are that the undertaking has—

2.2.a

substantial and entrenched market power (see  section 5 ), and

2.2.b

a position of strategic significance (see  section 6 ),

in respect of the digital activity.

2.3

Subsection  (1)  is subject to section  7  (the turnover condition).

2.4

The CMA may only designate an undertaking as having SMS in respect of a
digital activity after carrying out an SMS investigation in accordance with
this Chapter.

###### Digital activities

3

3.1

For the purposes of this Part, the following are “digital activities”—

3.1.a

the provision of a service by means of the internet, whether for consideration
or otherwise;

3.1.b

the provision of one or more pieces of digital content, whether for
consideration or otherwise;

3.1.c

any other activity carried out for the purposes of an activity within
paragraph  (a)  or  (b) .

3.2

For the purposes of this section, a service is provided by means of the
internet even where it is provided by means of a combination of—

3.2.a

the internet, and

3.2.b

an electronic communications service (within the meaning given by section
32(2) of the Communications Act 2003).

3.3

The CMA may treat two or more activities within  subsection (1)  that are
carried out by a single undertaking as a single digital activity where—

3.3.a

the activities have substantially the same or similar purposes, or

3.3.b

the activities can be carried out in combination with each other to fulfil a
specific purpose.

3.4

In any notice or other document that the CMA is required to give or publish
under or by virtue of this Part, the CMA may describe a digital activity by
reference to the nature of the activity, brand names or both.

###### Link to the United Kingdom

4

A digital activity is linked to the United Kingdom for the purposes of
section 2 (1) (a)  if—

4.a

the digital activity has a significant number of UK users,

4.b

the undertaking that carries out the digital activity carries on business in
the United Kingdom in relation to the digital activity, or

4.c

the digital activity or the way in which the undertaking carries on the
digital activity is likely to have an immediate, substantial and foreseeable
effect on trade in the United Kingdom.

###### Substantial and entrenched market power

5

In order to assess whether an undertaking has substantial and entrenched
market power in respect of a digital activity for the purposes of  section 2
(2) (a) , the CMA must carry out a forward-looking assessment of a period of
at least 5 years, taking into account developments that—

5.a

would be expected or foreseeable if the CMA did not designate the undertaking
as having SMS in respect of the digital activity, and

5.b

may affect the undertaking’s conduct in carrying out the digital activity.

###### Position of strategic significance

6

An undertaking has a position of strategic significance in respect of a
digital activity for the purposes of  section 2 (2) (b)  where one or more of
the following conditions is met—

6.a

the undertaking has achieved a position of significant size or scale in
respect of the digital activity;

6.b

a significant number of other undertakings use the digital activity as carried
out by the undertaking in carrying on their business;

6.c

the undertaking’s position in respect of the digital activity would allow it
to extend its market power to a range of other activities;

6.d

the undertaking’s position in respect of the digital activity allows it to
determine or substantially influence the ways in which other undertakings
conduct themselves, in respect of the digital activity or otherwise.

###### The turnover condition

7

7.1

The CMA may not designate an undertaking as having SMS in respect of a digital
activity unless the turnover condition is met in relation to the undertaking.

7.2

The turnover condition is met in relation to an undertaking if the CMA
estimates that—

7.2.a

the total value of the global turnover of an undertaking or, where the
undertaking is part of a group, the global turnover of that group in the
relevant period exceeds £25 billion, or

7.2.b

the total value of the UK turnover of an undertaking or, where the undertaking
is part of a group, the UK turnover of that group in the relevant period
exceeds £1 billion.

7.3

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend either of the sums mentioned
in  subsection (2) .

7.4

Regulations under  subsection (3)  are subject to the affirmative procedure.

7.5

The CMA must—

7.5.a

keep under review the sums mentioned in  subsection (2) , and

7.5.b

from time to time advise the Secretary of State as to whether the sums are
still appropriate.

7.6

In this section—

7.6.a

the “ relevant period ” means—

7.6.a.i

the most recent period of 12 months (“period A”) in respect of which the CMA
considers that it is able to make an estimate of the total value of the
relevant turnover of the undertaking or group, or

7.6.a.ii

if the CMA estimates that the relevant turnover of the undertaking or group in
the period of 12 months ending immediately before period A was higher than the
relevant turnover of the undertaking or group in period A, that earlier period
of 12 months;

7.6.b

the “relevant turnover” of the undertaking or group is the UK turnover or, as
the case may be, global turnover of the undertaking or group.

###### Turnover of an undertaking

8

8.1

This section  applies for the purposes of the turnover condition.

8.2

The total value of the global turnover of an undertaking or group in the
relevant period (as defined in section  7 (6) ) is, subject to regulations
under  subsection (4) , the total value of the turnover of the undertaking or
group arising in connection with any of its activities.

8.3

The total value of the UK turnover of an undertaking or group in the relevant
period is, subject to regulations under  subsection (4) , the total value of
the turnover of the undertaking or group—

8.3.a

arising in connection with any of its activities, and

8.3.b

relating to UK users or UK customers.

8.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision about how the total
value of the global turnover or UK turnover of an undertaking or group in a
period is to be estimated for the purposes of the turnover condition.

8.5

Regulations under  subsection (4)  may (among other things)—

8.5.a

make provision about amounts which are, or are not, to be regarded as
comprising the turnover of an undertaking or group;

8.5.b

confer on the CMA the power to determine matters specified in the regulations
(including the matter mentioned in paragraph  (a) ).

8.6

Regulations under  subsection (4)  are subject to the negative procedure.

##### Procedure

###### Initial SMS investigations

9

9.1

The CMA may begin an initial SMS investigation where it has reasonable grounds
to consider that it may be able to designate an undertaking as having SMS in
respect of a digital activity in accordance with  section 2 .

9.2

An “initial SMS investigation” is an investigation into whether to designate
an undertaking as having SMS in respect of a digital activity where the
undertaking is not already designated in respect of that activity (subject to
section 10 (4) ).

9.3

The CMA may begin an initial SMS investigation into whether to designate an
undertaking as having SMS in respect of a digital activity even if it has
previously made a decision not to designate the undertaking as having SMS in
respect of that activity.

###### Further SMS investigations

10

10.1

The CMA may begin a further SMS investigation in relation to the designation
of a designated undertaking in respect of a relevant digital activity at any
time during the designation period (see  section 18 ) relating to that
designation.

10.2

The CMA must begin a further SMS investigation in relation to the designation
of a designated undertaking in respect of a relevant digital activity not
later than 9 months before the end of the designation period relating to that
designation, if it is not already carrying one out at that time under
subsection  (1) .

10.3

A “further SMS investigation” is an investigation into whether—

10.3.a

to revoke a designated undertaking’s designation in respect of the relevant
digital activity or to designate the undertaking again in respect of that
activity, and

10.3.b

to make provision under  section 17  (existing obligations).

10.4

A further SMS investigation may also include an investigation into whether to
designate the designated undertaking in respect of a digital activity that the
CMA considers to be similar or connected to the relevant digital activity
(whether instead of, or in addition to, the relevant digital activity).

###### Procedure relating to SMS investigations

11

11.1

When the CMA begins an SMS investigation it must give the undertaking to which
the investigation relates a notice (an “SMS investigation notice”).

11.2

The SMS investigation notice must state—

11.2.a

in the case of an initial SMS investigation—

11.2.a.i

the reasonable grounds mentioned in  section 9 (1) ;

11.2.a.ii

that the CMA may close the investigation in accordance with  section 12 ;

11.2.b

the purpose and scope of the SMS investigation;

11.2.c

the period by the end of which the CMA must give the undertaking a notice
setting out its decisions as a result of the investigation (see  section 14
(2) );

11.2.d

the circumstances in which that period may be extended (see  section 104 ).

11.3

The statement of the purpose and scope of the investigation must include a
description of the undertaking and digital activities to which the
investigation relates.

11.4

The CMA must give the undertaking one or more revised versions of the SMS
investigation notice if it changes its view of the purpose and scope of the
investigation.

11.5

As soon as reasonably practicable after giving an SMS investigation notice or
a revised version of an SMS investigation notice, the CMA must—

11.5.a

publish the notice, and

11.5.b

give a copy of the notice to the FCA, OFCOM, the Information Commissioner, the
Bank of England and the PRA.

###### Closing an initial SMS investigation without a decision

12

12.1

The CMA may close an initial SMS investigation at any time before it has
reached a final view on the matters mentioned in paragraphs  (a)  and  (b)  of
section  2 (1) .

12.2

When the CMA decides to close an initial SMS investigation, the CMA must give
the undertaking to which the investigation related a notice to that effect.

12.3

The notice must include the CMA’s reasons for closing the investigation.

12.4

As soon as reasonably practicable after giving a notice under subsection  (2)
, the CMA must publish the notice.

###### Consultation on proposed decision

13

13.1

The CMA must—

13.1.a

carry out a public consultation on any decision that it is considering making
as a result of an SMS investigation (see  section 14 (1) ), and

13.1.b

bring the public consultation to the attention of such persons as it considers
appropriate.

13.2

Consultation under subsection  (1)  may be carried out at the same time as
consultation under  section 24 (1)  (consultation in relation to a conduct
requirement).

###### Outcome of SMS investigations

14

14.1

The CMA must—

14.1.a

in the case of an initial SMS investigation which it does not close under
section  12 , decide whether to designate the undertaking to which the
investigation relates as having SMS in respect of a digital activity to which
the investigation relates;

14.1.b

in the case of a further SMS investigation, make a decision on the matters
mentioned in  section 10 (3)  and, where relevant,  section 10 (4) .

14.2

The CMA must give the undertaking a notice (an “SMS decision notice”) setting
out its decisions under subsection  (1)  on or before the last day of the
period (the “SMS investigation period”) of 9 months beginning with the day on
which the SMS investigation notice is given.

14.3

The giving of a revised version of an SMS investigation notice under  section
11 (4)  does not change the day on which the SMS investigation period begins.

14.4

Sections  15  and  16  make provision about the content of an SMS decision
notice.

14.5

As soon as reasonably practicable after giving an SMS decision notice, the CMA
must publish the notice.

14.6

If the CMA does not give an SMS decision notice on or before the last day of
the SMS investigation period, the CMA and the undertaking to which the
investigation related are to be treated as if—

14.6.a

in the case of an initial SMS investigation, the CMA had given the undertaking
an SMS decision notice stating that it had decided not to designate the
undertaking in respect of any digital activity to which the investigation
related, and

14.6.b

in the case of a further SMS investigation, the CMA had given an SMS decision
notice stating that it had decided to revoke the designated undertaking’s
designation in respect of the relevant digital activity with effect from the
end of the SMS investigation period.

###### Notice requirements: decisions about whether to designate

15

15.1

Where the CMA decides as a result of an initial SMS investigation not to
designate the undertaking to which the investigation relates as having SMS in
respect of a digital activity to which the investigation relates, the SMS
decision notice must include the CMA’s reasons for its decision.

15.2

Subsections (3)  to  (6)  apply where the CMA decides to designate an
undertaking as having SMS in respect of a digital activity (whether or not
that undertaking is already a designated undertaking).

15.3

The SMS decision notice must include—

15.3.a

a description of the designated undertaking,

15.3.b

a description of the digital activity with respect to which the designation
has effect,

15.3.c

any provision that the CMA has decided to make in reliance on  section 17
(existing obligations),

15.3.d

the CMA’s reasons for its decisions under  section 14 (1) ,

15.3.e

a statement of the period (the “designation period”) for which the designation
has effect (see section  18 ),

15.3.f

a statement of the circumstances in which the designation period may be
extended (see  section 104 ), and

15.3.g

a statement of the circumstances in which the designation may be revoked
before the end of the designation period (see sections  10  and  14 (1) (b) ).

15.4

The CMA may give one or more revised versions of an SMS decision notice if it
changes its view of—

15.4.a

the undertaking, or

15.4.b

the digital activity,

provided that the undertaking or digital activity, as the case may be, remains
substantially the same.

15.5

The giving of a revised SMS decision notice providing for the designation of
an undertaking does not affect—

15.5.a

the day on which the designation period in relation to that designation
begins, or

15.5.b

anything done under this Part in relation to that undertaking.

15.6

As soon as reasonably practicable after giving a revised SMS decision notice,
the CMA must publish the revised notice.

###### Notice requirements: decisions to revoke a designation

16

16.1

This section  applies where the CMA decides, as a result of a further SMS
investigation, to revoke the existing designation of a designated undertaking
in respect of a digital activity without making a further designation in
respect of that digital activity under section  14 (1)(b).

16.2

The SMS decision notice must provide for the revocation of the existing
designation—

16.2.a

to have effect at the end of the day on which the notice is given, or

16.2.b

to have effect from such earlier time as the CMA may specify in the notice.

16.3

The SMS decision notice must include—

16.3.a

any provision that the CMA has decided to make in reliance on  section 17
(existing obligations);

16.3.b

the CMA’s reasons for its decisions under  section 14 (1) (b) .

###### Existing obligations

17

17.1

Where the CMA decides, as a result of a further SMS investigation, to revoke a
designated undertaking’s designation in respect of a relevant digital
activity, the CMA may make transitional, transitory or saving provision in
respect of any existing obligation.

17.2

Provision may be made in reliance on subsection  (1)  only for the purpose of
managing the impact of the revocation—

17.2.a

on any person who benefited from the existing obligation, and

17.2.b

in a way that appears to the CMA to be fair and reasonable.

17.3

In Chapters  6  (investigatory powers and compliance reports) and  7
(enforcement and appeals), references to a “designated undertaking” are to be
read as including an undertaking to which an existing obligation applies by
virtue of provision made in reliance on subsection  (1) .

17.4

Subsection  (5)  applies where the CMA decides, as a result of a further SMS
investigation, to—

17.4.a

designate an undertaking again in respect of a relevant digital activity, or

17.4.b

designate an undertaking in respect of a different digital activity in
reliance on  section 10 (4) .

17.5

Where this subsection applies, the CMA may—

17.5.a

apply any existing obligation, with or without modification, to the designated
undertaking in respect of the new designation;

17.5.b

make transitional, transitory or saving provision in respect of any existing
obligation.

17.6

For the purposes of this section, an “existing obligation” is any—

17.6.a

conduct requirement (see  section 19 ),

17.6.b

enforcement order (see  section 31 ),

17.6.c

commitment (see sections  36  and  56 );

17.6.d

final offer order (see section  41 (2) , or

17.6.e

pro-competition order (see  section 46 (3) (a) ),

that is in force in relation to a designated undertaking in respect of the
relevant digital activity before the revocation mentioned in subsection  (1)
or, as the case may be, the designation mentioned in  subsection (4) .

17.7

Provision made in reliance on this section is to be included in an SMS
decision notice.

###### Designation period

18

18.1

Where the CMA decides to designate an undertaking as having SMS in respect of
a digital activity, the designation period is 5 years beginning with the day
after the day on which the SMS decision notice is given.

18.2

See—

18.2.a

section 104  for circumstances in which the designation period may be
extended, and

18.2.b

sections  10  and  14 (1) (b)  for circumstances in which a designation may be
revoked before the end of the designation period.

#### Conduct requirements

##### Imposition of conduct requirements

###### Power to impose conduct requirements

19

19.1

The CMA may impose one or more conduct requirements on a designated
undertaking by giving the undertaking a notice containing the information set
out in section  21 .

19.2

The CMA may vary a conduct requirement imposed on a designated undertaking by
giving the undertaking a revised version of that notice.

19.3

“Conduct requirements” are requirements as to how the designated undertaking
must conduct itself in relation to a relevant digital activity, and references
in this Part to imposing conduct requirements include references to varying
conduct requirements in reliance on  subsection (2) .

19.4

As soon as reasonably practicable after giving a notice under  subsection (1)
or  (2) , the CMA must publish the notice.

19.5

The CMA may only impose a conduct requirement or a combination of conduct
requirements on a designated undertaking if it considers that it would be
proportionate to do so for the purposes of one or more of the following
objectives—

19.5.a

the fair dealing objective,

19.5.b

the open choices objective, and

19.5.c

the trust and transparency objective,

having regard to what the conduct requirement or combination of conduct
requirements is intended to achieve.

19.6

The fair dealing objective is that users or potential users of the relevant
digital activity are—

19.6.a

treated fairly, and

19.6.b

able to interact, whether directly or indirectly, with the undertaking on
reasonable terms.

19.7

The open choices objective is that users or potential users of the relevant
digital activity are able to choose freely and easily between the services or
digital content provided by the undertaking and services or digital content
provided by other undertakings.

19.8

The trust and transparency objective is that users or potential users of the
relevant digital activity have the information they require to enable them to—

19.8.a

understand the services or digital content provided by the undertaking through
the relevant digital activity, including the terms on which they are provided,
and

19.8.b

make properly informed decisions about whether and how they interact with the
undertaking in respect of the relevant digital activity.

19.9

A conduct requirement must be of a permitted type (see section  20 ).

19.10

Before imposing a conduct requirement or a combination of conduct requirements
on a designated undertaking, the CMA must have regard in particular to the
benefits for consumers that the CMA considers would likely result (directly or
indirectly) from the conduct requirement or combination of conduct
requirements.

19.11

A conduct requirement—

19.11.a

comes into force at a time determined by the CMA, and

19.11.b

ceases to have effect—

19.11.b.i

in accordance with a decision of the CMA to revoke the requirement (see
section  22 ), or

19.11.b.ii

subject to provision made in reliance on  section 17  (existing obligations),
when the designation to which the requirement relates ceases to have effect.

###### Permitted types of conduct requirement

20

20.1

Conduct requirements are of a permitted type if they are within subsection
(2)  or  (3) .

20.2

Requirements are within this subsection if they are for the purpose of
obliging a designated undertaking to—

20.2.a

trade on fair and reasonable terms;

20.2.b

have effective processes for handling complaints by and disputes with users or
potential users;

20.2.c

provide clear, relevant, accurate and accessible information about the
relevant digital activity to users or potential users;

20.2.d

give explanations, and a reasonable period of notice, to users or potential
users of the relevant digital activity, before making changes in relation to
the relevant digital activity where those changes are likely to have a
material impact on the users or potential users;

20.2.e

present to users or potential users any options or default settings in
relation to the relevant digital activity in a way that allows those users or
potential users to make informed and effective decisions in their own best
interests about those options or settings.

20.3

Requirements are within this subsection if they are for the purpose of
preventing a designated undertaking from—

20.3.a

applying discriminatory terms, conditions or policies to certain users or
potential users or certain descriptions of users or potential users;

20.3.b

using its position in relation to the relevant digital activity, including its
access to data relating to that activity, to treat its own products more
favourably than those of other undertakings;

20.3.c

carrying on activities other than the relevant digital activity in a way that
is likely to materially increase the undertaking’s market power, or materially
strengthen its position of strategic significance, in relation to the relevant
digital activity;

20.3.d

requiring or incentivising users or potential users of one of the designated
undertaking’s products to use one or more of the undertaking’s other products
alongside services or digital content the provision of which is, or is
comprised in, the relevant digital activity;

20.3.e

restricting interoperability between the relevant service or digital content
and products offered by other undertakings;

20.3.f

restricting whether or how users or potential users can use the relevant
digital activity;

20.3.g

using data unfairly;

20.3.h

restricting the ability of users or potential users to use products of other
undertakings.

20.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this section so as to modify
the permitted types of requirement.

20.5

Regulations under  subsection (4)  are subject to the affirmative procedure.

###### Content of notice imposing a conduct requirement

21

A notice under section  19 (1)  or  (2)  must include, in relation to each
conduct requirement or, as the case may be, each conduct requirement as
varied, a statement of—

21.a

the conduct requirement and the relevant digital activity to which it relates;

21.b

the CMA’s reasons for imposing the conduct requirement, including—

21.b.i

the objective for the purposes of which the CMA considers it is proportionate
to impose the conduct requirement (see  section 19 (5) ),

21.b.ii

the benefits that the CMA considers would likely result from the conduct
requirement (see section  19 (10) ), and

21.b.iii

the permitted type of requirement to which the CMA considers the conduct
requirement belongs (see section  20 );

21.c

when the conduct requirement comes into force;

21.d

the last day of the designation period for the designation to which the
conduct requirement relates;

21.e

how the conduct requirement interacts with any other conduct requirement that
has been imposed on the undertaking.

###### Revocation of conduct requirements

22

22.1

The CMA may revoke a conduct requirement with effect from such time as the CMA
may determine.

22.2

Where the CMA decides to revoke a conduct requirement it must give the
designated undertaking to which the requirement relates a notice specifying
when the revocation is to have effect.

22.3

As soon as reasonably practicable after giving the notice, the CMA must
publish the notice.

###### Transitional provision relating to conduct requirements etc

23

23.1

A notice under  section 19 (1)  or  (2)  (content of notice imposing a conduct
requirement), or under  section 22 (2)  (revocation of conduct requirements),
may include transitional, transitory or saving provision.

23.2

The fact that a conduct requirement ceases to have effect does not affect the
exercise of any digital markets functions in relation to a breach or possible
breach of that requirement.

###### Consultation in relation to a conduct requirement

24

24.1

Before imposing a conduct requirement on a designated undertaking, the CMA
must—

24.1.a

carry out a public consultation on the conduct requirement which it proposes
to impose, and

24.1.b

bring the public consultation to the attention of such persons as it considers
appropriate.

24.2

For the purposes of the consultation, the CMA must publish—

24.2.a

the conduct requirement which the CMA proposes to impose, or a description of
that requirement, and

24.2.b

a statement of the permitted type of requirement to which the CMA considers
the proposed conduct requirement belongs.

24.3

Consultation under subsection  (1)  may be carried out at the same time as
consultation under section  13  (consultation on proposed decision.

24.4

Before revoking a conduct requirement, the CMA must—

24.4.a

carry out a public consultation on the proposed revocation, and

24.4.b

bring the public consultation to the attention of such persons as it considers
appropriate.

###### Duty to keep conduct requirements under review

25

The CMA must keep under review, in relation to a designated undertaking—

25.a

whether to impose, vary or revoke a conduct requirement;

25.b

the extent to which it is complying with each conduct requirement to which it
is subject;

25.c

the effectiveness of each conduct requirement to which it is subject;

25.d

whether to take action in accordance with  sections 26  to 35  (enforcement of
conduct requirements) or  Chapter 7  (enforcement and appeals) in respect of
any breaches or suspected breaches of a conduct requirement.

##### Enforcement of conduct requirements

###### Power to begin a conduct investigation

26

26.1

The CMA may begin an investigation (a “conduct investigation”) where it has
reasonable grounds to suspect that an undertaking has breached a conduct
requirement.

26.2

A conduct investigation is an investigation into—

26.2.a

whether a breach has occurred, and

26.2.b

if it has, what action, if any, the CMA should take in relation to the breach.

26.3

When the CMA begins a conduct investigation it must give a notice (a “conduct
investigation notice”) to the undertaking which it suspects has breached a
conduct requirement.

26.4

The conduct investigation notice must—

26.4.a

state the conduct requirement which the CMA suspects has been breached;

26.4.b

describe the conduct which the CMA suspects constituted the breach;

26.4.c

state the period within which the undertaking may make representations in
relation to the conduct investigation (see subsection  (5) );

26.4.d

state the period by the end of which the CMA must give a notice to the
undertaking setting out its findings as a result of the conduct investigation
(see  section 30 (2) );

26.4.e

state the circumstances in which that period may be extended (see  section 104
);

26.4.f

state the effect of the following provisions—

26.4.f.i

section 28  (closing a conduct investigation without making a finding);

26.4.f.ii

section 30  (notice of findings);

26.4.f.iii

section 36  (commitments).

26.5

The period mentioned in  subsection (4) (c)  is such period as the CMA may
determine.

26.6

As soon as reasonably practicable after giving a conduct investigation notice,
the CMA must publish the conduct investigation notice.

###### Consideration of representations

27

Before making a finding that an undertaking to which a conduct investigation
relates has breached or is breaching a conduct requirement, the CMA must
consider any representations that the undertaking makes in relation to the
conduct investigation.

###### Closing a conduct investigation without making a finding

28

28.1

The CMA may close a conduct investigation at any time without making a finding
as to whether or not a breach of a conduct requirement has occurred.

28.2

When the CMA decides to close a conduct investigation, the CMA must give the
undertaking to which the investigation related a notice to that effect.

28.3

The notice must—

28.3.a

describe the undertaking in respect of which the CMA began the investigation,

28.3.b

state the conduct requirement to which the investigation related, and

28.3.c

include the CMA’s reasons for closing the investigation.

28.4

As soon as reasonably practicable after giving a notice under subsection (2),
the CMA must publish the notice.

###### Countervailing benefits exemption

29

29.1

The CMA must close a conduct investigation under section  28  where
representations made by the undertaking to which the investigation relates
lead the CMA to consider that the countervailing benefits exemption applies.

29.2

The countervailing benefits exemption applies where—

29.2.a

the conduct to which the investigation relates gives rise to benefits to users
or potential users of the digital activity in respect of which the conduct
requirement in question applies,

29.2.b

those benefits outweigh any actual or likely detrimental impact on competition
resulting from a breach of the conduct requirement,

29.2.c

those benefits could not be realised without the conduct,

29.2.d

the conduct is proportionate to the realisation of those benefits, and

29.2.e

the conduct does not eliminate or prevent effective competition.

29.3

Where the CMA closes a conduct investigation as a result of  subsection (1) ,
the undertaking to which the decision relates is to be treated as if the CMA
had found that the conduct did not constitute a breach of the conduct
requirement.

###### Notice of findings

30

30.1

The CMA must give a notice to the undertaking to which a conduct investigation
relates setting out its findings as a result of the conduct investigation
(subject to subsection  (5) ).

30.2

The notice must be given on or before the last day of the period (the “conduct
investigation period”) of 6 months beginning with the day on which the conduct
investigation notice is given to the undertaking.

30.3

The notice must—

30.3.a

state whether or not the CMA has found that a breach has occurred, and

30.3.b

include reasons for the CMA’s findings.

30.4

As soon as reasonably practicable after giving the notice, the CMA must
publish the notice.

30.5

Subsection  (1)  does not apply—

30.5.a

where the CMA closes the conduct investigation under section  28 , or

30.5.b

in relation to any behaviour in respect of which the CMA has accepted a
commitment from the undertaking (see section  36 ).

###### Enforcement orders

31

31.1

Where the CMA finds, as a result of a conduct investigation, that an
undertaking has breached a conduct requirement, it may make an order (an
“enforcement order”) imposing on the undertaking such obligations as the CMA
considers appropriate for one or more of the following purposes—

31.1.a

in a case where the breach is ongoing, stopping the breach;

31.1.b

preventing the breach from happening again;

31.1.c

addressing any damage caused by the breach.

31.2

The CMA may vary an enforcement order by making a revised version of that
order.

31.3

An enforcement order may include transitional, transitory or saving provision.

31.4

An enforcement order must—

31.4.a

specify the breach to which it relates;

31.4.b

include the CMA’s reasons for imposing the obligations in the order.

31.5

The CMA may consult such persons as the CMA considers appropriate before
making an enforcement order (including a revised version of an order).

31.6

Where the CMA decides to make an enforcement order (other than an interim
enforcement order under section  32 ), it must do so as soon as reasonably
practicable after giving the undertaking a notice of its findings under
section  30 (1) .

31.7

As soon as reasonably practicable after making an enforcement order (including
a revised version of an order), the CMA must publish the order.

31.8

The CMA may consent to an undertaking acting in a way that would otherwise
constitute a breach of an enforcement order.

###### Interim enforcement orders

32

32.1

The CMA may make an enforcement order on an interim basis (an “interim
enforcement order”) in relation to a suspected breach of a conduct requirement
where—

32.1.a

the CMA has begun a conduct investigation in relation to the suspected breach,
and

32.1.b

the CMA considers that it is necessary to act on an interim basis—

32.1.b.i

to prevent significant damage to a particular person or category of person,

32.1.b.ii

to prevent conduct which could reduce the effectiveness of any other steps the
CMA might take in relation to the conduct requirement which it suspects the
undertaking has breached or is breaching, or

32.1.b.iii

to protect the public interest.

32.2

An interim enforcement order must specify the suspected breach to which it
relates.

32.3

Before making an interim enforcement order, the CMA must give the undertaking
to which it would relate an opportunity to make representations to it about
the order which it proposes to make.

32.4

But the duty in subsection  (3)  does not apply where the CMA considers that
compliance would substantially reduce the effectiveness of the order.

32.5

Where the CMA makes an interim enforcement order in relation to an undertaking
without complying with subsection  (3) , the CMA must, as soon as reasonably
practicable, give the undertaking a notice including—

32.5.a

the reasons for the CMA’s decision to make the interim enforcement order
without complying with subsection  (3) , and

32.5.b

the period within which the undertaking may make representations in relation
to the interim enforcement order (see  subsection (7) ).

32.6

As soon as reasonably practicable after giving a notice under subsection  (5)
, the CMA must publish the notice.

32.7

The period mentioned in subsection  (5) (b)  is such period as the CMA may
determine.

32.8

The CMA must consider representations which it receives following a notice
under subsection  (5)  as soon as reasonably practicable.

###### Duration of enforcement orders

33

33.1

An enforcement order (including a revised version of an order) comes into
force at such time as the CMA may specify in the order.

33.2

An interim enforcement order ceases to have effect—

33.2.a

when revoked under section  34 ,

33.2.b

subject to provision made in reliance on  section 17  (existing obligations),
when the designation to which it relates ceases to have effect, or

33.2.c

when one of the following events occurs in relation to the suspected breach to
which the order relates—

33.2.c.i

the CMA gives the undertaking a notice stating that the CMA has found that no
breach has occurred (see  section 30 );

33.2.c.ii

the CMA accepts a commitment from the undertaking (see  section 36 );

33.2.c.iii

the CMA makes an enforcement order (see  section 31 (1) );

33.2.c.iv

the CMA notifies the undertaking that it has decided not to make an
enforcement order that is not an interim enforcement order.

33.3

An enforcement order other than an interim enforcement order ceases to have
effect—

33.3.a

when revoked under section  34 , or

33.3.b

subject to provision made in reliance on  section 17  (existing obligations),
when the designation to which it relates ceases to have effect.

33.4

The fact that an enforcement order ceases to have effect does not affect the
exercise of any functions in relation to a breach or possible breach of that
order.

###### Revocation of enforcement orders

34

34.1

The CMA may revoke an enforcement order by giving a notice to that effect to
the undertaking to which the order applies.

34.2

The notice must include the reasons for the CMA’s decision to revoke the
enforcement order.

34.3

The notice may include transitional, transitory or saving provision in
relation to the revocation of the enforcement order.

34.4

As soon as reasonably practicable after revoking an enforcement order, the CMA
must publish the notice.

34.5

The CMA may consult such persons as the CMA considers appropriate on any
proposal to revoke an enforcement order.

###### Duty to keep enforcement orders under review

35

The CMA must keep under review—

35.a

the extent to which an undertaking to which it has given an enforcement order
is complying with that order,

35.b

the effectiveness of an enforcement order,

35.c

whether to vary or revoke an enforcement order,

35.d

where an enforcement order is revoked, whether to make a new enforcement
order, and

35.e

whether to take action in accordance with  Chapter 7  (enforcement and
appeals) in respect of an undertaking which does not comply with an
enforcement order.

##### Commitments relating to conduct requirements

###### Commitments

36

36.1

The CMA may accept an appropriate commitment from an undertaking subject to a
conduct investigation as to its behaviour in respect of a conduct requirement
to which the investigation relates.

36.2

A commitment is appropriate where the CMA considers that compliance with the
commitment by the undertaking would mean that it would not be necessary to
carry out a conduct investigation so far as relating to the behaviour to which
the commitment relates.

36.3

Following the acceptance of a commitment by the CMA as to the behaviour of an
undertaking—

36.3.a

the undertaking that gave the commitment must comply with it at all times when
it is in force, and

36.3.b

so far as relating to the behaviour, the CMA may not give a notice to the
undertaking under  section 30  (notice of findings).

36.4

The acceptance of a commitment does not prevent—

36.4.a

a conduct investigation from continuing so far as it relates to other
behaviour in relation to the same or a different conduct requirement, or

36.4.b

the CMA beginning a new conduct investigation in relation to the behaviour to
which the commitment relates where—

36.4.b.i

it has reasonable grounds to believe that there has been a material change of
circumstances since the commitment was accepted,

36.4.b.ii

it has reasonable grounds to suspect that the undertaking has not complied
with one or more of the terms of the commitment, or

36.4.b.iii

it has reasonable grounds to suspect that information which led it to accept
the commitment was incomplete, false or misleading in a material particular.

36.5

A commitment under  this section  comes into force when a notice of its
acceptance is published by the CMA.

36.6

A commitment under this section ceases to have effect—

36.6.a

subject to provision made in reliance on section  17  (existing obligations)—

36.6.a.i

in accordance with any terms of the commitment about when it is to cease to
have effect, or

36.6.a.ii

when the conduct requirement to which the commitment relates ceases to have
effect, or

36.6.b

when the undertaking is released from the requirement to comply with the
commitment.

36.7

The CMA may by notice accept a variation to a commitment from time to time
provided the commitment as varied would still be appropriate.

36.8

The CMA may release an undertaking from the requirement to comply with a
commitment where it considers that it would be appropriate to do so.

36.9

The fact that a commitment ceases to have effect does not affect the exercise
of any functions in relation to a breach or possible breach of that
commitment.

36.10

Schedule 1  makes provision about—

36.10.a

accepting, or accepting a variation of, a commitment, and

36.10.b

releasing an undertaking from the requirement to comply with a commitment,

for the purposes of this Chapter and  Chapter 4  (pro-competition orders).

###### Duty to keep commitments under review

37

The CMA must keep under review—

37.a

the appropriateness of a commitment or releasing an undertaking from a
commitment,

37.b

the extent to which an undertaking which has given a commitment is complying
with it, and

37.c

the appropriateness of taking further action in accordance with  Chapter 7
(enforcement and appeals) in respect of an undertaking which does not comply
with a commitment which it has given.

##### Final offer mechanism

###### Power to adopt final offer mechanism

38

38.1

Where the CMA considers that the following three conditions are met in
relation to a transaction between a designated undertaking and a third party,
the CMA may—

38.1.a

require the undertaking, and

38.1.b

invite the third party,

to submit to the CMA terms as to payment (“final offer payment terms”) which
the undertaking or, as the case may be, the third party regards as fair and
reasonable for the transaction.

38.2

The first condition is that the transaction is a transaction in which the
designated undertaking would—

38.2.a

provide goods or services to the third party, or

38.2.b

acquire goods or services from, or use goods or services of, the third party.

38.3

The second condition is that, by failing to agree fair and reasonable terms as
to payment for the transaction, the designated undertaking has breached an
enforcement order, other than an interim enforcement order, made in relation
to a breach of a conduct requirement of the type permitted by  section 20 (2)
(a)  (requirement to trade on fair and reasonable terms).

38.4

The third condition is that the CMA could not satisfactorily address the
breach within a reasonable time frame by exercising any of its other digital
markets functions.

38.5

In subsection  (1) , “ transaction ” means—

38.5.a

a future transaction, or

38.5.b

the future performance of an ongoing transaction,

whether in accordance with a contract or otherwise.

38.6

In sections  39  to  44 —

      “ the designated undertaking ” means the undertaking mentioned in
subsection (1) ;           “ the transaction ” means the transaction mentioned
in  subsection (1) ;           “ the third party ” means the third party
mentioned in  subsection (1) .

###### Collective submissions

39

39.1

Where the CMA considers that—

39.1.a

the conditions in section  38 (2) ,  (3)  and  (4)  are met in relation to a
single transaction between the designated undertaking and two or more third
parties, and

39.1.b

the third parties are capable of acting jointly in relation to final offer
payment terms relating to the transaction,

the CMA may exercise the power in section  38 (1)  to invite the third parties
(the “joined third parties”) to make a single submission to the CMA of final
offer payment terms that the joined third parties collectively regard as fair
and reasonable for the transaction.

39.2

Where the CMA proceeds in reliance on  subsection (1) , sections  40  to  44
apply as if—

39.2.a

in section  40 (8)  references to “the third party” were to any one or more of
the joined third parties;

39.2.b

all other references to “the third party” were to the joined third parties.

39.3

Where the CMA considers that—

39.3.a

the conditions in section  38 (2) ,  (3)  and  (4)  are met in relation to two
or more transactions between the designated undertaking and two or more third
parties,

39.3.b

the same terms as to payment are capable of applying to the transactions, and

39.3.c

the third parties are capable of acting jointly in relation to final offer
payment terms relating to the transactions,

the CMA may exercise the power in section  38 (1)  to invite the third parties
(the “grouped third parties”) to make a single submission to the CMA of final
offer payment terms that the grouped third parties collectively regard as fair
and reasonable for the transactions (the “grouped transactions”).

39.4

Where the CMA proceeds in reliance on  subsection (3) , sections  40  to  44
apply as if—

39.4.a

in the following provisions, references to “the third party” were to any one
or more of the grouped third parties—

39.4.a.i

section  40 (8) ;

39.4.a.ii

section  41 (2) (b) ;

39.4.a.iii

section  42 (1) (b) ;

39.4.a.iv

section  43 (2) ;

39.4.b

all other references to “the third party” were to the grouped third parties;

39.4.c

in section  43 (1)  and  (2) , the reference to “the transaction” were to any
one or more of the grouped transactions;

39.4.d

all other references to “the transaction” were to the grouped transactions.

###### Final offer mechanism

40

40.1

The power conferred by  section 38 (1)  is to be exercised by giving a notice
(a “final offer initiation notice”) to the designated undertaking and the
third party.

40.2

The final offer initiation notice must—

40.2.a

specify the designated undertaking, the third party and the digital activity
in respect of which the power is being exercised;

40.2.b

describe the breach of the enforcement order in relation to which the second
condition in  section 38  is met;

40.2.c

summarise the transaction;

40.2.d

specify a date (the “submission date”) on or before which final offer payment
terms are to be submitted to the CMA;

40.2.e

state the period by the end of which the CMA must make any final offer order
(see  section 41 (3) );

40.2.f

state the circumstances in which that period may be extended (see  section 104
).

40.3

As soon as reasonably practicable after giving a final offer initiation
notice, the CMA must publish a statement which—

40.3.a

includes the information mentioned in  subsection (2) , and

40.3.b

if the CMA is considering taking any other action relating to any underlying
cause of the breach of the enforcement order, includes a summary of, and
explanation for considering, that action.

40.4

After giving a final offer initiation notice, the CMA may—

40.4.a

change its view of the transaction or the third party, provided that the new
transaction or third party remains substantially the same as the previous
transaction or third party,

40.4.b

revise any list of joined third parties or grouped third parties, or

40.4.c

change the submission date.

40.5

The powers conferred by  subsection (4)  are to be exercised by giving a
revised version of the final offer initiation notice to the designated
undertaking and the third party.

40.6

Where the power conferred by  subsection (4) (b)  is being exercised, the
reference in  subsection (5)  to “ the third party ” includes each person that
was a joined third party or a grouped third party prior to the exercise of the
power or that is to be a joined third party or a grouped third party after the
exercise of the power.

40.7

As soon as reasonably practicable after giving a revised version of a final
offer initiation notice, the CMA must publish a statement summarising the
contents of the revised notice.

40.8

To facilitate the submission of final offer payment terms, the CMA may (among
other things)—

40.8.a

use an information notice to require that the designated undertaking or the
third party give information to the CMA (see section  69 );

40.8.b

share information between the designated undertaking and the third party in
accordance with section 241 of EA 2002 (statutory functions);

40.8.c

specify the form or manner in which final offer payment terms must be
submitted.

###### Final offers: outcome

41

41.1

This section applies where—

41.1.a

the CMA has exercised its power under  section 38 (1) , and

41.1.b

either—

41.1.b.i

the CMA has received final offer payment terms from both the designated
undertaking and the third party, or

41.1.b.ii

the CMA has received final offer payment terms from either the designated
undertaking or the third party (but not both), and the submission date has
passed.

41.2

The CMA must, unless  section 43 (1)  applies, make an order (a “final offer
order”) requiring that final offer payment terms it has received from the
designated undertaking or the third party are to be given effect for the
purposes of—

41.2.a

the transaction, and

41.2.b

any transaction between the designated undertaking and the third party which
is substantially the same as the transaction.

41.3

The CMA must comply with subsection  (2)  on or before the last day of the
period (the “final offer period”) of 6 months beginning with the day on which
the final offer initiation notice is given to the designated undertaking and
the third party.

41.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this section so as to modify
the length of the final offer period.

41.5

Regulations under  subsection (4)  are subject to the affirmative procedure.

###### Final offer orders: supplementary

42

42.1

A final offer order must impose on the designated undertaking such obligations
as the CMA considers appropriate for the purpose of—

42.1.a

securing compliance with the requirement imposed by virtue of  section 41 (2)
, and

42.1.b

preventing the designated undertaking from making an agreement with the third
party which conflicts with that requirement.

42.2

At the same time as making a final offer order, the CMA must give the
designated undertaking and the third party a notice—

42.2.a

summarising the transaction,

42.2.b

including the reasons for the order, and

42.2.c

enclosing a copy of the order.

42.3

As soon as reasonably practicable after making a final offer order, the CMA
must publish a statement summarising the contents of the final offer order and
the notice given under subsection  (2) .

###### Decision not to make final offer order

43

43.1

The CMA may decide not to make a final offer order in relation to the
transaction where it has reasonable grounds to believe that there has been a
material change of circumstances since the final offer initiation notice was
given.

43.2

For the purposes of  this section  and  section 44 (3)  a material change of
circumstances includes an agreement between the designated undertaking and the
third party with respect to terms as to payment in relation to the
transaction.

43.3

Where the CMA decides not to make a final offer order, it must give a notice
to that effect to the designated undertaking and the third party.

43.4

The notice must include the reasonable grounds referred to in subsection  (1)
.

43.5

As soon as reasonably practicable after giving a notice under subsection  (3)
, the CMA must publish a statement summarising the contents of the notice.

###### Duration and revocation of final offer orders

44

44.1

A final offer order comes into force at such time as the CMA may specify in
the order.

44.2

A final offer order ceases to have effect—

44.2.a

when revoked under this section, or

44.2.b

subject to provision made in reliance on  section 17  (existing obligations),
when the designation to which it relates ceases to have effect.

44.3

The CMA may revoke, or partially revoke, a final offer order where it has
reasonable grounds to believe that there has been a material change of
circumstances since the final offer order was made.

44.4

Where the CMA decides to revoke, or partially revoke, a final offer order, it
must give a notice to that effect to the designated undertaking and the third
party.

44.5

The notice must include the reasons for the CMA’s decision.

44.6

The notice may include transitional, transitory or saving provision in
relation to the revocation, or partial revocation, of the final offer order.

44.7

As soon as reasonably practicable after revoking, or partially revoking, a
final offer order, the CMA must publish a statement summarising the contents
of the notice revoking, or partially revoking, the order.

44.8

The fact that a final offer order ceases to have effect does not affect the
exercise of any digital markets functions in relation to a breach or possible
breach of that order.

###### Duty to keep final offer orders under review

45

The CMA must keep under review—

45.a

the extent to which an undertaking to which it has given a final offer order
is complying with that order,

45.b

the effectiveness of the final offer order,

45.c

whether to revoke the final offer order, and

45.d

whether to take action in accordance with  Chapter 7  (enforcement and
appeals) in respect of an undertaking which does not comply with a final offer
order.

#### Pro-competition interventions

##### Power to make pro-competition interventions

46

46.1

The CMA may make a pro-competition intervention (a “PCI”) in relation to a
designated undertaking where, following a PCI investigation (see section  47
), the CMA considers that—

46.1.a

a factor or combination of factors relating to a relevant digital activity is
having an adverse effect on competition, and

46.1.b

it would be proportionate to make the PCI for the purposes of remedying,
mitigating or preventing the adverse effect on competition.

46.2

In considering whether to make a PCI, and the form and content of any PCI, the
CMA may have regard to any benefits to UK users or UK customers that the CMA
considers have resulted, or may be expected to result, from a factor or
combination of factors that is having an adverse effect on competition.

46.3

A PCI may take the form of one or both of the following—

46.3.a

an order imposing on the designated undertaking requirements as to how the
undertaking must conduct itself, in relation to the relevant digital activity
or otherwise (a “pro-competition order”: see section  51 );

46.3.b

recommendations made by the CMA to any person exercising functions of a public
nature about steps which the CMA considers the person ought to take in respect
of the designated undertaking or the digital activity, or otherwise.

46.4

A PCI may include provision for the purposes of remedying, mitigating or
preventing any detrimental effect on UK users or UK customers that the CMA
considers has resulted, or may be expected to result, from the adverse effect
on competition to which the PCI relates.

46.5

A factor or combination of factors relating to a digital activity has an
adverse effect on competition where it prevents, restricts or distorts
competition in connection with the relevant digital activity in the United
Kingdom.

##### Power to begin a PCI investigation etc

47

47.1

The CMA may begin an investigation (a “PCI investigation”) in relation to a
designated undertaking where it has reasonable grounds to consider that a
factor or combination of factors relating to a relevant digital activity may
be having an adverse effect on competition.

47.2

A PCI investigation is an investigation to enable the CMA to determine—

47.2.a

whether to make a PCI, and

47.2.b

if it concludes that it should make a PCI, the form and content of that PCI.

47.3

The CMA may begin a PCI investigation in relation to a designated undertaking
even if it has previously made a decision not to make a PCI in respect of that
undertaking.

##### Procedure relating to PCI investigations

48

48.1

Where the CMA begins a PCI investigation it must give the designated
undertaking to which the investigation relates a notice (a “PCI investigation
notice”).

48.2

The PCI investigation notice must state—

48.2.a

the reasonable grounds mentioned in section  47 (1) ;

48.2.b

the purpose and scope of the PCI investigation;

48.2.c

the period by the end of which the CMA must give the undertaking a notice
setting out its decision as a result of the investigation (see  section 50 (1)
);

48.2.d

the circumstances in which that period may be extended (see section  104 ).

48.3

The CMA may give the undertaking one or more revised versions of the PCI
investigation notice if it changes its view of the purpose and scope of the
investigation, provided that the purpose and scope of the investigation
remains substantially the same.

48.4

As soon as reasonably practicable after giving a PCI investigation notice or a
revised version of the PCI investigation notice, the CMA must publish the
notice or the revised version of the notice.

##### Consultation on proposed PCI decision

49

49.1

Before making a final decision (a “PCI decision”) on whether to make a PCI as
a result of a PCI investigation, the CMA must—

49.1.a

carry out a public consultation on its proposed decision, and

49.1.b

bring the public consultation to the attention of such persons as it considers
appropriate.

49.2

For the purposes of the consultation the CMA must publish a statement setting
out—

49.2.a

the CMA’s findings as a result of the investigation, and

49.2.b

a description of any PCI which the CMA is considering making.

##### PCI decision

50

50.1

The CMA must give the designated undertaking to which a PCI investigation
relates a notice of the PCI decision resulting from the investigation on or
before the last day of the period (the “PCI investigation period”) of 9 months
beginning with the day on which the PCI investigation notice is given to the
undertaking.

50.2

The notice must—

50.2.a

state the CMA’s findings as a result of the PCI investigation,

50.2.b

describe any PCI which the CMA intends to make, and

50.2.c

include reasons for the CMA’s findings and decision.

50.3

The giving of a revised version of the PCI investigation notice under  section
48 (3)  does not change the day on which the PCI investigation period begins.

50.4

The CMA must make any PCI within the period of 4 months beginning with the day
on which the CMA gives the notice under subsection  (1) .

50.5

The CMA may extend the period mentioned in subsection  (4)  by up to 2 months
where it considers that there are special reasons for doing so.

50.6

Where the CMA decides not to make a PCI having previously indicated in a
notice under subsection  (1)  that it intended to make a PCI, the CMA must
give the undertaking a further notice—

50.6.a

stating the CMA’s decision, and

50.6.b

including reasons for the decision.

50.7

As soon as reasonably practicable after giving a notice under subsection  (1)
or  (6) , the CMA must publish a copy of the notice.

##### Pro-competition orders

51

51.1

A pro-competition order may include any provision that may be included in an
enforcement order under section 161 of EA 2002 (final orders following market
investigation references; and see section 164 of and Schedule 8 to EA 2002 on
the provision that may be included).

51.2

For the purposes of  subsection (1) , Schedule 8 to EA 2002 (provision that
may be contained in certain enforcement orders) has effect as if—

51.2.a

the reference in paragraph 8(2) to “the relevant report” were to the notice
under section  50 (1)  of this Act;

51.2.b

paragraphs 20A to 20BA were omitted.

51.3

A pro-competition order may include provision imposing requirements on an
undertaking on a trial basis for the purpose of assisting the CMA in
establishing requirements that would be effective in remedying, mitigating or
preventing—

51.3.a

the adverse effect on competition to which the order relates;

51.3.b

any detrimental effect on UK users or UK customers resulting from, or expected
to result from, the adverse effect on competition.

51.4

The provision that may be made in reliance on subsection  (3)  includes
provision requiring an undertaking to act differently in respect of different
users or customers (and such provision may be by reference to a description of
users or customers, to absolute numbers of users or customers, or to a
proportion of the undertaking’s total number of users or customers).

51.5

A pro-competition order must contain provision in accordance with section  55
(3)  (duty to ensure order contains date of next review).

51.6

As soon as reasonably practicable after making a pro-competition order, the
CMA must publish the order.

##### Replacement of pro-competition orders

52

52.1

The CMA may, by making a further pro-competition order, replace a pro-
competition order where it considers that it is appropriate to do so, having
regard in particular to—

52.1.a

the effectiveness of the pro-competition order, or of particular provisions in
the pro-competition order, in remedying, mitigating or preventing the adverse
effect on competition and, where applicable, any detrimental effect on UK
users or UK customers identified in the PCI investigation, and

52.1.b

any change of circumstances since the pro-competition order was made.

52.2

The CMA may, in particular, replace a pro-competition order so as to—

52.2.a

replace requirements imposed by virtue of that order on a trial basis, or

52.2.b

impose requirements on an undertaking that are similar to or informed by one
or more requirements previously imposed on that undertaking, or on a different
undertaking, by virtue of another pro-competition order on a trial basis.

52.3

In this Chapter—

52.3.a

references to making a replacement order are to revoking a pro-competition
order (see section  53 ) made following a PCI investigation and making a new
pro-competition order in reliance on the findings of that PCI investigation,
and

52.3.b

references to a “replacement order” are to a pro-competition order made in
reliance on subsection  (1) .

##### Duration and revocation etc of pro-competition orders

53

53.1

A pro-competition order comes into force at such time as the CMA may specify
in the order.

53.2

A pro-competition order ceases to have effect—

53.2.a

when revoked under this section, or

53.2.b

subject to provision made in reliance on  section 17  (existing obligations),
when the designation to which it relates ceases to have effect.

53.3

The CMA may revoke a pro-competition order where it considers that it is
appropriate to do so, having regard in particular to any change of
circumstances since the pro-competition order was made.

53.4

Where the CMA decides to revoke a pro-competition order, it must give a notice
to that effect to the designated undertaking to which the order relates.

53.5

The notice may include transitional, transitory or saving provision in
relation to the revocation of the pro-competition order.

53.6

The CMA must publish the notice as soon as reasonably practicable after giving
it.

53.7

Where a pro-competition order resulting from a PCI investigation is revoked
without being replaced, the CMA may not make a new pro-competition order in
reliance on the same PCI investigation.

53.8

The fact that a pro-competition order ceases to have effect does not affect
the exercise of any functions in relation to a breach or possible breach of
that order.

##### Consultation

54

54.1

The CMA must carry out a public consultation on the terms of any pro-
competition order before making it (subject to  subsection (4) ).

54.2

The duty to consult imposed by subsection  (1)  may be satisfied by
consultation on a proposed PCI decision in a case where—

54.2.a

a draft pro-competition order was published for the purposes of that
consultation, and

54.2.b

the CMA proposes to make a pro-competition order that is the same or
materially the same as the draft pro-competition order.

54.3

Before revoking a pro-competition order, the CMA must (subject to subsection
(4) )—

54.3.a

carry out a public consultation on the proposed revocation, and

54.3.b

bring the public consultation to the attention of such persons as it considers
appropriate.

54.4

The duties in subsections  (1)  and  (3)  do not apply in relation to the
making of a replacement order which, in the opinion of the CMA, is not
materially different from the order which it replaces.

##### Duty to review pro-competition orders etc

55

55.1

The CMA must carry out a review of a pro-competition order, including a
replacement order, to determine whether to—

55.1.a

revoke it without making a replacement order, or

55.1.b

make a replacement order.

55.2

Each time the CMA makes a pro-competition order, including a replacement
order, it must identify a date by which it will carry out the review under
subsection  (1) .

55.3

The CMA must secure that the date is specified in the order.

55.4

The CMA must keep under review—

55.4.a

the effectiveness of a pro-competition order;

55.4.b

the extent to which an undertaking subject to a pro-competition order is
complying with it;

55.4.c

whether to take action in accordance with  Chapter 7  (enforcement and
appeals) in respect of any undertaking that breaches a pro-competition order.

##### Commitments

56

56.1

The CMA may accept an appropriate commitment from a designated undertaking as
to its conduct in respect of an adverse effect on competition or a detrimental
effect on UK users or UK customers that the CMA considers has resulted, or may
be expected to result, from an adverse effect on competition.

56.2

A commitment is appropriate where the CMA considers that compliance with the
commitment by the undertaking would contribute to or otherwise be of use in
remedying, mitigating or preventing—

56.2.a

the adverse effect on competition, or

56.2.b

the detrimental effect on UK users or UK customers.

56.3

Following the acceptance of a commitment by the CMA as to the conduct of an
undertaking—

56.3.a

the undertaking that gave the commitment must comply with it at all times when
it is in force, and

56.3.b

so far as relating to the conduct, the CMA may give a notice to the
undertaking—

56.3.b.i

ending a PCI investigation (if it has begun one) without making a PCI
decision, or

56.3.b.ii

changing the scope of a PCI investigation.

56.4

As soon as reasonably practicable after giving a notice under  subsection (3)
(b) , the CMA must publish a statement summarising the contents of the notice.

56.5

The acceptance of a commitment does not prevent—

56.5.a

a PCI investigation from continuing so far as it relates to conduct other than
that to which the commitment relates, or

56.5.b

the CMA beginning a new PCI investigation in relation to the conduct to which
the commitment relates where it has reasonable grounds—

56.5.b.i

to believe that there has been a material change of circumstances since the
commitment was accepted,

56.5.b.ii

to suspect that the undertaking has not complied with one or more of the terms
of the commitment, or

56.5.b.iii

to suspect that information which led it to accept the commitment was
incomplete, false or misleading in a material particular.

56.6

A commitment under  this section  comes into force when a notice of its
acceptance is published by the CMA.

56.7

A commitment under this section ceases to have effect—

56.7.a

subject to provision made in reliance on section  17  (existing obligations)—

56.7.a.i

in accordance with any terms of the commitment about when it is to cease to
have effect, or

56.7.a.ii

when the designation to which the commitment relates ceases to have effect, or

56.7.b

when the undertaking is released from the requirement to comply with the
commitment.

56.8

The following provisions apply in relation to commitments under  this section
as they apply in relation to commitments under section  36 —

56.8.a

subsections  (7)  to  (10)  of section  36 ;

56.8.b

section  37 .

#### Mergers

##### Duty to report possible mergers etc

57

57.1

A relevant person (in this Chapter, “P”) must report an event to which
subsection (2)  or  (3)  applies (a “reportable event”) to the CMA before the
event takes place.

57.2

This subsection  applies to an event where—

57.2.a

the event results in P having qualifying status (see  section 58 ) in respect
of shares or voting rights in relation to a UK-connected body corporate, and

57.2.b

the value of all consideration (see  section 59 ) provided by P, whether
before or as part of the event, for shares or voting rights in the UK-
connected body corporate is at least £25 million.

57.3

This subsection  applies to an event which consists of the formation by P and
at least one other person of a body corporate (in this Chapter, a “joint
venture vehicle”) where—

57.3.a

P expects or intends that the joint venture vehicle will be a UK-connected
body corporate,

57.3.b

P has qualifying status in respect of shares or voting rights in relation to
the joint venture vehicle, and

57.3.c

the total value of—

57.3.c.i

all capital and assets contributed by P to the joint venture vehicle when it
is formed, and

57.3.c.ii

all other consideration provided by P, whether directly or indirectly, in
relation to the formation of the joint venture vehicle,

is at least £25 million.

57.4

In this Chapter, “ relevant person ” means—

57.4.a

a designated undertaking, or

57.4.b

where a designated undertaking is part of a group, any member of that group.

57.5

In this Chapter, a “UK-connected body corporate” is any body corporate
(wherever established or recognised) which—

57.5.a

carries on activities in the United Kingdom, or

57.5.b

supplies goods or services (whether for consideration or otherwise) to a
person or persons in the United Kingdom.

57.6

For the purposes of subsection  (5) , anything done by a subsidiary of a body
corporate is to be treated as being done by the body corporate.

57.7

The reference in  subsection (3)  to an “other person” is to a person who is
not—

57.7.a

the designated undertaking or part of the designated undertaking, or

57.7.b

where the designated undertaking is part of a group, a member of that group.

57.8

The duty to report an event under subsection  (1)  is subject to provision
made by or under regulations under  section 67 .

57.9

For steps that the CMA may take in relation to a possible merger, see—

57.9.a

section 33 of EA 2002 (duty to make references in relation to anticipated
mergers), and

57.9.b

section 72 of that Act (initial enforcement orders).

##### Qualifying status

58

58.1

For the purposes of section  57 (2) , an event results in P having qualifying
status in respect of shares or voting rights in relation to a UK-connected
body corporate where the event results in the percentage of the shares or, as
the case may be, the voting rights that P holds in the body corporate
increasing—

58.1.a

from less than 15% to 15% or more,

58.1.b

from 25% or less to more than 25%, or

58.1.c

from 50% or less to more than 50%.

58.2

For the purposes of section  57 (3) , P has qualifying status in respect of
shares or voting rights in relation to a joint venture vehicle where the event
results in P holding at least 15% of the shares or, as the case may be, voting
rights in the joint venture vehicle.

58.3

In subsections  (1)  and  (2) , references to holding a percentage of shares
are—

58.3.a

in the case of a body corporate that has a share capital, to holding shares
comprised in the issued share capital of the body corporate of a nominal value
(in aggregate) of that percentage of the share capital,

58.3.b

in the case of a body corporate that does not have a share capital, to holding
a right to a share of that percentage of the capital or profits of the body
corporate, and

58.3.c

in the case of a limited liability partnership, to holding a right to a share
of that percentage of any surplus assets of the partnership on a winding up.

58.4

For the purposes of subsection  (3) (c) , to the extent that rights to share
in any surplus assets of the limited liability partnership on a winding up are
not expressly provided for, each member of the partnership is to be treated as
holding the right to an equal share of such assets.

58.5

In subsections  (1)  and  (2) , references to voting rights are—

58.5.a

in the case of a body corporate that has a share capital, to the rights
conferred on shareholders in respect of their shares to vote at general
meetings of the body corporate on all or substantially all matters, and

58.5.b

in the case of a body corporate that does not have a share capital, to the
rights conferred on members to vote at general meetings of the body corporate
on all or substantially all matters,

and, in the case of a body corporate that does not have general meetings at
which matters are decided by such votes, include any rights in relation to the
body corporate that have the equivalent effect.

58.6

A person is to be treated for the purposes of this Chapter as acquiring an
interest or right (to the extent that the person would not otherwise be
regarded as doing so) where the interest or right becomes treated as held by
the person by virtue of  Schedule 2 .

##### Value of consideration

59

59.1

The references in section  57 (2) (b)  to the value of all consideration
provided by P for shares or voting rights in a UK-connected body corporate is
a reference to the value of all consideration provided by P, whether directly
or indirectly, for shares or voting rights in the body corporate in all
transactions which result in P holding shares or voting rights in the body
corporate (whether or not the transaction is an event within section  57 (2)
).

59.2

In this Chapter, references to “consideration” are to fees, remuneration,
assets of any description, liabilities assumed and any other kind of
consideration, however provided, and include conditional and deferred
consideration.

59.3

The Secretary of State may by regulations make further provision about how the
value of—

59.3.a

consideration,

59.3.b

capital, or

59.3.c

assets,

is to be calculated for the purposes of this Chapter.

59.4

The Secretary of State must consult the CMA before making regulations under
subsection (3) .

59.5

Regulations under  subsection (3)  are subject to the negative procedure.

##### Content of report etc

60

60.1

The CMA must by notice make provision setting out—

60.1.a

the information which a report for the purposes of  section 57 (1)  must
contain;

60.1.b

the form in which such a report must be made.

60.2

The notice may not require a report to contain information other than
information which the CMA considers necessary to allow it to determine whether
to—

60.2.a

begin an investigation for the purposes of deciding whether to make a
reference under section 33 of EA 2002 in relation to a reportable event, or

60.2.b

make an initial enforcement order under section 72 of that Act in relation to
a reportable event.

60.3

The CMA may from time to time replace the notice.

60.4

The CMA must publish any notice or replacement notice which it makes under
this section .

60.5

The CMA must consult—

60.5.a

the Secretary of State, and

60.5.b

such other persons as it considers appropriate,

before making or replacing a notice under  this section .

##### Application of the duty to report etc

61

61.1

Two or more persons may comply with the duty in  section 57 (1)  by making a
joint report to the CMA.

61.2

For the purposes of this Chapter, where a designated undertaking is part of a
group—

61.2.a

anything which a member of a group does or fails to do is to be treated as
being done or not done by each member of the group;

61.2.b

each member of a group is to be treated as providing the combined
consideration provided by all members of the group;

61.2.c

each member of a group is to be treated as holding the combined interests or
rights of all members of the group.

61.3

Schedule 2 makes further provision about cases in which a person is to be
treated for the purposes of this Chapter as holding an interest or right.

61.4

The duty to make a report under  section 57 (1)  does not apply—

61.4.a

in relation to a reportable event which does not differ in any material
respect from an event which has already been reported under  section 57 (1) ;

61.4.b

in relation to a reportable event so far as it consists of “notified
arrangements” within the meaning of section 96(6) of EA 2002;

61.4.c

in relation to a reportable event so far as the CMA has informed P that it has
begun an investigation for the purposes of deciding whether it has to make a
reference under section 33 of EA 2002 (duty to make references in relation to
anticipated mergers) in relation to a matter that does not differ in any
