material respect from the reportable event;

61.4.d

in relation to a reportable event so far as the Secretary of State has given
the CMA an intervention notice under section 42 of EA 2002 (intervention by
the Secretary of State in certain public interest cases) in relation to a
relevant merger situation that does not differ in any material respect from
the reportable event;

61.4.e

in relation to a reportable event so far as the Secretary of State has given
the CMA a special intervention notice under section 59 of EA 2002
(intervention by the Secretary of State in special public interest cases) in
relation to a special merger situation that does not differ in any material
respect from the reportable event.

61.5

This Chapter does not require any steps to be taken in relation to an event
where, after it has been reported to the CMA—

61.5.a

the Secretary of State gives the CMA an intervention notice under section 42
of EA 2002 in relation to a relevant merger situation that does not differ in
any material respect from the event;

61.5.b

the Secretary of State gives the CMA a special intervention notice under
section 59 of EA 2002 in relation to a special merger situation that does not
differ in any material respect from the event;

61.5.c

the CMA makes an initial enforcement order under section 72 of EA 2002
imposing obligations, prohibitions or restrictions in relation to the event;

61.5.d

the undertaking to which the event relates ceases to be a designated
undertaking.

##### Acceptance of report

62

62.1

Where the CMA receives a report under  section 57 (1) , the CMA must, within
the period of 5 working days beginning with the first working day after the
day on which it receives the report, give a notice to the person that made the
report confirming whether the CMA accepts that the report is sufficient.

62.2

Where the CMA does not accept that a report is sufficient it must, in its
notice under  subsection (1) , include reasons for its decision.

62.3

The CMA may not decide that a report is not sufficient where the report—

62.3.a

contains all information required by notice under section  60 (1) (a) , and

62.3.b

is made in the form required by notice under section  60 (1) (b) .

62.4

A person who makes a report under  section 57 (1)  may withdraw that report at
any time before the CMA gives notice that it has accepted that the report is
sufficient.

62.5

Where a report is withdrawn, this Chapter applies as if the event to which it
related had not been reported to the CMA.

##### Delay to possible mergers etc

63

63.1

A person to whom the duty in  section 57 (1)  applies in relation to a
reportable event must not allow the event to take place—

63.1.a

without a report in relation to the event having been given to the CMA under
section 57 (1) , or

63.1.b

before the end of the waiting period in relation to the event.

63.2

The waiting period in relation to a reportable event is the period of 5
working days beginning with the first working day after the day on which the
CMA gives the person that made a report a notice under  section 62 (1)
confirming that the CMA accepts that the report relating to the event is
sufficient.

63.3

If a reportable event takes place in contravention of  subsection (1) , each
person to whom the duty in  section 57 (1)  applied in relation to the event
is to be treated as having breached  subsection (1) .

63.4

The CMA may—

63.4.a

give its consent to a reportable event happening before the end of the waiting
period;

63.4.b

revoke that consent before the reportable event happens.

63.5

Subsection (1)  does not apply in relation to a reportable event where the CMA
gives and does not revoke consent under subsection  (4)  in relation to a
reportable event.

63.6

Section 95 of EA 2002 (rights to enforce statutory restrictions) applies in
relation to the obligation to comply with subsection  (1)  as it applies in
relation to the obligation to comply with section 77(2) or (3) or 78(2) of
that Act.

##### Timing of a reportable event

64

Where a reportable event results from an agreement providing for P to acquire
shares or voting rights, or to form a joint venture vehicle together with at
least one other person, the event is to be treated as taking place for the
purposes of  section 57 (1)  and  section 63 (1)  when P becomes
unconditionally obliged to acquire the shares or voting rights, or to form the
joint venture vehicle.

##### Authorisation for one person to act for another

65

65.1

P may authorise another person to make a report under  section 57 (1)  and
receive the notice under  section 62 (1)  which relates to the report on P’s
behalf by giving a notice of the authorisation to the CMA.

65.2

P may revoke an authorisation made under this section by giving a notice to
that effect to the CMA.

65.3

A notice under  subsection (1)  or  (2)  must be signed by an officer of P.

65.4

In this section, references to an “officer” of an undertaking are to an
officer of a body corporate that is, or is comprised in, the undertaking.

##### Applications for review of decisions relating to mergers

66

Section 120 of EA 2002 (review of decisions under Part 3 of EA 2002: mergers)
applies in relation to a decision made by the CMA in connection with its
functions under this Chapter, other than a decision about the imposition of a
penalty under section  85 (4)  or  87 , as it applies in relation to decisions
listed in subsection (1A) of that section.

##### Regulations about duty to report

67

67.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision about the duty to
report a reportable event.

67.2

The Secretary of State must consult the CMA before making regulations under
subsection (1) .

67.3

Regulations under  subsection (1)  may (among other things) make provision—

67.3.a

varying, adding or removing circumstances in which the duty to make a report
applies;

67.3.b

varying the period in  section 62 (1) ;

67.3.c

varying the waiting period in  section 63 ;

67.3.d

about exemptions from the duty to make a report;

67.3.e

varying, adding or removing circumstances in which one person may act on
behalf of another under  section 65 ;

67.3.f

modifying how  section 332  applies for the purposes of this Chapter or
Schedule 2 ;

67.3.g

conferring functions on the CMA in relation to the duty to report, including
power to make provision by notice or general or specific directions about a
matter mentioned in  paragraph (d) ;

67.3.h

amending this Chapter or  Schedule 2 .

67.4

Regulations under  subsection (1)  that contain provision made in reliance on
any of paragraphs  (a) ,  (b) ,  (c) ,  (d) ,  (e)  or  (h)  of subsection
(3) , whether alone or with other provision, are subject to the affirmative
procedure.

67.5

Any other regulations under  subsection (1)  are subject to the negative
procedure.

##### Duty to keep compliance under review

68

The CMA must keep under review—

68.a

the extent to which persons comply with provisions made by, under or by virtue
of this Chapter, and

68.b

the appropriateness of taking action—

68.b.i

in accordance with section 95 of EA 2002 (rights to enforce statutory
restrictions) in respect of any person to whom section  63 (1)  applies, and

68.b.ii

in accordance with  Chapter 7  (enforcement and appeals) in respect of any
person that does not comply with provisions made by, under or by virtue of
this Chapter.

#### Investigatory powers etc and compliance reports

##### Investigatory powers etc

###### Power to require information

69

69.1

For the purpose of exercising, or deciding whether to exercise, any of its
digital markets functions, the CMA may require a person (“ P ”) to give
specified information to it where it considers that the information is
relevant to a digital markets function.

69.2

The power conferred by  subsection (1)  is to be exercised by giving P a
notice (an “information notice”).

69.3

The CMA must include in an information notice—

69.3.a

the time and place at which the specified information must be given to the
CMA;

69.3.b

the manner and form in which the information must be given to the CMA;

69.3.c

information about the possible consequences of not complying with the notice.

69.4

The power under  this section  to require P to give information to the CMA
includes the power to—

69.4.a

take copies of or extracts from information;

69.4.b

require P to obtain or generate information;

69.4.c

require P to collect or retain information that they would not otherwise
collect or retain;

69.4.d

if any specified information is not given to the CMA, require P to state, to
the best of their knowledge and belief, both where that information is and why
it has not been given to the CMA.

69.5

For the purposes of  subsection (4) (b) , the CMA may include in an
information notice—

69.5.a

a requirement for P to vary their usual conduct (whether in relation to some
or all users or potential users of any service or digital content that P
provides);

69.5.b

a requirement for P to perform a specified demonstration or test.

69.6

In this section, “ specified ” means—

69.6.a

specified, or described, in the information notice, or

69.6.b

falling within a category which is specified, or described, in the information
notice.

69.7

The powers conferred by this section are exercisable in relation to
information whether it is stored within or outside the United Kingdom.

###### Requirement to name a senior manager

70

70.1

Where the CMA gives an information notice to a designated undertaking or an
undertaking that is the subject of a breach investigation, the CMA may include
in the notice a requirement that the undertaking must name, in response to the
notice, an individual who—

70.1.a

the undertaking considers to be a senior manager of the undertaking, and

70.1.b

may reasonably be expected to be in a position to ensure compliance with the
requirements of the notice.

70.2

Where the CMA imposes a requirement to name an individual, the information
notice must require the undertaking to inform the individual about the
consequences for the individual of any failure by the undertaking to comply
with the notice (see section  87 ).

70.3

An individual can be considered to be a senior manager of an undertaking only
if the individual plays a significant role in—

70.3.a

making decisions about how the undertaking’s relevant activities are to be
managed or organised, or

70.3.b

managing or organising the undertaking’s relevant activities.

70.4

An undertaking’s “relevant activities” are activities relating to the
undertaking’s compliance with requirements imposed on it by or under this
Part.

###### Power of access

71

71.1

The CMA may exercise the powers in  this section  where it considers that a
designated undertaking or an undertaking that is the subject of a breach
investigation—

71.1.a

has not complied with the requirements of an information notice (see  section
69 ), or

71.1.b

has not complied with the duty to assist a skilled person with the preparation
of a report (see  section 79 (12) ).

71.2

The CMA may access business premises, equipment, services, information or
individuals in order to—

71.2.a

supervise the obtaining, generation, collection or retention of information by
the undertaking,

71.2.b

observe the undertaking’s conduct in relation to users, or

71.2.c

observe a demonstration or test performed by the undertaking,

for the purpose of securing compliance with requirements imposed on the
undertaking under  section 69  or  section 79 (12) .

71.3

Where the CMA requires access under subsection  (2) , it must give the
undertaking a notice specifying—

71.3.a

the access that it requires,

71.3.b

a date by which the access must be provided, and

71.3.c

the manner in which the access must be provided (which may be remote).

71.4

The undertaking must give the CMA the access specified in the notice under
subsection (3) .

71.5

The powers conferred by this section are not exercisable in relation to
premises, equipment or individuals outside the United Kingdom.

71.6

But the powers conferred by this section are exercisable in relation to
information and services whether stored or provided within or outside the
United Kingdom.

71.7

In this Chapter, “ business premises ” means premises (or any part of
premises) not used as a dwelling.

###### Power to interview

72

72.1

If the CMA considers that an individual (“ X ”) has information relevant to a
digital markets investigation, the CMA may give a notice to X requiring X to
answer questions with respect to any matter relevant to that digital markets
investigation—

72.1.a

at a place or in a manner (which may be remote) specified in the notice, and

72.1.b

either at a time specified in the notice or on receipt of the notice.

72.2

The CMA must include in the notice—

72.2.a

details of the digital markets investigation;

72.2.b

information about the possible consequences of not complying with the notice.

72.3

Where X is connected to (see section  118 (3) ) the undertaking that is the
subject of the digital markets investigation, the CMA must give a copy of the
notice under  subsection (1)  to the undertaking.

72.4

The CMA must comply with the requirement under  subsection (3) —

72.4.a

at the time the notice is given to X, or

72.4.b

where that is not practicable, as soon as reasonably practicable after the
notice is given to X.

72.5

The CMA, or any person nominated by it, may take evidence in answer to
questions under  subsection (1)  on oath, and for that purpose may administer
oaths.

72.6

The powers conferred by  this section  are not exercisable in relation to an
individual outside the United Kingdom.

###### Use of interview statements in prosecution

73

73.1

A statement by X in response to a requirement imposed by virtue of  section 72
(a “ section 72  statement”) may only be used in evidence against X—

73.1.a

on a prosecution for an offence under section  93  or  94 ;

73.1.b

on a prosecution for some other offence in a case falling within  subsection
(2) .

73.2

A prosecution falls within  this subsection  if, in the proceedings—

73.2.a

in giving evidence, X makes a statement inconsistent with the  section 72
statement, and

73.2.b

evidence relating to the  section 72  statement is adduced, or a question
relating to it is asked, by or on behalf of X.

###### Power to enter business premises without a warrant

74

74.1

For the purposes of a breach investigation, the CMA may authorise an officer
of the CMA (“ an investigating officer ”) to enter any business premises (see
section  71 (7) ) and exercise the powers in subsection  (5)  if the CMA has
reasonable grounds to suspect that information is on or accessible from the
premises that is relevant to the breach investigation.

74.2

No investigating officer is to enter any premises in the exercise of their
powers under  this section  unless they have given to the occupier of the
premises a notice which—

74.2.a

gives at least two working days’ notice of the intended entry,

74.2.b

describes the subject matter and purpose of the breach investigation, and

74.2.c

includes information about the possible consequences of not complying with the
notice.

74.3

Subsection (2)  does not apply if—

74.3.a

the CMA has a reasonable suspicion that the premises are, or have been,
occupied by the undertaking which is the subject of the breach investigation,
or

74.3.b

the investigating officer has taken all such steps as are reasonably
practicable to give notice but has not been able to do so.

74.4

In a case falling within  subsection (3) , the power of entry conferred by
subsection (1)  is to be exercised by the investigating officer on production
of—

74.4.a

evidence of their authorisation, and

74.4.b

a document containing the information referred to in paragraphs  (b)  and  (c)
of  subsection (2) .

74.5

An investigating officer may, in addition to entering any premises—

74.5.a

take with them such equipment as appears to them to be necessary;

74.5.b

require any person on the premises to—

74.5.b.i

give information to the officer which the officer considers relevant to the
breach investigation;

74.5.b.ii

if any required information is not given to the officer, state, to the best of
the person’s knowledge and belief, where that information may be found;

74.5.c

take copies of, or extracts from, any information given to an investigating
officer;

74.5.d

take any steps which appear to be necessary for the purpose of preserving or
preventing interference with any information which the officer considers
relevant to the breach investigation.

74.6

Any information which is given to an investigating officer under subsection
(5)  must be in a form—

74.6.a

in which it can be taken away, and

74.6.b

which is visible and legible or from which it can be readily be generated in a
visible and legible form.

74.7

The powers conferred by  this section  are not exercisable in relation to
premises outside the United Kingdom.

74.8

But the powers conferred by this section are exercisable in relation to
information whether it is stored within or outside the United Kingdom.

###### Power to enter premises under a warrant

75

75.1

On an application made to it by the CMA for the purposes of a breach
investigation, the court or the Tribunal may issue a warrant if it is
satisfied that—

75.1.a

there are reasonable grounds for suspecting that there is information on or
accessible from any premises which is relevant to the breach investigation
(“information of the relevant kind”), and

75.1.b

one or both of the following applies—

75.1.b.i

the exercise by the CMA of another digital markets investigation power has not
resulted in the CMA being given the information of the relevant kind;

75.1.b.ii

there are reasonable grounds for suspecting that there is no other digital
markets investigation power the exercise of which would result in the CMA
being given the information of the relevant kind.

75.2

A warrant under  this section  authorises a named officer of the CMA (“the
authorised officer”), and any other of the CMA’s officers whom the CMA has
authorised in writing to accompany the authorised officer, to—

75.2.a

enter the premises specified in the warrant, using such force as is reasonably
necessary;

75.2.b

take onto the premises such equipment as appears to the authorised officer to
be necessary;

75.2.c

search the premises for information appearing to be information of the
relevant kind;

75.2.d

operate any equipment found on the premises for the purpose of producing
information;

75.2.e

require any person on the premises to provide such assistance as the
authorised officer may reasonably require (including providing passwords or
encryption keys and operating equipment on the premises);

75.2.f

require any person on the premises to give information to the authorised
officer;

75.2.g

require any person on the premises to state, to the best of their knowledge
and belief, where information appearing to be of the relevant kind may be
found;

75.2.h

take copies of, or extracts from, any information appearing to be information
of the relevant kind;

75.2.i

take possession of any information appearing to be information of the relevant
kind that is produced under paragraph  (d)  or given to the authorised officer
under  paragraph (f) ;

75.2.j

take possession of any other information appearing to be information of the
relevant kind if—

75.2.j.i

such action appears to be necessary for preserving the information or
preventing interference with it, or

75.2.j.ii

it is not reasonably practicable to take copies of the information on the
premises;

75.2.k

take any other steps which appear to be necessary for the purpose of
preserving any information appearing to be information of the relevant kind or
preventing interference with it.

75.3

Any information which is given to an investigating officer under subsection
(2)  must be in a form—

75.3.a

in which it can be taken away, and

75.3.b

which is visible and legible or from which it can be readily be generated in a
visible and legible form.

75.4

A warrant under  this section  may authorise persons specified in the warrant
to accompany the authorised officer who is executing it.

75.5

A warrant under  this section  continues in force until the end of the period
of one month beginning with the day on which it is issued.

75.6

Any information which the CMA obtains under  subsection (2)  may be retained
for a period of three months.

75.7

For the purposes of  this section  and section  76 —

      “ domestic premises ” means premises (or any part of premises) that are
used as a dwelling and are—         premises also used in connection with the
affairs of an undertaking or, where the undertaking is part of a group, a
member of that group, or           premises where information relating to the
affairs of an undertaking or, where the undertaking is part of a group, a
member of that group, is located;                 “ occupier ”, in relation to
any premises, means a person whom the authorised officer reasonably believes
is the occupier of those premises;           “ premises ” includes business
premises (see section  71 (7) ) and domestic premises.

###### Power to enter premises under a warrant: supplementary

76

76.1

A warrant under  section 75  must describe—

76.1.a

the subject matter and purpose of the breach investigation, and

76.1.b

the offence created by  section 95 .

76.2

The powers conferred by  section 75  are to be exercised on production of the
warrant issued under that section.

76.3

If there is no one at the premises when the authorised officer proposes to
execute the warrant they must, before executing it—

76.3.a

take reasonable steps to inform the occupier of the intended entry, and

76.3.b

if the occupier is informed, afford them or their legal or other
representative a reasonable opportunity to be present when the warrant is
executed.

76.4

If the authorised officer is unable to inform the occupier of the intended
entry they must, when executing the warrant, leave a copy of it in a prominent
place on the premises.

76.5

On leaving any premises which they have entered by virtue of a warrant under
section 75 , the authorised officer must, if the premises are unoccupied or
the occupier is temporarily absent, leave them as effectively secured as they
found them.

76.6

The powers conferred by  section 75  are not exercisable in relation to
premises outside the United Kingdom.

76.7

But the powers conferred by  section 75  are exercisable in relation to
information whether it is stored within or outside the United Kingdom.

###### Amendments to the Criminal Justice and Police Act 2001

77

77.1

The Criminal Justice and Police Act 2001 is amended as follows.

77.2

In section 50 (additional powers of seizure from premises), at the end insert—

77.2.7

Without prejudice to any power conferred by this section to take a copy of any
document, nothing in this section, so far as it has effect by reference to the
power to take copies of, or extracts from, information under section  75 (2)
(h)  of the Digital Markets, Competition and Consumers Act 2024, is to be
taken to confer any power to seize any information.

77.3

In section 57 (retention of seized items), in subsection (1), at the end
insert—

77.3.v

section  75 (6)  of the Digital Markets, Competition and Consumers Act 2024.

77.4

In section 63 (powers of seizure: copies), in subsection (1), at the end
insert—

77.4.d

for the purposes of this Part, except sections 50 and 51, the powers in
section  75 (2) (d)  and  (f)  of the Digital Markets, Competition and
Consumers Act 2024 are to be treated as powers of seizure, and references to
seizure and to seized property are to be construed accordingly.

77.5

In section 64 (meaning of “ appropriate judicial authority ”), in subsection
(3), in paragraph (a), at the end insert—

77.5.iv

section  75 (2)  of the Digital Markets, Competition and Consumers Act 2024.

77.6

In section 65 (meaning of “ legal privilege ”), after subsection (3A) insert—

77.6.3B

In relation to property which has been seized in exercise, or purported
exercise, of—

77.6.3B.a

the power of seizure conferred by section  75 (2)  of the Digital Markets,
Competition and Consumers Act 2024, or

77.6.3B.b

so much of any power of seizure conferred by section 50 as is exercisable by
reference to that power,

references in this Part to an item subject to legal privilege are to be read
as references to a privileged communication within the meaning of section  81
(privileged communications) of that Act.

77.7

In section 66 (general interpretation of Part 2), in subsection (5), after
paragraph (i) insert—

77.7.j

section  75 (2) (j)  of the Digital Markets, Competition and Consumers Act
2024;

77.8

In Part 1 of Schedule 1 (powers of seizure to which section 50 of that Act
applies), at the end insert—

77.8.73W

Digital Markets, Competition and Consumers Act 2024

Each of the powers of seizure conferred by section  75 (2) (i)  and  (j)  of
the Digital Markets, Competition and Consumers Act 2024 (seizure of
information for the purposes of a breach investigation).

###### Application for a warrant

78

78.1

An application for a warrant under  section 75  must be made—

78.1.a

in the case of an application to the court, in accordance with rules of court;

78.1.b

in the case of an application to the Tribunal, in accordance with Tribunal
rules.

78.2

In Schedule 4 to EA 2002 (tribunal: procedure), in paragraph 10A, in sub-
paragraph (1), after “the 1998 Act” insert  “or  section 75  of the Digital
Markets, Competition and Consumers Act 2024” .

###### Reports by skilled persons

79

79.1

The CMA may exercise the powers in  this section  in relation to a designated
undertaking, an undertaking that is the subject of a breach investigation or
an undertaking that is the subject of an SMS investigation (in each case, “U”)
for the purpose of exercising, or deciding whether to exercise, any of its
digital markets functions.

79.2

The CMA may appoint a skilled person to provide it with a report in a
specified form about matters relevant to the purposes for which the powers
under  this section  are or may be exercised (“the relevant matters”).

79.3

Where the CMA makes such an appointment, the CMA must give a notice to U—

79.3.a

confirming the appointment;

79.3.b

specifying the relevant matters.

79.4

A notice under  subsection (3)  may also make provision for U to be liable for
payment, directly to the skilled person, of the skilled person’s remuneration
and expenses relating to the preparation of the report.

79.5

As an alternative to subsection  (2) , the CMA may give a notice to U—

79.5.a

requiring U to appoint a skilled person to provide the CMA with a report in
such form as may be specified in the notice;

79.5.b

specifying the relevant matters to be explored in the report;

79.5.c

specifying the date by which the report must be provided.

79.6

Where the skilled person is to be appointed by U, U may not make an
appointment unless the CMA has approved in writing—

79.6.a

the identity of the skilled person, and

79.6.b

the terms on which they will be appointed, including in relation to their
remuneration and expenses.

79.7

Subsections (8)  to  (10)  apply in relation to an amount due to a skilled
person from U under  this section .

79.8

In England and Wales, such an amount is recoverable—

79.8.a

if the county court so orders, as if it were payable under an order of that
court;

79.8.b

if the High Court so orders, as if it were payable under an order of that
court.

79.9

In Scotland, such an amount may be enforced in the same manner as an extract
registered decree arbitral bearing a warrant for execution issued by the
sheriff court of any sheriffdom in Scotland.

79.10

In Northern Ireland, such an amount is recoverable—

79.10.a

if a county court so orders, as if it were payable under an order of that
court;

79.10.b

if the High Court so orders, as if it were payable under an order of that
court.

79.11

References in  this section  to a skilled person are to a person appearing to
the CMA to have the skills necessary to prepare a report about the relevant
matters.

79.12

It is the duty of—

79.12.a

U, and

79.12.b

any person connected to (see section  118 (3) ) U,

to give a skilled person who has been appointed under this section all such
assistance (including access to such business premises (see section  71 (7) ),
equipment, services, information and individuals) as the skilled person may
reasonably require to prepare the report.

79.13

The duty in  section 79 (12)  does not include a duty to give access to
premises, equipment or individuals outside the United Kingdom.

79.14

But the duty in  section 79 (12)  does include a duty to give access to
information and services whether stored or provided within or outside the
United Kingdom.

###### Duty to preserve information

80

80.1

A person to whom any of subsections  (2) ,  (3) ,  (4)  and  (5)  applies must
not, without reasonable excuse—

80.1.a

destroy, otherwise dispose of, falsify or conceal, or

80.1.b

cause or permit the destruction, disposal, falsification or concealment of,

any relevant information.

80.2

This subsection applies to a person where the person knows or suspects that a
breach investigation or a PCI investigation is being or is likely to be
carried out in relation to an undertaking.

80.3

This subsection applies to a person where the person is, or is connected to
(see section  118 (3) ), an undertaking that is not a designated undertaking
and knows that the undertaking is the subject of an initial SMS investigation.

80.4

This subsection applies to a person where the person is, or is connected to, a
designated undertaking and knows that—

80.4.a

the undertaking is required to produce a compliance report under section  84 ,
or

80.4.b

the undertaking is the subject of a further SMS investigation.

80.5

This subsection applies to a person where the person is, or is connected to,
an undertaking and knows or suspects that the CMA is assisting, or is likely
to assist, an overseas regulator in carrying out, in relation to the
undertaking, any of its functions which correspond or are similar to the
functions of the CMA under this Part (see  Chapter 2  of  Part 5  (provision
of investigative assistance to overseas regulators)).

80.6

For the purposes of this section, relevant information is information which
the person knows or suspects is or would be—

80.6.a

relevant to the investigation mentioned in subsection  (2) ,  (3) ,  (4)  or
(5) , as the case may be,

80.6.b

used by an undertaking to produce the compliance report, or

80.6.c

relevant to the provision of assistance to the overseas regulator.

###### Privileged communications

81

81.1

A person may not be required under any provision of this Chapter to produce,
generate or give to the CMA or an officer of the CMA a privileged
communication.

81.2

Nothing in this Chapter authorises the CMA or an officer of the CMA to produce
or take possession of, or take copies of or extracts from, a privileged
communication (but this is subject to Part 2 of the Criminal Justice and
Police Act 2001, as amended by  section 77  of this Act).

81.3

A “privileged communication” is a communication—

81.3.a

between a professional legal adviser and their client, or

81.3.b

made in connection with, or in contemplation of, legal proceedings and for the
purposes of those proceedings,

which in proceedings in the High Court would be protected from disclosure on
grounds of legal professional privilege.

81.4

In the application of this section to Scotland—

81.4.a

the reference to the High Court is to be read as a reference to the Court of
Session, and

81.4.b

the reference to legal professional privilege is to be read as a reference to
the confidentiality of communications.

###### Power of CMA to publish notice of investigative assistance

82

82.1

Where the CMA assists an overseas regulator in carrying out any of its
functions which correspond or are similar to the functions of the CMA under
this Part (see  Chapter 2  of  Part 5  (provision of investigative assistance
to overseas regulators)), the CMA may publish a notice of its decision to do
so which may, in particular—

82.1.a

identify the overseas regulator concerned;

82.1.b

summarise the matter in respect of which the assistance is requested;

82.1.c

identify the undertaking in respect of which the assistance is requested.

82.2

Section  112  does not apply to a notice under subsection  (1)  to the extent
that it includes information other than information mentioned in that
subsection.

##### Compliance reports etc

###### Nominated officer

83

83.1

An undertaking must ensure that, at all times when the undertaking is subject
to a digital markets requirement, it has an officer with responsibility for
carrying out the functions set out in  subsection (2)  in relation to that
digital markets requirement (a “nominated officer”).

83.2

The functions are—

83.2.a

monitoring the undertaking’s compliance with the digital markets requirement
and all related requirements;

83.2.b

cooperating with the CMA for the purposes of securing that the undertaking
complies with the digital markets requirement and all related requirements to
the satisfaction of the CMA;

83.2.c

securing that the undertaking complies with  section 84  (compliance reports).

83.3

A “digital markets requirement” is any of the following—

83.3.a

a conduct requirement under  section 19 ;

83.3.b

a requirement imposed by virtue of a pro-competition order under  section 46 ;

83.3.c

a requirement to comply with a commitment given under section  56 .

83.4

A “related requirement” is any of the following relating to a digital markets
requirement—

83.4.a

a requirement imposed by virtue of an enforcement order under  section 31  or
section 32 ;

83.4.b

the requirement to comply with a commitment given under  section 36 ;

83.4.c

a requirement imposed by virtue of a final offer order under section  41 (2)
or  section 42 ;

83.4.d

a requirement in a direction under section 87 of EA 2002 (delegated power of
directions) given by virtue of a pro-competition order (see  section 51 (1) ).

83.5

A nominated officer must be an individual who the undertaking—

83.5.a

considers to be a senior manager of the undertaking, within the meaning of
section 70 (3) , and

83.5.b

reasonably expects to be in a position to fulfil the functions set out in
subsection (2)  in relation to the digital markets requirement.

83.6

An undertaking that is required to have a nominated officer under  subsection
(1)  must, as soon as reasonably practicable, inform the CMA of the identity
of the nominated officer (including any replacement officer).

###### Compliance reports

84

84.1

An undertaking that is subject to a digital markets requirement (as defined in
section  83 (3) ) must provide the CMA with a compliance report in relation to
that digital markets requirement for each reporting period (as specified in a
notice under subsection  (3) ).

84.2

A compliance report is a report setting out—

84.2.a

the extent to which the nominated officer considers that the undertaking has
complied with the digital markets requirement and each related requirement
(see section  83 (4) ) during the reporting period;

84.2.b

how the undertaking has complied, and intends to continue to comply, with the
digital markets requirement and each related requirement;

84.2.c

such other information as the CMA may direct in relation to compliance with
the digital markets requirement and each related requirement.

84.3

At the same time as imposing a digital markets requirement on an undertaking,
the CMA must give a notice to the undertaking specifying—

84.3.a

the manner and form of the compliance report to be provided in relation to
that digital markets requirement, and

84.3.b

the reporting period for that digital markets requirement.

84.4

The CMA may amend the requirements specified in a notice under subsection  (3)
by giving a further notice to the undertaking.

84.5

The CMA may give a notice to an undertaking requiring it to publish a
compliance report or a summary of a compliance report at such time, and in
such manner and form, as the CMA may set out in the notice.

#### Enforcement and appeals

##### Civil penalties

###### Penalties for failure to comply with competition requirements

85

85.1

Where the CMA considers that an undertaking has, without reasonable excuse,
failed to comply with a requirement listed in  subsection (2) , it may impose
a penalty on the undertaking.

85.2

The requirements are—

85.2.a

a requirement imposed by virtue of an enforcement order under  section 31  or
section 32 ,

85.2.b

a requirement imposed by virtue of a final offer order under  section 41
(including a requirement imposed in reliance on  section 42 ),

85.2.c

a requirement imposed by virtue of a pro-competition order under  section 46 ,
and

85.2.d

the requirement to comply with a commitment given under  section 36  or  56 .

85.3

The CMA may impose a penalty on an undertaking where the CMA considers that
the undertaking has, without reasonable excuse, failed to comply with a
conduct requirement under  section 19 .

85.4

The CMA may impose a penalty on an undertaking or, where the undertaking is
part of a group, the group, where the CMA considers that the undertaking or
any member of the group has, without reasonable excuse, failed to comply with
a requirement in  Chapter 5  (mergers).

###### Amount of penalties under section 

86

86.1

The amount of a penalty imposed on a person under section  85  may be such
amount as the CMA considers appropriate, provided it does not exceed the
amounts set out in subsection  (4) .

86.2

The amount of a penalty under section  85 (1)  must be—

86.2.a

a fixed amount,

86.2.b

an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, or

86.2.c

a combination of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a
daily rate.

86.3

The amount of a penalty under section  85 (3)  or  (4)  must be a fixed
amount.

86.4

The maximum amounts of a penalty that may be imposed are—

86.4.a

in the case of a fixed amount, an amount equal to 10% of the total value of
the turnover of the undertaking or, where the undertaking is part of a group,
the turnover of the group;

86.4.b

in the case of an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, for each day
an amount equal to 5% of the total value of the daily turnover of the
undertaking or, where the undertaking is part of a group, the daily turnover
of the group;

86.4.c

in the case of a combination of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by
reference to a daily rate, the amounts mentioned in paragraph  (a) , in
relation to the fixed amount, and paragraph  (b) , in relation to the amount
calculated by reference to a daily rate.

86.5

In  subsection (4) , references to the total value of the turnover or daily
turnover of an undertaking or group are to the total value of the turnover or
daily turnover of the undertaking or, as the case may be, group, both inside
and outside the United Kingdom.

###### Penalties for failure to comply with investigative requirements

87

87.1

The CMA may impose a penalty on a person where it considers that the person
has, without reasonable excuse—

87.1.a

failed to comply with a requirement imposed by or under  Chapter 6 ,

87.1.b

given information which is false or misleading in a material particular in
connection with any function of the CMA under this Part, or

87.1.c

given information which is false or misleading in a material particular to
another person knowing that the information was to be used for the purpose of
giving information to the CMA in connection with any function of the CMA under
this Part.

87.2

The CMA may impose a penalty on an individual named as a senior manager under
section 70  as well as on the undertaking that names the individual where—

87.2.a

the CMA considers that the individual has failed, without reasonable excuse,
to prevent a failure or an action by the undertaking of a sort mentioned in
subsection  (1) , and

87.2.b

the failure or action relates to an information notice in response to which
the individual was named as a senior manager.

87.3

The CMA may impose a penalty on an individual who is appointed by an
undertaking to be a nominated officer under  section 83  in relation to a
digital markets requirement (within the meaning of that section), as well as
on the undertaking that appoints the individual, where the CMA considers that
the individual has failed, without reasonable excuse, to prevent the
undertaking from failing to comply with a requirement in or under  section 84
(compliance reports) in relation to that digital markets requirement.

87.4

The CMA may impose a penalty on an individual where it considers that the
individual has, without reasonable excuse, obstructed an officer of the CMA
acting in the exercise of the officer’s powers under—

87.4.a

section  74 , or

87.4.b

a warrant issued under section  75 .

###### Amount of penalties under section 

88

88.1

The amount of a penalty imposed on a person under section  87  may be such
amount as the CMA considers appropriate, provided it does not exceed the
amounts set out in subsections  (3)  and  (5) .

88.2

The amount of a penalty under section  87  must be—

88.2.a

a fixed amount,

88.2.b

an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, or

88.2.c

a combination of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a
daily rate.

88.3

The maximum amounts of a penalty that may be imposed on an undertaking that is
not an individual are—

88.3.a

in the case of a fixed amount, an amount equal to 1% of the total value of the
person’s turnover (both inside and outside the United Kingdom);

88.3.b

in the case of an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, for each day
an amount equal to 5% of the total value of the person’s daily turnover (both
inside and outside the United Kingdom);

88.3.c

in the case of a combination of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by
reference to a daily rate, the amounts mentioned in paragraph (a), in relation
to the fixed amount, and paragraph (b), in relation to the amount calculated
by reference to a daily rate.

88.4

Where a person is an undertaking that is part of a group, references in
subsection  (3)  to the person’s turnover are to the turnover of that group.

88.5

The maximum amounts of a penalty that may be imposed on an individual or a
person that is not an undertaking are—

88.5.a

in the case of a fixed amount, £30,000,

88.5.b

in the case of an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, £15,000 per
day, or

88.5.c

in the case of a combination of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by
reference to a daily rate, the amounts mentioned in paragraph  (a) , in
relation to the fixed amount, and paragraph  (b) , in relation to the amount
calculated by reference to a daily rate.

88.6

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend the amounts mentioned in
paragraphs  (a)  and  (b)  of subsection  (5) .

88.7

The Secretary of State must consult the CMA and such other persons as the
Secretary of State considers appropriate before making regulations under
subsection  (6) .

88.8

Regulations under subsection  (6)  are subject to the affirmative procedure.

###### Procedure and appeals etc

89

89.1

Sections 112 (penalties: main procedural requirements), 113 (payments and
interest by instalments), 114 (appeals), and 115 (recovery of penalties) of EA
2002 apply in relation to a penalty imposed under section  85  or  87  as they
apply in relation to a penalty imposed under section 110(1) of that Act.

89.2

For the purposes of this section—

89.2.a

sections 112 to 115 of EA 2002 are to be read as if references to “the
appropriate authority” were references to “the CMA” only;

89.2.b

section 114(5A) of that Act is to be read as if the words “In the case of a
penalty imposed on a person by the CMA or OFCOM,” were omitted;

89.2.c

section 114(12) of that Act is to be read as if, for paragraph (b), there were
substituted—

89.2.c.b

“ the relevant guidance ” means the statement of policy which was most
recently published under section  91  of the Digital Markets, Competition and
Consumers Act 2024 at the time of the act or omission giving rise to the
penalty.

###### Calculation of daily rates and turnover

90

90.1

In imposing a penalty by reference to a daily rate—

90.1.a

no account is to be taken of any days before the service on the person
concerned of the provisional penalty notice under section 112(A1) of EA 2002
(as applied by section  89 ), and

90.1.b

unless the CMA determines an earlier day (whether before or after the penalty
is imposed), the amount payable ceases to accumulate at the beginning of—

90.1.b.i

the day on which the person first complies with the requirement in question,
or

90.1.b.ii

if earlier, where the requirement was imposed in connection with the provision
by the CMA of assistance to an overseas regulator (see  section 319
(provision of investigative assistance to overseas regulators)), the day on
which the overseas regulator no longer requires that assistance.

90.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision for determining the
turnover (both inside and outside the United Kingdom) of a person for the
purposes of this Chapter.

90.3

The regulations may (among other things)—

90.3.a

make provision about amounts which are, or are not, to be included in a
person’s turnover;

90.3.b

make provision about the date or dates by reference to which a person’s
turnover is to be determined;

90.3.c

confer on the CMA the power to determine and make provision about matters
specified in the regulations (including the matters mentioned in paragraphs
(a)  and  (b) ).

90.4

Regulations under subsection  (2)  are subject to the negative procedure.

###### Statement of policy on penalties

91

91.1

The CMA must prepare and publish a statement of policy in relation to the
exercise of powers to impose a penalty under sections  85  and  87 .

91.2

The statement must include a statement about the considerations relevant to
the determination of—

91.2.a

whether to impose a penalty under section  85  or  87 ;

91.2.b

the nature and amount of any such penalty.

91.3

The CMA may revise its statement of policy and, where it does so, must publish
the revised statement.

91.4

In preparing or revising its statement of policy the CMA must consult—

91.4.a

the Secretary of State, and

91.4.b

such other persons as the CMA considers appropriate.

91.5

A statement of policy, or revised statement, may not be published under  this
section  without the approval of the Secretary of State.

91.6

Subsection  (7)  applies where the CMA proposes to impose a penalty on a
person.

91.7

The CMA must have regard to the statement of policy most recently published
under this section at the time of the act or omission giving rise to the
penalty when deciding—

91.7.a

whether to impose the penalty, and

91.7.b

if so, the amount of the penalty.

###### Monetary penalties: criminal proceedings and convictions

92

92.1

The CMA may not impose a penalty on a person under section  87  in relation to
an act or omission which constitutes an offence under section  93 ,  94  or
95  if the person has, in relation to that act or omission, been found guilty
of that offence.

92.2

A person may not be found guilty of an offence under section  93 ,  94  or  95
by virtue of an act or omission if the person has paid a penalty imposed under
section  87  in relation to that act or omission.

##### Offences

###### Destroying or falsifying information

93

93.1

A person (“ P ”) commits an offence if, having been required to give
information to the CMA or any other person under a provision of  Chapter 6 ,
P—

93.1.a

intentionally or recklessly destroys or otherwise disposes of it, falsifies it
or conceals it, or

93.1.b

causes or permits its destruction, disposal, falsification or concealment.

93.2

See  section 97  for provision restricting the application of this section in
relation to acts done by a person who is outside the United Kingdom.

###### False or misleading information

94

94.1

A person (“ P ”) commits an offence if—

94.1.a

P gives information to the CMA in connection with any of the CMA’s digital
markets functions,

94.1.b

the information is false or misleading in a material particular, and

94.1.c

P knows that it is or is reckless as to whether it is.

94.2

A person (“ P ”) commits an offence if P gives information to another person
which is false or misleading in a material particular and P—

94.2.a

either—

94.2.a.i

knows the information to be false or misleading in a material particular, or

94.2.a.ii

is reckless as to whether the information is false or misleading in a material
particular, and

94.2.b

knows that the information will be given to the CMA in connection with any of
its digital markets functions.

94.3

See  section 97  for provision restricting the application of this section in
relation to acts done by a person who is outside the United Kingdom.

###### Obstructing an officer

95

95.1

A person (“ P ”) commits an offence if P intentionally obstructs an officer of
the CMA acting in the exercise of the officer’s powers under—

95.1.a

section  74 , or

95.1.b

a warrant issued under section  75 .

95.2

See  section 97  for provision restricting the application of this section in
relation to acts done by a person who is outside the United Kingdom.

###### Offences by officers of a body corporate etc

96

96.1

If an offence under section  93 ,  94  or  95  committed by a body corporate
is proved—

96.1.a

to have been committed with the consent or connivance of an officer of the
body corporate, or

96.1.b

to be attributable to neglect on the part of an officer of the body corporate,

the officer as well as the body corporate is guilty of the offence and liable
to be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

96.2

If the affairs of a body corporate are managed by its members, subsection  (1)
applies in relation to the acts and defaults of a member in connection with
the member’s functions of management as if the member were an officer of the
body corporate.

96.3

If an offence under section  93 ,  94  or  95  committed by a partnership in
Scotland is proved—

96.3.a

to have been committed with the consent or connivance of a partner, or

96.3.b

to be attributable to neglect on the partner’s part,

the partner as well as the partnership is guilty of the offence and liable to
be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

96.4

In subsection  (3) , “ partner ” includes a person purporting to act as a
partner.

96.5

See  section 97  for provision restricting the application of this section in
relation to acts done by a person who is outside the United Kingdom.

###### Offences: limits on extra-territorial jurisdiction

97

A person does not commit an offence under section  93 ,  94  or  95
(including as those sections are applied by section  96 ) by virtue of an act
done when the person is outside the United Kingdom unless one or more of the
following applies at the time of the act—

97.a

the person is a United Kingdom national;

97.b

the person is an individual who is habitually resident in the United Kingdom;

97.c

the person is a body incorporated under the law of any part of the United
Kingdom.

###### Sentences

98

A person guilty of an offence under section  93 ,  94  or  95  is liable—

98.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to a fine;

98.b

on summary conviction in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding
the statutory maximum;

98.c

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or to a fine or to both.

##### Further enforcement provisions etc

###### Director disqualification

99

99.1

In the Company Directors Disqualification Act 1986, in section 9A (competition
disqualification order), in subsection (4)—

99.1.a

in the words before paragraph (a), for “either” substitute  “any” ;

99.1.b

at the end insert—

99.1.b.e

a requirement imposed by or under  Chapter 3  of Part 1 of the Digital
Markets, Competition and Consumers Act 2024 (undertakings with strategic
market status in respect of a digital activity: conduct requirements);

99.1.b.f

a requirement imposed by or under  Chapter 4  of Part 1 of that Act (pro-
competition interventions).

99.2

In the Company Directors Disqualification (Northern Ireland) Order 2002 ( S.I.
2002/3150 (N.I. 4)) , in Article 13A (competition disqualification order), in
paragraph (4)—

99.2.a

in the words before paragraph (a), for “either” substitute  “any” ;

99.2.b

at the end insert—

99.2.b.e

a requirement imposed by or under  Chapter 3  of Part 1 of the Digital
Markets, Competition and Consumers Act 2024 (undertakings with strategic
market status in respect of a digital activity: conduct requirements);

99.2.b.f

a requirement imposed by or under  Chapter 4  of Part 1 of that Act (pro-
competition interventions).

###### Enforcement of requirements

100

100.1

If a person fails, without reasonable excuse, to comply with a requirement
mentioned in  subsection (2)  (a “ subsection (2)  requirement”), the CMA may
apply to the court for an order—

100.1.a

requiring the person to comply with the  subsection (2)  requirement within a
time specified in the court’s order, or

100.1.b

if the  subsection (2)  requirement related to anything to be done in the
management or administration of an undertaking, requiring the undertaking, or
any of its officers, members or partners, to do it.

100.2

The requirements are—

100.2.a

a requirement imposed by virtue of an enforcement order (see  section 31  and
section 32 );

100.2.b

a requirement to comply with a commitment given under section  36  or  56 ;

100.2.c

a requirement imposed by virtue of a final offer order (see  section 41 (2)
and  section 42 );

100.2.d

a requirement imposed by virtue of a pro-competition order (see section  46 ).

100.3

An order of the court under  subsection (1)  may provide for all of the costs
of, or incidental to, the application for the order to be borne by—

100.3.a

the person that failed to comply with the  subsection (2)  requirement, or

100.3.b

where the person responsible for the failure is an undertaking, any officer of
a body corporate that is or is comprised in that undertaking.

100.4

In the application of  subsection (3)  to Scotland, the reference to “costs”
is to be read as a reference to “expenses”.

100.5

In  this section , references to an “officer”, “member” or “partner” of an
undertaking are to an officer, member or partner of a body corporate or, as
the case may be, partnership, that is, or is comprised in, the undertaking.

###### Rights to enforce requirements of this Part

101

101.1

A relevant requirement is to be treated as a duty owed by the person that is
subject to the requirement to any other person (“ P ”) who may be affected by
a breach of the requirement.

101.2

Where a breach of a relevant requirement causes P to sustain loss or damage, P
may bring civil proceedings against the person that has breached the
requirement before the appropriate court or the Tribunal for damages, an
injunction or interdict or any other appropriate relief or remedy.

101.3

Subsections  (1)  and  (2)  are subject to the defences and other incidents
applying to actions for breach of statutory duty.

101.4

For the purposes of this section and section  102 , a relevant requirement is—

101.4.a

a conduct requirement under section  19 ;

101.4.b

a requirement imposed by virtue of a pro-competition order under section  46 ;

101.4.c

a requirement to comply with a commitment given under section  36  or  56 .

101.5

Rules of court and Tribunal rules may make provision about the transfer from
the Tribunal to the appropriate court or from the appropriate court to the
Tribunal of all or any part of a claim made in proceedings under  subsection
(2) .

101.6

For the purposes of this section and section  102 , the “ appropriate court ”
means—

101.6.a

in relation to England and Wales or Northern Ireland, the High Court, and

101.6.b

in relation to Scotland, the Court of Session or a sheriff court of any
sheriffdom.

101.7

In Schedule 4 to EA 2002 (tribunal: procedure), in paragraph 1A, in sub-
paragraph (1) after “the 1998 Act” insert  “or  section 101  of the Digital
Markets, Competition and Consumers Act 2024” .

###### Treatment of CMA breach decisions etc

102

102.1

The appropriate court (see  section 101 ) and the Tribunal are bound by a CMA
breach decision once it has become final.

102.2

A CMA breach decision becomes final—

102.2.a

when the time for applying for a review of that decision has passed without an
application being made, or

102.2.b

where an application has been made, when the application has been finally
determined or has otherwise ended.

102.3

For the purposes of  subsection (2) (b) , an application is not finally
determined until any appeal relating to it has been determined (ignoring any
possibility of an appeal out of time with permission).

102.4

This section applies to the extent that the appropriate court or the Tribunal
would not otherwise be bound by the CMA breach decision in question.

102.5

In this section, a “CMA breach decision” is a decision by the CMA in
accordance with this Part that a person has breached a relevant requirement
(as defined in section  101 ).

102.6

Rules of court or Tribunal rules may make provision in respect of assistance
to be given by the CMA to the appropriate court or the Tribunal in proceedings
brought otherwise than by the CMA in respect of a breach, or an alleged
breach, of a relevant requirement.

##### Applications for review

###### Applications for review etc

103

103.1

A person with a sufficient interest in any decision to which subsection  (2)
applies may apply to the Tribunal in accordance with Tribunal rules for a
review of that decision.

103.2

This subsection applies to any decision made by the CMA in connection with its
digital markets functions (including a decision not to exercise a function)
apart from—

103.2.a

a decision made by the CMA in connection with its functions under  Chapter 5
(but see section  66 );

103.2.b

a decision about the imposition of a penalty under section  85  or  87  (but
see section  89 (1) ).

103.3

The making of an application under  subsection (1)  does not suspend the
effect of the decision to which the application relates except so far as a
direction to the contrary is given by the Tribunal.

103.4

In determining an application under  this section , the Tribunal must apply
the same principles as would be applied—

103.4.a

in the case of proceedings in England and Wales or Northern Ireland, by the
High Court in determining proceedings on judicial review;

103.4.b

in the case of proceedings in Scotland, by the Court of Session on an
application to the supervisory jurisdiction of that Court.

103.5

The Tribunal may—

103.5.a

dismiss the application or quash the whole or part of the decision to which it
relates, and

103.5.b

where it quashes the whole or part of that decision, refer the matter back to
the CMA with a direction to reconsider and make a new decision in accordance
with the ruling of the Tribunal.

103.6

An appeal lies on any point of law arising from a decision of the Tribunal
under  this section  to the appropriate court.

103.7

An appeal under subsection  (6)  requires the permission of the Tribunal or
the appropriate court.

103.8

In  this section , “ the appropriate court ” means—

103.8.a

in relation to England and Wales or Northern Ireland, the Court of Appeal, or

103.8.b

in relation to Scotland, the Court of Session.

#### Administration etc

##### Administration

###### Extension etc of periods

104

104.1

The CMA may publish a notice extending a relevant investigation period or a
final offer period by a period of up to 3 months where it considers that there
are special reasons for doing so.

104.2

A notice under  subsection (1)  must specify how long the extension is for.

104.3

The CMA may also publish a notice extending a relevant investigation period or
a final offer period where it considers that—

104.3.a

in relation to a relevant investigation period—

104.3.a.i

a person has failed to comply with any requirement of a notice under section
69  (power to require information) or under section  72  (power to interview)
which was given in relation to an SMS investigation, a conduct investigation
or a PCI investigation, and

104.3.a.ii

the failure is preventing the CMA from properly discharging the digital
markets functions to which the investigation relates, or

104.3.b

in relation to a final offer period—

104.3.b.i

a person has failed to comply with any requirement of a notice under section
69 , and

104.3.b.ii

the failure is preventing the CMA from properly discharging any of its
functions under sections  38  to  45  (final offer mechanism).

104.4

An extension under  subsection (3)  is for the period—

104.4.a

beginning with the day on which it comes into force, and

104.4.b

ending with the day on which the CMA publishes a notice of its decision to end
the extension.

104.5

The CMA must publish a notice under  subsection (4) (b)  where the person who
had failed to comply as mentioned in  subsection (3)  gives the information in
question to the CMA or, as the case may be, answers questions and provides
explanations to the satisfaction of the CMA.

104.6

An extension under  subsection (1)  or  (3)  begins with the day on which the
notice under  subsection (1)  or  (3) , as the case may be, is published.

104.7

Where—

104.7.a

the CMA extends an SMS investigation period relating to a further SMS
investigation under  subsection (1)  or  (3) ,

104.7.b

the extension means that the SMS investigation period would (apart from this
subsection) continue after the end of the designation period for the existing
designation which is the subject of the further SMS investigation, and

104.7.c

in the case of an extension under  subsection (3) , the person who had failed
to comply is, or is connected to, the designated undertaking,

the designation period for the existing designation is extended until the end
of the SMS investigation period.

104.8

In  this section  and in  section 105  references to a “relevant investigation
period” are to—

104.8.a

an SMS investigation period;

104.8.b

a conduct investigation period;

104.8.c

a PCI investigation period.

###### Extensions: supplementary

105

105.1

A period may be extended under both section  104 (1)  and  (3) .

105.2

No more than one extension is possible under section  104 (1) .

105.3

Where a relevant investigation period or a final offer period is extended or
further extended under section  104 (1)  or  (3) , the period as extended or,
as the case may be, further extended is, subject to  subsection (4) , to be
calculated by taking the period being extended and adding to it the period of
the extension (whether or not those periods overlap in time).

105.4

Where—

105.4.a

a relevant investigation period or a final offer period is further extended
under  section 104 (3) , and

105.4.b

the further extension overlaps with a previous extension under section  104
(3) ,

the period of overlap is to be disregarded in calculating the period of the
further extension.

###### Exercise and delegation of functions

106

106.1

The CMA may make a reference to the CMA chair for the constitution of a group
under Schedule 4 to ERRA 2013 in respect of any non-reserved digital markets
function.

106.2

A reference under  this section  must specify the non-reserved digital markets
function in respect of which the reference is made (“the referred function”).

106.3

A CMA group constituted under ERRA 2013 for the purposes of a reference under
this section  must carry out the referred function.

106.4

For the purposes of  this section , a “non-reserved digital markets function”
is any digital markets function other than a digital markets function that the
CMA Board may not delegate—

106.4.a

under paragraph 29(1) of Schedule 4 to ERRA 2013, as a result of paragraph
29(2) of that Schedule as it has effect from time to time, or

106.4.b

under paragraph 29(1)(a) of that Schedule, as a result of paragraph 29(2A) of
that Schedule as it has effect from time to time.

106.5

In  subsection (1) , “ CMA chair ” means the person appointed under paragraph
1(1)(a) of Schedule 4 to ERRA 2013.

106.6

In Schedule 4 to ERRA 2013 (the Competition and Markets Authority), paragraph
29 (delegation) is amended as follows.

106.7

In sub-paragraph (2) (functions which cannot be delegated), at the end insert—

106.7.g

whether to begin an initial SMS investigation under  section 9  of the Digital
Markets, Competition and Consumers Act 2024 (“ the 2024 Act ”);

106.7.h

whether to begin a further SMS investigation under  section 10  of the 2024
Act;

106.7.i

whether to begin a PCI investigation under section  47  of the 2024 Act.

106.8

After sub-paragraph (2) insert—

106.8.2A

Sub-paragraph (1)(a) does not apply to the functions of deciding—

106.8.2A.a

whether to make a designation under section  2  of the 2024 Act;

106.8.2A.b

what, if any, provision to make in reliance on section  17  of the 2024 Act;

106.8.2A.c

whether to impose a conduct requirement under section  19  of the 2024 Act;

106.8.2A.d

whether to revoke a conduct requirement under section  22  of the 2024 Act;

106.8.2A.e

whether to make, and the form of, an enforcement order, other than an interim
enforcement order, under section  31  of the 2024 Act;

106.8.2A.f

whether to accept a commitment under section  36  or section  56  of the 2024
Act;

106.8.2A.g

whether to exercise the power conferred by section  38 (1)  of the 2024 Act
(power to adopt final offer mechanism);

106.8.2A.h

whether to make, and the form of, a pro-competition intervention under section
46  of the 2024 Act;

106.8.2A.i

the contents of a notice under  section 50  of the 2024 Act (notice of
decision on pro-competition intervention);

106.8.2A.j

whether to replace a pro-competition order under section  52  of the 2024 Act;

106.8.2A.k

whether to revoke a pro-competition order under section  53  of the 2024 Act.

106.8.2A.l

whether to impose a penalty on a person under section  85  or section  87  of
the 2024 Act;

106.8.2A.m

the amount of any such penalty.

106.8.2B

A committee or sub-committee of the CMA Board may not be authorised to carry
out any of the functions listed in sub-paragraph  (2A)  unless—

106.8.2B.a

the committee or sub-committee includes—

106.8.2B.a.i

at least two members of the Board who are not members of the CMA’s staff, or

106.8.2B.a.ii

the chair and at least one member of the Board who is not a member of the
CMA’s staff, and

106.8.2B.b

at least half of the members of the committee or sub-committee are—

106.8.2B.b.i

members of the Board who are not members of the CMA’s staff, or

106.8.2B.b.ii

members of the CMA panel.

106.9

After sub-paragraph (3) insert—

106.9.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations made by statutory instrument amend
sub-paragraphs (2) or (2A) so as to add or remove functions of the CMA under
Part  1  of the 2024 Act.

106.9.5

The regulations may make incidental, transitional or saving provision.

106.9.6

A statutory instrument containing regulations under sub-paragraph  (4)  may
not be made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved
by a resolution of each House of Parliament.

##### Regulatory coordination and information sharing

###### Coordination with relevant regulators

107

107.1

The CMA must consult the FCA on a proposal to exercise a regulatory digital
markets function in respect of a matter where the CMA considers the matter is
a matter in relation to which the CMA and the FCA may have concurrent
functions (see sections 234I (functions under Part 4 of EA 2002) and 234J
(functions under CA 1998) of the Financial Services and Markets Act 2000 (as
amended by this Act) (“ FSMA ”)).

107.2

The CMA must consult OFCOM on a proposal to exercise a regulatory digital
markets function in respect of a matter where the CMA considers the matter is
a matter in relation to which the CMA and OFCOM may have concurrent functions
(see sections 370 (functions under Part 4 of EA 2002) and 371 (functions under
CA 1998) of the Communications Act 2003 (as amended by this Act)).

107.3

The CMA must consult the Information Commissioner on a proposal to exercise a
regulatory digital markets function in a manner that the CMA considers is
likely to have a material adverse effect on the ability of the Information
Commissioner to exercise functions under—

107.3.a

the data protection legislation,

107.3.b

the Privacy and Electronic Communications (EC Directive) Regulations 2003 (
S.I. 2003/2426 ), or

107.3.c

the Network and Information Systems Regulations 2018 ( S.I. 2018/506 ).

107.4

The CMA must consult the Bank of England on a proposal to exercise a
regulatory digital markets function in a manner that the CMA considers is
likely to have a material adverse effect on the ability of the Bank of England
to advance the Financial Stability Objective as defined in section 2A of the
Bank of England Act 1998.

107.5

The CMA must consult the PRA on a proposal to exercise a regulatory digital
markets function in a manner that the CMA considers is likely to have a
material adverse effect on the ability of the PRA to advance—

107.5.a

its general objective under section 2B of FSMA, or

107.5.b

its insurance objective under section 2C of FSMA.

107.6

The duties in  subsections (1)  to  (5)  apply only to the extent that the CMA
considers that compliance does not impose a burden on it that outweighs the
benefits of compliance.

###### Recommendations to the CMA

108

108.1

The FCA or OFCOM may make a recommendation to the CMA where they consider that
the CMA should exercise a regulatory digital markets function in relation to
an undertaking and a digital activity.

108.2

A recommendation under  subsection (1)  must—

108.2.a

describe the undertaking, the digital activity, and the regulatory digital
markets function to which it relates, and

108.2.b

be given to the CMA in writing.

108.3

A recommendation under  this section  must be accompanied by a statement of
reasons for the recommendation.

108.4

Within the period of 90 days beginning with the day on which it receives a
recommendation, the CMA must—

108.4.a

give notice to the regulator that made the recommendation—

108.4.a.i

setting out the action that the CMA has taken or intends to take in response
to the recommendation, and

108.4.a.ii

including the reasons for its decision, and

108.4.b

publish a summary of the notice.

###### Information sharing

109

109.1

In Schedule 14 to EA 2002 (provisions about disclosure of information) at the
appropriate place insert—

      Part 1  of the Digital Markets, Competition and Consumers Act 2024.

109.2

In Schedule 15 to EA 2002 (provisions about disclosure of information) at the
appropriate places insert—

      Privacy and Electronic Communications (EC Directive) Regulations 2003 (
S.I. 2003/2426 ).

;

      “ Regulation (EU) No 910/2014  of the European Parliament and of the
Council of 23 July 2014 on electronic identification and trust services for
electronic transactions in the internal market and repealing  Directive
1999/93/EC .

;

      “ Regulation (EU) 2016/679  of the European Parliament and of the
Council of 27 April 2016 on the protection of natural persons with regard to
the processing of personal data and on the free movement of such data (United
Kingdom General Data Protection Regulation).

;

      “Part 4 of the Network and Information Systems Regulations 2018 ( S.I.
2018/506 ).

;

      “Data Protection Act 2018.

;

      “ Part 1  of the Digital Markets, Competition and Consumers Act 2024.

##### Miscellaneous

###### Power to charge levy

110

110.1

The CMA may require an undertaking to pay it a levy in respect of a chargeable
year during the whole or part of which the undertaking is a designated
undertaking.

110.2

The amount of the levy is to be calculated in accordance with rules made for
the purposes of  this section  by the CMA (“the levy rules”).

110.3

The CMA may amend or replace the levy rules.

110.4

The levy rules must—

110.4.a

secure that the aggregate amount payable in respect of a chargeable year is
not to exceed the costs which the CMA incurs in exercising its digital markets
functions during that year;

110.4.b

make provision about how the aggregate amount payable in respect of a
chargeable year is to be divided between the undertakings which are designated
undertakings for the whole or part of that year;

110.4.c

secure that where an undertaking is a designated undertaking for only part of
a chargeable year, the amount of the levy payable by that undertaking in
respect of that chargeable year is proportionately reduced;

110.4.d

set out how the CMA is to estimate the costs which it expects to incur in
exercising its digital markets functions during a chargeable year;

110.4.e

set out how the CMA is to calculate the costs which it actually incurs in
exercising its digital markets functions during a chargeable year;

110.4.f

make provision about the repayment or crediting of any amounts of levy paid in
respect of a chargeable year on the basis of the CMA’s estimate of the costs
it would incur in exercising its digital markets functions during that year
where the CMA’s estimated costs exceed the CMA’s actual costs of exercising
those functions during that year;

110.4.g

secure that any repayment or crediting in respect of a chargeable year in
accordance with provision made under  paragraph (f) , so far as relating to an
undertaking, is in proportion to the amount paid by that undertaking in
respect of that year;

110.4.h

make provision about the charging of amounts of levy in respect of a
chargeable year where the CMA’s actual costs of exercising its digital markets
functions during that year exceed the costs which the CMA estimated it would
incur;

110.4.i

secure that, where an undertaking is required to pay an amount of levy in
respect of a chargeable year in accordance with provision made under
paragraph (h) , the amount which the undertaking is required to pay is in
proportion to the amount already paid by the undertaking in respect of that
year;

110.4.j

make provision about the administration and payment of the levy.

110.5

The levy rules may make provision for interest to be charged, at the rate
specified for the time being in section 17 of the Judgments Act 1838, on any
amount of levy not paid by the date on which it is due.

110.6

References in  subsection (4)  to an amount payable by an undertaking do not
include interest charged in accordance with provision made under  subsection
(5) .

110.7

The CMA must pay any amount that it receives in accordance with provision made
under  subsection (5)  into the Consolidated Fund.

110.8

The CMA must consult such persons as it considers appropriate before making
the levy rules, including any amended or replacement levy rules (see  section
113 ).

110.9

The consultation must include a draft of the proposed levy rules.

110.10

The CMA must, at the same time as beginning consultation under  subsection (8)
, arrange for the draft of the proposed levy rules to be laid before
Parliament.

110.11

The CMA must publish the levy rules, including amended or replacement rules.

110.12

An amount payable by an undertaking in accordance with  this section  and the
levy rules is recoverable as a civil debt due to the CMA.

110.13

For the purposes of  this section —

110.13.a

a chargeable year is a period of 12 months ending with 31 March;

110.13.b

the CMA’s costs of exercising its digital markets functions do not include
costs incurred by the CMA for the purposes of litigation.

###### Extra-territorial application

111

111.1

Unless otherwise stated, this Part applies in relation to persons outside the
United Kingdom.

111.2

A power to give a notice to a person outside the United Kingdom by virtue of
this Part  is exercisable only if the person is within  subsection (3) ,  (4)
or  (5) .

111.3

A person is within  this subsection  if the person is, or is part of—

111.3.a

a designated undertaking or an undertaking to which an obligation applies by
virtue of provision made in reliance on section  17 (1)  (existing
obligations);

111.3.b

an undertaking that is the subject of a digital markets investigation.

111.4

A person is within this subsection if the person is an individual—

111.4.a

who is named as a senior manager under  section 70  or appointed as a
nominated officer under  section 83 , and

111.4.b

on whom the CMA has imposed or is considering imposing a penalty under
section 87 (2)  or  87 (3) , as the case may be.

111.5

A person is within  this subsection  if the person—

111.5.a

is a United Kingdom national,

111.5.b

is an individual who is habitually resident in the United Kingdom,

111.5.c

is a body incorporated under the law of any part of the United Kingdom, or

111.5.d

carries on business in the United Kingdom.

111.6

Nothing in  this section  is to be taken to limit any other power of the CMA
to give a notice to a person outside the United Kingdom.

###### Defamation

112

For the purposes of the law relating to defamation, absolute privilege
attaches to anything done by the CMA in the exercise of any of its functions
under  this Part .

###### Consultation and publication of documents

113

113.1

The CMA must comply with any duty to consult under  this Part  in such manner
as it considers practicable, having regard in particular to—

113.1.a

any need to keep information confidential, and

113.1.b

the timetable for making a final decision or taking any action following the
consultation.

113.2

Any consultation which the CMA carries out under  this Part  must include—

113.2.a

reasons for the finding, decision or proposal to which the consultation
relates, and

113.2.b

such other information as the CMA considers necessary to allow a proper
understanding of those reasons (subject to  subsection (1) (b) ).

113.3

The CMA must comply with any duty to publish a notice or any other document
under this Part by publishing the notice or document online, having regard to
any need to keep information confidential.

113.4

In order to give effect to any need to keep information confidential, the CMA
may publish the notice or other document in a redacted form.

###### Guidance

114

114.1

The CMA must publish guidance on how it will exercise its functions under this
Part.

114.2

The CMA may revise or replace guidance published under this section.

114.3

The CMA must publish any revised or replacement guidance.

114.4

Before publishing guidance (including any revised or replacement guidance)
under this section, the CMA must—

114.4.a

consult such persons as it considers appropriate, and

114.4.b

obtain the approval of the Secretary of State.

114.5

When the CMA seeks the approval of the Secretary of State for guidance, the
Secretary of State must—

114.5.a

approve the guidance, or

114.5.b
