give reasons to the CMA for not approving it.

114.6

The Secretary of State must comply with  subsection (5)  before the end of the
30th working day after the day on which the CMA seeks the Secretary of State’s
approval.

###### Protected disclosures

115

In the Public Interest Disclosure (Prescribed Persons) Order 2014 ( S.I.
2014/2418 ), in the table in the Schedule, in the entry for the Competition
and Markets Authority, in the right hand column, after “Kingdom” insert  “,
including matters relating to Part 1 of the Digital Markets, Competition and
Consumers Act 2024 (digital markets)” .

###### Restriction on disclosure orders

116

116.1

This section applies for the purposes of—

116.1.a

digital markets proceedings, or

116.1.b

competition proceedings.

116.2

A court or the Tribunal must not make a disclosure order requiring the CMA to
disclose or produce information where the court or the Tribunal is satisfied
that another person would be reasonably able to provide the information.

116.3

A court or the Tribunal must not make a disclosure order requiring the
disclosure or production of digital markets investigation information before
the CMA gives notice of the closure or outcome of each investigation to which
the information relates.

116.4

In this section—

      “ competition proceedings ” has the meaning given by paragraph 2(4) of
Schedule 8A to the Competition Act 1998 (further provision about claims in
respect of loss or damage before a court or the Tribunal);           “ digital
markets investigation information ” means information—         prepared by a
person other than the CMA for the purpose of a digital markets investigation;
sent by the CMA in connection with such an investigation to a person that is
the subject of the investigation;                 “ digital markets
proceedings ” means proceedings under  section 101  (rights to enforce
requirements of  Part 1 ) or proceedings on appeal from such proceedings.

116.5

Paragraphs 7 and 27 of Schedule 8A to the Competition Act 1998 (other
definitions; disclosure orders) apply for the purposes of this section as they
apply for the purposes of Part 6 of that Schedule.

116.6

In Schedule 8A to the Competition Act 1998—

116.6.a

in paragraph 7 (other definitions), after sub-paragraph (2) insert—

116.6.a.2A

“ Digital markets proceedings ” means proceedings under  section 101  of the
Digital Markets, Competition and Consumer Act 2024 (rights to enforce
requirements of  Part 1 ).

;

116.6.b

in paragraph 28, after “competition proceedings” insert  “or digital markets
proceedings” ;

116.6.c

in paragraph 29, after “competition proceedings” insert  “or digital markets
proceedings” ;

116.6.d

in paragraph 30(1), after “competition proceedings” insert  “or digital
markets proceedings” .

##### Interpretation

###### Groups

117

117.1

This section  makes provision about groups for the purposes of  this Part .

117.2

An undertaking is part of a group if one or more bodies corporate which are
comprised in the undertaking are members of the same group as one or more
other bodies corporate.

117.3

For the purposes of  this Part , two bodies corporate are members of the same
group if—

117.3.a

one is the subsidiary of the other, or

117.3.b

both are subsidiaries of the same body corporate.

###### General interpretation

118

118.1

In  this Part —

      “ breach investigation ” means an investigation (including a conduct
investigation) into whether an undertaking is breaching or has breached a
requirement imposed on the undertaking under this Part by virtue of the
undertaking being, or having been, a designated undertaking;           “
conduct investigation ” has the meaning given by section  26 (1) ;           “
conduct investigation notice ” has the meaning given by section  26 (3) ;
“ conduct investigation period ” has the meaning given by  section 30 (2) ;
“ conduct requirements ” has the meaning given by  section 19 (3) ;
“ consumer ” has the meaning given by section 129(1) of EA 2002;           “
the court ”, except where otherwise stated, means—         in relation to
England and Wales or Northern Ireland, the High Court, and           in
relation to Scotland, the Court of Session;                 “ customer ”
includes a customer who is not a consumer;           “ designated undertaking
” means an undertaking which the CMA has designated as having SMS in respect
of a digital activity;           “ designation ” means the designation of an
undertaking as having SMS in respect of a relevant digital activity;
“ designation period ” has the meaning given by  section 15 (3) (e) ;
“ digital activity ” has the meaning given by  section 3 (1) ;           “
digital content ” has the meaning given by  section 330 ;           “ digital
markets functions ” means—         the functions that the CMA has under  this
Part , and           the CMA’s power to do anything that is calculated to
facilitate, or is conducive or incidental to, the performance of those
functions (see paragraph 20 of Schedule 4 to ERRA 2013 (additional powers));
“ digital markets investigation ” means—         an SMS investigation;
a breach investigation (including a conduct investigation);           a PCI
investigation;                 the “ digital markets investigation powers ”
are the powers that the CMA has under—         section 69  (power to require
information);           section 71  (power of access);           section 72
(power to interview);           section 74  (power to enter business premises
without a warrant);           section 75  (power to enter premises under a
warrant);           section 79  (reports by skilled persons);
“ enforcement order ” has the meaning given by  section 31 (1) ;           “
the FCA ” means the Financial Conduct Authority;           “ final offer
initiation notice ” has the meaning given by  section 40 (1) ;           “
final offer order ” has the meaning given by  section 41 (2) ;           “
final offer payment terms ” has the meaning given by  section 38 (1) ;
“ final offer period ” has the meaning given by  section 41 (3) ;           “
further SMS investigation ” has the meaning given by  section 10 (3) ;
“ grouped third parties ” has the meaning given by  section 39 (3) ;
“ grouped transactions ” has the meaning given by  section 39 (3) ;
“ information ” includes—         information in the form of a document,
whether in draft or final form;           information in any other form;
data, code, algorithms, estimates, forecasts, returns and explanations;
“ information notice ” has the meaning given by  section 69 (2) ;           “
initial SMS investigation ” has the meaning given by  section 9 (2) ;
“ interim enforcement order ” has the meaning given by  section 32 (1) ;
“ joined third parties ” has the meaning given by  section 39 (1) ;
“ OFCOM ” means the Office of Communications;           “ officer ”, in
relation to a body corporate, means a director, manager, secretary or other
similar officer of the body;           “ PCI ” stands for “pro-competition
intervention”;           “ PCI decision ” has the meaning given by  section 49
(1) ;           “ PCI investigation ” has the meaning given by  section 47 (1)
;           “ PCI investigation notice ” has the meaning given by  section 48
(1) ;           “ PCI investigation period ” has the meaning given by  section
50 (1) ;           “ person ”, in addition to the meaning given by the
Interpretation Act 1978, includes an undertaking;           “ the PRA ” means
the Prudential Regulation Authority;           “ pro-competition order ” has
the meaning given by  section 46 (3) (a) ;           “ product ” means—
goods;           services;           digital content;                 the “
regulatory digital markets functions ” are—         the power to open an SMS
investigation under  section 9 (1)  (initial SMS investigation) or  section 10
(1)  or  (2)  (further SMS investigation);           the power to designate an
undertaking as having SMS under  Chapter 2  (strategic market status);
the power to revoke a designation under  Chapter 2  (strategic market status);
the power to impose or revoke conduct requirements under  Chapter 3  (conduct
requirements);           the power to make, replace or revoke PCIs under
Chapter 4  (pro-competition interventions);                 “ relevant digital
activity ” in relation to a designated undertaking means a digital activity in
respect of which the undertaking has been designated as having SMS;
the “ relevant service or digital content ” in relation to a digital activity
means the service or digital content the provision of which constitutes
(together with any other activity carried out for the purposes of that
provision) the digital activity;           “ SMS ” stands for “strategic
market status”;           “ SMS conditions ” are the conditions set out in
section 2 (2) ;           “ SMS decision notice ” has the meaning given by
section 14 (2) ;           “ SMS investigation ” means an initial SMS
investigation and a further SMS investigation;           “ SMS investigation
notice ” has the meaning given by  section 11 (1) ;           “ SMS
investigation period ” has the meaning given by  section 14 (2) ;           “
submission date ” has the meaning given by  section 40 (2) (d) ;           “
subsidiary ” has the meaning given by section 1159 of the Companies Act 2006;
“ the Tribunal ” means the Competition Appeal Tribunal;           “ Tribunal
rules ” means rules under section 15 of EA 2002;           “ the turnover
condition ” has the meaning given by  section 7 ;           “ UK user ” and
“UK customer” mean any user or, as the case may be, customer who it is
reasonable to assume—         in the case of an individual, is normally in the
United Kingdom, and           in any other case, is established in the United
Kingdom;                 “ undertaking ” has the same meaning as it has for
the purposes of Part 1 of CA 1998 (competition: agreements, abuse of dominant
position etc);           “ user ” includes any person, legal or natural, and,
in relation to a digital activity, means any user of the relevant service or
digital content.

118.2

In  this Part —

118.2.a

references to “giving notice” or “giving a notice” are to giving notice or
giving a notice in writing;

118.2.b

references to “using” include, in relation to a service or digital content,
interacting, or carrying out activities that interact, in any way, directly or
indirectly, with the service or digital content;

118.2.c

references to the supply, provision, acquisition or use of goods or services
include the supply, provision, acquisition or use of digital content.

118.3

In this Part, a person is “connected to” an undertaking if that person—

118.3.a

is concerned in the management or control of the undertaking,

118.3.b

is employed by the undertaking, or

118.3.c

works for the undertaking in any other capacity.

Subject to section 3, agreements between undertakings, decisions by
associations of undertakings or concerted practices which have as their object
or effect the prevention, restriction or distortion of competition within the
United Kingdom and which—

119.2.1.a

in the case of agreements, decisions or practices implemented, or intended to
be implemented in the United Kingdom, may affect trade in the United Kingdom,
or

119.2.1.b

in any other case, are likely to have an immediate, substantial and
foreseeable effect on trade within the United Kingdom,

are prohibited unless they are exempt in accordance with the provisions of
this Part.

Subsection (2)  applies where a person knows or suspects that an investigation

###### Declaratory relief

###### Exemplary damages

126

126.1

In section 47C of CA 1998 (collective proceedings: damages and costs), before
subsection (2) insert—

126.1.1

The Tribunal may not award exemplary damages in collective proceedings.

126.2

In Schedule 8A of CA 1998 (further provision about claims in respect of loss
or damage before a court or the Tribunal)—

126.2.a

in Part 4 (cartels), in paragraph 15 (liability of immunity recipients)—

126.2.a.i

the existing text becomes sub-paragraph (1);

126.2.a.ii

loss and damage suffered by” substitute  “to” ;

126.2.a.iii

after that sub-paragraph insert—

126.2.a.iii.2

But an immunity recipient is not liable (either alone or jointly) by virtue of
sub-paragraph (1)(e) to pay exemplary damages.

;

126.2.b

omit Part 8 (exemplary damages);

126.2.c

in Part 10 (application), in paragraph 42, in sub-paragraph (1) omit “, 8”.

126.3

The amendments made by this section have effect in relation to competition
claims, competition proceedings, claims for contribution arising from
competition claims and proceedings relating to such claims to the extent that—

126.3.a

the claims and proceedings relate to an infringement of competition law that
takes place after the coming into force of this section, and

126.3.b

the loss or damage (if any) to which the claims or proceedings relate is
suffered after the coming into force of this section.

126.4

For the purposes of  subsection (3) , where an infringement of competition law
takes place over a period of two or more days it is to be taken to have taken
place on the first of those days.

126.5

Terms used in  subsection (3)  and in Schedule 8A to CA 1998 have the same
meaning in  subsection (3)  as they do in that Schedule (see Part 1 of that
Schedule).

##### Mergers involving newspaper enterprises and foreign powers

130

130.1

130.2

130.2.a

before the effective date;

130.2.b

apply in relation to arrangements in progress or in contemplation on or after
the effective date which, if carried into effect, would result in the creation
of a foreign state newspaper merger situation by virtue of enterprises ceasing
to be distinct on or after the effective date.

130.3

In  subsection (2) , “ the effective date ” means 13 March 2024.

in connection with provision made by  Schedule 9 .

provision for the CMA or Secretary of State to be able to modify, or request
that another person modifies, any agreement, arrangement, condition, licence,
statement (or anything of a similar nature) in connection with an
implementation trial measure (within the meaning of Part 4 of EA 2002, as
amended by  Schedule 9 ).

########### Duty of CMA to monitor effectiveness of undertakings and orders: Part 4

139.4.162A

139.4.162A.1

The CMA must keep under review the effectiveness of enforcement undertakings
accepted under this Part and enforcement orders made under this Part.

139.4.162A.2

The CMA must, whenever requested to do so by the Secretary of State and
otherwise from time to time, prepare a report of its findings under
subsection (1) .

139.4.162A.3

The CMA must—

139.4.162A.3.a

give a copy of any report prepared by it under  subsection (2)  to the
Secretary of State, and

139.4.162A.3.b

publish the report.

139.4.162A.4

Subsection (5)  applies, in relation to an adverse effect on competition
identified in a report mentioned in section 138(1), where—

139.4.162A.4.a

the report was published within the previous 10 years,

139.4.162A.4.b

the CMA last took action in accordance with section 138(2) or  subsection (5)
of this section no less than two years ago, and

139.4.162A.4.c

the CMA concludes, as a result of a review under  subsection (1) , that the
action mentioned in  paragraph (b)  has been ineffective for the purposes
mentioned in that section.

139.4.162A.5

The CMA must take such action as it considers appropriate for the purposes
mentioned in section 138(2) in relation to—

139.4.162A.5.a

any possible variation or release by the CMA of an enforcement undertaking
accepted by it;

139.4.162A.5.b

any possible new enforcement undertaking to be accepted by the CMA so as to
supersede another enforcement undertaking given to it;

139.4.162A.5.c

any possible variation or revocation by the CMA of an enforcement order made
by it;

139.4.162A.5.d

any possible enforcement undertaking to be accepted by the CMA instead of an
enforcement order made by it, or any possible enforcement order to be made by
the CMA instead of an enforcement undertaking accepted by it.

139.4.162A.6

the action within the period of six months beginning with the date on which
that decision is published under section 172(2) (h) .

139.4.162A.7

effect adverse to the public interest identified in a report mentioned in

172(10) within the previous 10 years,

139.4.162A.7.b

the Secretary of State last took action in accordance with section 142(2) or
147A(2) (as the case may be) no less than two years ago, and

139.4.162A.7.c

the CMA concludes, as a result of a review under  subsection (1) , that action
taken in accordance with that section has been ineffective for the purposes
mentioned in that section.

139.4.162A.8

appropriate for the purposes mentioned in section 147(2) or 147A(2) (as the
case may be) in relation to—

139.4.162A.8.a

any possible variation or release by the Secretary of State of an enforcement
undertaking accepted by the Secretary of State;

139.4.162A.8.b

any possible new enforcement undertaking to be accepted by the Secretary of
State under that section so as to supersede another enforcement undertaking
given to the Secretary of State;

139.4.162A.8.c

any possible variation or revocation by the Secretary of State of an
enforcement order made by the Secretary of State;

139.4.162A.8.d

in section 54 (decision of Secretary of State in public interest cases)—

146.3.a.i

in subsection (5), after “30” insert  “working” ;

146.3.a.ii

omit subsection (8);

146.3.b

in section 56 (competition cases where intervention on public interest grounds
ceases)—

146.3.b.i

in subsection (4), in paragraph (b), after “20” insert  “working” ;

146.3.b.ii

omit subsection (5).

146.4

In Chapter 4 (enforcement), in section 73A (time limits for consideration of
undertakings) omit subsection (12).

146.5

In Chapter 5 (supplementary)—

146.5.a

in section 129(1) (other interpretative provisions), at the appropriate place
insert—

      “ working day ” means any day other than—         a Saturday or Sunday,
or           a day that is a bank holiday in any part of the United Kingdom
under the Banking and Financial Dealings Act 1971.

;

146.5.b

in section 130 (index of defined expressions), at the appropriate place
insert—

    Working day Section 129(1)

.

146.6

In Part 4 of EA 2002 (market studies and market investigations), in section
151 (public interest intervention cases: interaction with general procedure)—

146.6.a

in subsection (3), after “20” insert  “working” ;

146.6.b

in subsection (5), after “20” insert  “working” ;

146.6.c

omit subsection (6);

146.6.d

at the end insert—

146.6.d.7

In this section, “ working day ” means any day other than—

146.6.d.7.a

a Saturday or Sunday, or

146.6.d.7.b

a day that is a bank holiday in any part of the United Kingdom under the
Banking and Financial Dealings Act 1971.

146.7

In regulation 2(1) of the Enterprise Act 2002 (Merger Prenotification)
Regulations 2003 ( S.I. 2003/1369 ), for the definition of “working day”
substitute—

      “ working day ” means any day other than—         a Saturday or Sunday,
or           a day that is a bank holiday in any part of the United Kingdom
under the Banking and Financial Dealings Act 1971.

### Enforcement of consumer protection law

#### Overview

##### Overview

147

147.1

This Part  confers enforcement powers, and makes provision about other
remedies, in connection with infringements of consumer protection law.

147.2

Chapter 2  provides for the kinds of infringements in respect of which
enforcement powers conferred by  Chapter 3  or  4  are available.

147.3

Chapter 3 —

147.3.a

confers powers on courts to make consumer protection orders, and

147.3.b

provides for the acceptance of undertakings as an alternative to the making of
such orders.

147.4

Chapter 4  confers powers on the CMA in connection with certain kinds of
infringements, including powers of the CMA to impose monetary penalties.

147.5

Chapter 5  contains general provisions about monetary penalties imposed under
Chapter 3  or  4 .

147.6

Chapter 6  amends Schedule 5 to CRA 2015 in relation to the giving of
information notices.

147.7

Chapter 7  contains miscellaneous provisions and  Chapter 8  contains
interpretative provisions.

#### Relevant infringements

##### Relevant infringements

148

148.1

A commercial practice is a relevant infringement for the purposes of  Chapter
3  or  4  if it—

148.1.a

harms the collective interests of consumers,

148.1.b

meets the UK connection condition (see  section 149 ), and

148.1.c

meets the specified prohibition condition (see  section 150 ).

148.2

In this Part—

      “ commercial practice ” means an act or omission by a trader relating to
the promotion or supply of—         the trader’s goods, services or digital
content to a consumer,           another trader’s goods, services or digital
content to a consumer, or           a consumer’s goods, services or digital
content to the trader or another person;                 “ consumer ” means an
individual acting for purposes that are wholly or mainly outside the
individual’s business;           “ trader ” means—         a person (“ P ”)
acting for purposes relating to P’s business, or           a person acting in
the name of, or on behalf of, P for purposes relating to P’s business.

148.3

It is immaterial for the purposes of the definition of “commercial practice”
in subsection  (2)  whether the act or omission takes place—

148.3.a

at the time of the promotion or supply in question, or

148.3.b

before or after that time.

148.4

It is immaterial for the purposes of the definition of “trader” in subsection
(2) —

148.4.a

in relation to paragraph (a) of that definition, whether P is acting
personally or through another person acting in P’s name or on P’s behalf;

148.4.b

in relation to paragraph (b) of that definition, whether or not the purposes
relating to P’s business are the only or main purposes for which the person is
acting.

148.5

For the purposes of  this Part —

148.5.a

references to consumers include persons who may become consumers in the
future;

148.5.b

the collective interests of consumers are capable of being harmed by a single
act or omission (as well as by repeated acts or omissions).

##### The UK connection condition

149

149.1

A commercial practice meets the UK connection condition for the purposes of
section 148  if at least one of the following conditions is met—

149.1.a

the trader has a place of business in the United Kingdom;

149.1.b

the trader carries on business in the United Kingdom;

149.1.c

the commercial practice occurs in the carrying on of activities by the trader
that are, by any means, directed to consumers in the United Kingdom.

149.2

It is immaterial for the purposes of subsection  (1) (c)  whether the
activities are carried on in the United Kingdom or elsewhere.

##### The specified prohibition condition

150

150.1

A commercial practice meets the specified prohibition condition for the
purposes of  section 148  as it applies for the purposes of  Chapter 3  if the
commercial practice is—

150.1.a

in breach of an enactment listed in Part 1 of  Schedule 15  (to the extent
specified), or

150.1.b

in breach of an obligation or rule of law listed in  Part 2  of that Schedule.

150.2

A commercial practice meets the specified prohibition condition for the
purposes of  section 148  as it applies for the purposes of Chapter 4 if it is
in breach of an enactment listed in  Schedule 16  (to the extent specified).

150.3

In the Table listing enactments in Part 1 of  Schedule 15 —

150.3.a

the first column lists the enactments;

150.3.b

the corresponding entry in the second column specifies the authorised
enforcers in relation to the enactment for the purposes of  section 153 ;

150.3.c

the third column provides information about transitional provision etc in
relation to certain enactments.

150.4

In the Table listing obligations and rules of law in  Part 2  of  Schedule 15
—

150.4.a

the first column describes the obligations or rules of law;

150.4.b

the corresponding entry in the second column specifies the authorised
enforcers in relation to the obligation or rule of law for the purposes of
section 153 .

#### Consumer protection orders and undertakings

##### Enforcers for purposes of Chapter

###### Enforcers

151

151.1

Each of the following is a public designated enforcer for the purposes of
this Chapter —

151.1.a

the CMA;

151.1.b

every local weights and measures authority in Great Britain;

151.1.c

the Department for the Economy in Northern Ireland;

151.1.d

the Civil Aviation Authority;

151.1.e

the Financial Conduct Authority;

151.1.f

the Gas and Electricity Markets Authority;

151.1.g

the Department of Health in Northern Ireland;

151.1.h

the Department for Infrastructure in Northern Ireland;

151.1.i

the Northern Ireland Authority for Utility Regulation;

151.1.j

an enforcement authority within the meaning of section 120(15) of the
Communications Act 2003 (regulation of premium rate services);

151.1.k

the Information Commissioner;

151.1.l

the Maritime and Coastguard Agency;

151.1.m

the Office of Communications;

151.1.n

the Office of Rail and Road;

151.1.o

the Office for the Traffic Commissioner;

151.1.p

the Secretary of State;

151.1.q

the Water Services Regulation Authority.

151.2

The Consumers’ Association is a private designated enforcer for the purposes
of  this Chapter .

151.3

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend  subsection (1)  or  (2)  so
as to—

151.3.a

add or remove a person as a public designated enforcer;

151.3.b

add or remove a person as a private designated enforcer;

151.3.c

vary the entry of a person as a public or private designated enforcer.

151.4

The power under  subsection (3) (a)  to add a person as a public designated
enforcer is exercisable only if the Secretary of State considers that the
person is a public body that has, as one of their purposes, the protection of
the collective interests of consumers.

151.5

The power under  subsection (3) (b)  to add a person as a private designated
enforcer is exercisable only if the Secretary of State considers that the
person—

151.5.a

is not a public body,

151.5.b

satisfies the designation criteria in  section 152 , and

151.5.c

has, as one of their purposes, the protection of the collective interests of
consumers.

151.6

The power under subsection  (3) (a)  and  (c)  to remove a person as a public
designated enforcer, or to vary the entry of such a person, does not apply so
far as relating to the persons listed in paragraphs  (a)  to  (c)  of
subsection  (1) .

151.7

Regulations under this section are subject to the affirmative procedure.

###### Designation criteria

152

152.1

These are the designation criteria in respect of a person (“ P ”) for the
purposes of  section 151 (5) (b) —

152.1.a

P is constituted, managed and controlled in such a way as to be expected to
act independently, impartially and with integrity;

152.1.b

P has established procedures to ensure that any potential conflicts of
interest are properly dealt with;

152.1.c

P has demonstrated experience, competence and expertise in promoting or
protecting the collective interests of consumers;

152.1.d

P has demonstrated the ability to protect the interests of consumers by
promoting high standards of integrity and fair dealing in the conduct of
business in relation to consumers;

152.1.e

P has the capability to investigate infringements and carry out enforcement
procedures under  this Chapter ;

152.1.f

P is ready and willing to follow best practice in enforcement;

152.1.g

P is ready and willing to co-operate with other enforcers and relevant
persons.

152.2

P does not fail to meet the criteria in  subsection (1) (a)  by reason only of
a connection with another person carrying on a business of a kind that could
be affected (directly or indirectly) by action taken under  this Chapter  if—

152.2.a

the other person does not control P, and

152.2.b

the profits of the other person’s business are used for the purposes of
furthering the objectives of P.

152.3

For the purposes of  subsection (1) (g) —

152.3.a

“relevant persons” are any persons responsible for the regulation of matters
in respect of which acts or omissions may constitute a relevant infringement;

152.3.b

co-operation includes, in particular—

152.3.b.i

sharing of information (so far as legally permitted), and

152.3.b.ii

participating in arrangements to co-ordinate action under  this Part .

##### Applications for enforcement orders and interim enforcement orders

###### Applications

153

153.1

An enforcer may (subject to  subsection (2) ) apply to the appropriate court
for an enforcement order or an interim enforcement order if the enforcer
considers that—

153.1.a

a person has engaged in, is engaging in or is likely to engage in a commercial
practice which constitutes a relevant infringement, or

153.1.b

a person is an accessory to such a practice.

153.2

An enforcer may make an application in respect of a relevant infringement only
if—

153.2.a

in the case of a commercial practice in breach of an enactment listed in the
first column of the Table in  Part 1  of  Schedule 15 , the enforcer is an
authorised enforcer in respect of that enactment in accordance with the second
column of that Table;

153.2.b

in the case of a commercial practice in breach of an obligation or rule of law
listed in the first column of the Table in  Part 2  of  Schedule 15 , the
enforcer is an authorised enforcer in respect of that obligation or rule of
law in accordance with the second column of that Table.

153.3

An application for an enforcement order or an interim enforcement order—

153.3.a

must be made in respect of the person the enforcer considers falls within
subsection (1) (a)  or  (b)  (“ the respondent ”), and

153.3.b

must (where known) name the respondent.

153.4

An application by a public designated enforcer for an enforcement order may,
subject to subsection (5), include an application for the respondent to pay a
monetary penalty.

153.5

In the case of a respondent within subsection (1)(a), an application under
subsection (4) may be made only in respect of a commercial practice that the
enforcer considers a person has engaged, or is engaging, in (but not in
respect of a practice that the enforcer considers a person is likely to engage
in).

###### CMA directions to other enforcers

154

154.1

This section  applies where it appears to the CMA that another enforcer
intends to make an application for an enforcement order or an interim
enforcement order.

154.2

The CMA may direct that an application for such an order in respect of a
particular relevant infringement—

154.2.a

may be made only by the CMA,

154.2.b

may be made only by such other enforcer as may be specified in the direction,
or

154.2.c

is not to be made by any enforcer.

154.3

A direction under  subsection (2) —

154.3.a

does not prevent the acceptance of an undertaking under  section 163  by the
CMA or another enforcer;

154.3.b

does not prevent the CMA from taking such other steps as it considers
appropriate for the purpose of securing that the infringement is not
committed, continued or repeated.

154.4

A direction under  subsection (2) (c)  may be made—

154.4.a

only in respect of an infringement that is a relevant infringement for the
purposes of  Chapter 4  (in addition to being a relevant infringement for the
purposes of this Chapter), and

154.4.b

only if the CMA is conducting, or proposes to conduct, an investigation under
section 180  in relation to that infringement.

154.5

A direction under  this section  may be varied or withdrawn.

154.6

The CMA must take such steps as it considers appropriate to bring a direction
(or its variation or withdrawal) to the attention of enforcers likely to be
affected by it.

###### Consultation

155

155.1

Before making an application for an enforcement order or an interim
enforcement order, an enforcer must (subject to subsection (5)) engage in
appropriate consultation with the person in respect of whom the order would be
made (“ the respondent ”).

155.2

Consultation is “ appropriate consultation ” for the purposes of  subsection
(1)  if it is carried out for the purposes of—

155.2.a

achieving the cessation of a relevant infringement (in a case where the
infringement is occurring) and ensuring it does not recur;

155.2.b

ensuring there is no repetition of a relevant infringement in a case where the
infringement has occurred;

155.2.c

ensuring that a relevant infringement does not take place in a case where the
infringement has yet to occur;

155.2.d

ensuring, in the case of consultation carried out by a public designated
enforcer, that the respondent is aware that an application for an enforcement
order may include an application for the respondent to pay a monetary penalty.

155.3

Engagement under  subsection (1)  must be initiated by the giving of a
consultation request to the respondent.

155.4

A consultation request must be given by notice in writing.

155.5

The requirement to consult under  this section  does not apply if—

155.5.a

the CMA considers that an application for the order in question should be made
without delay, or

155.5.b

it is not reasonably practicable for the enforcer to ascertain the identity
and whereabouts of the respondent.

155.6

The requirement to consult under  this section  ceases to apply—

155.6.a

in the case of an application for an enforcement order, at the end of the
applicable period;

155.6.b

in the case of an application for an interim enforcement order, at the end of
the period of 7 days beginning with the day after the respondent receives a
consultation request.

155.7

In  subsection (6) (a)  the “ applicable period ” means—

155.7.a

in a case where the respondent is a member of, or is represented by, an
approved representative body, the period of 28 days beginning with the day
after the respondent receives a consultation request;

155.7.b

in any other case, the period of 14 days beginning with the day after the
respondent receives a consultation request.

155.8

In  subsection (7) (a)  “ approved representative body ” means a
representative body that operates a consumer code which has been approved by—

155.8.a

a public designated enforcer,

155.8.b

a body which represents a public designated enforcer,

155.8.c

a group of public designated enforcers, or

155.8.d

a community interest company whose objects include the approval of consumer
codes.

155.9

In  subsection (8) —

      “ consumer code ” means an agreement or set of rules regulating, with a
view to safeguarding or promoting the interests of consumers, the behaviour of
traders who—         are engaged in commercial practices, and           choose
to be bound by the agreement or set of rules;                 “ representative
body ” means an organisation established to represent the interests of two or
more businesses in a particular sector or area.

##### Powers of court on application under 

###### Enforcement orders and undertakings

156

156.1

This section  applies if, on an application under  section 153  for an
enforcement order, the court finds that the person in respect of whom the
application is made (“ the respondent ”)—

156.1.a

has engaged, is engaging or is likely to engage in a commercial practice which
constitutes a relevant infringement (“the infringing practice”), or

156.1.b

is an accessory to the infringing practice.

156.2

The court may—

156.2.a

make an enforcement order against the respondent, or

156.2.b

accept an undertaking from the respondent given under  subsection (5) .

156.3

In considering whether to make an enforcement order the court must have regard
to whether the respondent—

156.3.a

has given an undertaking under  section 163  or  185  in respect of the
infringing practice, and

156.3.b

if so, whether the respondent has failed to comply with the undertaking.

156.4

An enforcement order is an order that—

156.4.a

indicates the nature of the infringing practice, and

156.4.b

directs the respondent to comply with  subsection (6) .

156.5

The respondent gives an undertaking under  this subsection  by undertaking—

156.5.a

to comply with  subsection (6) , or

156.5.b

to take steps which the court believes will secure that the respondent
complies with  subsection (6) .

156.6

The respondent complies with  this subsection  by—

156.6.a

in the case of a respondent within  subsection (1) (a) , not continuing or
repeating the infringing practice (where it is alleged that the person has
engaged or is engaging in that practice);

156.6.b

in the case of a respondent within  subsection (1) (b) , not consenting to or
conniving in the infringing practice;

156.6.c

in either case, not engaging in the infringing practice in the course of the
respondent’s business or another business;

156.6.d

in either case, not consenting to or conniving in the carrying out of the
infringing practice by a body corporate with which the respondent has a
special relationship (see section  220 ).

156.7

See also—

156.7.a

section 157  about the inclusion of enhanced consumer measures in an
enforcement order or undertaking;

156.7.b

section 158  about the inclusion of a requirement to pay a monetary penalty in
an enforcement order.

156.8

An enforcement order may require the respondent to publish—

156.8.a

the order;

156.8.b

a corrective statement.

156.9

An undertaking under  subsection (5)  may include a further undertaking by the
respondent to publish—

156.9.a

the terms of the undertaking;

156.9.b

a corrective statement.

156.10

Publication under  subsection (8)  or  (9) —

156.10.a

must be made in such form and manner, and to such extent, as the court
considers appropriate for the purpose of eliminating any continuing effects of
the conduct in respect of which the order was made or undertaking given;

156.10.b

is not an enhanced consumer measure for the purposes of  this Chapter .

156.11

Where the court has accepted from the respondent an undertaking under
subsection  (5) —

156.11.a

the court may accept from the respondent any variation of the undertaking that
the court considers appropriate for meeting the purposes for which the
undertaking was given;

156.11.b

the court may release the respondent from the undertaking (whether on its own
initiative or at the respondent’s request) if the court considers that the
undertaking is no longer necessary to further those purposes.

###### Enforcement orders and undertakings: enhanced consumer measures

157

157.1

An enforcement order or undertaking may include a requirement to take such
enhanced consumer measures as the court considers just and reasonable.

157.2

For this purpose, the court must in particular consider whether any proposed
enhanced consumer measures are proportionate having regard to—

157.2.a

the likely benefit of the measures to consumers,

157.2.b

the costs likely to be incurred by the respondent, and

157.2.c

the likely cost to consumers of obtaining the benefit of the measures.

157.3

The costs referred to in  subsection (2) (b)  are—

157.3.a

the cost of the measures, and

157.3.b

the reasonable administrative costs associated with taking the measures.

157.4

Where the respondent is required under an enforcement order or an undertaking
to take enhanced consumer measures, the order or undertaking may include
requirements for the respondent to provide information or documents to the
court in order that the court may determine whether the respondent is taking
those measures.

157.5

Subsection (6)  applies if—

157.5.a

an enforcement order or undertaking includes enhanced consumer measures
offering compensation, and

157.5.b

a settlement agreement is entered into in connection with the payment of
compensation.

157.6

A waiver of a person’s rights in the settlement agreement is not valid if it
is a waiver of the right to bring civil proceedings in respect of conduct
other than conduct which has given rise to the enforcement order or
undertaking.

157.7

This section  is subject to  section 177  (private designated enforcers).

157.8

In  this section  “ undertaking ” means an undertaking given under section
156 (5) .

157.9

References in  this Part  to “enhanced consumer measures” are to be read in
accordance with  section 221 .

###### Enforcement orders: requirement to pay monetary penalty

158

158.1

This section  applies where the court makes an enforcement order against the
respondent on an application made by a public designated enforcer.

158.2

The order may, subject to  subsection (3) , include a requirement for the
respondent to pay a monetary penalty.

158.3

In the case of a respondent within  section 156 (1) (a) , a requirement to pay
a monetary penalty may be imposed only if the court finds that the respondent
has engaged, or is engaging, in a commercial practice constituting a relevant
infringement (and not in respect of a practice that the court finds that the
person is likely to engage in).

158.4

Where the order includes a requirement under  subsection (2) , the order, or a
notice accompanying service of the order, must set out the monetary penalty
information (see  section 203 ).

158.5

The amount of a monetary penalty must be a fixed amount not exceeding £300,000
or, if higher, 10% of the total value of the turnover (if any) of the
respondent.

158.6

A monetary penalty may not be imposed on the respondent by virtue of  this
section  in respect of any conduct that constitutes an offence if the
respondent has been found guilty of that offence.

158.7

The respondent does not commit an offence in relation to any conduct in
respect of which a monetary penalty is imposed on the respondent by virtue of
this section.

158.8

In addition to any right of appeal on a point of law, a person liable to pay a
monetary penalty by virtue of  this section  may appeal in respect of—

158.8.a

the decision to impose the penalty, or

158.8.b

the nature or amount of the penalty.

158.9

In the application of  subsection (4)  to Scotland, “ service of the order ”
includes service of an extract order in execution of or diligence on the
order.

###### Interim enforcement orders and undertakings

159

159.1

This section  applies if—

159.1.a

it is alleged in an application under  section 153  for an interim enforcement
order that a person (“ the respondent ”)—

159.1.a.i

has engaged, is engaging or is likely to engage in a commercial practice which
constitutes a relevant infringement (“the infringing practice”), or

159.1.a.ii

is an accessory to the infringing practice,

159.1.b

it appears to the court that if the application had been an application for an
enforcement order it would be likely to be granted, and

159.1.c

the court considers it is expedient that the infringing practice is prohibited
or prevented immediately.

159.2

The court may—

159.2.a

make an interim enforcement order against the respondent, or

159.2.b

accept an undertaking from the respondent to comply with  subsection (5)  or
to take steps which the court believes will secure such compliance.

159.3

If no notice of the application has been given to the respondent, the court
may proceed under  subsection (2) (a)  only if it considers it appropriate to
make an interim enforcement order without notice.

159.4

An interim enforcement order is an order that—

159.4.a

indicates the nature of the infringing practice, and

159.4.b

directs the respondent to comply with  subsection (5) .

159.5

The respondent complies with  this subsection  by—

159.5.a

in the case of a respondent within  subsection (1) (a) (i) , not continuing or
repeating the infringing practice (where it is alleged that the person has
engaged or is engaging in that practice);

159.5.b

in the case of a respondent within  subsection (1) (a) (ii) , not consenting
to or conniving in the infringing practice;

159.5.c

in either case, not engaging in the infringing practice in the course of the
respondent’s business or another business;

159.5.d

in either case, not consenting to or conniving in the carrying out of the
infringing practice by a body corporate with which the respondent has a
special relationship (see section  220 ).

159.6

An application for an interim enforcement order in respect of alleged conduct
of the respondent may not be made at any time after—

159.6.a

an application for an enforcement order against the respondent in respect of
that conduct is determined, or

159.6.b

a final infringement notice in respect of that conduct has been given to the
respondent (see  section 182 ).

159.7

An application for an interim enforcement order must—

159.7.a

include all information known to the applicant that is material to the
question of whether or not the application is granted;

159.7.b

if made without notice, state why no notice has been given.

159.8

The court may vary or discharge an interim enforcement order on the
application of the applicant or the respondent.

159.9

An interim enforcement order made in respect of conduct of the respondent is
discharged—

159.9.a

on the determination of an application for an enforcement order made against
the respondent in respect of that conduct, or

159.9.b

on the giving of a final infringement notice to the respondent in respect of
that conduct.

##### Online interface orders and interim online interface orders

###### Applications

160

160.1

A public designated enforcer may apply to the appropriate court for an online
interface order, or an interim online interface order, if the enforcer
considers that a person has engaged, is engaging or is likely to engage in a
commercial practice that constitutes a relevant infringement.

160.2

An application for an online interface order, or an interim online interface
order, may be made in respect of—

160.2.a

the person that the enforcer considers has engaged, is engaging or is likely
to engage in a commercial practice that constitutes a relevant infringement,
or

160.2.b

any other person (subject to  subsection (3) ).

160.3

An application under  subsection (2) (b)  in respect of a person who is
outside the United Kingdom may be made only if the person—

160.3.a

is a United Kingdom national,

160.3.b

is an individual who is habitually resident in the United Kingdom,

160.3.c

is a firm established in the United Kingdom, or

160.3.d

carries on business in the United Kingdom or by any means directs activities
in the course of carrying on a business to consumers in the United Kingdom.

160.4

For the purposes of  subsection (3) (c) , a firm is “established in the United
Kingdom” if—

160.4.a

it is incorporated or formed under the law of a part of the United Kingdom, or

160.4.b

it is administered under arrangements governed by the law of a part of the
United Kingdom.

160.5

Section  154  (CMA directions to other enforcers) applies where it appears to
the CMA that another public designated enforcer intends to make an application
for an online interface order, or an interim online interface order, as it
applies in relation to intended applications for enforcement orders and
interim enforcement orders, but for this purpose the reference to such other
enforcer in subsection  (2) (b)  is to be taken as a reference only to such
other public designated enforcer.

160.6

Nothing in  this section  or in  section 161  or  162  limits other powers
under  this Chapter  to make enforcement orders or interim enforcement orders
or to accept undertakings.

###### Online interface orders

161

161.1

The court may make an online interface order on an application under  section
160  if the court finds that—

161.1.a

a person has engaged, is engaging or is likely to engage in a commercial
practice that constitutes a relevant infringement,

161.1.b

there are no other available means under this Chapter of bringing about the
cessation or prohibition of the infringement which, by themselves, would be
wholly effective, and

161.1.c

it is necessary to make the order to avoid the risk of serious harm to the
collective interests of consumers.

161.2

An online interface order is an order that directs the person against whom it
is made to do, or to co-operate with another person so that person can do, one
or more of the following—

161.2.a

remove content from, or modify content on, an online interface;

161.2.b

disable or restrict access to an online interface;

161.2.c

display a warning to consumers accessing an online interface;

161.2.d

delete a fully qualified domain name and take any steps necessary to
facilitate the registration of that domain name by the public designated
enforcer that applied for the order.

161.3

Where an online interface order is made, the public designated enforcer that
applied for the order may publish—

161.3.a

the order, and

161.3.b

where known, the identity of the person who has engaged, is engaging or is
likely to engage in a commercial practice which constitutes the relevant
infringement.

161.4

Publication under  subsection (3)  is to be made in such form and manner as
the enforcer considers appropriate for the purpose of eliminating any
continuing effects of the relevant infringement.

161.5

In  subsection (2)  “ online interface ” means any software, including a
website, part of a website, an application or other digital content which—

161.5.a

is operated by a person (“ P ”) acting for purposes relating to P’s business
or by a person acting in the name of, or on behalf of, P, and

161.5.b

is operated for or in connection with the purposes of giving access to, or
promoting, goods, services or digital content that P or another person
supplies.

###### Interim online interface orders

162

162.1

The court may make an interim online interface order against a person (“ the
respondent ”) on an application under  section 160  if—

162.1.a

it is alleged that there has been or is likely to be a relevant infringement,

162.1.b

it appears to the court that if the application had been an application for an
online interface order it would be likely to be granted, and

162.1.c

the court considers it expedient to bring about the cessation or prohibition
of the infringement immediately.

162.2

If no notice of the application has been given to the respondent—

162.2.a

the application must state why no notice has been given, and

162.2.b

the court may make the order only if it considers it appropriate for the order
to be made without notice.

162.3

An interim online interface order is an order that directs the respondent to
do, or to co-operate with another person so that person can do, one or more of
the following—

162.3.a

remove content from, or modify content on, an online interface;

162.3.b

disable or restrict access to an online interface;

162.3.c

display a warning to consumers accessing an online interface;

162.3.d

delete a fully qualified domain name and take any steps necessary to
facilitate the registration of that domain name by the public designated
enforcer that applied for the order.

In  this subsection  “ online interface ” has the meaning given by  section
161 (5) .

162.4

An application for an interim online interface order against the respondent
may not be made at any time after—

162.4.a

an application for an online interface order against the respondent in respect
of the same relevant infringement is determined, or

162.4.b

an online interface notice in respect of the same relevant infringement has
been given to the respondent (see  section 184 ).

162.5

An application for an interim online interface order must include all
information known to the public designated enforcer making the application
that is material to the question of whether or not the application is granted.

162.6

The court may vary or discharge an interim online interface order on the
application of the enforcer that applied for the order or the respondent.

162.7

An interim online interface order against the respondent is discharged on the
determination of—

162.7.a

an application for an online interface order made against the respondent in
respect of the same relevant infringement, or

162.7.b

an online interface notice in respect of the same relevant infringement has
been given to the respondent.

##### Undertakings and further proceedings

###### Acceptance of undertakings by enforcers

163

163.1

This section  applies where an enforcer could make an application under
section 153  for an enforcement order, or an interim enforcement order,
against a person (“ the respondent ”) whom the enforcer believes—

163.1.a

has engaged, is engaging or is likely to engage in a commercial practice which
constitutes a relevant infringement (“the infringing practice”), or

163.1.b

is an accessory to the infringing practice.

163.2

The enforcer may accept an undertaking from the respondent to do one or more
of the following—

163.2.a

in the case of a respondent within  subsection (1) (a) , not to continue or
repeat the infringing practice (where it is alleged that the respondent has
engaged or is engaging in that practice);

163.2.b

in the case of a respondent within  subsection (1) (b) , not to consent to or
connive in the infringing practice;

163.2.c

in either case, not to engage in the infringing practice in the course of the
respondent’s business or another business;

163.2.d

in either case, not to consent to or connive in the carrying out of the
infringing practice by a body corporate with which the respondent has a
special relationship (see section  220 ).

163.3

See also  section 164  about the inclusion of enhanced consumer measures in an
undertaking under  this section .

163.4

Where the enforcer accepts an undertaking under  subsection (2)  the enforcer
may publish the undertaking or accept a further undertaking from the
respondent to do so.

163.5

Publication under  subsection (4) —

163.5.a

must be made in such form and manner, and to such an extent, as the enforcer
considers appropriate for the purpose of eliminating any continuing effects of
the infringing practice;

163.5.b

is not an enhanced consumer measure for the purposes of  this Chapter .

163.6

Where an enforcer has accepted from the respondent an undertaking under this
section—

163.6.a

the enforcer may accept from the respondent any such variation of the
undertaking that the enforcer considers appropriate for meeting the purposes
for which the undertaking was given;

163.6.b

the enforcer may release the respondent from the undertaking (whether on its
own initiative or at the respondent’s request) if the enforcer considers that
the undertaking is no longer necessary to meet those purposes.

163.7

Each enforcer must keep a record of—

163.7.a

undertakings it has accepted under this section, and

163.7.b

reviews it has carried out into the effectiveness of such undertakings.

163.8

In determining for the purposes of subsection  (1)  whether an enforcer could
make an application under  section 153 , section  169  is to be ignored.

###### Undertakings under 

164

164.1

An undertaking under  section 163 (2)  may include a requirement to take such
enhanced consumer measures as the enforcer accepting the undertaking considers
just and reasonable.

164.2

For this purpose, the enforcer must in particular consider whether any
proposed enhanced consumer measures are proportionate having regard to—

164.2.a

the likely benefit of the measures to consumers,

164.2.b

the costs likely to be incurred by the respondent, and

164.2.c

the likely cost to consumers of obtaining the benefit of the measures.

164.3

The costs referred to in  subsection (2) (b)  are—

164.3.a

the cost of the measures, and

164.3.b

the reasonable administrative costs associated with taking the measures.

164.4

Where the respondent is required by an undertaking to take enhanced consumer
measures, the undertaking may include requirements for the respondent to
provide information or documents to the enforcer accepting the undertaking in
order that the enforcer may determine if the respondent is taking those
measures.

164.5

Subsection (6)  applies if—

164.5.a

an undertaking under  section 163 (2)  includes enhanced consumer measures
offering compensation, and

164.5.b

a settlement agreement is entered into in connection with the payment of
compensation.

164.6

A waiver of a person’s rights in the settlement agreement is not valid if it
is a waiver of the right to bring civil proceedings in respect of conduct
other than conduct which has given rise to the undertaking.

164.7

This section  is subject to  section 177  (private designated enforcers).

###### Undertakings under section 

165

165.1

This section  applies where an enforcer proposes to—

165.1.a

accept a material variation of an undertaking under  section 163 , or

165.1.b

release the respondent from any such undertaking,

and the proposed variation or release has not been requested by the
respondent.

165.2

Before taking the proposed action mentioned in  subsection (1)  the enforcer
must—

165.2.a

give notice to the respondent under  subsection (3) , and

165.2.b

consider any representations made in accordance with the notice.

165.3

A notice under  this subsection  must state—

165.3.a

the fact that the enforcer is proposing to act as mentioned in  subsection (1)
,

165.3.b

the reasons for doing so, and

165.3.c

the means by which, and the time by which, representations may be made in
relation to the proposed action.

165.4

If after considering any representations made in accordance with a notice
under  subsection (3)  an enforcer decides to take an action mentioned in
subsection (1) , the enforcer must give notice to the respondent of that
decision.

165.5

The reference in  subsection (1) (a)  to a material variation is a reference
to any variation that the enforcer considers to be material in any respect.

###### Consumer protection orders or undertakings to court: further proceedings

166

166.1

This section  applies if the court—

166.1.a

makes a consumer protection order against a person (“ the respondent ”) on an
application made by an enforcer (“ the original application ”), or

166.1.b

accepts an undertaking from the respondent under  section 156  or  159  on the
making of the original application.

166.2

References in this Part to a “consumer protection order” are references to—

166.2.a

an enforcement order,

166.2.b

an interim enforcement order,

166.2.c

an online interface order, or

166.2.d

an interim online interface order.

166.3

An application may (subject to  subsection (7) ) be made to the same court to
which the original application was made in respect of a failure to comply with
the order or undertaking in question—

166.3.a

by the enforcer that made the original application, or

166.3.b

by any other enforcer other than a private designated enforcer.

166.4

An application to the court in respect of a failure to comply with an
undertaking may include an application for a consumer protection order of any
kind that the enforcer concerned is authorised under this Chapter to apply
for.

166.5

If on an application under  this section  the court finds that an undertaking
is not being complied with, the court may do either or both of the following—

166.5.a

make a consumer protection order (instead of making any other order it has
power to make);

166.5.b

make an order requiring the respondent to pay a monetary penalty.

166.6

Where an application is made under  subsection (4)  for a consumer protection
order—

166.6.a

sections  154  and  160 (5)  (directions by CMA) and section  155
(consultation) do not apply;

166.6.b

the application may be made only in respect of a commercial practice that the
enforcer considers a person has engaged or is engaging in (and not in respect
of a practice that a person is likely to engage in);

166.6.c

a power of the court to accept an undertaking instead of making a consumer
protection order does not apply,

and the preceding provisions of  this Chapter  apply subject to  this
subsection .

166.7

An application may not be made under  subsection (3)  in the case of a failure
to comply with an order or undertaking which consists only of a failure to
provide information or documents required by the order or undertaking under
section 157 (4) .

166.8

In addition to any right of appeal on a point of law, a person liable to pay a
penalty by virtue of an order under subsection  (5) (b)  may appeal in respect
of—

166.8.a

the decision to impose the penalty, or

166.8.b

the nature or amount of the penalty.

166.9

In connection with orders under  subsection (5) (b) , see further—

166.9.a

section 168 , which provides for the amount of penalties, and

166.9.b

section 203 , which provides for information to accompany such orders.

###### Undertakings to public designated enforcers: further proceedings

167

167.1

This section  applies where a public designated enforcer accepts an
undertaking from a person (“ the respondent ”) under  section 163 .

167.2

The enforcer may apply to the court in respect of a failure to comply with the
undertaking.

167.3

An application under  subsection (2)  may include an application for a
consumer protection order of any kind that the enforcer concerned is
authorised under this Chapter to apply for.

167.4

If the court finds that the undertaking is not being complied with, the court
may do either or both of the following—

167.4.a

make a consumer protection order (instead of making any other order it has
power to make);

167.4.b

make an order requiring the respondent to pay a monetary penalty.

167.5

A requirement under  subsection (4) (b)  to pay a monetary penalty may be
imposed only if the court is satisfied that the respondent’s failure in
question is without reasonable excuse.

167.6

Where an application is made under  subsection (2)  for a consumer protection
order—

167.6.a

sections  154  and  160 (5)  (directions by CMA) and section  155
(consultation) do not apply;

167.6.b

the application may be made only in respect of a commercial practice that the
enforcer considers a person has engaged or is engaging in (and not in respect
of a practice that a person is likely to engage in);

167.6.c

a power of the court to accept an undertaking instead of making a consumer
protection order does not apply,

and the preceding provisions of  this Chapter  apply subject to  this
subsection .

167.7

An application may not be made under  subsection (2)  in the case of a failure
to comply with an undertaking which consists only of a failure to provide
information or documents under  section 164 (4) .

167.8

In addition to any right of appeal on a point of law, a person liable to pay a
penalty by virtue of an order under subsection (4)(b) may appeal in respect
of—

167.8.a

the decision to impose the penalty, or

167.8.b

the nature or amount of the penalty.

167.9

In connection with orders under  subsection (4) (b) , see further—

167.9.a

section 168 , which provides for the amount of penalties, and

167.9.b

section 203 , which provides for information to accompany such orders.

###### Monetary penalties under 

168

168.1

This section  applies in relation to a monetary penalty imposed on a person (“
the respondent ”) by an order made under  section 166  or  167 .

168.2

The amount of the penalty must be—

168.2.a

a fixed amount,

168.2.b

an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, or

168.2.c

a combination of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a
daily rate.

168.3

The penalty must not exceed—

168.3.a

in the case of a fixed amount, £150,000 or, if higher, 5% of the total value
of the turnover (if any) of the respondent;

168.3.b

in the case of an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, for each day
£15,000 or, if higher, 5% of the total value of the daily turnover (if any) of
the respondent;

168.3.c

in the case of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a daily
rate, such fixed amount and such amount per day.

168.4

In imposing a penalty by reference to a daily rate—

168.4.a

no account is to be taken of any days before notice of the application under
section 166 (3)  or  167 (2)  was given to the respondent, and

168.4.b

unless the court determines an earlier date, the amount payable ceases to
accumulate on the day on which the requirements of the undertaking that the
respondent has failed to comply with are complied with.

##### Notification of CMA

###### Notification requirements: applications

169

169.1

This section  applies to an enforcer that is not the CMA.

169.2

Before making an application for a consumer protection order the enforcer—

169.2.a

must by notice inform the CMA of its intention to do so, and

169.2.b

may only proceed to make the application after expiry of the minimum period
or, if sooner, after the CMA has by notice informed the enforcer that it
consents to the making of the application.

169.3

The “minimum period” is—

169.3.a

in the case of an enforcement order or an online interface order, 14 days
beginning with the day on which the notice under  subsection (2) (a)  is
given;

169.3.b

in the case of an interim enforcement order or an interim online interface
order, 7 days beginning with the day on which the notice under  subsection (2)
(a)  is given.

169.4

Where an enforcer proceeds to make an application for a consumer protection
order, the enforcer must by notice inform the CMA of the result of the
application.

169.5

Subsection (6)  applies where the enforcer makes an application under  section
166  in respect of a failure to comply with—

169.5.a

a consumer protection order, or

169.5.b

an undertaking given under  section 156  or  159 .

169.6

The enforcer must by notice inform the CMA of the making of the application
and of any order made by the court on the application.

###### Notification requirements: undertakings

170

170.1

This section  applies to an enforcer that is not the CMA which accepts an
undertaking under  section 163 .

170.2

The enforcer must by notice inform the CMA of—

170.2.a

the terms of the undertaking, and

170.2.b

the identity of the person who gave it.

###### Notification requirements: proceedings

171

171.1

This section  applies where a local weights and measures authority in England
and Wales intends to start proceedings for an offence under an enactment
listed in Part 1 of  Schedule 15 .

171.2

Before starting the proceedings the authority—

171.2.a

must by notice inform the CMA of its intention to do so, and

171.2.b

may only start the proceedings on or after the relevant day.

171.3

The “relevant day” is—

171.3.a

the day on which the CMA notifies the authority that the CMA has received the
authority’s notice given under  subsection (2) (a) , or

171.3.b

if sooner, the day beginning 14 days after the day on which that notice was
given.

171.4

Where the authority starts the proceedings, the authority must by notice
inform the CMA of outcome of the proceedings.

171.5

A failure of an authority to comply with a requirement under this section does
not invalidate any proceedings started by the authority.

###### Notification requirements: convictions and judgments

172

172.1

This section  applies where—

172.1.a

a person is convicted of an offence by or before a court in the United
Kingdom, or

172.1.b

a judgment is given against a person by a court in civil proceedings in the
United Kingdom.

172.2

The court may make arrangements to bring the conviction or judgment to the
attention of the CMA if it appears to the court—

172.2.a

having regard to the functions of the CMA under this Chapter or Chapter 4,
that it is expedient for the conviction or judgment to be brought to the
attention of the CMA, and

172.2.b

without such arrangements the conviction or judgment may not be brought to the
attention of the CMA.

172.3

For the purposes of  subsection (2)  it is immaterial whether the proceedings
have been finally disposed of by the court.

172.4

Judgment includes an order or decree (and references to the giving of a
judgment are to be construed accordingly).

##### Jurisdiction etc

###### Appropriate court

173

173.1

This section applies for the purposes of determining the appropriate court in
relation to an application for, or the making of, a consumer protection order
against a person (“ the respondent ”) in connection with a relevant
infringement.

173.2

If the respondent has a place of business in, or carries on business in, a
part of the United Kingdom, the appropriate court is—

173.2.a

the High Court or the county court in England and Wales, if the respondent
carries on business in England and Wales or has a place of business in England
and Wales;

173.2.b

the High Court or a county court in Northern Ireland, if the respondent
carries on business in Northern Ireland or has a place of business in Northern
Ireland;

173.2.c

the Court of Session or the sheriff, if the respondent carries on business in
Scotland or has a place of business in Scotland.

173.3

If the respondent does not have a place of business in, and does not carry on
business in, any part of the United Kingdom, the appropriate court is—

173.3.a

the High Court or the county court in England and Wales, if a relevant
consumer is domiciled in England or Wales;

173.3.b

the High Court or a county court in Northern Ireland, if a relevant consumer
is domiciled in Northern Ireland;

173.3.c

the Court of Session or the sheriff, if a relevant consumer is domiciled in
Scotland.

173.4

References in subsection (3) to a “relevant consumer” are to any consumer—

173.4.a

to or for whom goods, services or digital content are supplied in connection
with which the relevant infringement has, or is alleged to have, taken place,

173.4.b

to whom activities are directed the carrying out of which constitutes, or is
alleged to constitute, the relevant infringement, or

173.4.c

from whom goods are received in connection with which the relevant
infringement has, or is alleged to have, taken place.

173.5

Section 41 of the Civil Jurisdiction and Judgments Act 1982 applies for the
purposes of determining the part of the United Kingdom in which a relevant
consumer is domiciled.

###### Effect of orders in other parts of the United Kingdom

174

A consumer protection order made in a part of the United Kingdom by a court
specified in relation to that part in the second or third column of the Table
has effect in another part of the United Kingdom as if made by a court
specified in relation to that other part in the same column of the Table—

    England and Wales The High Court The county court Scotland The Court of
Session The sheriff Northern Ireland The High Court A county court.

###### Evidence

175

175.1

Proceedings under  this Chapter  are civil proceedings for the purposes of—

175.1.a

section 11 of the Civil Evidence Act 1968 (convictions admissible as evidence
in civil proceedings);

175.1.b

section 10 of the Law Reform (Miscellaneous Provisions) (Scotland) Act 1968
(corresponding provision in Scotland);

175.1.c

section 7 of the Civil Evidence Act (Northern Ireland)  1971 (c.36 (N.I.))
(corresponding provision in Northern Ireland).

175.2

In proceedings under  this Chapter  any finding by a court in civil
proceedings that a person has engaged in infringing conduct—

175.2.a

is admissible as evidence that the conduct has occurred;

175.2.b

unless the contrary is proved, is sufficient evidence that the conduct has
occurred.

175.3

But  subsection (2)  does not apply to any finding—

175.3.a

which has been reversed on appeal;

175.3.b

which has been varied on appeal so as to negate it.

175.4

For the purposes of subsection (2), a person engages in “infringing conduct”
if—

175.4.a

the person has engaged in a commercial practice that constitutes a relevant
infringement, or

175.4.b

the person is an accessory to such a practice.

##### Miscellaneous

###### Interconnected bodies corporate

176

176.1

This section  applies if—

176.1.a

a court makes a consumer protection order against a body corporate (“ the
respondent ”), and

176.1.b

the interconnection condition applies in relation to the respondent.

176.2

The interconnection condition applies in relation to the respondent if—

176.2.a

at the time the order is made the respondent is a member of a group of
interconnected bodies corporate,

176.2.b

at any time when the order is in force the respondent becomes a member of a
group of interconnected bodies corporate, or

176.2.c

at any time when the order is in force a group of interconnected bodies
corporate of which the respondent is a member is increased by the addition of
one or more further members.

176.3

The order may include provision for the requirements (or any particular
requirements) imposed by the order to be binding upon all other members of the
group (in addition to the respondent) as if each of them were the respondent.

176.4

Provision may be included in an order under  subsection (3)  only if the court
considers it just, reasonable and proportionate to include that provision.

176.5

A group of interconnected bodies corporate is a group consisting of two or
more bodies corporate all of whom are interconnected with each other.

176.6

Any two bodies corporate are interconnected—

176.6.a

if one of them is a subsidiary of the other, or

176.6.b

if both of them are subsidiaries of the same body corporate.

176.7

Where an order includes provision under  subsection (3) , a copy of the order
must be given to any other member of the respondent’s group in relation to
which the requirements imposed by the order are to be binding.

###### Enhanced consumer measures: private designated enforcers

177

177.1

This section  applies where—

177.1.a

an enforcement order is made on the application of a private designated
enforcer,

177.1.b

an undertaking is given under  section 156  on an application for an
enforcement order made by a private designated enforcer, or

177.1.c

an undertaking is given under  section 163  to a private designated enforcer.

177.2

The enforcement order or undertaking may include a requirement for the taking
of any enhanced consumer measures only if both of the following conditions are
met.

177.3

The first condition is that the private designated enforcer is specified for
the purposes of  this section  in regulations made by the Secretary of State.

177.4

The second condition is that the enhanced consumer measures do not directly
benefit the private designated enforcer or an associated undertaking.

177.5

Enhanced consumer measures directly benefiting an enforcer or an associated
undertaking include (for example) measures which—

177.5.a

require a person to pay money to the enforcer or an associated undertaking;

177.5.b

require a person to participate in a scheme, administered by the enforcer or
associated undertaking, that is designed to recommend persons supplying goods,
services or digital content to consumers;

177.5.c

would give the enforcer or associated undertaking a commercial advantage over
any of its competitors.

177.6

An enforcer may be specified in regulations under  subsection (3)  only if—

177.6.a

the functions of the enforcer under  this Chapter  have been specified under
section 24 of the Legislative and Regulatory Reform Act 2006 (functions to
which principles under section 21 and code of practice under section 22
apply), so far as capable of being so specified, and

177.6.b

the Secretary of State is satisfied that to do so is likely to—

177.6.b.i

improve the availability to consumers of redress for relevant infringements,

177.6.b.ii

improve the availability to consumers of information which enables them to
choose more effectively between persons supplying goods, services or digital
content, or

177.6.b.iii

improve compliance with consumer law.

177.7

Subsection (8)  applies if—

177.7.a

an enforcer exercises a function in relation to a person by virtue of  this
section ,

177.7.b

the function is a relevant function for the purposes of Part 2 of the
Regulatory Enforcement and Sanctions Act 2008 (co-ordination of regulatory
enforcement), and

177.7.c

a primary authority (within the meaning of that Part) has given advice or
guidance under section 24A(1) or (2) of that Act—

177.7.c.i

to that person in relation to the function, or

177.7.c.ii

to other local authorities (within the meaning of that Part) with that
function as to how they should exercise it in relation to that person.

177.8

The enforcer must have regard to the advice or guidance in exercising the
function in relation to that person.

177.9

Regulations under this section are subject to the negative procedure.

177.10

In  this section  “ associated undertaking ”, in relation to a private
designated enforcer, means—

177.10.a

a parent undertaking or subsidiary undertaking of the enforcer, or

177.10.b

a subsidiary undertaking of a parent undertaking of the enforcer,

and for this purpose “parent undertaking” and “subsidiary undertaking” have
the meanings given by section 1162 of the Companies Act 2006.

###### Substantiation of claims

178

178.1

This section  applies where an application for a consumer protection order is
made to a court in respect of a relevant infringement involving a
contravention of  Chapter 1  of  Part 4  (protection from unfair trading).

178.2

The court may, for the purpose of considering the application, require a
respondent to provide evidence as to the accuracy of any factual claim made as
part of a commercial practice of the respondent.

178.3

The court may find that a factual claim of a respondent is inaccurate if—

178.3.a

the respondent fails to provide evidence of the accuracy of the claim in
response to a requirement imposed under  subsection (2) , or

178.3.b

the court considers that any such evidence that is provided is inadequate.

178.4

In  this section  “ respondent ”, in relation to an application for a consumer
protection order, means—

178.4.a

where the application is for an enforcement order or an interim enforcement
order, the person against whom the order is sought;

178.4.b

where the application is for an online interface order or an interim online
interface order, the person against whom the order is sought or another person
who is a party to the proceedings.

###### Crown application

179

179.1

Subject to  subsection (2) , this Chapter binds the Crown.

179.2

The Crown is not liable for any monetary penalty imposed by virtue of this
Chapter.

#### Direct enforcement powers of CMA

##### Investigations

###### Power of CMA to investigate suspected infringements

180

180.1

This section  applies where the CMA has reasonable grounds for suspecting
that—

180.1.a

a person has engaged, is engaging or is likely to engage in a commercial
practice that constitutes a relevant infringement, or

180.1.b

a person is an accessory to such a practice.

180.2

The CMA may conduct an investigation into the matter.

180.3

Where the CMA conducts an investigation, it may publish a notice which (among
other things) may—

180.3.a

state its decision to conduct the investigation,

180.3.b

summarise the matter under investigation (including the industry sectors
affected),

180.3.c

identify, so far as possible, the persons under investigation (including
whether they are suspected of falling within  subsection (1) (a)  or  (b) ),
and

180.3.d
