indicate the timetable for the conduct of the investigation.

180.4

If after giving a notice under  subsection (3)  the CMA decides to close an
investigation, the CMA must publish a notice confirming that the investigation
is to be closed.

##### Infringement notices and penalties

###### Provisional infringement notice

181

181.1

This section  applies where—

181.1.a

the CMA has started an investigation under  section 180  that is continuing,
and

181.1.b

the condition in  subsection (2)  is met in respect of any person (“ the
respondent ”) who is subject to the investigation.

181.2

The condition in  this subsection  is met in respect of the respondent if the
CMA has reasonable grounds to believe that—

181.2.a

the respondent has engaged, is engaging or is likely to engage in a commercial
practice constituting a relevant infringement (“the infringing practice”), or

181.2.b

the respondent is an accessory to such a practice.

181.3

The CMA may give to the respondent a notice under  this section  (a
“provisional infringement notice”).

181.4

A provisional infringement notice must—

181.4.a

set out the grounds on which it is given, including the respondent’s acts or
omissions giving rise to the CMA’s belief that the condition in  subsection
(2)  is met;

181.4.b

set out proposed directions for the purposes of securing that the respondent
complies with  subsection (5) ;

181.4.c

invite the respondent to make representations to the CMA about the giving of
the notice;

181.4.d

specify the means by which, and the time by which, such representations must
be made.

181.5

The respondent complies with  this subsection  by—

181.5.a

in the case of a respondent within  subsection (2) (a) , not continuing or
repeating the infringing practice (where it is believed that the respondent
has engaged or is engaging in that practice);

181.5.b

in the case of a respondent within  subsection (2) (b) , not consenting to or
conniving in the infringing practice;

181.5.c

in either case, not engaging in the infringing practice in the course of the
respondent’s business or another business;

181.5.d

in either case, not consenting to or conniving in the carrying out of the
infringing practice by a body corporate with which the respondent has a
special relationship (see section  220 ).

181.6

If the proposed directions mentioned in  subsection (4) (b)  include the
taking by the respondent of enhanced consumer measures, the notice must state
that fact and include details of the proposed measures to be taken (but
section 183  applies in respect of any such proposed measures specified in a
provisional infringement notice as that section applies to such measures
specified in a final infringement notice).

181.7

The means specified under  subsection (4) (d)  for making representations must
include arrangements for them to be made orally if the respondent chooses to
make representations in that way.

181.8

If the CMA is considering the imposition of a monetary penalty on the
respondent (see  section 182 (4) (b) ), the provisional infringement notice
must also state—

181.8.a

that the CMA is considering imposing a monetary penalty;

181.8.b

the proposed amount of the penalty;

181.8.c

any further factors (in addition to those provided under  subsection (4) (a) )
which the CMA considers may justify the imposition of the proposed penalty and
its amount.

###### Final infringement notice

182

182.1

This section  applies where—

182.1.a

the CMA has given to the respondent a provisional infringement notice under
section 181 ,

182.1.b

the time for the respondent to make representations to the CMA in accordance
with that notice has expired, and

182.1.c

after considering such representations (if any), the CMA is satisfied that—

182.1.c.i

the respondent has engaged, is engaging or is likely to engage in a commercial
practice constituting a relevant infringement, or

182.1.c.ii

the respondent is an accessory to such a practice.

182.2

The CMA may give to the respondent a notice under  this section  (a “final
infringement notice”).

182.3

In deciding whether to give a final infringement notice the CMA must, in
particular, have regard to whether the respondent has previously given an
undertaking under  this Chapter  or  Chapter 3  in respect of the acts or
omissions in relation to which the final infringement notice would be given.

182.4

A final infringement notice may impose on the respondent a requirement to do
either or both of the following—

182.4.a

a requirement to comply with such directions as the CMA considers appropriate
for or in connection with the purpose of securing that the respondent complies
with  section 181 (5)  (which may include directions to take enhanced consumer
measures in accordance with  section 183 );

182.4.b

subject to  subsection (5) , a requirement to pay a monetary penalty.

182.5

In the case of a respondent within  subsection (1) (c) (i) , a requirement to
pay a monetary penalty may be imposed only if the CMA is satisfied that the
respondent has engaged, or is engaging, in a commercial practice constituting
a relevant infringement (and not in respect of a practice that the CMA is
satisfied that the person is likely to engage in).

182.6

The amount of a monetary penalty imposed under  subsection (4) (b)  must be a
fixed amount not exceeding £300,000 or, if higher, 10% of the total value of
the turnover (if any) of the respondent.

182.7

A final infringement notice must—

182.7.a

set out the grounds on which it is given, including the respondent’s acts or
omissions on account of which the notice is given;

182.7.b

state any further factors (in addition to those provided under  paragraph (a)
) which the CMA considers justify the giving of the notice;

182.7.c

if a penalty is imposed by the notice under  subsection (4) (b) , contain the
monetary penalty information (see  section 203 );

182.7.d

state that the respondent has a right to appeal against the notice and the
main details of that right (so far as not stated in accordance with  paragraph
(c) ).

182.8

A final infringement notice may require the respondent to publish—

182.8.a

the notice;

182.8.b

a corrective statement.

182.9

Publication under  subsection (8)  must be made in such form and manner, and
to such extent, as the CMA considers appropriate for the purpose of
eliminating any continuing effects of the relevant infringement.

###### Final infringement notice: directions to take enhanced consumer measures

183

183.1

Directions contained in a final infringement notice may include directions
requiring the respondent to take such enhanced consumer measures as the CMA
considers just and reasonable.

183.2

For this purpose, in deciding whether to require the taking of enhanced
consumer measures the CMA must in particular consider whether any proposed
enhanced consumer measures are proportionate having regard to—

183.2.a

the likely benefit of the measures to consumers,

183.2.b

the costs likely to be incurred by the respondent, and

183.2.c

the likely cost to consumers of obtaining the benefit of the measures.

183.3

The costs referred to in  subsection (2) (b)  are—

183.3.a

the cost of the measures, and

183.3.b

the reasonable administrative costs associated with taking the measures.

183.4

Where the respondent is required by a final infringement notice to take
enhanced consumer measures, the notice may include requirements for the
respondent to provide information or documents to the CMA in order that the
CMA may determine if the respondent is taking those measures.

183.5

Subsection (6)  applies if—

183.5.a

a final infringement notice requires the taking of enhanced consumer measures
offering compensation, and

183.5.b

a settlement agreement is entered into in connection with the payment of
compensation.

183.6

A waiver of a person’s rights in the settlement agreement is not valid if it
is a waiver of the right to bring civil proceedings in respect of conduct
other than conduct which has given rise to the final infringement notice.

##### Online interface notices

###### Online interface notices

184

184.1

This section  applies where the CMA is satisfied that a person has engaged, is
engaging or is likely to engage in a commercial practice that constitutes a
relevant infringement.

184.2

The CMA may give a notice under  this section  (an “online interface notice”)
to—

184.2.a

the person that the CMA is satisfied has engaged, is engaging or is likely to
engage in the commercial practice constituting the relevant infringement, or

184.2.b

any other person (subject to  subsection (3) ).

184.3

A notice under  subsection (2) (b)  may be given to a person who is outside
the United Kingdom only if the person—

184.3.a

is a United Kingdom national,

184.3.b

is an individual who is habitually resident in the United Kingdom,

184.3.c

is a firm established in the United Kingdom, or

184.3.d

carries on business in the United Kingdom or by any means directs activities
in the course of carrying on a business to consumers in the United Kingdom.

184.4

An online interface notice may contain whatever directions the CMA considers
appropriate for the purpose of requiring the person to whom it is given to do,
or to co-operate with another person so that person can do, one or more of the
following—

184.4.a

remove content from, or modify content on, an online interface;

184.4.b

disable or restrict access to an online interface;

184.4.c

display a warning to consumers accessing an online interface;

184.4.d

delete a fully qualified domain name and take any steps necessary to
facilitate the registration of that domain name by the CMA.

184.5

An online interface notice may be given to a person only if the CMA is
satisfied that—

184.5.a

there are no other available means under  section 162  or under another
provision of  this Chapter  of bringing about the cessation or prohibition of
the infringement which, by themselves, would be wholly effective, and

184.5.b

it is necessary for the directions contained in the notice to be given to
avoid the risk of serious harm to the collective interests of consumers.

184.6

An online interface notice must—

184.6.a

set out the grounds on which it is given;

184.6.b

state that the respondent has the right to appeal against the notice and the
main details of that right.

184.7

Where an online interface notice is given, the CMA may publish—

184.7.a

the notice, and

184.7.b

where known, the identity of the person who has engaged, is engaging or is
likely to engage in a commercial practice which constitutes the relevant
infringement.

184.8

Publication under  subsection (7)  must be made in such form and manner as the
CMA considers appropriate for the purpose of eliminating any continuing
effects of the relevant infringement.

184.9

For the purposes of subsection  (3) (c) , a firm is “established in the United
Kingdom” if—

184.9.a

it is incorporated or formed under the law of a part of the United Kingdom, or

184.9.b

it is administered under arrangements governed by the law of a part of the
United Kingdom.

184.10

In  subsection (4)  “ online interface ” means any software, including a
website, part of a website, an application or other digital content which—

184.10.a

is operated by a person (“ P ”) acting for purposes relating to P’s business
or by a person acting in the name of, or on behalf of, P, and

184.10.b

is operated for or in connection with the purposes of giving access to, or
promoting, the goods, services or digital content that P or another person
supplies.

##### Undertakings

###### Undertakings

185

185.1

This section  applies where the CMA—

185.1.a

has started an investigation under  section 180  which is continuing, and

185.1.b

has not given a final infringement notice or an online interface notice in
relation to the matter under investigation.

185.2

The CMA may accept an undertaking under  this section  in connection with that
matter from any person whom the CMA believes—

185.2.a

has engaged, is engaging or is likely to engage in a commercial practice that
constitutes a relevant infringement (“the infringing practice”), or

185.2.b

is an accessory to such a practice.

185.3

Subsections  (1)  to  (6)  of  section 164  (inclusion of enhanced consumer
measures in undertakings) apply to an undertaking under this section as they
apply to an undertaking under  section 163 (2) .

185.4

An undertaking under  this section  is an undertaking to do one or more of the
following—

185.4.a

in the case of an undertaking from a person within  subsection (2) (a) , not
to continue or repeat the infringing practice (where the CMA believes the
person has engaged or is engaging in the practice);

185.4.b

in the case of an undertaking from a person within  subsection (2) (b) , not
to consent to or connive in the infringing practice;

185.4.c

in either case, not to engage in the infringing practice in the course of the
person’s business or another business;

185.4.d

in either case, not to consent to, or connive in, the carrying out of the
infringing practice by a body corporate with which the person has a special
relationship (see section  220 ).

185.5

Where the CMA has accepted from a person an undertaking under  this section —

185.5.a

the CMA may accept from the person any such variation of the undertaking that
the CMA considers appropriate for meeting the purposes for which the
undertaking was given;

185.5.b

the CMA may release the person from the undertaking (whether on its own
initiative or at the person’s request) if the CMA considers that the
undertaking is no longer necessary to further those purposes.

185.6

The powers of the CMA under  this section  do not limit other powers of the
CMA to accept, vary or release undertakings under  Chapter 3 .

###### Effect of undertakings under 

186

186.1

This section  applies where the CMA accepts an undertaking from a person under
section 185  in connection with a matter that it was investigating under
section 180 .

186.2

The CMA may not give a final infringement notice or an online interface notice
to the person in relation to the matter.

186.3

Subsection  (2)  does not prevent the CMA from giving a final infringement
notice or an online interface notice to the person—

186.3.a

if and to the extent that the notice relates to anything not addressed by the
acceptance of the undertaking mentioned in  subsection (1) ;

186.3.b

if the CMA considers that there has been a material change of circumstances
since the undertaking was accepted;

186.3.c

if the CMA has reasonable grounds for suspecting that a person from whom the
undertaking was accepted has failed to adhere to one or more of the terms of
the undertaking;

186.3.d

if the CMA has reasonable grounds for suspecting that information which led it
to accept the undertaking was incomplete, false or misleading in a material
way.

186.4

If the CMA gives a final infringement notice or an online interface notice by
virtue of  subsection (3) (b) ,  (c)  or  (d) , the undertaking is to be
treated as released as from the date on which the notice is given.

###### Undertakings under 

187

187.1

This section  applies where the CMA proposes to—

187.1.a

accept a material variation of an undertaking under  section 185 , or

187.1.b

release a person from any such undertaking,

and the proposed variation or release has not been requested by the person who
gave the undertaking.

187.2

Before taking the proposed action mentioned in  subsection (1)  the CMA must—

187.2.a

give notice to the person under  subsection (3) , and

187.2.b

consider any representations made in accordance with the notice.

187.3

A notice under  this subsection  must state—

187.3.a

the fact that the CMA is proposing to act as mentioned in  subsection (1) ,

187.3.b

the reasons for doing so, and

187.3.c

the means by which, and the time by which, representations may be made in
relation to the proposed action.

187.4

If after considering any representations made in accordance with a notice
under  subsection (3)  the CMA decides to take an action mentioned in
subsection (1) , the CMA must give notice to the person of that decision.

187.5

The reference in  subsection (1) (a)  to a material variation is a reference
to any variation that the CMA considers to be material in any respect.

###### Provisional breach of undertakings enforcement notice

188

188.1

This section  applies where—

188.1.a

the CMA has accepted an undertaking from a person (“ the respondent ”) under
section 185 , and

188.1.b

the CMA has reasonable grounds to believe that the respondent has failed to
comply with one or more of the terms of the undertaking.

188.2

The CMA may give to the respondent a notice under  this section  (a
“provisional breach of undertakings enforcement notice”).

188.3

A provisional breach of undertakings enforcement notice must—

188.3.a

set out the grounds on which it is given, including the respondent’s alleged
acts or omissions giving rise to the belief mentioned in  subsection (1) (b) ;

188.3.b

set out proposed directions for the purpose of securing that the respondent
complies with  subsection (5) ;

188.3.c

invite the respondent to make representations to the CMA about the giving of
the notice;

188.3.d

specify the means by which, and the time by which, such representations must
be made.

188.4

The means specified under  subsection (3) (d)  for making representations must
include arrangements for them to be made orally if the respondent chooses to
make representations in that way.

188.5

The respondent complies with  this subsection  by—

188.5.a

in the case of a respondent within  section 185 (2) (a) , not continuing or
repeating the infringing practice (where it is believed that the respondent
has engaged or is engaging in that practice);

188.5.b

in the case of a respondent within  section 185 (2) (b) , not consenting to or
conniving in the infringing practice;

188.5.c

in either case, not engaging in the infringing practice in the course of the
respondent’s business or another business;

188.5.d

in either case, not consenting to or conniving in the carrying out of the
infringing practice by a body corporate with which the respondent has a
special relationship (see section  220 ).

188.6

If the CMA is considering the imposition of a monetary penalty on the
respondent (see  section 189 (3) (b) ), the provisional breach of undertakings
enforcement notice must also state—

188.6.a

that the CMA is considering imposing a monetary penalty;

188.6.b

the proposed amount of the penalty (including whether the penalty would be a
fixed amount, an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate or both a
fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate);

188.6.c

any further factors (in addition to those provided under  subsection (3) (a) )
which the CMA considers justify the imposition of the proposed penalty and its
amount or amounts.

###### Final breach of undertakings enforcement notice

189

189.1

This section  applies where—

189.1.a

the CMA has given to the respondent a provisional breach of undertakings
enforcement notice under  section 188 ,

189.1.b

the time for the respondent to make representations to the CMA in accordance
with that notice has expired, and

189.1.c

after considering such representations (if any), the CMA is satisfied that the
respondent has failed to comply with one or more of the terms of the
undertaking.

189.2

The CMA may give to the respondent a notice under  this section  (a “final
breach of undertakings enforcement notice”).

189.3

A final breach of undertakings enforcement notice may, subject to  subsection
(4) , impose on the respondent a requirement to do either or both of the
following—

189.3.a

to comply with such directions as the CMA considers appropriate for the
purpose of securing that the respondent complies with  section 188 (5) ;

189.3.b

to pay a monetary penalty in respect of the failure mentioned in  subsection
(1) (c) .

189.4

A requirement under subsection (3)(b) to pay a monetary penalty may be imposed
only if the CMA is satisfied that the failure in question is without
reasonable excuse.

189.5

A final breach of undertakings enforcement notice must—

189.5.a

set out the grounds on which it is given, including the respondent’s acts or
omissions giving rise to the failure mentioned in  subsection (1) (c) ;

189.5.b

state any further factors (in addition to those provided under  paragraph (a)
) which the CMA considers justify the giving of the notice;

189.5.c

if directions are given under  subsection (3) (a) , specify the actions to be
taken by the respondent in accordance with the directions;

189.5.d

if a penalty is imposed under  subsection (3) (b) , specify the monetary
penalty information (see  section 203 );

189.5.e

state that the respondent has a right to appeal against the notice and the
main details of that right (so far as not stated in accordance with  paragraph
(d) ).

189.6

The CMA may publish a final breach of undertakings enforcement notice in such
manner, and to such extent, as the CMA considers appropriate.

###### Monetary penalties under 

190

190.1

This section  applies in relation to a requirement imposed on the respondent
to pay a monetary penalty under a final breach of undertakings enforcement
notice.

190.2

The amount of the penalty must be—

190.2.a

a fixed amount,

190.2.b

an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, or

190.2.c

a combination of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a
daily rate.

190.3

The penalty must not exceed—

190.3.a

in the case of a fixed amount, £150,000 or, if higher, 5% of the total value
of the turnover (if any) of the respondent;

190.3.b

in the case of an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, for each day
£15,000 or, if higher, 5% of the total value of the daily turnover (if any) of
the respondent;

190.3.c

in the case of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a daily
rate, such fixed amount and such amount per day.

190.4

In imposing a penalty by reference to a daily rate—

190.4.a

no account is to be taken of any days before the date on which the provisional
breach of undertakings enforcement notice was given to the respondent, and

190.4.b

unless the CMA determines an earlier date, the amount payable ceases to
accumulate on the day on which the requirements of the final breach of
undertakings enforcement notice are complied with.

##### Directions

###### Provisional breach of directions enforcement notice

191

191.1

This section  applies where—

191.1.a

an enforcement direction has been given to a person (“ the respondent ”), and

191.1.b

the CMA has reasonable grounds to believe that the respondent has without
reasonable excuse failed to comply with the direction (fully or to any
respect).

191.2

The CMA may give to the respondent a notice under  this section  (a
“provisional breach of directions enforcement notice”).

191.3

A provisional breach of directions enforcement notice must—

191.3.a

set out the grounds on which it is given, including the respondent’s acts or
omissions giving rise to the belief mentioned in  subsection (1) (b) ;

191.3.b

set out proposed directions for the purpose of securing that the respondent
complies with the direction;

191.3.c

invite the respondent to make representations to the CMA about the giving of
the notice;

191.3.d

specify the means by which, and the time by which, such representations must
be made.

191.4

The means specified under subsection (3)(d) for making representations must
include arrangements for them to be made orally if the respondent chooses to
make representations in that way.

191.5

A provisional breach of directions enforcement notice must also state—

191.5.a

that the CMA is considering imposing a monetary penalty;

191.5.b

the proposed amount of the penalty (including whether the penalty would be a
fixed amount, an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate or both a
fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate);

191.5.c

any further factors (in addition to those provided under  subsection (3) (a) )
which the CMA considers justify the imposition of the proposed penalty and its
amount or amounts.

191.6

In  this Chapter  “ enforcement direction ” means a direction given in—

191.6.a

a final infringement notice,

191.6.b

an online interface notice, or

191.6.c

a final breach of undertakings enforcement notice.

###### Final breach of directions enforcement notice

192

192.1

This section  applies where—

192.1.a

the CMA has given to the respondent a provisional breach of directions
enforcement notice under  section 191  in respect of a suspected failure to
comply with an enforcement direction,

192.1.b

the time for the respondent to make representations to the CMA in accordance
with that notice has expired, and

192.1.c

after considering such representations (if any), the CMA is satisfied that the
respondent has, without reasonable excuse, failed to comply with the
direction.

192.2

The CMA may give to the respondent a notice under this section (a “final
breach of directions enforcement notice”).

192.3

A final breach of directions enforcement notice is a notice that imposes on
the respondent a requirement to pay a monetary penalty.

192.4

A final breach of directions enforcement notice must—

192.4.a

set out the grounds on which it is given, including the respondent’s acts or
omissions giving rise to the failure mentioned in  subsection (1) (c) ;

192.4.b

state any further factors (in addition to those provided under  paragraph (a)
) which the CMA considers justify the giving of the notice;

192.4.c

specify the monetary penalty information (see  section 203 ).

192.5

A final breach of directions enforcement notice may—

192.5.a

vary or revoke the enforcement direction mentioned in  subsection (1) ;

192.5.b

specify such other directions as the CMA considers appropriate for the purpose
of securing that the respondent complies with the requirements in respect of
which the enforcement direction was given.

192.6

Where a final breach of directions enforcement notice includes provision under
subsection  (5)  that varies an enforcement direction or specifies other
directions, the notice must (in addition to the requirements under subsection
(4) ) also state that the respondent has a right to appeal against the notice
and the main details of that right.

192.7

The CMA may publish a final breach of directions enforcement notice in such
manner, and to such extent, as the CMA considers appropriate.

###### Monetary penalties under 

193

193.1

This section  applies in relation to a requirement imposed on the respondent
to pay a monetary penalty under a final breach of directions enforcement
notice.

193.2

The amount of the penalty must be—

193.2.a

a fixed amount,

193.2.b

an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, or

193.2.c

a combination of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a
daily rate.

193.3

The penalty imposed on a person must not exceed—

193.3.a

in the case of a fixed amount, £150,000 or, if higher, 5% of the total value
of the turnover (if any) of the respondent;

193.3.b

in the case of an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, for each day
£15,000 or, if higher, 5% of the total value of the daily turnover (if any) of
the respondent;

193.3.c

in the case of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a daily
rate, such fixed amount and such amount per day.

193.4

In imposing a penalty by reference to a daily rate—

193.4.a

no account is to be taken of any days before the date on which the provisional
breach of directions enforcement notice was given to the respondent, and

193.4.b

unless the CMA determines an earlier date, the amount payable ceases to
accumulate on the day on which the relevant directions are fully complied
with.

193.5

In  subsection (4) (b)  the “relevant directions” are—

193.5.a

the enforcement direction mentioned in  section 192 (1) (a)  (if not revoked
under  section 192 (5) (a) );

193.5.b

any further directions specified under  section 192 (5) (b) .

###### Powers of court to enforce directions

194

194.1

This section  applies where the CMA considers that a person (“ the respondent
”) has failed to comply with—

194.1.a

an enforcement direction, or

194.1.b

a direction given in a final breach of directions enforcement notice under
section 192 (5) (b) .

194.2

The CMA may make an application to the appropriate court under  this section .

194.3

If on an application under  subsection (2)  the court finds that the
respondent has failed to comply with the direction concerned, the court may
make an order imposing such requirements on the respondent as the court
considers appropriate for the purpose of remedying the failure.

194.4

An order under  this section  may provide for all of the costs or expenses of,
and incidental to, the application for the order to be met by the respondent
or any officer of a person that is responsible for the respondent’s failure to
comply with the direction.

194.5

Nothing in  this section  limits the powers of the court to make orders under
Chapter 3  or otherwise (and an application under  this section  may be
combined with an application under that Chapter for a consumer protection
order).

194.6

The following provisions of  Chapter 3  apply to an order under  this section
as if the order were a consumer protection order—

194.6.a

section 173  (appropriate court);

194.6.b

section 174  (effect of orders in other parts of the United Kingdom);

194.6.c

section 178  (substantiation of claims).

###### Substantiation of claims

195

195.1

This section  applies where—

195.1.a

the CMA gives a provisional notice under  this Chapter  to a person (“ the
respondent ”) in respect of a relevant infringement involving a contravention
of  Chapter 1  of  Part 4  (protection from unfair trading), and

195.1.b

the respondent makes representations to the CMA in response to that notice.

195.2

The CMA may, for the purpose of considering the representations, require the
respondent to provide evidence as to the accuracy of any factual claim made as
part of a commercial practice of the respondent.

195.3

The CMA may determine that a factual claim of the respondent is inaccurate if—

195.3.a

the respondent fails to provide evidence of the accuracy of the claim in
response to a requirement imposed under  subsection (2) , or

195.3.b

the CMA considers that any such evidence that is provided is inadequate.

195.4

In this section “ provisional notice ” means—

195.4.a

a provisional infringement notice,

195.4.b

a provisional breach of undertakings enforcement notice, or

195.4.c

a provisional breach of directions enforcement notice.

###### Variation or revocation of directions

196

196.1

This section  applies where the CMA proposes to—

196.1.a

make a material variation of an enforcement direction given to a person (“ the
respondent ”), or

196.1.b

revoke any such direction.

196.2

Before taking the proposed action mentioned in  subsection (1)  the CMA must—

196.2.a

give notice to the respondent under  subsection (3) , and

196.2.b

consider any representations made in accordance with the notice.

196.3

A notice under  this subsection  must state—

196.3.a

the fact that CMA is proposing to act as mentioned in  subsection (1) ,

196.3.b

the reasons for doing so, and

196.3.c

the means by which, and the time by which, representations may be made in
relation to the proposed variation or revocation.

196.4

If after considering any representations made in accordance with a notice
under  subsection (3)  the CMA decides to take the action mentioned in
subsection (1) , the CMA must give notice to the respondent of that decision.

196.5

The reference in  subsection (1) (a)  to a material variation is a reference
to any variation that the CMA considers to be material in any respect.

196.6

In  this section  “ enforcement direction ” includes a direction given in a
notice under section  192 (5) (b) .

##### False or misleading information

###### Provisional false information enforcement notice

197

197.1

This section  applies if—

197.1.a

the CMA has reasonable grounds to believe that a person (“ the respondent ”)
has, without reasonable excuse, provided information to the CMA that is
materially false or misleading, and

197.1.b

the information was provided in connection with the carrying out by the CMA of
a direct enforcement function.

197.2

The CMA may give to the respondent a notice under  this section  (a
“provisional false information enforcement notice”).

197.3

A provisional false information enforcement notice must—

197.3.a

set out the grounds on which it is given;

197.3.b

state that the CMA is considering imposing a monetary penalty;

197.3.c

state the proposed amount of the penalty;

197.3.d

state any further factors (in addition to those provided under paragraph (a))
which the CMA considers justify the imposition of the proposed penalty and its
amount;

197.3.e

invite the respondent to make representations to the CMA about the giving of
the notice;

197.3.f

specify the means by which, and the time by which, such representations must
be made.

197.4

The means specified under subsection (3)(f) for making representations must
include arrangements for them to be made orally if the respondent chooses to
make representations in that way.

197.5

In  this Part  “ direct enforcement function ” means—

197.5.a

a function of the CMA under  this Chapter , or

197.5.b

a function of the CMA under paragraph 16B or 16C of Schedule 5 to CRA 2015.

###### Final false information enforcement notice

198

198.1

This section  applies where—

198.1.a

the CMA has given to the respondent a provisional false information
enforcement notice under  section 197  in connection with the provision of
information,

198.1.b

the time for the respondent to make representations to the CMA in accordance
with the notice has expired, and

198.1.c

after considering such representations (if any), the CMA is satisfied that—

198.1.c.i

the information mentioned in  paragraph (a)  is materially false or
misleading, and

198.1.c.ii

the respondent provided the false or misleading information without reasonable
excuse.

198.2

The CMA may give to the respondent a notice under  this section  (“a final
false information enforcement notice”).

198.3

A final false information enforcement notice is a notice that imposes on the
respondent a requirement to pay a monetary penalty.

198.4

The amount of the penalty must be a fixed amount not exceeding £30,000 or, if
higher, 1% of the total value of the turnover (if any) of the respondent.

198.5

A final false information enforcement notice must—

198.5.a

set out the grounds on which it is given;

198.5.b

state any further factors (in addition to those provided under  paragraph (a)
) which the CMA considers justify the giving of the notice;

198.5.c

specify the monetary penalty information (see  section 203 ).

198.6

The CMA may publish a final false information enforcement notice in such
manner, and to such extent, as the CMA considers appropriate.

##### Miscellaneous and appeals

###### Statement of policy in relation to monetary penalties

199

199.1

The CMA must prepare and publish a statement of policy in relation to the
exercise of powers to impose a monetary penalty under this Chapter.

199.2

The statement must include a statement about the considerations relevant to
the determination of—

199.2.a

whether to impose a penalty under this Chapter, and

199.2.b

the nature and amount of any such penalty.

199.3

The CMA may revise its statement of policy and, where it does so, must publish
the revised statement.

199.4

In preparing or revising its statement of policy the CMA must consult—

199.4.a

the Secretary of State, and

199.4.b

such other persons as the CMA considers appropriate.

199.5

A statement of policy, or revised statement, may not be published under  this
section  without the approval of the Secretary of State.

199.6

Subsection (7)  applies where the CMA proposes to impose under this Chapter a
monetary penalty on a person.

199.7

The CMA must have regard to the statement of policy most recently published
under  this section  at the time of the act or omission giving rise to the
penalty in deciding—

199.7.a

whether to impose the penalty, and

199.7.b

if so, the nature and amount of the penalty.

###### Interconnected bodies corporate

200

200.1

This section applies where—

200.1.a

the CMA gives to a body corporate (“ the respondent ”) a final notice, and

200.1.b

the interconnection condition applies in relation to the respondent.

200.2

The interconnection condition applies in relation to the respondent if—

200.2.a

at the time the final notice is given, the respondent is a member of a group
of interconnected bodies corporate,

200.2.b

at any time when requirements imposed by the final notice remain in force, the
respondent becomes a member of a group of interconnected bodies corporate, or

200.2.c

at any time when requirements imposed by the final notice remain in force, a
group of interconnected bodies corporate of which the respondent is a member
is increased by the addition of one or more further members.

200.3

The notice may include provision for the requirements (or any particular
requirements) imposed by the final notice on the respondent also to be binding
upon all other members of the group (in addition to the respondent), as if
each of them were the respondent.

200.4

Provision may be included in a notice under  subsection (3)  only if the CMA
considers it just, reasonable and proportionate to include that provision.

200.5

A group of interconnected bodies corporate is a group consisting of two or
more bodies corporate all of whom are interconnected with each other.

200.6

Any two bodies corporate are interconnected—

200.6.a

if one of them is a subsidiary of the other, or

200.6.b

if both of them are subsidiaries of the same body corporate.

200.7

Where a final notice includes provision under  subsection (3) , the notice
must also be given to any other member of the respondent’s group in relation
to which the requirements imposed by the notice are to be binding.

200.8

In this section “ final notice ” means—

200.8.a

a final infringement notice,

200.8.b

an online interface notice, or

200.8.c

a final breach of directions enforcement notice.

###### Record-keeping and reporting requirements

201

201.1

The CMA must keep a record of—

201.1.a

undertakings it has accepted and enforcement directions it has given, and

201.1.b

reviews it has carried out in relation to the effectiveness of such
undertakings and directions.

201.2

If requested to do so by the Secretary of State, the CMA must prepare a report
on—

201.2.a

the effectiveness of undertakings and enforcement directions, and

201.2.b

the number and outcome of appeals brought under  section 202 .

201.3

The CMA must—

201.3.a

provide to the Secretary of State a report prepared under  this section , and

201.3.b

publish the report in such manner as the CMA considers appropriate.

201.4

In  this section —

201.4.a

“ undertakings ” means undertakings given under  section 185 ;

201.4.b

“ enforcement directions ” includes directions given in a notice under
section 192 (5) (b) .

###### Appeals

202

202.1

A person to whom a relevant notice is given may appeal to the appropriate
appeal court against—

202.1.a

a decision to impose a monetary penalty by virtue of the notice,

202.1.b

the nature or amount of any such penalty, or

202.1.c

the giving of directions by virtue of the notice.

202.2

The grounds for an appeal under  subsection (1) (a)  or (b) are that—

202.2.a

the decision to impose a monetary penalty was based on an error of fact,

202.2.b

the decision was wrong in law,

202.2.c

the amount of the penalty is unreasonable, or

202.2.d

the decision was unreasonable or wrong for any other reason.

202.3

The grounds for an appeal under  subsection (1) (c)  are that—

202.3.a

the decision to give the directions was based on an error of fact,

202.3.b

the decision was wrong in law,

202.3.c

the nature of the directions is unreasonable, or

202.3.d

the decision was unreasonable or wrong for any other reason.

202.4

On an appeal under  this section  the appropriate appeal court may quash,
confirm or vary the relevant notice.

202.5

Except in the case of an appeal relating to a final false information
enforcement notice, in addition to the powers conferred by subsection  (4)
the appropriate appeal court may also remit any matter that is the subject of
the appeal to the CMA.

202.6

An appeal under  this section  must be brought before the end of the
applicable period beginning with the day on which the relevant notice was
given to the person seeking to bring the appeal.

202.7

The appropriate appeal court may extend the applicable period for bringing an
appeal.

202.8

Where an appeal is brought in respect of—

202.8.a

a requirement to pay a monetary penalty, or

202.8.b

a requirement to pay compensation under directions imposing enhanced consumer
measures,

the penalty or compensation is not required to be paid until after the appeal
is determined, withdrawn or otherwise dealt with.

202.9

In  this section —

      “ applicable period ” means—         in relation to a final false
information enforcement notice, the period of 28 days;           in relation
to any other relevant notice, the period of 60 days;                 “
appropriate appeal court ” means—         in relation to England and Wales or
Northern Ireland, the High Court;           in relation to Scotland, the Outer
House of the Court of Session;                 “ relevant notice ” means—
a final infringement notice,           an online interface notice,           a
final breach of undertakings enforcement notice,           a final breach of
directions enforcement notice, or           a final false information
enforcement notice.

#### Monetary penalties: general provisions

##### Information to accompany orders or notices imposing monetary penalties

203

203.1

An order or notice under Chapter  3  or  4  under which a person (“ the
respondent ”) is required to pay a monetary penalty must state the following
information (referred to in those Chapters as the “monetary penalty
information”)—

203.1.a

the amount of the penalty (including whether it is a fixed amount, an amount
calculated by reference to a daily rate or both a fixed amount and an amount
calculated by reference to a daily rate);

203.1.b

the grounds on which the penalty is imposed together with any other factors
that the court (in the case of an order) or the CMA (in the case of a notice)
considers justify the giving of the penalty or its amount;

203.1.c

in the case of an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, the day on
which the amount first starts to accumulate and the day or days on which it
might cease to accumulate;

203.1.d

how the penalty is to be paid;

203.1.e

the date or dates, no earlier than the end of the applicable period beginning
with the date on which the order was served on or the notice was given to the
respondent, by which the penalty or (as the case may be) different portions of
it are required to be paid;

203.1.f

that the penalty or (as the case may be) different portions of it may be paid
earlier than the date or dates by which it or they are required to be paid;

203.1.g

that the respondent has the right to apply under  subsection (3)  (in the case
of an order) or  subsection (4)  (in the case of a notice);

203.1.h

the rights available to the respondent to appeal in respect of the imposition
of the penalty;

203.1.i

the main details of the rights mentioned in paragraphs  (g)  and  (h) .

203.2

In subsection (1)(e) “ the applicable period ” means—

203.2.a

in the case of an order or a final false information enforcement notice, the
period of 28 days;

203.2.b

in any other case, the period of 60 days.

203.3

The respondent may, within 14 days of the date on which an order imposing a
monetary penalty is served on the respondent, apply to the court for the court
to specify a different date or dates by which the penalty, or different
portions of it, are to be paid.

203.4

The respondent may, within 14 days of the date on which a notice imposing a
monetary penalty is given to the respondent, apply to the CMA to specify a
different date or dates by which the penalty, or different portions of it, are
required to be paid.

203.5

References in subsections  (1)  and  (2)  to an order include references to a
notice accompanying such an order given under  section 158 (4) .

203.6

In the application of this section to Scotland, the references in subsections
(1) (e)  and  (3)  to an order being served include service of an extract
order in execution of or diligence on the order.

##### Determination of turnover

204

204.1

In  this Part  references to “turnover” of a person include—

204.1.a

turnover both in and outside the United Kingdom;

204.1.b

where the person controls another person, the turnover of that other person;

204.1.c

where the person is controlled by another person, the turnover of that person.

204.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

204.2.a

make provision for determining when a person is to be treated as controlled by
another person for the purposes of subsection (1)(b) and (c);

204.2.b

make provision for determining the turnover of a person for the purposes of
this Part.

204.3

Regulations under this section may, in particular, make provision as to—

204.3.a

the amounts which are, or which are not, to be treated as comprising a
person’s turnover or daily turnover;

204.3.b

the date or dates by reference to which a person’s turnover or daily turnover
is to be determined.

204.4

Regulations under this section may include provision enabling the court or the
CMA to determine matters of a description specified in the regulations
(including any of the matters mentioned in paragraphs (a) and (b) of
subsection (3) ).

204.5

Regulations under  this section  are subject to the negative procedure.

##### Power to amend amounts

205

205.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend any of the following
provisions for the purpose of substituting a different monetary amount for an
amount of fixed or daily penalty for the time being specified—

205.1.a

section 158 (5) ;

205.1.b

section 168 (3) (a)  and  (b) ;

205.1.c

section 182 (6) ;

205.1.d

section 190 (3) (a)  and  (b) ;

205.1.e

section 193 (3) (a)  and  (b) ;

205.1.f

section 198 (4) .

205.2

Before making regulations under  this section  the Secretary of State must
consult such persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

205.3

Regulations under  this section  are subject to the affirmative procedure.

##### Recovery of monetary penalties

206

206.1

This section  applies where a monetary penalty imposed under  Chapter 4 , or
any part of such a penalty, has not been paid by the date on which it is
required to be paid and—

206.1.a

an appeal to a court against the imposition of the penalty has not been
brought before the end of the period within which it is required to be
brought, or

206.1.b

any such appeal that was brought has been determined, withdrawn or otherwise
disposed of.

206.2

The CMA may recover from the person on whom the penalty was imposed any of the
penalty and any interest which has not been paid.

206.3

Any such penalty and interest may be recovered summarily (or, in Scotland,
recovered) as a civil debt by the CMA.

206.4

Subsection (5)  applies where—

206.4.a

a penalty is payable by a person by virtue of a final infringement notice,

206.4.b

the notice also includes directions imposing a requirement on the person to
take enhanced consumer measures, and

206.4.c

the enhanced consumer measures that the person is required to take are or
include redress measures (see  section 221 (2) ).

206.5

In deciding whether to recover the penalty from the person under  subsection
(2) , the CMA must have regard to—

206.5.a

whether any compensation required to be paid to consumers under the redress
measures has been, or is likely to be, paid, and

206.5.b

where any such payments have not yet been paid (in full or in part), the
effect that recovery of the penalty from the person may have on the person’s
ability to make those compensatory payments.

##### Monetary penalties: further provision

207

207.1

If the whole or any portion of a monetary penalty imposed is not paid by the
date by which it is required to be paid, the unpaid balance from time to time
carries interest at the statutory rate.

207.2

Where an application has been made under  section 203 (3)  or  (4) , the
penalty is not required to be paid until the application has been determined,
withdrawn or otherwise disposed of.

207.3

Where an application has been made to appeal to a court in respect of a
monetary penalty, the penalty is not required to be paid until the application
has been determined, withdrawn or otherwise disposed of.

207.4

If a portion of a monetary penalty imposed by an order of the court has not
been paid by the date required for it, the court may, where it considers it
appropriate to do so, by order require so much of the penalty as has not
already been paid (and is capable of being paid immediately) to be paid
immediately.

207.5

If a portion of a monetary penalty imposed by virtue of a notice given by the
CMA has not been paid by the date required for it, the CMA may, where it
considers it appropriate to do so, by notice require so much of the penalty as
has not already been paid (and is capable of being paid immediately) to be
paid immediately.

207.6

Where on an appeal under  section 202  the court substitutes a penalty of a
different nature or of a lesser amount, the court may require the payment of
interest at the statutory rate on the substituted penalty from whatever date
it considers appropriate (which may include a date before the determination of
the appeal).

207.7

In the case of a monetary penalty imposed on a firm that is not a body
corporate, the penalty is to be paid out of the assets or funds of the firm.

207.8

Sums received from a person towards payment of a monetary penalty must be
paid—

207.8.a

in the case of a penalty imposed by an order of the Court of Session or the
Sheriff, into the Scottish Consolidated Fund;

207.8.b

in the case of a penalty imposed by an order of a court in Northern Ireland,
into the Consolidated Fund of Northern Ireland;

207.8.c

in any other case, into the Consolidated Fund of the United Kingdom.

207.9

In  this section —

      “ monetary penalty ” means a monetary penalty imposed under Chapter  3
or  4 ;           “ the statutory rate ” means the rate for the time being
specified in section 17 of the Judgments Act 1838.

#### Investigatory powers

##### Investigatory powers of enforcers

208

208.1

Schedule 17  contains amendments to Schedule 5 to CRA 2015 (investigatory
powers), including amendments about—

208.1.a

the giving of monetary penalties in connection with a failure to comply with
an information notice;

208.1.b

the giving of information notices to persons outside the United Kingdom;

208.1.c

the means by which information notices are to be given;

208.1.d

entry to premises where documents are accessible from the premises.

208.2

In  subsection (1)  “ information notice ” means a notice given under
paragraph 14 of Schedule 5 to CRA 2015.

#### Miscellaneous

##### Powers to amend 

209

209.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend—

209.1.a

the first column of the Table in Part 1 of  Schedule 15  so as to add, remove
or vary an entry for an enactment;

209.1.b

the second column of that Table so as to add, remove or vary an entry
providing for the authorised enforcers in respect of an enactment;

209.1.c

the third column of that Table in consequence of amendments made under the
power conferred by paragraph (a);

209.1.d

the second column of the Table in  Part 2  of  Schedule 15  so as to add,
remove or vary an entry providing for the authorised enforcers in respect of
an obligation or rule of law;

209.1.e

Schedule 16  so as to add, remove or vary an entry for an enactment.

209.2

The power under  subsection (1) (a)  or  (e)  is exercisable so as to add or
vary an entry in respect of an enactment only if, and to the extent that, one
or more of the following is provided for under or by virtue of the enactment
so added or varied—

209.2.a

a duty, prohibition or restriction enforceable by criminal proceedings;

209.2.b

a duty owed to a person that is enforceable by civil proceedings;

209.2.c

a remedy or sanction enforceable by civil proceedings;

209.2.d

an agreement or security relating to a supply of goods, services or digital
content to be void or unenforceable to any extent;

209.2.e

a right or remedy exercisable by a person supplying goods, services or digital
content to be restricted or excluded;

209.2.f

the avoidance (to any extent) of liability relating to the supply of goods,
services or digital content to be restricted or prevented.

209.3

It is immaterial for the purposes of  subsection (2)  whether or not—

209.3.a

a duty, prohibition or restriction exists in relation to consumers as such;

209.3.b

a remedy or sanction is provided for the benefit of consumers as such;

209.3.c

proceedings have been brought in relation to the act or omission concerned;

209.3.d

a person has been convicted of an offence in relation to the act or omission
concerned.

209.4

Regulations under  this section  are subject to the affirmative procedure.

##### Rules

210

210.1

The CMA may make rules about procedural and other matters in connection with
the carrying out of its direct enforcement functions.

210.2

Rules may provide for any of the CMA’s direct enforcement functions to be
carried out on its behalf—

210.2.a

by one or more members of the CMA Board (see Part 2 of Schedule 4 to the
Enterprise and Regulatory Reform Act 2013);

210.2.b

by one or more members of the CMA Panel (see Part 3 of Schedule 4 to that
Act);

210.2.c

by one or more members of staff of the CMA;

210.2.d

jointly by one or more of the persons mentioned in  paragraphs (a)  to  (c) .

210.3

Rules may (among other things) include provision as to the following matters
so far as relating to the carrying out of direct enforcement functions—

210.3.a

the form and manner in which a notice given by the CMA under a direct
enforcement function is to be given (subject to  section 332 );

210.3.b

the person (or persons) to whom the notice is to be given;

210.3.c

if the CMA is required to publish the notice, the manner in which it is to do
so;

210.3.d

arrangements to ensure the protection of confidential information;

210.3.e

the disclosure of information to persons under investigation;

210.3.f

the form and manner in which representations may or must be made to the CMA;

210.3.g

the procedure to be followed in relation to the holding of oral hearings as
part of an investigation;

210.3.h

the procedure to be followed in cases where a person under investigation
accepts that there has been a relevant infringement of a kind to which the
investigation relates;

210.3.i

arrangements for the making of, and dealing with, complaints.

210.4

In  this section  and  section 211  “ rules ” means rules made under  this
section .

##### Procedural requirements for making of rules

211

211.1

In preparing rules the CMA must consult such persons as the CMA considers
appropriate.

211.2

The CMA may not bring a rule into operation until the rule has been approved
by regulations made by the Secretary of State.

211.3

The Secretary of State may approve a rule—

211.3.a

in the form in which it is submitted, or

211.3.b

subject to whatever modifications the Secretary of State considers
appropriate.

211.4

Where the Secretary of State proposes to approve a rule subject to
modifications, the Secretary of State must—

211.4.a

inform the CMA of the proposed modifications, and

211.4.b

take into account any comments made by the CMA about the proposed
modifications.

211.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

211.5.a

vary or revoke rules, or

211.5.b

direct the CMA to vary or revoke rules in accordance with the direction.

211.6

Subsections (2)  to  (4)  apply to any variation of rules made by the CMA,
except where acting under a direction given under  subsection (5) (b) .

211.7

Regulations under this section are subject to the negative procedure.

##### Guidance

212

212.1

The CMA must prepare and publish guidance about its general approach to the
carrying out of its direct enforcement functions.

212.2

Guidance under  subsection (1)  must provide information about the factors
that the CMA will take into account in determining—

212.2.a

whether it will exercise a power under  Chapter 4  to accept, vary or release
an undertaking;

212.2.b

in cases where the exercise of any such power is exercisable only if the CMA
considers a person has acted (or failed to act) without a reasonable excuse,
whether a reasonable excuse exists;

212.2.c

in a case where a monetary penalty has not been paid (or paid in full),
whether to start proceedings for recovery of the penalty.

212.3

Guidance under  subsection (1)  may include information about any other
matters in connection with the carrying out of direct enforcement functions,
including the factors that the CMA will take into account in determining
whether to give a notice to a person in the carrying out of those functions.

212.4

The CMA—

212.4.a

must keep the guidance under review, and

212.4.b

may from time to time revise or replace the guidance.

212.5

Before issuing the first guidance under  this section  the CMA must consult—

212.5.a

the Secretary of State, and

212.5.b

such other persons as the CMA considers appropriate.

212.6

The CMA must—

212.6.a

before publishing the first guidance under this section, obtain the approval
of the Secretary of State in respect of the proposed guidance;

212.6.b

before revising or replacing any guidance published under this section, inform
the Secretary of State of the proposed revision or replacement.

##### Defamation

213

For the purposes of the law relating to defamation, absolute privilege
attaches to anything done by the CMA in exercise of its functions under this
Part.

##### Minor and consequential amendments relating to this Part

214

Schedule 18  contains minor and consequential amendments relating to this
Part.

##### Transitional and saving provision relating to this Part

215

Schedule 19  contains transitional and saving provision relating to this Part.

216.2.a.2A

The Competition and Markets Authority may also enforce the provisions of this
Chapter.

;

in subsection (3) for “and (2)” substitute  “, (2) and (2A)” .

216.3

    The Competition and Markets Authority The Breaching of Limits on Ticket

.

#### Interpretation of Part

##### Supply of goods or digital content

217

217.1

This section  provides for how references to the supply of goods or digital
content are to be read for the purposes of  this Part .

217.2

References to a person who supplies goods or digital content are to be read as
including references to a person who seeks to supply goods or digital content
(and references to a person who receives goods or digital content are to be
read in a corresponding way).

217.3

The supply of goods includes, in relation to buildings and other structures,
construction of them by one person for another.

217.4

References to a person supplying goods under—

217.4.a

a hire-purchase agreement,

217.4.b

a credit-sale agreement, or

217.4.c

a conditional sale agreement,

are to be read as including references to a person who conducts any antecedent
negotiations relating to the agreement.

217.5

The following terms have the meanings given by section 189(1) of the Consumer
Credit Act 1974—

      “ antecedent negotiations ”;           “ conditional sale agreement ”;
“ credit sale agreement ”;           “ hire-purchase agreement ”.

##### Supply of services

218

218.1

This section  provides for how references to the supply of services are to be
read for the purposes of  this Part .

218.2

References to a person who supplies services are to be read as including
references to a person who seeks to supply services (and references to a
person who receives services are to be read in a corresponding way).

218.3

The supply of services does not include the provision of services under a
contract of service or of apprenticeship.

218.4

It is immaterial whether the contract mentioned in  subsection (3) —

218.4.a

is express or implied, or

218.4.b

if express, is oral or in writing.

218.5

The supply of services includes—

218.5.a

performing for gain or reward any activity other than the supply of goods or
digital content;

218.5.b

rendering services to order;

218.5.c

the provision of services by making them available to potential users;

218.5.d

making arrangements for sharing the use of electronic communications apparatus
by means of a relevant agreement, within the meaning of paragraph 18 of
Schedule 3A to the Communications Act 2003 (the electronic communications
code);

218.5.e

agreeing to the full or partial settlement of a consumer’s liabilities or
purported liabilities in return for the consumer meeting a demand for payment.

##### Accessories

219

219.1

This section  applies for the purposes of  this Part .

219.2

A person (“ A ”) is an accessory to a commercial practice of another person (“
B ”) if—

219.2.a

B is a body corporate,

219.2.b

A has a special relationship with B,

219.2.c

the commercial practice is one that B has engaged in or is engaging in, and

219.2.d

the commercial practice takes place with the consent or connivance of A.

##### Special relationships

220

220.1

This section  applies for the purposes of  this Part .

220.2

A person has a special relationship with a body corporate if the person is—

220.2.a

a controller of the body corporate, or

220.2.b

a director, manager, secretary or other similar officer of the body corporate
or a person purporting to act in such a capacity.

220.3

A person is a controller of a body corporate if—

220.3.a

the directors of the body corporate, or of another body corporate which is its
controller, are accustomed to act in accordance with the person’s directions
or instructions, or

220.3.b

either alone or with one or more associates, the person is entitled to
exercise or control the exercise of one third or more of the voting power at
any general meeting of the body corporate or of another body corporate which
is its controller.

220.4

A person (“ P ”) is an associate of an individual if—

220.4.a

P is the spouse or civil partner of the individual;

220.4.b

P is a relative of the individual;

220.4.c

P is a relative of the individual’s spouse or civil partner;

220.4.d

P is the spouse or civil partner of a relative of the individual;

220.4.e

P is a spouse or civil partner of a relative of the individual’s spouse or
civil partner;

220.4.f

P lives in the same household as the individual otherwise than merely because
P, or the individual, is the other’s employer, tenant, lodger or boarder;

220.4.g

P is the relative of a person who is an associate of the individual by virtue
of  paragraph (f) ;

220.4.h

P has at some time in the past fallen within any of  paragraphs (a)  to  (g) ;

220.4.i

P is in partnership with the individual;

220.4.j

the individual is an associate of an individual with whom P is in partnership.

220.5

A person (“ P ”) is an associate of a body corporate if—

220.5.a

P is a controller of the body corporate, or

220.5.b

P is an associate of a person who is a controller of the body corporate.

220.6

A body corporate is an associate of another body corporate if—

220.6.a

the same person is a controller of both;

220.6.b

a person (“ P ”) is a controller of one and persons who are P’s associates are
controllers of the other;

220.6.c

a person (“ P ”) is a controller of one and P and persons who are P’s
associates are controllers of the other;

220.6.d

a group of two or more persons is a controller of each company and the groups
consist of the same persons;

220.6.e

a group of two or more persons is a controller of each company and the groups
may be regarded as consisting of the same persons by treating (in one or more
cases) a member of either group as replaced by a person of whom that person is
an associate.

220.7

In  this section  “ relative ” means a brother, sister, uncle, aunt, nephew,
niece, lineal ancestor or lineal descendant.

##### Enhanced consumer measures

221

221.1

References in  this Part  to “enhanced consumer measures” are references to—

221.1.a

redress measures (see  subsection (2) ),

221.1.b

compliance measures (see  subsection (3) ), or

221.1.c

choice measures (see  subsection (4) ).

221.2

Redress measures are—

221.2.a

measures offering compensation or other redress to affected consumers;

221.2.b

in cases where the commercial practice constituting a relevant infringement
relates to a contract, measures enabling affected consumers the option to
terminate (but not vary) the contract;

221.2.c

in cases where the affected consumers cannot be identified, or cannot be
identified without disproportionate cost to the person giving the undertaking
in question or against whom the order in question is made, measures intended
to be in the collective interests of consumers.

221.3

Compliance measures are measures intended to prevent, or reduce the risk of
the occurrence or repetition of, the infringing conduct (which may include
measures imposed for the purpose of improving compliance with consumer law
more generally).

221.4

Choice measures are measures intended to enable consumers to choose more
effectively between persons supplying goods, services or digital content.

221.5

In  this section —

221.5.a

references to affected consumers are references to consumers who have suffered
loss as a result of the infringing conduct or who have otherwise been affected
in any other way by the conduct;

221.5.b

references to the “ infringing conduct ” are to the conduct that has given
rise to the enforcement order or undertaking concerned.

##### Other interpretative provisions

222

In  this Part —

      “ business ” includes—         a trade, craft or profession,
any other undertaking carried on for gain or reward, and           the
activities of any government department or local or public authority;
“ enforcement order ” means an order made under  section 156 ;           “
enforcer ” means a public designated enforcer or a private designated
enforcer;           “ goods ” includes—         immoveable property, and
rights and obligations;                 “ interim enforcement order ” means an
order made under  section 159 ;           “ interim online interface order ”
means an order made under  section 162 ;           “ online interface order ”
means an order made under  section 161 ;           “ subsidiary ” has the
meaning given by section 1159 of the Companies Act 2006;           “ supply ”
includes supply by means of sale, lease, hire or hire purchase.
