### Consumer rights and disputes

#### Protection from unfair trading

##### Introduction

###### Overview

224

224.1

This Chapter confers protections on consumers from unfair commercial
practices.

224.2

Section  225  sets out what are unfair commercial practices and prohibits the
use and promotion of them.

224.3

Sections  226  to  230  provide more detail about commercial practices which
are unfair because they are misleading, aggressive or omit material
information, or because they contravene the requirements of professional
diligence.

224.4

Section  231  requires, or confers power on, specified public bodies to
enforce the prohibitions in section  225 .

224.5

Sections  232  to  235  confer rights on consumers in relation to unfair
commercial practices and make related provision.

224.6

Section  236  sets out what happens when a trader supplies a product to a
consumer that the consumer has not requested.

224.7

Sections  237  to  241  create criminal offences in relation to unfair
commercial practices and make related provision.

224.8

Sections  242  to  252  contain miscellaneous and interpretative provisions in
relation to this Chapter.

##### Prohibition of unfair commercial practices

###### Prohibition of unfair commercial practices

225

225.1

Unfair commercial practices are prohibited.

225.2

The promotion of unfair commercial practices in, or in connection with, a code
of conduct by—

225.2.a

a person responsible for the content of a code of conduct, or

225.2.b

a person responsible for monitoring compliance with a code of conduct,

is prohibited.

225.3

In this Chapter—

      “ commercial practice ” means an act or omission by a trader relating to
the promotion or supply of—         the trader’s product to a consumer,
another trader’s product to a consumer, or           a consumer’s product to
the trader or another person;                 “ consumer ” means an individual
acting for purposes that are wholly or mainly outside the individual’s
business;           “ trader ” means—         a person (“ P ”) acting for
purposes relating to P’s business, or           a person acting in the name
of, or on behalf of, P for purposes relating to P’s business.

225.4

A commercial practice is unfair if—

225.4.a

it is likely to cause the average consumer to take a transactional decision
that the consumer would not have taken otherwise as a result of the practice
involving one or more of the following—

225.4.a.i

a misleading action (see section  226 );

225.4.a.ii

a misleading omission (see section  227 );

225.4.a.iii

an aggressive practice (see section  228 );

225.4.a.iv

a contravention of the requirements of professional diligence (see section
229 ),

225.4.b

it omits material information from an invitation to purchase (see section  230
), or

225.4.c

it is listed in  Schedule 20  (commercial practices which are in all
circumstances considered unfair).

225.5

It is immaterial for the purposes of the definition of “commercial practice”
in subsection  (3)  whether the act or omission takes place—

225.5.a

at the time of the promotion or supply in question, or

225.5.b

before or after that time.

225.6

It is immaterial for the purposes of the definition of “trader” in subsection
(3) —

225.6.a

in relation to paragraph (a) of that definition, whether P is acting
personally or through another person acting in P’s name or on P’s behalf;

225.6.b

in relation to paragraph (b) of that definition, whether or not the purposes
relating to P’s business are the only or main purposes for which the person is
acting.

###### Misleading actions

226

226.1

For the purposes of this Chapter, a commercial practice involves a misleading
action if the practice involves—

226.1.a

the provision of false or misleading information relating to a product, a
trader or any other matter relevant to a transactional decision,

226.1.b

an overall presentation which is likely to deceive the average consumer about
a matter relating to a product, a trader or any other matter relevant to a
transactional decision,

226.1.c

any marketing of a product which creates confusion, or is likely to create
confusion, with any product, trade mark, trade name or other distinguishing
mark of another trader, or

226.1.d

a failure to comply with a requirement in a code of conduct to which
subsection  (5)  applies in circumstances where the trader asserts that the
trader acts in compliance with that code.

226.2

In subsection  (1) (a) , the reference to misleading information includes a
reference to information which, although true, is presented in a misleading
way.

226.3

For the purposes of subsection  (1) (b) , an overall presentation may be
deceiving even if the information it contains is true.

226.4

In subsection  (1) (c) , the reference to another trader is a reference to a
trader other than the trader supplying the product that is being marketed.

226.5

This subsection applies to a requirement in a code of conduct if—

226.5.a

there is no discretion afforded to the trader in relation to the requirement,
and

226.5.b

compliance with the requirement is capable of being verified.

###### Misleading omissions

227

227.1

For the purposes of this Chapter, a commercial practice involves a misleading
omission if, considering the matters mentioned in subsection  (3) , the
practice—

227.1.a

omits material information,

227.1.b

omits information which the trader is required under any other enactment to
give to a consumer as part of the practice, or

227.1.c

fails to identify its commercial intent (unless it is already apparent from
the context).

227.2

In subsection  (1) (a) , “ material information ” means information that the
average consumer needs to take an informed transactional decision.

227.3

The matters referred to in subsection  (1)  are—

227.3.a

any limitations resulting from the means of communication used in the
commercial practice (including limitations of space or time), and

227.3.b

any steps taken by the trader to overcome those limitations by providing
information by other means.

227.4

In this section, references to omitting information include providing
information—

227.4.a

in a way that is unclear or untimely, or

227.4.b

in such a way that the consumer is unlikely to see it.

###### Aggressive practices

228

228.1

For the purposes of this Chapter, a commercial practice involves an aggressive
practice if it uses harassment, coercion or undue influence.

228.2

In determining whether a commercial practice uses harassment, coercion or
undue influence, account must be taken of—

228.2.a

the nature of the practice;

228.2.b

the timing and location of the practice;

228.2.c

whether the practice involves the use of any threatening or abusive language
or behaviour;

228.2.d

whether the practice exploits any vulnerability of a consumer (including any
vulnerability of a kind mentioned in  section 247 (4) );

228.2.e

whether the practice involves a threat to take action which cannot legally be
taken;

228.2.f

whether the practice requires a consumer to take onerous or disproportionate
action in order to exercise rights that the consumer has in relation to a
product.

228.3

In this section—

228.3.a

“ coercion ” includes the use or threat of physical force;

228.3.b

“ undue influence ” means exploiting a position of power in relation to a
consumer so as to apply pressure in a way which significantly limits the
consumer’s ability to make an informed decision.

###### Contravention of the requirements of professional diligence

229

For the purposes of this Chapter, a commercial practice involves a
contravention of the requirements of professional diligence if the practice
falls short of the standard of skill and care which a trader may reasonably be
expected to exercise towards consumers which is commensurate with either—

229.a

honest market practice in the trader’s field of activity, or

229.b

the general principle of good faith in the trader’s field of activity.

###### Omission of material information from invitation to purchase

230

230.1

For the purposes of this Chapter, a commercial practice which is an invitation
to purchase omits material information if, considering the matters mentioned
in subsection  (8) , it omits any of the information which is—

230.1.a

set out in subsection  (2) , and

230.1.b

not already apparent from the context.

230.2

The information referred to in subsection  (1)  is—

230.2.a

the main characteristics of the product (to the extent appropriate considering
the means used to communicate the invitation to purchase and the nature of the
product);

230.2.b

the total price of the product (so far as paragraph  (c)  does not apply);

230.2.c

if, owing to the nature of the product, the whole or any part of the total
price cannot reasonably be calculated in advance, how the price (or that part
of it) will be calculated;

230.2.d

the identity of the trader and the identity of any other person on whose
behalf the trader is acting;

230.2.e

the business address and, if different, the service address of the trader and
any business email address of the trader;

230.2.f

in relation to any other person on whose behalf the trader is acting—

230.2.f.i

the person’s business address and business email address (if the person has
such addresses), and

230.2.f.ii

if different to the person’s business address, the person’s service address;

230.2.g

any freight, delivery or postal charges, including any taxes, not included in
the total price of the product but which the consumer may choose to incur (or
where those additional charges or taxes cannot reasonably be calculated in
advance, the fact that they may be payable);

230.2.h

for products involving a right of withdrawal or cancellation, the existence of
such a right;

230.2.i

to the extent that the trader’s practice in relation to any of the
arrangements mentioned in subsection  (3)  departs from the trader’s published
practice in relation to those arrangements, the practice which the trader is
currently operating;

230.2.j

any information which the trader is required under any other enactment to give
to a consumer as part of an invitation to purchase.

230.3

The arrangements referred to in subsection  (2) (i)  are—

230.3.a

the arrangements for payment;

230.3.b

the arrangements for delivery of the product;

230.3.c

the arrangements for performance;

230.3.d

the arrangements for handling complaints.

230.4

For the purposes of subsection  (2) (b)  the total price of a product includes
any fees, taxes, charges or other payments that the consumer will necessarily
incur if the consumer purchases the product.

230.5

For the purposes of subsection  (2) (c)  (and subject to the matters mentioned
in subsection  (8) ) the information given must—

230.5.a

be such that it enables the consumer to calculate the total price, and

230.5.b

be set out with as much prominence as any information that is set out in
compliance with  subsection (2) (b) .

230.6

For the purposes of  subsection (2) (d)  “ identity ”, in relation to a
trader, means—

230.6.a

the name of the trader, and

230.6.b

if different, the name under which the trader trades.

230.7

For the purposes of  subsection (2) (e) —

      “ business address ”, in relation to a person, means—         where the
person is a body corporate, the address of its registered or principal office,
where the person is a firm that is not a body corporate, the address of the
principal office of the firm, or           in a case where neither paragraph
(a) or (b) applies, the address of the person’s principal place of business;
“ business email address ”, in relation to a person, means any email address
used by the person for conducting business;           “ service address ”, in
relation to a person, means the address at which the person will accept
service of documents.

230.8

The matters referred to in subsection  (1)  are—

230.8.a

any limitations resulting from the means of communication used in the
commercial practice (including limitations of space or time), and

230.8.b

any steps taken by the trader to overcome those limitations by providing
information by other means.

230.9

In this section, references to omitting information include providing
information—

230.9.a

in a way that is unclear or untimely, or

230.9.b

in such a way that the consumer is unlikely to see it.

230.10

In this Chapter, “ invitation to purchase ” means a commercial practice
involving the provision of information to a consumer—

230.10.a

which indicates the characteristics of a product and its price, and

230.10.b

which enables, or purports to enable, the consumer to decide whether to
purchase the product or take another transactional decision in relation to the
product.

##### Public enforcement

###### Public enforcement

231

231.1

It is the duty of every local weights and measures authority in Great Britain
to enforce in its area the prohibitions in section  225 .

231.2

It is the duty of the Department for the Economy in Northern Ireland to
enforce the prohibitions in section  225  in Northern Ireland.

231.3

The CMA may also enforce the provisions of this Chapter.

231.4

In exercising functions under this section, every local weights and measures
authority in Great Britain, the Department for the Economy in Northern Ireland
and the CMA must have regard to the desirability of encouraging control of
unfair commercial practices by such established means as it considers
appropriate having regard to all the circumstances of the particular case.

231.5

Nothing in this section authorises a local weights and measures authority in
Great Britain to bring proceedings in Scotland for an offence.

##### Consumers’ rights of redress relating to unfair commercial practices

###### Rights of redress

232

232.1

A consumer has rights of redress under this Chapter if each of the following
four conditions is met.

232.2

The first condition is that—

232.2.a

the consumer enters into a contract with a trader under which the trader
supplies a product to the consumer (a “business-to-consumer contract”),

232.2.b

the consumer enters into a contract with a trader under which—

232.2.b.i

the consumer supplies a product to the trader, and

232.2.b.ii

the trader does not supply a product to the consumer (a “consumer-to-business
contract”), or

232.2.c

the consumer makes a payment to the trader for the supply of a product (a
“consumer payment”).

232.3

The second condition is that—

232.3.a

the trader engages in a prohibited practice in relation to the product, or

232.3.b

in a case where a consumer enters into a business-to-consumer contract for
goods or digital content—

232.3.b.i

a producer engages in a prohibited practice in relation to the goods or
digital content, and

232.3.b.ii

when the contract is entered into, the trader is aware of the commercial
practice that constitutes the prohibited practice or could reasonably be
expected to be aware of it.

232.4

The third condition is that the prohibited practice is a significant factor in
the consumer’s decision—

232.4.a

to enter into the contract mentioned in subsection  (2) (a)  or (b), or

232.4.b

to make the payment mentioned in subsection  (2) (c) .

232.5

The fourth condition is that the product concerned is not a product excluded
from the application of rights of redress by regulations under section  233 .

232.6

In subsection  (3) , “ producer ” means—

232.6.a

a manufacturer of the goods or digital content,

232.6.b

an importer of the goods or digital content into the United Kingdom, or

232.6.c

a person purporting to be such a manufacturer or importer by placing the
person’s name, trade mark or other distinctive sign on the goods or by using
it in connection with the digital content,

and includes a producer acting personally or through another person acting in
the producer’s name or on the producer’s behalf.

232.7

In this Chapter, “ prohibited practice ” means an unfair commercial practice
involving—

232.7.a

a misleading action, or

232.7.b

an aggressive practice.

232.8

For the purposes of  subsection (7) , section  225 (4) (a)  applies as if the
reference to a transactional decision were a reference to any decision taken
by a consumer to—

232.8.a

enter into a business-to-consumer contract,

232.8.b

enter into a consumer-to-business contract, or

232.8.c

make a consumer payment.

###### Rights of redress: further provision

233

233.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations provide for any of the following
descriptions of rights to be exercisable by a consumer who has rights of
redress under this Chapter—

233.1.a

a right to unwind in respect of a relevant contract or consumer payment;

233.1.b

a right to a discount in respect of a supply of a product under a relevant
contract;

233.1.c

a right to damages in respect of financial loss, distress or physical
inconvenience or discomfort.

233.2

Regulations under this section may include provision—

233.2.a

about how a right is to be exercised by the consumer;

233.2.b

for an amount of discount mentioned in subsection  (1) (b)  to be determined
in accordance with the regulations;

233.2.c

about the circumstances in which damages mentioned in  subsection (1) (c)  are
or are not payable;

233.2.d

imposing conditions or restrictions on the exercise of a right;

233.2.e

about the consequences of the exercise of a right;

233.2.f

excluding products of a description specified in the regulations from the
application of the rights of redress available under this Chapter.

233.3

Provision under  subsection (2) (e)  about the consequences of the exercise of
a right may (among other things)—

233.3.a

provide for the termination of a relevant contract;

233.3.b

require the trader to make a refund of an amount determined in accordance with
the regulations;

233.3.c

require goods supplied under a relevant contract to be returned or for payment
to be made in respect of such goods.

233.4

In this section, “ relevant contract ” means—

233.4.a

a business-to-consumer contract;

233.4.b

a consumer-to-business contract.

233.5

Regulations under this section are subject to the affirmative procedure.

###### Enforcement of rights of redress

234

234.1

A consumer with a right to unwind, a right to a discount or a right to damages
by virtue of regulations under section  233  may bring a claim in civil
proceedings to enforce that right.

234.2

In Scotland, proceedings to enforce a right to unwind may be brought before
the Sheriff or the Court of Session.

234.3

If in proceedings under this section the consumer establishes that the
consumer has one of the rights mentioned in subsection  (1) , the court must
make an order that gives effect to—

234.3.a

that right, and

234.3.b

any associated obligations of the consumer imposed by regulations under
section  233 .

234.4

The Limitation Act 1980 applies to a claim under this section in England and
Wales as if it were an action founded on simple contract.

234.5

The Limitation (Northern Ireland) Order 1989 ( S.I. 1989/1339 (N.I. 11))
applies to a claim under this section in Northern Ireland as if it were an
action founded on simple contract.

###### Relationship between rights of redress and other claims relating to prohibited practices

235

235.1

Nothing in this Chapter affects the ability of a consumer to make a claim
under a rule of law or equity, or under an enactment, in respect of conduct
constituting a prohibited practice.

235.2

But a consumer may not—

235.2.a

make a claim to be compensated under a rule of law or equity, or under an
enactment, in respect of such conduct if the consumer has been compensated in
respect of the conduct by virtue of regulations under section  233 , or

235.2.b

make a claim to be compensated under this Chapter in respect of such conduct
if the consumer has been compensated under a rule of law or equity, or under
an enactment, in respect of the conduct.

##### Inertia selling

###### Inertia selling

236

236.1

This section applies where a trader engages in the unfair commercial practice
described at paragraph  31  of  Schedule 20 .

236.2

The consumer is exempted from any obligation to pay for (or provide any other
consideration for) the products supplied by the trader.

236.3

In the case of a supply of goods that has not been requested, the consumer
may, as between the consumer and the trader, use, deal with or dispose of the
goods as if they were an unconditional gift to the consumer.

236.4

The absence of a response from a consumer following the supply of the product
does not constitute consent from the consumer to comply with the trader’s
demand for the consumer to—

236.4.a

pay for the product;

236.4.b

return the product;

236.4.c

safely store the product.

##### Offences relating to unfair commercial practices

###### Offences

237

237.1

A trader commits an offence if, in breach of section  225 (1) , the trader
engages in an unfair commercial practice which involves a misleading action
within section  226 (1) (a) ,  (b)  or  (c)  (see section  225 (4) (a) (i) ).

237.2

A trader commits an offence if, in breach of section  225 (1) , the trader
engages in an unfair commercial practice which involves a misleading omission
(see section  225 (4) (a) (ii) ).

237.3

A trader commits an offence if, in breach of section  225 (1) , the trader
engages in an unfair commercial practice which involves an aggressive practice
(see section  225 (4) (a) (iii) ).

237.4

A trader commits an offence if, in breach of section  225 (1) —

237.4.a

the trader engages in an unfair commercial practice which involves a
contravention of the requirements of professional diligence (see section  225
(4) (a) (iv) ), and

237.4.b

the trader knows, or is reckless as to whether, the commercial practice
involves a contravention of the requirements of professional diligence.

237.5

For the purposes of subsection  (4)  a trader who fails to have regard to
whether a commercial practice involves a contravention of the requirements of
professional diligence is to be treated as being reckless as to whether it
does (regardless of whether the trader has reason to believe that it might).

237.6

A trader commits an offence if, in breach of section  225 (1) , the trader
engages in an unfair commercial practice by omitting material information from
an invitation to purchase (see section  225 (4) (b) ).

237.7

A trader commits an offence if, in breach of section  225 (1) , the trader
engages in a commercial practice which is unfair by virtue of it being of a
description listed in  Schedule 20  (see section  225 (4) (c) ) other than an
excluded description.

237.8

The following are excluded descriptions for the purposes of subsection  (7) —

237.8.a

the description of practice mentioned in paragraph  12  of  Schedule 20 ;

237.8.b

the descriptions of practices mentioned in  paragraph 13  of that Schedule;

237.8.c

the description of practice mentioned in paragraph  30  of that Schedule.

###### Defence of due diligence and innocent publication

238

238.1

It is a defence for a person (“ the defendant ”) charged with an offence under
subsection  (1) ,  (2) ,  (3) ,  (6)  or  (7)  of section  237  to prove—

238.1.a

that the commission of the offence was due to—

238.1.a.i

the act or omission of another person,

238.1.a.ii

reliance on information given by another person,

238.1.a.iii

a mistake or accident, or

238.1.a.iv

another cause beyond the defendant’s control, and

238.1.b

that the defendant took all reasonable precautions and exercised all due
diligence to avoid the commission of such an offence by the defendant or any
other person under the defendant’s control.

238.2

Subsection  (3)  applies in a case where a person (“ the defendant ”) has been
charged with an offence under subsection (1), (2), (3), (6) or (7) of section
237  alleged to have been committed by the publication of an advertisement.

238.3

It is a defence for the defendant to prove that—

238.3.a

the defendant’s business is to publish or arrange for the publication of
advertisements,

238.3.b

the defendant received the advertisement for publication in the ordinary
course of business, and

238.3.c

the defendant did not know and had no reason to suspect that its publication
would amount to the offence with which the defendant is charged.

238.4

A defendant is not entitled to rely on the defence provided by subsection  (1)
by reason of the matters referred to in  paragraph (a) (i)  or  (a) (ii)  of
that subsection without the permission of the court unless—

238.4.a

the defendant has served on the prosecutor a notice in writing giving such
information as was then in the defendant’s possession identifying, or
assisting in the identification of, the other person, and

238.4.b

the notice is served on the prosecutor at least seven clear days before the
hearing of the proceedings or, in Scotland, at least seven clear days before
the trial diet.

238.5

In subsection  (3) , “advertisement”—

238.5.a

means anything published (in any form) for the purpose of promoting a product
to the public or a section of the public, and

238.5.b

includes a catalogue, a circular and a price list.

###### Offences: criminal liability of others

239

239.1

Subsections  (2)  and  (3)  apply where a trader—

239.1.a

commits an offence under subsection (1), (2), (3), (6) or (7) of section  237
, or

239.1.b

would have committed an offence under that subsection but for a defence under
section  238 ,

and the commission of the offence, or of what would have been the offence, is
due to the act or omission of another person “P”.

239.2

P commits the offence (whether or not P is a trader and whether or not P’s act
or omission is a commercial practice).

239.3

P may be charged with and convicted of the offence by virtue of subsection
(2)  whether or not proceedings are taken against the trader.

239.4

In other provisions of this Chapter (including the rest of this section),
references to an offence under subsection (1), (2), (3), (6) or (7) of section
237  include references to an offence under that subsection by virtue of
subsection  (2) .

239.5

If an offence under section  237  committed by a body corporate is proved—

239.5.a

to have been committed with the consent or connivance of an officer of the
body, or

239.5.b

to be attributable to any neglect on the part of an officer,

the officer as well as the body corporate is guilty of the offence and liable
to be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

239.6

If the affairs of a body corporate are managed by its members, subsection  (5)
applies in relation to the acts and defaults of a member in connection with
the member’s functions of management as if the member were an officer of the
body corporate.

239.7

If an offence under section  237  committed by a Scottish partnership is
proved—

239.7.a

to have been committed with the consent or connivance of a partner, or

239.7.b

to be attributable to any neglect on the part of a partner,

the partner as well as the partnership is guilty of the offence and liable to
be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

239.8

In other provisions of this Chapter, references to an offence under section
237  include references to an offence under that section by virtue of
subsection  (5)  or  (7) .

239.9

In subsection  (5)  a reference to an officer of a body corporate includes a
reference to—

239.9.a

a director, manager, secretary or other similar officer, or

239.9.b

a person purporting to act as a director, manager, secretary or other similar
officer.

239.10

In subsection  (7) , a reference to a partner includes a person purporting to
act as a partner.

###### Penalty for offences

240

A person guilty of an offence under section  237  is liable—

240.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to a fine;

240.b

on summary conviction in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding
the statutory maximum;

240.c

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or to a fine (or both).

###### Time limit for prosecution

241

241.1

No proceedings for an offence under section  237  may be commenced after the
earlier of—

241.1.a

the end of the period of 3 years beginning with the date of the commission of
the offence, or

241.1.b

the end of the period of 1 year beginning with the date of discovery of the
offence by the prosecutor.

241.2

For the purposes of subsection  (1) (b) —

241.2.a

a certificate signed by or on behalf of the prosecutor and stating the date on
which the prosecutor discovered the offence is conclusive evidence of that
fact, and

241.2.b

a certificate stating that matter and purporting to be so signed is to be
treated as so signed unless the contrary is proved.

##### Miscellaneous

###### Powers to amend this Chapter

242

242.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend  Schedule 20  (commercial
practices which are in all circumstances considered unfair) so as to—

242.1.a

add a description of a commercial practice;

242.1.b

remove a description of a commercial practice;

242.1.c

amend a description of a commercial practice.

242.2

If regulations under subsection  (1)  amend  Schedule 20  so as to add a
description of a commercial practice, the regulations must also amend section
237 (8)  so as to make that practice an excluded description of practice.

242.3

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend section  232 (7)  (rights of
redress: prohibited practices) so as to—

242.3.a

add further commercial practices that are unfair under this Chapter to the
list of prohibited practices;

242.3.b

remove from the list of prohibited practices any commercial practices that
have been added by regulations.

242.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend section  230 (2)  (material
information in respect of an invitation to purchase) so as to—

242.4.a

add descriptions of information;

242.4.b

modify descriptions of information;

242.4.c

remove descriptions of information added by regulations under this subsection.

242.5

Before making regulations under this section, the Secretary of State must
consult such persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

242.6

Regulations under this section are subject to the affirmative procedure.

###### Crown application

243

243.1

Subject to subsection  (2) , this Chapter binds the Crown.

243.2

The Crown is not criminally liable as a result of anything in this Chapter.

243.3

Subsection  (2)  does not affect the application of any provision of this
Chapter in relation to persons in the public service of the Crown.

###### Validity of agreements

244

Except as resulting from a consumer’s rights of redress under this Chapter, a
contract or any other agreement is not void or unenforceable by reason only of
a breach of the prohibition in section  225 (1)  or  (2)  (prohibition of
unfair commercial practices or the promotion of unfair commercial practices).

##### Interpretation

###### Meaning of “transactional decision”

245

In this Chapter, “ transactional decision ” means any decision made by a
consumer relating to—

245.a

the purchase or supply of a product (including whether, how or on what terms
to make the purchase or supply);

245.b

the retention, disposal or withdrawal of a product (including whether, how or
on what terms to retain or dispose of it);

245.c

the exercise of contractual rights in relation to a product (including
whether, how or on what terms to exercise such rights).

###### Meaning of “average consumer”: general

246

246.1

This section provides for how references to the average consumer are to be
read for the purposes of this Chapter.

246.2

The average consumer is—

246.2.a

reasonably well informed,

246.2.b

reasonably observant, and

246.2.c

reasonably circumspect.

246.3

The average consumer is to be treated as not knowing information in relation
to a commercial practice where such information has been concealed by the
trader (even if the average consumer might know the information from another
source).

246.4

Where a commercial practice is directed at a particular group, the average
consumer is an average member of that group (and the attributes of the average
consumer in subsection  (2)  are to be read accordingly).

246.5

This section is subject to  section 247 .

###### Meaning of “average consumer”: vulnerable persons

247

247.1

Subsection  (2)  applies where a group of consumers is particularly vulnerable
to a commercial practice in a way that the trader could reasonably be expected
to foresee.

247.2

References in this Chapter to the average consumer, so far as relating to
cases to which this subsection applies, are to be read as references to an
average member of the group mentioned in subsection  (1)  (and the attributes
of the average consumer in  section 246 (2)  are to be read accordingly).

247.3

For the purposes of subsection  (1) , the reference to a group of consumers
being particularly vulnerable to a commercial practice—

247.3.a

is a reference to the members of the group being particularly vulnerable to
the commercial practice causing them to take a transactional decision that
they would not have taken otherwise, and

247.3.b

includes a reference to a group of consumers being vulnerable to a practice
because of the product to which it relates.

247.4

For the purposes of subsection  (1) , a group of consumers may be vulnerable
as a result of (among other things)—

247.4.a

their age;

247.4.b

their physical or mental health;

247.4.c

their credulity;

247.4.d

the circumstances they are in.

###### Meaning of “product”

248

248.1

In this Chapter, “ product ” means—

248.1.a

goods;

248.1.b

a service;

248.1.c

digital content.

248.2

For the purposes of this Chapter, a trader agreeing to the full or partial
settlement of a consumer’s liabilities or purported liabilities in return for
the consumer meeting a demand for payment is supplying a service.

###### General interpretation

249

In this Chapter—

      “ business ” includes—         a trade, craft or profession,
any other undertaking carried on for gain or reward, and           the
activities of any government department or local or public authority;
“ code of conduct ” means an agreement or set of rules which defines the
behaviour of traders who choose to be bound by it;           “ goods ”
includes—         immoveable property, and           rights and obligations,
but includes water, gas and electricity only if they are put up for sale in a
limited volume or set quantity;           “ supply ”, in relation to a
product, includes supply by means of sale, lease, hire or hire purchase.

###### Index of defined terms

250

In this Chapter, the expressions listed in the left-hand column have the
meaning given by, or are to be interpreted in accordance with, the provisions
listed in the right-hand column.

    Expression Provision   Aggressive practice Section  228   Average consumer
