##### Consequential amendments and transitional provision

###### Consequential amendments relating to this Chapter

251

251.1

The Consumer Protection from Unfair Trading Regulations 2008 ( S.I. 2008/1277
) are revoked.

251.2

Schedule 21  contains further consequential amendments relating to this
Chapter.

###### Transitional and saving provision relating to this Chapter

252

252.1

This Chapter applies only in relation to an act or omission which takes place
on or after the commencement date.

252.2

The CPUTR 2008 continue to have effect in relation to any act or omission
which takes place before the commencement date.

252.3

In this section—

      “ the commencement date ” means—         for the purposes of the saving
by subsection  (2)  of Part 4A of the CPUTR 2008 (and other provisions of
those Regulations so far as relating to that Part), the date on which the
first regulations made under section  233  come into force;           for all
other purposes, the date on which section  225  comes into force;
“ CPUTR 2008 ” means the Consumer Protection from Unfair Trading Regulations
2008 ( S.I. 2008/1277 ).

#### Subscription contracts

##### Introduction

###### Overview

253

253.1

This Chapter—

253.1.a

imposes duties on traders in relation to subscription contracts,

253.1.b

provides rights for consumers if those duties are breached, and

253.1.c

provides rights for consumers to cancel subscription contracts during cooling-
off periods.

253.2

Sections  254  and  255  set out what is a “ subscription contract ” for the
purposes of this Chapter.

253.3

Sections  256  to  261  impose duties on traders in relation to subscription
contracts.

253.4

Sections  262  and  263  provide rights for consumers to cancel subscription
contracts if traders breach those duties.

253.5

Sections  264  to  266  provide rights for consumers to cancel subscription
contracts during cooling-off periods.

253.6

Section  267  confers powers to make further provision about the cancellation
of subscription contracts under this Chapter.

253.7

Sections  268  to  271  make provision for the offence of failing to provide
information about cooling-off rights.

253.8

Sections  272  to  281  contain miscellaneous provisions in relation to this
Chapter.

###### Meaning of “subscription contract”

254

254.1

For the purposes of this Chapter, a subscription contract is a contract
between a trader and a consumer—

254.1.a

for the supply of goods, services or digital content by the trader to the
consumer in exchange for payment by the consumer,

254.1.b

to which either or both of subsections  (2)  and  (3)  apply, and

254.1.c

which is not an excluded contract (see section  255 ).

254.2

This subsection applies to a contract if it contains terms which have the
effect of providing—

254.2.a

for an automatically recurring, or continuing, supply of goods, services or
digital content to the consumer for an indefinite period or a fixed period,

254.2.b

for the consumer to automatically incur liability for each supply, or
recurring liabilities for the continuing supply, and

254.2.c

a right for the consumer to bring the contract to an end.

254.3

This subsection applies to a contract if it contains terms which have the
effect of providing—

254.3.a

for a supply of goods, services or digital content to a consumer free of
charge, or at a rate specified in the contract (the “original rate”), for a
period specified in the contract,

254.3.b

for the consumer to become automatically liable for payments, or payments at a
rate higher than the original rate, for supplies after that period (including
where the trader has an option to impose a charge or a higher charge after the
end of the period), and

254.3.c

a right for the consumer to bring the contract to an end before such liability
is incurred.

254.4

In this Chapter, references to a consumer’s right to bring a subscription
contract to an end are references to a right provided under the contract
which—

254.4.a

in the case of a contract for a fixed period, may be exercised to bring the
contract to an end before the end of the fixed period;

254.4.b

in any case, may be exercised without the consumer incurring any penalty which
is more than nominal,

and include references to a right that is expressed in terms of a right to
stop a subscription contract from automatically renewing or continuing or any
other similar expression.

###### Excluded contracts

255

255.1

A contract is an excluded contract for the purposes of this Chapter if, and to
the extent that, it is of a description set out in  Schedule 22 .

255.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend  Schedule 22  so as to add,
remove or modify a description of a contract.

255.3

The power under subsection  (2)  includes power to provide for a contract to
be an excluded contract—

255.3.a

generally for the purposes of this Chapter, or

255.3.b

only for such purposes of this Chapter as are specified.

255.4

Regulations under subsection  (2)  are subject to the affirmative procedure.

255.5

See  section 275 (4)  to  (8)  for how this Chapter applies in relation to a
contract that—

255.5.a

was an excluded contract at the time it was entered into, and

255.5.b

on subsequently ceasing to be an excluded contract, becomes a subscription
contract.

##### Duties of traders

###### Pre-contract information

256

256.1

Before a trader enters into a subscription contract with a consumer, the
trader must—

256.1.a

give to the consumer the information set out in  Part 1  of  Schedule 23
(“key pre-contract information”), and

256.1.b

give, or make available, to the consumer the information set out in  Part 2
of  Schedule 23  (“full pre-contract information”).

256.2

The duty imposed by subsection  (1)  must be carried out—

256.2.a

as close in time to entering into the contract as is practicable,

256.2.b

in accordance with subsections  (3)  and  (4) , and

256.2.c

in accordance with any other requirements specified in regulations under
section  277 (1) (a) .

256.3

Key pre-contract information must be given under subsection  (1) (a)  in
accordance with the following requirements—

256.3.a

it must all be given together;

256.3.b

it must be given separately from the full pre-contract information and any
other information;

256.3.c

in relation to a contract entered into in person, it must be given in writing
and on a durable medium;

256.3.d

in relation to a contract entered into online and remotely (but not orally),
it must be given in writing and in such a way that the consumer is not
required to take any steps to read the information, other than the steps the
consumer must take to enter into the contract;

256.3.e

in relation to a contract entered into orally and remotely, it must be given
orally.

256.4

Full pre-contract information must be given, or made available, under
subsection  (1) (b)  in accordance with the following requirements—

256.4.a

it must all be given, or made available, together;

256.4.b

in relation to a contract entered into in person, it must be given in writing
and on a durable medium.

256.5

The duty under subsection  (1) (b)  to give, or make available, full pre-
contract information applies in relation to the information set out in
paragraphs  14  to  28  of  Schedule 23  only to the extent that the
information is applicable to the contract and not already apparent from the
context.

256.6

For the purposes of this section, information is made available to a consumer
only if the consumer can reasonably be expected to—

256.6.a

know how to access it, and

256.6.b

be able to access it;

256.7

For the purposes of this Chapter—

256.7.a

references to a contract being entered into in person are references to it
being entered into in the simultaneous physical presence of the trader and the
consumer;

256.7.b

references to a contract being entered into remotely are references to it
being entered into without the simultaneous physical presence of the trader
and the consumer.

256.8

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend Parts  1  and  2  of  Schedule
23  so as to add, modify or remove descriptions of information.

256.9

Regulations under subsection  (8)  are subject to the affirmative procedure.

###### Pre-contract information: additional requirements

257

257.1

Subsections  (2)  and  (3)  apply in relation to a subscription contract
entered into online.

257.2

The trader must ensure that the final step which the consumer is required to
take to enter into the contract involves the consumer expressly acknowledging
that the contract imposes an obligation on the consumer to make payments to
the trader.

257.3

The trader must ensure that the information mentioned in subsection  (4)  is
given to a consumer—

257.3.a

in writing and in such a way that the consumer is not required to take any
steps to read the information, other than the steps the consumer must take to
enter into the contract, and

257.3.b

in accordance with any other requirement specified in regulations under
section  277 (1) (a) .

257.4

The information referred to in subsection  (3)  is—

257.4.a

whether there are any restrictions on the delivery of the product to be
supplied under the contract, and

257.4.b

which means of payment are accepted in relation to the product.

257.5

If the trader does not comply with subsection  (2) , the consumer is not bound
by the subscription contract.

257.6

Subsection  (7)  applies in relation to a subscription contract entered into
orally and remotely.

257.7

If a trader contacts the consumer, the trader must, from the outset, disclose—

257.7.a

the trader’s identity,

257.7.b

where applicable, the identity of the person on whose behalf the trader is
making contact, and

257.7.c

the commercial purpose of making contact with the consumer.

257.8

In cases where—

257.8.a

the contract has been entered into in person, and

257.8.b

the consumer has signed the contract,

the trader must give to the consumer a copy of the signed contract immediately
after the consumer has signed the contract.

257.9

In cases where full pre-contract information has not been given under section
256 (1) (b)  in writing on a durable medium before the contract is entered
into, the trader must give the consumer that information in writing on a
durable medium as soon as reasonably practicable after the contract has been
entered into and—

257.9.a

where goods are to be supplied under the contract, before the supply of any
goods;

257.9.b

where services are to be supplied under the contract, before the supply of any
service.

###### Reminder notices

258

258.1

Where a trader enters into a subscription contract with a consumer that does
not include a concessionary period, the trader must give to the consumer a
notice (referred to in this Chapter as a “reminder notice”) in respect of each
renewal payment that relates to the end of a relevant six-month period.

258.2

A “ relevant six-month period ” for the purposes of subsection  (1)  is—

258.2.a

the period of 6 months beginning with the day after the day on which the
contract was entered into, and

258.2.b

each subsequent period of 6 months beginning with the day after the day on
which the consumer last became liable for a renewal payment in respect of
which a reminder notice was required under subsection  (1) .

258.3

Where a trader enters into a subscription contract with a consumer that
includes a concessionary period, the trader must give to the consumer a
reminder notice in respect of—

258.3.a

the first renewal payment for which the consumer will become liable under the
contract, and

258.3.b

each subsequent renewal payment that relates to the end of a relevant six-
month period.

258.4

A “ relevant six-month period ” for the purposes of subsection  (3)  is each
period of 6 months beginning with the day after the day on which the consumer
last became liable for a renewal payment in respect of which a reminder notice
was required under subsection  (3) .

258.5

A renewal payment “relates” to the end of a relevant six-month period for the
purposes of subsections  (1)  and  (3)  if—

258.5.a

it is the last (or only) renewal payment for which the consumer becomes liable
during that period, or

258.5.b

in a case where the consumer does not become liable for any renewal payment
during that period, it is the first renewal payment for which the consumer
becomes liable after the end of that period.

258.6

For the purposes of this section a subscription contract includes a
concessionary period if it is a contract to which section  254 (3)  applies.

258.7

In this Chapter, a “ renewal payment ”, in relation to a subscription
contract, means a payment for which the consumer could avoid liability by
exercising a right to bring the contract to an end.

258.8

Section  259  contains further provision about—

258.8.a

the contents of reminder notices,

258.8.b

the times at which they must be given, and

258.8.c

how they must be given.

258.9

The Secretary of State may by regulations provide for the requirements imposed
by this section and section  259 —

258.9.a

not to apply in relation to specified descriptions of traders or contracts;

258.9.b

to apply subject to modifications in relation to specified descriptions of
traders or contracts.

258.10

Regulations under subsection  (9)  are subject to the affirmative procedure.

###### Content and timing etc of reminder notices

259

259.1

A reminder notice must contain—

259.1.a

the information set out in  Part 3  of  Schedule 23 , and

259.1.b

any other information required by regulations under section  277 (1) (b) ,

and that information must be given to the consumer all together.

259.2

A reminder notice must be given—

259.2.a

in accordance with subsections  (3)  to  (8) ,

259.2.b

in such a way that the information referred to in  subsection (1)  is more
prominent than any other information given to the consumer at the same time,
and

259.2.c

in accordance with any other requirements specified in regulations under
section  277 (1) (a) .

259.3

A reminder notice must be given within the period specified by the trader for
the purposes of this section in the key pre-contract information given to the
consumer in relation to the contract (see  paragraph 10  of  Schedule 23 ).

259.4

A period specified in key pre-contract information for the purposes of this
section must be a period in advance of the last cancellation date which is
reasonable for the purposes of—

259.4.a

informing the consumer that they will soon become liable for the renewal
payment to which the notice relates, and

259.4.b

enabling the consumer to decide whether to bring the subscription contract to
an end before incurring that liability (and to take the necessary steps to do
so).

259.5

The “ last cancellation date ”, in relation to a reminder notice, means the
last day on which the consumer could avoid becoming liable for the renewal
payment to which the notice relates by exercising a right to bring the
contract to an end.

259.6

Where subsection  (7)  applies, in addition to giving a reminder notice in
accordance with subsection (3), an additional reminder notice must be given—

259.6.a

prior to the notice given in accordance with subsection (3), and

259.6.b

at a time which is reasonable for the purpose of providing additional
notification to the consumer that they will soon become liable for the renewal
payment to which the notice relates.

259.7

This subsection applies where—

259.7.a

the consumer will not become liable for a further renewal payment until after
the end of the 12-month period, or

259.7.b

the consumer will not become liable for any further renewal payment but the
contract continues beyond the end of the 12-month period.

259.8

In subsection  (7) , the “ 12-month period ” means the period of 12 months
beginning with the day before the day on which the consumer will become liable
for the renewal payment to which the reminder notice relates.

###### Arrangements for consumers to exercise right to end contract

260

260.1

A trader must make arrangements to enable a consumer to exercise a right to
bring a subscription contract to an end—

260.1.a

in a way which is straightforward, and

260.1.b

without having to take any steps which are not reasonably necessary for
bringing the contract to an end.

260.2

A consumer may, alternatively, exercise a right to bring a subscription
contract to an end by notifying the trader in accordance with subsection  (6)
that the consumer is bringing the contract to an end.

260.3

A consumer may exercise a right to bring a subscription contract to an end at
any time permitted by regulations under section  277 (1) (c) .

260.4

In relation to a subscription contract entered into online, arrangements under
subsection  (1)  must—

260.4.a

enable a consumer to bring the contract to an end online, and

260.4.b

ensure that instructions for doing so are displayed online in a place or
places that a consumer seeking to end the contract is likely to find them.

260.5

Arrangements under this section must comply with any other requirements
specified in regulations under section  277 (1) (c) .

260.6

A notification under subsection  (2)  may be given by the consumer making a
clear statement setting out their decision to bring the contract to an end.

###### Duties of trader on cancellation or end of subscription contract

261

261.1

This section applies where a consumer—

261.1.a

has exercised a right under this Chapter to cancel a subscription contract, or

261.1.b

has exercised a right to bring a subscription contract to an end.

261.2

The trader must—

261.2.a

give the consumer a notice acknowledging that fact (referred to in this
Chapter as an “end of contract notice”), and

261.2.b

if an overpayment has been received by the trader from the consumer, refund
that overpayment.

261.3

An end of contract notice must set out—

261.3.a

the date on which the contract was or will be cancelled or on which it came,
or will come, to an end, and

261.3.b

any other information required by regulations under section  277 (1) (b) .

261.4

An end of contract notice must be given—

261.4.a

in accordance with subsection  (5) ,

261.4.b

in writing on a durable medium, and

261.4.c

in accordance with any other requirements specified in regulations under
section  277 (1) (a) .

261.5

An end of contract notice must be given—

261.5.a

before the end of such period as may be specified in regulations under section
277 (1) (a) , or

261.5.b

if no such period is specified—

261.5.b.i

in the case of a consumer exercising a right mentioned in subsection  (1)  by
giving a notification online, before the end of the period of 24 hours from
the time that the consumer gives the notification;

261.5.b.ii

in a case where the consumer exercises such a right by giving a notification
in any other way, before the end of the period of 3 working days beginning
with the day after the day that the consumer gives that notification.

261.6

In subsection  (2) (b)  “ overpayment ”, in relation to a subscription
contract, means any payment made by the consumer for which the consumer is not
liable as a result of cancelling the subscription contract or bringing it to
an end.

##### Rights of consumers to cancel contract for breach

###### Terms implied into contracts

262

A trader’s compliance with the following duties is an implied term in every
subscription contract—

262.a

the duty set out in section  256 (1) (a)  (key pre-contract information);

262.b

the duty set out in section  256 (1) (b)  (full pre-contract information);

262.c

the duty set out in section  258  (reminder notices);

262.d

the duty set out in section  259 (4)  to specify in key pre-contract
information a reasonable period for the giving of a reminder notice under
section  259 (3)  (timing for the giving of reminder notices);

262.e

the duty set out in section  260 (1)  (arrangements for consumer to end
contract);

262.f

the duties set out in section  261 (2)  (end or cancellation of subscription
contract).

###### Right to cancel for breach of implied term

263

263.1

This section applies where a trader is in breach of the term implied into a
subscription contract by section  262 (a) ,  (c) ,  (d)  or  (e) .

263.2

The consumer has the right to cancel the contract.

263.3

The right is exercisable by the consumer notifying the trader in accordance
with subsection  (4)  that the consumer is cancelling the contract.

263.4

A notification under subsection  (3)  may be given by the consumer making a
clear statement setting out their decision to cancel the contract.

263.5

A subscription contract is cancelled from the time the notification is given.

263.6

Where a subscription contract is cancelled under this section—

263.6.a

the cancellation ends both the trader’s and the consumer’s obligations to
perform the contract in respect of any rights or liabilities that would arise
(but for the cancellation) after the time at which the contract was cancelled,

263.6.b

the consumer’s liability for payments that have arisen under the contract is
extinguished to any extent set out in regulations under section  267 (1) (b)
(and, accordingly, the consumer may be entitled to a refund), and

263.6.c

any other provision made under those regulations in relation to the treatment
of goods, services or digital content supplied under a cancelled subscription
contract applies.

263.7

No penalty or charge may be imposed on a consumer for cancelling a
subscription contract under subsection  (2) .

263.8

For further provision about the exercise of a right to cancel under this
section, see section  267 .

##### Cooling-off rights

###### Right to cancel during cooling-off periods

264

264.1

A consumer has the right to cancel a subscription contract during—

264.1.a

the initial cooling-off period, and

264.1.b

any renewal cooling-off period.

264.2

The right conferred by subsection  (1) —

264.2.a

is exercisable in any circumstances, and

264.2.b

may not be subject to any conditions other than those set out in or under this
Chapter.

264.3

The right is exercisable by the consumer notifying the trader in accordance
with subsection  (4)  that the consumer is cancelling the contract.

264.4

A notification under subsection  (3)  may be given by the consumer making a
clear statement setting out their decision to cancel the contract.

264.5

A subscription contract is cancelled from the time that such a notification is
given.

264.6

Where a subscription contract is cancelled under this section—

264.6.a

the cancellation ends both the consumer’s and the trader’s obligations to
perform the contract in respect of any rights or liabilities that would arise
(but for the cancellation) after the time at which the contract was cancelled,

264.6.b

the consumer’s liability for payments that have arisen under the contract is
extinguished to any extent set out in regulations under section  267 (1) (b)
(and, accordingly, the consumer may be entitled to a refund), and

264.6.c

any other provision made under those regulations in relation to the treatment
of goods, services or digital content supplied under a cancelled subscription
contract applies.

264.7

No penalty or charge may be imposed on a consumer for cancelling a
subscription contract under subsection  (1) .

264.8

For further provision about the exercise of a right to cancel under this
section, see section  267 .

###### Meaning of “initial cooling-off period” and “renewal cooling-off period”

265

265.1

In this Chapter, the “ initial cooling-off period ”, in relation to a
subscription contract, means the period—

265.1.a

beginning with the day the contract is entered into, and

265.1.b

ending—

265.1.b.i

in the case of a contract under which goods are supplied, at the end of the
period of 14 days beginning with the day after the day on which the consumer
receives the first supply of goods under the contract;

265.1.b.ii

in any other case, at the end of the period of 14 days beginning with the day
after the day on which the contract is entered into.

265.2

In this Chapter, a “ renewal cooling-off period ”, in relation to a
subscription contract, means a period—

265.2.a

beginning with the day on which a relevant renewal of the contract occurs, and

265.2.b

ending at the end of the period of 14 days beginning with the day after that
day.

265.3

A “relevant renewal” of a subscription contract occurs for the purposes of
subsection  (2) —

265.3.a

when the consumer becomes liable under the contract for a first renewal
payment following the end of a concessionary period, or

265.3.b

at any time when the consumer becomes liable under the contract for a renewal
payment and either—

265.3.b.i

the consumer will not become liable for the next renewal payment until after
the end of the 12-month period, or

265.3.b.ii

the consumer will not become liable for any further renewal payment but the
contract continues beyond the end of the 12-month period.

265.4

In subsection  (3) —

265.4.a

in paragraph (a), “ concessionary period ” means a period of time mentioned in
section  254 (3) (a) , and

265.4.b

in paragraph (b), the “ 12-month period ” means the period of 12 months
beginning with the day before the day on which the consumer became liable for
the renewal payment.

265.5

For the purposes of subsection  (1) (b) (i) , the first supply of goods under
a subscription contract is not to be treated as having taken place until such
time as the consumer receives all of the goods that the consumer is due to
receive as part of that supply.

265.6

This section is subject to such extensions of a cooling-off period as may be
provided for by regulations under section  267 (1)(c).

###### Cooling-off notice

266

266.1

In relation to each renewal cooling-off period, a trader must give the
consumer a notice (referred to in this Chapter as a “cooling-off notice”).

266.2

A cooling-off notice must set out—

266.2.a

that the subscription contract is continuing,

266.2.b

that the consumer has a right to cancel the subscription contract during the
cooling-off period to which the notice relates,

266.2.c

when that period begins and ends,

266.2.d

how the consumer may exercise the right to cancel,

266.2.e

if the consumer may lose the right, the circumstances under which that will
happen,

266.2.f

the consequences of the consumer exercising the right, including—

266.2.f.i

any refund the consumer may be entitled to,

266.2.f.ii

any reason that refund might be diminished, and

266.2.f.iii

in respect of a contract for the supply of goods, whether the consumer will be
responsible for returning those goods to the trader, and

266.2.g

any other information required by regulations under section  277 (1) (b) .

266.3

A cooling-off notice must be given—

266.3.a

on the first day of the renewal cooling-off period to which it relates or as
soon as reasonably practicable after that day,

266.3.b

separately from the giving of any other information, and

266.3.c

in accordance with any other requirements specified in regulations under
section  277 (1) (a) .

##### Cancellation of contracts under this Chapter: further provision

###### Cancellation of subscription contract: further provision

267

267.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision—

267.1.a

about the exercise of the rights of a consumer to cancel a subscription
contract under this Chapter;

267.1.b

about the consequences that follow a consumer exercising such rights;

267.1.c

extending a cooling-off period in such cases, and to such extent, as the
regulations may specify.

267.2

Regulations under subsection  (1) (a)  may include provision—

267.2.a

requiring a right to cancel to be exercised before the end of a specified
period;

267.2.b

imposing other conditions or restrictions on the exercise of a right to cancel
(for example, provision that a consumer may lose the right to cancel a
subscription contract during a cooling-off period if they choose to be
supplied with digital content or services under the contract during that
period).

267.3

Regulations under subsection  (1) (b)  may include provision—

267.3.a

setting out the extent to which a consumer’s liability for payments that have
arisen under a cancelled subscription contract is extinguished;

267.3.b

as a consequence of provision made under paragraph  (a) , requiring a trader
to refund a consumer for payments the consumer has made under the contract;

267.3.c

treating the consumer as having paid for goods, services or digital content
received under a cancelled subscription contract;

267.3.d

about the trader’s right to recover goods or digital content that have been
supplied under a cancelled subscription contract;

267.3.e

setting out the consequences of a consumer—

267.3.e.i

bringing a subscription contract to an end at a time when the consumer has one
or more rights to cancel the contract under this Chapter;

267.3.e.ii

cancelling a subscription contract at a time when the consumer has more than
one right to cancel the contract under this Chapter.

267.4

Provision under  subsection (3) (a)  and  (b)  may secure the result (for
example, in cases where a consumer has been supplied with digital content or
services under a contract before it is cancelled during a cooling-off period)
that—

267.4.a

the consumer remains liable (partly or fully) for payments falling due before
the cancellation of the contract, and

267.4.b

the consumer is entitled to a reduced or no refund.

267.5

Provision under subsection  (3) (e) (ii)  must secure the result that, unless
the consumer chooses otherwise, the consumer is to be taken to exercise the
right to cancel under this Chapter that results in the most advantageous
remedy to the consumer (and the regulations may include provision for
determining what remedy is “most advantageous” to a consumer in different
descriptions of case).

267.6

Before making regulations under subsection  (1) (c) , the Secretary of State
must consult such persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

267.7

The following regulations under this section are subject to the affirmative
procedure—

267.7.a

the first regulations to be made under this section;

267.7.b

any other regulations under this section that include provision within
subsection (1) (c) .

267.8

Regulations under this section to which subsection  (7)  does not apply are
subject to the negative procedure.

##### Offence of failing to provide information about cooling-off rights

###### Offence of failing to provide information about initial cooling-off rights

268

268.1

A trader commits an offence if the trader—

268.1.a

enters into an off-premises subscription contract, and

268.1.b

fails to—

268.1.b.i

give the consumer the information listed in paragraph  11 (a)  of  Schedule 23
in accordance with section  256 (1) (a) , or

268.1.b.ii

give, or make available, the information set out in paragraph  21  of that
Schedule in accordance with section  256 (1) (b) .

268.2

Subsections  (3)  and  (4)  apply where a trader—

268.2.a

commits an offence under subsection  (1) , or

268.2.b

would have committed an offence under that subsection but for a defence under
section  269 ,

and the commission of the offence, or of what would have been the offence, is
due to the act or omission of another person (“ P ”).

268.3

P commits the offence (whether or not P is a trader).

268.4

P may be charged with and convicted of the offence by virtue of subsection
(3)  whether or not proceedings are taken against the trader.

268.5

In this section, an “ off-premises subscription contract ” means a
subscription contract—

268.5.a

entered into in person, in a place which is not the business premises of the
trader,

268.5.b

entered into by any means immediately after the consumer was individually and
personally addressed by the trader in person in a place which is not the
business premises of the trader, or

268.5.c

entered into during an excursion organised by the trader with the aim or
effect of promoting and selling goods or services to the consumer.

268.6

In subsection  (5) , “ business premises ”, in relation to a trader, means—

268.6.a

any immovable retail premises where the activity of the trader is carried out
on a permanent basis, or

268.6.b

any movable retail premises where the activity of the trader is carried out on
a usual basis.

268.7

In other provisions of this Chapter, references to an offence under subsection
(1)  include references to an offence under that subsection by virtue of
subsection  (3) .

###### Defence of due diligence

269

269.1

It is a defence for a person (“ the defendant ”) charged with an offence under
section  268 (1)  to prove—

269.1.a

that the commission of the offence was due to—

269.1.a.i

the act or omission of another person, or

269.1.a.ii

reliance on information given by another person, and

269.1.b

that the defendant took all reasonable precautions and exercised all due
diligence to avoid the commission of such an offence by the defendant or any
other person under the defendant’s control.

269.2

A defendant is not entitled to rely on the defence provided by subsection  (1)
without the permission of the court unless—

269.2.a

the defendant has served on the prosecutor a notice in writing giving such
information as was then in the defendant’s possession identifying, or
assisting in the identification of, the other person, and

269.2.b

the notice is served on the prosecutor at least seven clear days before the
hearing of the proceedings or, in Scotland, at least seven clear days before
the trial diet.

###### Offences by officers of a body corporate etc

270

270.1

If an offence under section  268 (1)  committed by a body corporate is proved—

270.1.a

to have been committed with the consent or connivance of an officer of the
body, or

270.1.b

to be attributable to any neglect on the officer’s part,

the officer as well as the body corporate is guilty of the offence and liable
to be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

270.2

In subsection  (1)  a reference to an officer of a body corporate includes a
reference to—

270.2.a

a director, manager, secretary or other similar officer;

270.2.b

a person purporting to act as a director, manager, secretary or other similar
officer.

270.3

If the affairs of a body corporate are managed by its members, subsection  (1)
applies in relation to the acts and defaults of a member in connection with
the member’s functions of management as if the member were an officer of the
body corporate.

270.4

Where an offence under section  268 (1)  committed by a Scottish partnership
is proved—

270.4.a

to have been committed with the consent or connivance of a partner, or

270.4.b

to be attributable to any neglect on the part of a partner,

the partner as well as the partnership is guilty of the offence and liable to
be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

270.5

In subsection  (4) , a reference to a partner includes a person purporting to
act as a partner.

###### Penalty for offence and enforcement

271

271.1

A person who is guilty of an offence under section  268 (1)  is liable—

271.1.a

on summary conviction in England Wales, to a fine;

271.1.b

on summary conviction in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding
level 5 on the standard scale.

271.2

It is the duty of every local weights and measures authority in Great Britain
to enforce section  268 (1)  in its area.

271.3

It is the duty of the Department for the Economy in Northern Ireland to
enforce section  268 (1)  in Northern Ireland.

271.4

No proceedings for an offence under section  268 (1)  may be instituted in
England and Wales except by or on behalf of a local weights and measures
authority in Great Britain.

271.5

Nothing in subsection  (2)  authorises any local weights and measures
authority in Great Britain to bring proceedings in Scotland for an offence.

##### General and miscellaneous provision

###### Information and notices: timing and burden of proof

272

272.1

This section applies for the purposes of this Chapter.

272.2

Where a trader gives any information or notice under this Chapter by email, by
a message sent online, or by any other means of electronic communication, the
information or notice is to be treated as given by the trader, and as received
by the consumer, at the time that the communication is sent to the consumer.

272.3

Subsection  (2)  applies even if the consumer does not receive the
communication where the reason for that is beyond the control of the trader.

272.4

Subsection  (5)  applies for the purposes of determining whether a consumer
has—

272.4.a

given notice that the consumer is cancelling a subscription contract in
exercise of a right conferred by this Chapter within the period of time
specified for the consumer to exercise the right;

272.4.b

given notice that the consumer is bringing a subscription contract to an end
within a period of time, or before a date, specified or described in the
contract as the period during which, or date before which, the consumer may
exercise the right.

272.5

The consumer is to be treated as having given notice within the required
period, or before the specified date, if the communication by which the notice
is given is sent before the end of that period or date (and for this purpose
it is immaterial whether or not the trader receives the notice).

272.6

The burden of proof lies with the trader in any dispute between the trader and
a consumer as to whether information or a notice has been given by the trader
to the consumer in accordance with this Chapter.

272.7

The burden of proof lies with the consumer in any dispute between the consumer
and a trader as to—

272.7.a

whether the consumer has notified the trader that the consumer is bringing to
an end, or cancelling, a subscription contract in accordance with this
Chapter;

272.7.b

when the consumer gave such notice.

272.8

Any information that a trader gives to a consumer under this Chapter must be
given in clear and plain language and

272.8.a

if given in writing, be in a legible form;

272.8.b

if given orally, be audible and comprehensible.

###### Terms of a subscription contract which are of no effect

273

273.1

Any term of a subscription contract that is in contravention of this Chapter
is, to that extent, of no effect (including any term that seeks to exclude or
restrict a trader’s liability arising from the terms implied into the contract
by section  262 ).

273.2

In cases to which this subsection applies, any term of a subscription contract
which seeks to impose on a consumer liability for a renewal payment before the
day on which the contract renews is, to that extent, of no effect.

273.3

Subsection  (2)  applies to cases of a description specified in regulations
under section  277 (1) (e)  (and the regulations may include provision for
determining when a contract renews in each description of case).

###### Other remedies for breach by trader

274

274.1

Nothing in this Chapter is to be taken as limiting the taking of any other
remedies available to a consumer for breach of any term (whether express,
implied by section  262  or otherwise) of a subscription contract.

274.2

Those other remedies may be sought—

274.2.a

in addition to the rights conferred on the consumer by this Chapter (but not
so as to recover twice for the same loss), or

274.2.b

instead of the exercise of any of those rights by the consumer.

274.3

Those other remedies include any of the following—

274.3.a

claiming damages;

274.3.b

seeking specific performance;

274.3.c

seeking an order for specific implement;

274.3.d

relying on the breach against a claim by the trader under the contract;

274.3.e

for breach of a term, exercising a right to treat the contract at an end.

###### Application of this Chapter

275

275.1

Subsection  (2)  applies if—

275.1.a

the law of a country or territory other than the United Kingdom or any part of
the United Kingdom is chosen by the parties to be applicable to a subscription
contract, but

275.1.b

the contract has a close connection with the United Kingdom.

275.2

This Chapter applies in relation to the contract despite that choice.

275.3

This Chapter does not apply in relation to contracts entered into before
section  254  comes into force.

275.4

Subsections  (5)  and  (6)  apply where—

275.4.a

a trader enters into a contract that is an excluded contract,

275.4.b

but for it being an excluded contract, the contract would have been a
subscription contract, and

275.4.c

on a later day (the “relevant day”), the contract ceases to be an excluded
contract and, accordingly, becomes a subscription contract.

275.5

This Chapter applies to the contract with the following modifications—

275.5.a

sections  256  and  257  (pre-contract information) do not apply;

275.5.b

section  258  (reminder notices) applies as if—

275.5.b.i

in subsection  (1) , the reference to a trader entering into a subscription
contract with a consumer that does not involve a concessionary period were a
reference to a trader entering into the contract,

275.5.b.ii

the reference in subsection  (2) (a)  to the day that the contract was entered
into were a reference to the relevant day, and

275.5.b.iii

subsections  (3) ,  (4)  and  (6)  were omitted;

275.5.c

section  259  (content and timing etc of reminder notices) applies as if, in
subsections  (3)  and  (4) , references to the period specified by the trader
in pre-contract information were references to the period specified by the
trader in information given under subsection  (6)  of this section;

275.5.d

section  262  (terms implied into contracts) applies as if—

275.5.d.i

in paragraph  (a) , the reference to the duty set out in section  256 (1) (a)
were a reference to the duty set out in subsection  (6)  of this section;

275.5.d.ii

paragraph  (b)  was omitted;

275.5.d.iii

in paragraph  (d) , the reference to pre-contract information were a reference
to the information given under subsection  (6)  of this section;

275.5.e

section 264  (right to cancel during cooling-off periods) applies as if
subsection  (1) (a)  were omitted.

275.6

As soon as reasonably practicable after the relevant day, and in any event
before the end of 12 months beginning with that day, the trader must give to
the consumer key pre-contract information and full pre-contract information in
relation to the contract, other than any such information that is excluded by
subsection  (7) .

275.7

Information is excluded by this subsection if—

275.7.a

it relates to the initial cooling-off period under the contract;

275.7.b

it relates to a period mentioned in section  254 (3) (a)  (initial
concessionary period) and the relevant day falls after the end of that period.

275.8

For the purposes of the duty under subsection  (6) —

275.8.a

it is irrelevant whether any of the information required has already been
given to the consumer before the relevant day,

275.8.b

section  256 (5)  applies as it applies for the purposes of the duty under
section  256 (1) (b) , and

275.8.c

paragraph  13  of Schedule  23  is to be ignored.

###### Crown application

276

276.1

Subject to subsection  (2) , this Chapter binds the Crown.

276.2

The Crown is not criminally liable as a result of anything in this Chapter.

276.3

Subsection  (2)  does not affect the application of any provision of this
Chapter in relation to persons in the public service of the Crown.

###### Power to make further provision in connection with this Chapter

277

277.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision—

277.1.a

about how and when information or a notice that a trader is required to give
to a consumer under this Chapter may or must be given;

277.1.b

about the information that is to be contained in a notice given under this
Chapter;

277.1.c

about the arrangements that a trader must make under section  260  to enable a
consumer to exercise a right to bring a subscription contract to an end, and
about when a consumer may exercise such a right;

277.1.d

specifying the period of time within which the refund of an overpayment must
be made under section  261 (2) (b) ;

277.1.e

specifying descriptions of cases for the purposes of section  273 (2)  (and
about the day on which a contract renews for those purposes).

277.2

Regulations under subsection  (1) (c)  may include (among other things)
provision restricting the period of notice that a trader may require a
consumer to give to bring a subscription contract to an end.

277.3

Regulations under this section are subject to the negative procedure.

##### General interpretation

###### Interpretation

280

280.1

In this Chapter—

      “ business ” includes—         a trade, craft or profession,
any other undertaking carried on for gain or reward, and           the
activities of any government department or local or public authority;
“ consumer ” means an individual acting for purposes that are wholly or mainly
outside the individual’s business;           “ durable medium ” means paper,
email or any other medium that—         allows information to be addressed
personally to the consumer,           enables the consumer to store
information in a way accessible for future reference for a period that is long
enough for the purposes of the information, and           allows the unchanged
reproduction of information stored;                 “ goods ” includes—
immoveable property;           rights and obligations;           water, gas
and electricity if they are put up for sale in a limited volume or set
quantity;                 “ trader ” means a person (“ P ”) acting for
purposes relating to P’s business, whether acting personally or through
another person acting in P’s name or on P’s behalf.

280.2

In this Chapter—

280.2.a

references to a contract for the supply of goods, services or digital content
include references to a contract for the supply of any combination of goods,
services and digital content;

280.2.b

references to payment or to a consumer being charged are references to
payment, or a consumer being charged, in money or money’s worth;

280.2.c

references to something happening automatically under a subscription contract
are references to it happening without any action on the part of the consumer
to cause it to happen (ignoring the consumer’s action of entering into the
contract or any action taken in connection with, or for the purpose of,
entering into it);

280.2.d

references to something recurring are references to it happening more than
once;

280.2.e

references to a supply of goods, services or digital content for a fixed term
include references to a supply of goods, services or digital content which is
fixed to any extent;

280.2.f

references to a consumer entering into a subscription contract include
references to a consumer placing an order for the supply of goods, services or
digital content under a subscription contract in circumstances where—

280.2.f.i

the trader is (in any way) inviting such orders, and

280.2.f.ii

the consumer is not required to take any further action for the contract to be
concluded.

###### Index of defined expressions

281

In this Part, the expressions listed in the left-hand column have the meaning
given by, or are to be interpreted in accordance with, the provisions listed
in the right-hand column.

    Expression   Business Section  280 (1)   Consumer Section  280 (1)
Cooling-off notice Section  266 (1)   Digital content Section 330   Durable
medium Section  280 (1)   Excluded contract Section  255   Full pre-contract
information Section  256 (1) (b)   Goods Section  280 (1)   Initial cooling-
off period Section  265 (1)   Key pre-contract information Section  256 (1)
(a)   Reminder notice Section  258   Renewal cooling-off period Section  265
(2)   Renewal payment Section  258 (7)   Subscription contract Section  254
Trader Section  280 (1)   Working day Section 330

#### Consumer Savings Schemes

##### Meaning of “consumer savings scheme contract”

282

282.1

For the purposes of this Chapter, a consumer savings scheme contract is a
contract—

282.1.a

under which—

282.1.a.i

a consumer makes payments to a trader,

282.1.a.ii

the trader credits those payments to an account that is held by the trader for
the consumer (“the consumer’s account”), and

282.1.a.iii

the payments credited to the consumer’s account provide a fund for the
consumer to redeem as goods, services or digital content in accordance with
the terms of the contract,

282.1.b

to which one or more of subsections (2), (3) or (4) applies, and

282.1.c

which is not an excluded arrangement (see section  284 ).

282.2

This subsection applies to a contract if it contains terms which have the
effect of restricting the times at, or periods of time during, which the
consumer may redeem funds from the consumer’s account.

282.3

This subsection applies to a contract if it contains terms which have the
effect of incentivising the consumer to redeem, or refrain from redeeming,
funds in the consumer’s account at a time, or during a period of time,
specified in the terms of the contract.

282.4

This subsection applies to a contract if it is marketed or advertised in such
a way as to encourage the consumer to redeem, or refrain from redeeming, funds
in the consumer’s account at a time, or during a period of time, specified in
material used for the purposes of marketing or advertising the contract.

##### Other defined terms

283

283.1

In this Chapter, references to a trader operating a consumer savings scheme
are references to a trader entering into a consumer savings scheme contract.

283.2

For the purposes of  section 282 (1) (a) (ii) , it is sufficient for a trader
to hold the consumer’s payments in some way other than crediting those
payments to a specific account for that consumer and references in this
Chapter to a “consumer’s account” are to be construed accordingly.

283.3

In this Chapter, “protected payments” are payments, made by a consumer under a
consumer savings scheme contract, in respect of which funds in the consumer’s
account have not been redeemed.

283.4

Subject to  subsection (5) , in this Chapter, funds are treated as redeemed
when the trader provides the consumer with goods, services or digital content
in accordance with the terms of the consumer savings scheme contract.

283.5

Where a trader provides a consumer with vouchers or credit-tokens which may be
redeemed only in respect of goods, services or digital content provided by
that trader, funds are treated as redeemed for the purposes of this Chapter
only when those vouchers or credit-tokens are redeemed.

##### Excluded arrangements

284

284.1

An arrangement is an excluded arrangement for the purposes of this Chapter if
it is of a description set out in  Schedule 24 .

284.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend  Schedule 24  so as to—

284.2.a

add a description of an arrangement to the Schedule;

284.2.b

remove a description of an arrangement from the Schedule;

284.2.c

modify a description of an arrangement set out in the Schedule.

284.3

The power under  subsection (2) (a)  and  (c)  includes power to provide for
an arrangement to be an excluded arrangement—

284.3.a

generally for the purposes of this Chapter;

284.3.b

only for such purposes of this Chapter as are specified.

284.4

Regulations under  subsection (2)  are subject to the affirmative procedure.

##### Insolvency protection requirement

285

285.1

A trader operating a consumer savings scheme must make and maintain the
arrangements set out in  section 286  (insurance arrangements) or in  section
287  (trust arrangements) to cover, in the event of the trader’s insolvency,
the cost of returning to the consumer any protected payments at the time of
the insolvency.

285.2

It is an implied term of every consumer savings scheme contract that the
trader complies with the requirements of this section.

285.3

A trader operating a consumer savings scheme in the United Kingdom, who is not
established in the United Kingdom, must comply with the requirements of this
section.

285.4

References in this Chapter to a trader’s insolvency are references to—

285.4.a

a bankruptcy order having been made in relation to the trader (or, in
Scotland, the trader’s estate having been sequestrated),

285.4.b

a winding up order having been made in relation to the trader as a result of
the trader’s insolvency,

285.4.c

an appointment of a liquidator (otherwise than following the making of a
winding up order) as a result of the trader’s insolvency,

285.4.d

the trader being in administration,

285.4.e

the appointment of an administrative receiver (or, in Scotland, a receiver) in
relation to the trader, or

285.4.f

in any jurisdiction, the trader being subject to an order or procedure that
corresponds to any order or procedure mentioned in paragraphs  (a)  to  (e) .

##### Insurance arrangements

286

286.1

Where a trader relies on arrangements under this section for the purpose of
satisfying section  285 , the trader must maintain insurance under one or more
appropriate policies with an insurer authorised in respect of such business in
the United Kingdom, the Channel Islands or the Isle of Man.

286.2

In this section “ appropriate policy ” means a policy—

286.2.a

under which the insurer agrees to indemnify consumers in the event of the
insolvency of the trader;

286.2.b

under which consumers are insured persons in respect of the costs referred to
in paragraph (d);

286.2.c

which does not contain a condition which provides (in whatever terms) that no
liability arises, or that any liability arising ceases—

286.2.c.i

in the event of some specified thing being done or omitted to be done after
the happening of the event giving rise to a claim under the policy;

286.2.c.ii

in the event of the policy holder not making payments under or in connection
with other policies; or

286.2.c.iii

unless the policy holder keeps specified records or makes available to, or
provides the insurer with, information from those records; and

286.2.d

which covers the costs of returning to the consumer any protected payments at
the time of the insolvency.

286.3

The trader must meet the costs of arranging and maintaining an appropriate
policy and any related charges or taxes, without recourse to the consumer
payments which are to be protected under that policy.

##### Trust arrangements

287

287.1

Where a trader relies on arrangements under this section for the purpose of
satisfying  section 285 , the trader must ensure that all payments made by a
consumer under a consumer savings scheme contract are held on trust for the
consumer, in the United Kingdom, by one or more persons appointed as trustees
for the consumer.

287.2

Subject to subsection (3), the monies are to be held on trust for the consumer
as required by subsection (1) until—

287.2.a

the funds in the consumer’s account have been redeemed, or

287.2.b

any payments made by the consumer in respect of the consumer savings scheme
contract have been returned to the consumer.

287.3

The trustees may authorise the use of monies held on trust for the consumer as
required by subsection (1)—

287.3.a

to pay suppliers for goods, services or digital content to be provided to the
consumer in accordance with the terms of the consumer savings scheme contract,

287.3.b

to return payments to the consumer in exceptional circumstances, or

287.3.c

to pay any profits after the consumer has redeemed all of the funds in their
account.

287.4

For the purposes of subsection (3)(a), trustees may only authorise the release
of monies on receipt of a declaration by the trader that the trader is
solvent.

287.5

The trustee, or where there is more than one trustee, the majority of persons
appointed as trustees for the purpose of subsection (1), must be independent
of the trader.

287.6

For the purpose of  subsection (5) , a person is independent of the trader in
relation to a trust only if—

287.6.a

the person has no interest in the assets of the trader or of the trust
otherwise than as a trustee of that trust, and

287.6.b

the person is neither connected with, nor an associate of—

287.6.b.i

the trader, or

287.6.b.ii

any person for the time being acting as an insolvency practitioner in relation
to the trader.

287.7

The cost of administering the trust must be paid for by the trader.

287.8

The trader must arrange for an independent auditor to be appointed to audit
the accounts of the trust every three years.

287.9

In the event of a trader’s insolvency, monies held on trust for a consumer by
the trustees in accordance with this section must be returned to the consumer.

##### Information requirements

288

288.1

A trader must, before the end of 30 working days beginning with the day on
which a consumer makes the first payment to the trader under a consumer
savings scheme contract, provide to the consumer the following information—

288.1.a

the name, address, telephone number and email address of the insurer or
trustees responsible for protecting the consumer’s payments;

288.1.b

where insurance arrangements are in place, the policy number for the policy
under which the consumer’s payments are protected;

288.1.c

where trust arrangements are in place, a copy of the trust deed under which
the consumer’s payments are held.

288.2

The trader must notify the consumer of any change to any of the information
provided under subsection (1) before the end of 30 working days, beginning
with the day on which the change takes effect.

288.3

Where a consumer makes a written request to the trader for the information
mentioned in subsection (1), the trader must, before the end of 30 working
days beginning with the day on which the request is received, provide, without
charge, the information requested.

288.4

The information provided under this section must be in clear and plain
language and, if in writing, in a legible form.

288.5

The information provided under this section must—

288.5.a

in cases where the contract is to be entered into in the simultaneous physical
presence of the trader and the consumer, be given in writing on a durable
medium;

288.5.b

in cases where the contract is to be entered into online without the
simultaneous physical presence of the trader and the consumer—

288.5.b.i

be given in writing by being displayed in any location online where the
consumer may take steps to enter into the contract, and

288.5.b.ii

be accessible in that location without the need for any action by the
consumer;

288.5.c

in cases where the contract is to be entered into orally without the
simultaneous physical presence of the trader and the consumer, be given to the
consumer orally and in a way that is audible and comprehensible.

288.6

In cases not falling within  subsection (5) (a)  the trader must also, as soon
as reasonably practicable after the contract has been entered into, give the
consumer the information in writing on a durable medium.

288.7

A trader operating a consumer savings scheme in the United Kingdom, who is not
established in the United Kingdom, must comply with the requirements of this
section.

288.8

It is an implied term of every consumer savings scheme contract that the
trader complies with the requirements of this section.

288.9

The Consumer Contracts (Information, Cancellation and Additional Charges)
Regulations 2013 ( S.I. 3134/2013 ) apply to consumer savings scheme contracts
to the extent that requirements under those regulations are not met by
compliance with this section.

;

##### Interpretation

290

In this Chapter—

      “ business ” includes—         a trade, craft or profession, and
any other undertaking carried on for gain or reward,         but does not
include the activities of any government department or local or public
authority;           “ consumer ” means an individual acting for purposes that
are wholly or mainly outside the individual’s business;           “ durable
medium ” means, in relation to the provision of information, paper, email or
any other medium that—         allows the information to be addressed
personally to the consumer,           enables the consumer to store the
information in a way accessible for future reference for a period that is long
enough for the purposes of the information, and           allows the unchanged
reproduction of the information stored;                 “ excluded arrangement
” is to be read in accordance with section  284 ;           “ goods ” includes
vouchers, rights and obligations but does not include buildings or other
structures or immovable property;           “ trader ” means a person (“ P ”)
acting for purposes relating to P’s business whether acting personally or
through another person acting in P’s name or on P’s behalf;           “
turnover ” has the same meaning as in  section 204  (determination of
turnover) and references to “this Part” in  section 204  are to be read, for
the purposes of this Chapter, as references to this Chapter.

#### Alternative dispute resolution for consumer contract disputes

##### Interpretation of 

###### Meaning of “ADR” and related terms

291

291.1

This section  has effect for the purposes of this Chapter.

291.2

“ ADR ” means any method of securing or facilitating an out-of-court
resolution of a consumer contract dispute that is carried out by an
independent third party acting in relation to both parties to the dispute.

291.3

But the term “ ADR ” does not include anything carried out by a person in
their capacity as—

291.3.a

a judge, or

291.3.b

a member of the staff of a court or tribunal.

291.4

The following are examples of ADR (if carried out as mentioned in  subsection
(2)  in relation to a consumer contract dispute)—

291.4.a

mediation;

291.4.b

arbitration;

291.4.c

early neutral evaluation;

291.4.d

action under an ombudsman scheme.

291.5

In  subsection (2)  “ resolution ” includes—

291.5.a

a decision binding both parties;

291.5.b

a decision which, if accepted by the consumer, binds the trader;

291.5.c

settlement of the dispute between the parties.

291.6

“ ADR provider ” means a person who does either or both of the following—

291.6.a

carrying out ADR in relation to a consumer contract dispute, or

291.6.b

making special ADR arrangements.

291.7

“Special ADR arrangements” are (subject to  subsection (8) ) arrangements made
by an ADR provider with another person (whether or not that other person is an
exempt or accredited ADR provider) for ADR to be carried out by that other
person in relation to one or more consumer contract disputes.

291.8

Arrangements made by a person acting for only one of the parties to a consumer
contract dispute are not special ADR arrangements.

291.9

For the meaning of “exempt ADR provider” and “exempt redress scheme” see
section 295 .

291.10

“ Accredited ADR provider ” means a person who is for the time being
accredited under this Chapter (whether or not their accreditation is limited
to particular descriptions of ADR or special ADR arrangements).

291.11

In  this section  “ judge ” includes—

291.11.a

a member of a tribunal,

291.11.b

a justice of the peace or, in Northern Ireland, a lay magistrate,

291.11.c

a clerk or other officer entitled to exercise the jurisdiction of a court or
tribunal, and

291.11.d

a holder of any other public office with functions of a judicial nature.

###### Other definitions

292

292.1

This section  has effect for the purposes of this Chapter.

292.2

“ Consumer contract ” means (subject to the following provisions of this
section) a contract between a trader and a consumer which is—

292.2.a

a contract to which Chapter 2 of Part 1 of CRA 2015 (contracts to supply
goods) applies;

292.2.b

a contract to which Chapter 3 of that Part (contracts to supply digital
content) applies;

292.2.c

a contract to which Chapter 4 of that Part (contracts to supply services)
applies;

292.2.d

a mixed contract, that is to say a contract to which any two or three of those
Chapters apply (see section 1(3) and (4) of that Act).

292.3

The reference in  subsection (2) (a)  to a contract to which Chapter 2 of Part
1 of CRA 2015 applies includes a reference to—

292.3.a

a contract between a gas supplier and a consumer for the supply of gas to any
premises;

292.3.b

a contract deemed by paragraph 8(1) or (2) of Schedule 2B to the Gas Act 1986,
or by section 12(1) or (2) of the Energy Act (Northern Ireland)  2011 (c. 6
(N.I.)) , to exist between a gas supplier and a consumer for the supply of gas
to any premises;

292.3.c

a contract between an electricity supplier and a consumer for the supply of
electricity to any premises;

292.3.d

a contract deemed to exist by paragraph 3(1) or (2) of Schedule 6 to the
Electricity Act 1989 or by paragraph 3(1) or (2) of Schedule 6 to the
Electricity (Northern Ireland) Order 1992 ( S.I. 1992/231 (N.I.1)) ;

292.3.e

the terms applying as between a water supplier and a consumer in respect of
the supply of water to any premises by a water supplier.

292.4

In subsection (3)—

      “ electricity supplier ” means a person who is authorised to supply
electricity by a licence or exemption under Part 1 of the Electricity Act 1989
or Part 2 of the Electricity (Northern Ireland) Order 1992;           “ gas
supplier ” means a person who is authorised to supply gas by a licence or
exemption under Part 1 of the Gas Act 1986 or Part 2 of the Gas (Northern
Ireland) Order 1996 ( S.I. 1996/275 (N.I.2)) ;           “ water supplier ”
means—         a water undertaker or a water supply licensee within the
meaning of the Water Industry Act 1991,           a person supplying water
under a water services licence within the meaning of the Water Services etc.
(Scotland) Act  2005 (asp 3) , or           a water undertaker within the
meaning of the Water and Sewerage Services (Northern Ireland) Order 2006 (
S.I. 2006/3336 (N.I.21)) .

292.5

The reference in  subsection (2) (c)  to a contract to which Chapter 4 of CRA
2015 applies includes a contract between a heat supplier and a consumer for
the supply of heating, cooling or hot water by means of thermal energy
provided from a heat network.

292.6

In  subsection (5) —

      “ heat network ” has the meaning given by section 216 of the Energy Act
2023, and           “ heat supplier ” means a person who charges for making a
supply of heating, cooling or hot water by means of thermal energy provided
from a heat network.

292.7

In the application of provisions of Part 1 of CRA 2015 for determining whether
a contract is a consumer contract for the purposes of this Chapter, the
following provisions are to be disregarded—

292.7.a

section 32(2) (provisions excluded from the operation of section 32(1));

292.7.b

section 48(5) (power to exclude services from scope of Chapter 4 of Part 1).

292.8

The Secretary of State may by regulations provide that contracts of a
description specified in the regulations are excluded from being consumer
contracts for the purposes of this Chapter.

292.9

The power in subsection (8) includes power to provide that the exclusion only
applies in circumstances specified in the regulations.

292.10

Regulations under subsection (8) are subject to the affirmative procedure.

292.11

“ Consumer contract dispute ” means a dispute between the parties to a
consumer contract which relates to the contract, including a dispute
concerning—

292.11.a

anything done by either party before making the contract,

292.11.b

the making of the contract,

292.11.c

obligations under or relating to the contract, or

292.11.d

the performance by either party of their obligations under or relating to the
contract.

292.12

In  subsection (11)  “ dispute ” means a legal dispute, that is to say one
which may be determined by a court or tribunal in proceedings brought by
either of the parties to the contract.

292.13

The “parties” to a consumer contract, or a consumer contract dispute, are the
consumer and the trader.

292.14

The following terms have the meaning given by section 2 of CRA 2015—

      “consumer”           “goods”           “trader”.

But in interpreting the term “consumer” section 2(4) to (6) of that Act is to
be disregarded.

##### Prohibition on acting as ADR provider without accreditation etc

###### Prohibitions relating to acting as ADR provider

293

293.1

A person must not carry out ADR in relation to a consumer contract dispute
unless the person—

293.1.a

is an exempt ADR provider whose exemption covers the ADR being carried out,

293.1.b

is an accredited ADR provider whose accreditation covers the ADR being carried
out, or

293.1.c

is acting under special ADR arrangements made by—

293.1.c.i

an exempt ADR provider whose exemption covers the making of those special ADR
arrangements, or

293.1.c.ii

an accredited ADR provider whose accreditation covers the making of those
special ADR arrangements.

293.2

A person must not make special ADR arrangements in relation to any one or more
consumer contract disputes unless the person is—

293.2.a

an exempt ADR provider whose exemption covers the making of those special ADR
arrangements, or

293.2.b

an accredited ADR provider whose accreditation covers the making of those
special ADR arrangements.

###### Prohibitions relating to charging fees to consumers

294

294.1

An accredited ADR provider must not charge the consumer a fee in respect of
ADR being carried out (or to be carried out) in relation to a consumer
contract—

294.1.a

by the accredited ADR provider, or

294.1.b

by another ADR provider under special ADR arrangements made by the accredited
ADR provider,

unless the fee is charged in accordance with provisions for the charging of
fees to consumers which meet the conditions in subsection (2).

294.2

The conditions are that the provisions in question—

294.2.a

have been made by the accredited ADR provider,

294.2.b

are approved by the Secretary of State for the purposes of this subsection,
and

294.2.c

are published in a manner likely to come to the attention of consumers whose
consumer contract disputes may be dealt with by the accredited ADR provider.

294.3

An ADR provider who carries out (or is to carry out) ADR in relation to a
consumer contract dispute under special ADR arrangements must not charge the
consumer any fee in respect of carrying out the ADR in question.

##### Exempt ADR providers

###### Exempt ADR providers

295

295.1

In this Chapter—

      “ exempt ADR provider ” means a person who—         is listed (or of a
description of persons listed) in Part 1 of  Schedule 25 , or           is
(when carrying out ADR or making special ADR arrangements) acting under or for
the purposes of an exempt redress scheme;                 “ exempt redress
scheme ” means a scheme or other similar arrangement which is listed (or of a
description listed) in Part 2 of  Schedule 25 .

295.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend  Schedule 25  for the purpose
of—

295.2.a

adding a new entry in Part 1 or 2;

295.2.b

varying or removing an entry for the time being included in Part 1 or 2;

295.2.c

varying the supplementary provision in Part 3.

295.3

Regulations under subsection (2) may, in particular—

295.3.a

provide for an entry in Part 1 of  Schedule 25  to apply to a specified person
or to any person of a specified description;

295.3.b

provide for an entry in Part 2 of that Schedule to apply to a specified scheme
or any scheme of a specified description;

295.3.c

limit the scope of the exemption given to a person by virtue of an entry in
Part 1 or 2 of that Schedule, whether in relation to carrying out ADR or
making special ADR arrangements (or both).

295.4

For the purposes of subsection (3)—

295.4.a

descriptions of ADR may be framed by reference to kinds of ADR or types of
dispute (or both), and

295.4.b

descriptions of special ADR arrangements may be framed by reference to any
features of such arrangements, including in particular the kinds of ADR
involved or the types of dispute involved (or both).

295.5

Subject to any limitation on its scope provided for by  Schedule 25 —

295.5.a

an exemption given to a person by virtue of an entry in Part 1 of that
Schedule covers anything done by the person in the exercise of the person’s
functions that would otherwise be prohibited, and

295.5.b

an exemption given to a person by virtue of an entry in Part 2 of that
Schedule covers anything done under or for the purposes of an exempted redress
scheme that would otherwise be prohibited.

295.6

In this section—

      “ prohibited ” means prohibited by section  293 (1) or (2);           “
specified ” means specified in the regulations.

295.7

Regulations under  subsection (2)  are subject to the negative procedure.

##### Accreditation: procedure etc

###### Applications for accreditation or variation of accreditation

296

296.1

A person who wishes to be an accredited ADR provider must—

296.1.a

apply to the Secretary of State for accreditation to enable the person to
carry out ADR or to make special ADR arrangements (or to do both), and

296.1.b

pay to the Secretary of State the appropriate application fee (if any)
prescribed by regulations under  section 300 .

296.2

An application for accreditation to carry out ADR may be limited to one or
more particular descriptions of ADR.

296.3

An application for accreditation to make special ADR arrangements may be
limited to one or more particular descriptions of special ADR arrangements.

296.4

An accredited ADR provider may apply to the Secretary of State for their
accreditation to be varied by the addition, variation or removal of—

296.4.a

any limitation affecting the descriptions of ADR or special ADR arrangements
(as the case may be) covered by the accreditation, or

296.4.b

any condition on the accreditation.

296.5

An application under subsection  (4)  must be accompanied by the appropriate
application fee (if any) prescribed by regulations under  section 300 .

296.6

The Secretary of State may determine the procedure to be followed in relation
to an application for accreditation or an application for the variation of an
accreditation.

296.7

The matters which may be determined under  subsection (6)  include (among
other things)—

296.7.a

the form in which applications are to be made;

296.7.b

the particular descriptions of ADR for which limited accreditation may be
applied for and granted;

296.7.c

the particular descriptions of special ADR arrangements for which limited
accreditation may be applied for and granted;

296.7.d

the information to be given by applicants.

296.8

Section 295 (4)  applies for the purposes of  subsection (7)  as it applies
for the purposes of  section 295 (3) .

296.9

The Secretary of State must publish anything determined under  subsection (6)
in a manner likely to come to the attention of potential applicants for
accreditation.

296.10

The powers of the Secretary of State under  subsection (6)  may be exercised
differently for different purposes.

###### Determination of applications for accreditation or variation of accreditation

297

297.1

This section  applies where an application for accreditation, or for the
variation of an accreditation, has been made to the Secretary of State (and
has not been withdrawn).

297.2

In the case of an application for accreditation, the Secretary of State must,
as soon as is reasonably practicable—

297.2.a

consider the application,

297.2.b

decide whether—

297.2.b.i

to grant the accreditation applied for,

297.2.b.ii

to grant a more limited accreditation, or

297.2.b.iii

to refuse the application, and

297.2.c

give notice in writing to the applicant of the decision and, in the case of a
decision mentioned in  paragraph (b) (ii)  or  (iii) , the reasons for the
decision.

297.3

Accreditation granted under  subsection (2) (b) (ii)  may be limited to such
descriptions of ADR or such descriptions of special ADR arrangements (or both)
as the Secretary of State considers appropriate and specifies in the
accreditation.

297.4

If accreditation is granted, the Secretary of State may also decide to impose
conditions on the accreditation.

297.5

The Secretary of State may only grant accreditation if satisfied that the
accreditation criteria will be met by or in relation to the applicant after
accreditation is granted.

297.6

An accreditation is not time limited unless—

297.6.a

the Secretary of State determines that it is to have effect for a limited
period, and

297.6.b

the notice of the decision on the application states that the accreditation is
time limited and specifies the period for which it has effect.

297.7

The notice of a decision to grant accreditation must specify the day on which
the accreditation takes effect.

297.8

In the case of an application for the variation of an accreditation, the
Secretary of State must, as soon as is reasonably practicable—

297.8.a

consider the application,

297.8.b

decide whether—

297.8.b.i

to grant the application,

297.8.b.ii

to vary the accreditation, but to a different extent than applied for, or

297.8.b.iii

to refuse the application, and

297.8.c

give notice in writing to the applicant of the decision and, in the case of a
decision mentioned in  paragraph (b) (ii)  or  (iii) , the reasons for the
decision.

297.9

If the Secretary of State decides to vary the accreditation under  subsection
(8) (b) (i)  or  (ii) , the Secretary of State may also decide—

297.9.a

to impose new conditions on the accreditation, or

297.9.b

to vary or remove any existing condition on the accreditation.

297.10

The Secretary of State may only vary an accreditation if satisfied that the
accreditation criteria will be met by or in relation to the applicant after
the accreditation is varied.

297.11

A variation of an accreditation is not time limited unless the Secretary of
State determines that the variation is to have effect only for a limited
period and the notice of the decision on the application for variation—

297.11.a

states that the variation is time limited (unless made permanent following a
subsequent application by the ADR provider),

297.11.b

specifies the period for which the variation has effect, and

297.11.c

makes provision as to the terms of the accreditation in the event that the
variation lapses at the end of that period.

297.12

The notice of a decision to vary an accreditation must specify the day on
which the variation takes effect.

297.13

Where the Secretary of State decides—

297.13.a

to impose conditions under  subsection (4) , or

297.13.b

to impose new conditions, or to remove or vary any existing condition on the
accreditation, under  subsection (9) ,

the notice of the decision on the relevant application must set out the
conditions on the accreditation or the accreditation as varied, and give the
Secretary of State’s reasons for the decisions made under  subsection (4)  or
(9)  (as the case may be).

297.14

Where an accreditation covers the making of special ADR arrangements,
conditions on the accreditation may be framed so as to secure that the
accredited ADR provider is responsible for acts or omissions of other ADR
providers who carry out ADR under special ADR arrangements made by the
accredited ADR provider.

###### Revocation or suspension of accreditations etc

298

298.1

This section  confers powers on the Secretary of State in relation to the
