accreditation of an accredited ADR provider.

298.2

The Secretary of State may, by notice to the ADR provider, revoke the
accreditation on the application of the ADR provider.

298.3

Subsection (4)  applies in relation to the ADR provider where the Secretary of
State considers that any one or more of the following conditions are met—

298.3.a

the ADR provider is contravening, or has contravened, any of the prohibitions
in  section 293  and  294 ;

298.3.b

the ADR provider is failing, or has failed, to comply with any of the
accreditation criteria;

298.3.c

the ADR provider is failing, or has failed, to comply with any conditions on
its accreditation;

298.3.d

the ADR provider is failing, or has failed, to comply with an enforcement
notice under  section 302 .

298.4

The Secretary of State may by notice to the ADR provider—

298.4.a

vary the accreditation, by doing either or both of the following—

298.4.a.i

limiting, or further limiting, the accreditation to such descriptions of ADR
or such descriptions of special ADR arrangements (or both) as the Secretary of
State considers appropriate, and

298.4.a.ii

imposing new conditions on the accreditation, varying any existing condition
or removing any existing condition,

298.4.b

suspend the accreditation, or

298.4.c

revoke the accreditation.

298.5

In  subsection (4) (a) (i)  the reference to limiting (or further limiting)
the accreditation to particular descriptions of ADR or of special ADR
arrangements includes, in particular, limiting it to ADR relating to consumer
contract disputes that have already been referred for ADR or to special ADR
arrangements that already exist (as the case may be), whether for a limited
period or otherwise.

298.6

Before giving such a notice the Secretary of State must give the ADR provider
a reasonable opportunity to make representations as to—

298.6.a

whether one or more of the conditions mentioned in  subsection (3)  are met in
relation to the ADR provider, and

298.6.b

if so, what action (if any) it is appropriate for the Secretary of State to
take under  subsection (4) .

298.7

Any variations made under  subsection (4) (a)  must be variations the
Secretary of State considers necessary to secure compliance with the
prohibitions in  sections 293  and  294 , the accreditation criteria, the
existing conditions on the accreditation or the enforcement notice (as the
case may be).

298.8

In  subsection (7)  “ existing conditions ” means the existing conditions
disregarding any previous variations made under  subsection (4) (a)  or  (9)
(b) .

298.9

Where variations of the accreditation are made under  subsection (4) (a) , the
Secretary of State must—

298.9.a

keep those variations under review, and

298.9.b

by notice to the ADR provider vary the accreditation for the purpose of
revoking or reversing the effect of all or any of the variations, to the
extent that the Secretary of State considers that they are no longer necessary
for the purpose set out in  subsection (7) .

298.10

A notice that the accreditation is being varied must specify the day on which
the variations take effect.

298.11

A notice that the accreditation is suspended or revoked must specify the day
on which the accreditation ceases to be in force.

298.12

Where the accreditation is suspended the notice must also set out when or in
what circumstances the suspension is to cease to have effect so that the
accreditation is again in force.

298.13

The provision required by  subsection (12)  may consist of any one or more of
the following—

298.13.a

provision for the suspension to cease to have effect at the end of a period
specified in the notice,

298.13.b

provision for it to cease to have effect on the satisfaction of conditions
specified in the notice, and

298.13.c

provision for it to cease to have effect when a decision to lift it is made by
the Secretary of State and notified to the ADR provider.

###### Fees payable by accredited ADR providers

299

299.1

Accredited ADR providers must pay to the Secretary of State, at such times as
may be prescribed, the appropriate prescribed fee (if any).

299.2

In subsection  (1)  “ prescribed ” means prescribed by regulations under
section 300 .

###### ADR fees regulations

300

300.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision about the following
descriptions of fees, namely—

300.1.a

fees to be paid by applicants for accreditation under section  296 (1) ;

300.1.b

fees to be paid by applicants for the variation of their accreditation under
section  296 (5) ;

300.1.c

fees to be paid by accredited ADR providers under section  299 (1) .

300.2

The power to make provision about a description of fees includes power to
provide—

300.2.a

for fees of different specified amounts to be payable in different cases or
circumstances;

300.2.b

for cases or circumstances in which no fees are to be payable;

300.2.c

in the case of fees to be paid under section  299 , the times at which the
fees are to be paid.

300.3

In making regulations under this section the Secretary of State must have
regard to the need to secure that, taking one year with another—

300.3.a

the total amount of fees paid does not exceed the costs to the Secretary of
State of carrying out functions under this Chapter;

300.3.b

the total amount of fees paid under section  296 (1)  does not exceed the
costs to the Secretary of State of processing and determining applications for
accreditation;

300.3.c

the total amount of fees paid under section  296 (5)  does not exceed the
costs to the Secretary of State of processing and determining applications for
the variation of an accreditation.

300.4

Regulations under this section are subject to the negative procedure.

###### Accreditation criteria

301

301.1

For the purposes of this Chapter the accreditation criteria are the criteria
set out in  Schedule 26 .

301.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend  Schedule 26  for the purpose
of—

301.2.a

adding a new criterion, or

301.2.b

removing or varying any criterion for the time being set out in that Schedule.

301.3

Regulations under  subsection (2)  are subject to the affirmative procedure.

##### Enforcement of prohibitions etc

###### Enforcement notices

302

302.1

The Secretary of State may give an enforcement notice to an ADR provider if
satisfied that the provider is contravening, or has contravened, any one or
more of the following—

302.1.a

the prohibition in  section 293 (1)  or  (2) ;

302.1.b

the prohibition in  section 294 (1)  or  (3) ;

302.1.c

a condition on its accreditation;

302.1.d

the duty to pay a fee due under  section 299 (1) ;

302.1.e

a duty imposed by regulations under  section 303 ;

302.1.f

a duty imposed by a direction under  section 304 .

302.2

Before reaching a final view as to whether or not to give an enforcement
notice to an ADR provider, the Secretary of State must give the provider a
reasonable opportunity to make representations as to—

302.2.a

whether the condition in  subsection (1)  is met, and

302.2.b

if so, whether an enforcement notice should be given to it.

302.3

An enforcement notice is a notice requiring the ADR provider in question to
do, or not to do, such things as are specified in the notice or are of a
description so specified, with a view to securing compliance with the
prohibition, condition or duty in question.

302.4

An enforcement notice may—

302.4.a

include requirements for the ADR provider to give information to the Secretary
of State, or

302.4.b

include other supplementary, incidental or consequential provision.

302.5

The notice must make clear, in particular—

302.5.a

what requirements are being imposed by the notice, and

302.5.b

when they are to be complied with (whether immediately or otherwise).

302.6

The Secretary of State may, by notice to the ADR provider to whom an
enforcement notice has been given—

302.6.a

revoke the enforcement notice, or

302.6.b

revoke any requirement contained in the notice and, if necessary, make any
consequential changes to the other provisions of the notice.

302.7

The power under  subsection (6)  may be exercised on the application of the
ADR provider or otherwise.

302.8

An enforcement notice may, with the permission of the High Court or the Court
of Session, be enforced as if it were an order made by that court.

302.9

The Secretary of State may publish information about enforcement notices given
under  this section .

##### Provision of Information etc

###### ADR information regulations

303

303.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations require persons of a specified
description (being persons within  subsection (2) )—

303.1.a

to provide ADR information to the Secretary of State;

303.1.b

to provide ADR information to a person with functions conferred by regulations
under  section 307 ;

303.1.c

to provide ADR information to consumers by publishing it.

303.2

Regulations under this section may impose requirements on—

303.2.a

accredited ADR providers,

303.2.b

exempt ADR providers,

303.2.c

persons (not being accredited or exempt ADR providers) who carry out ADR under
special ADR arrangements,

303.2.d

persons who have been, but are no longer, within paragraph  (a) ,  (b)  or
(c) ,

303.2.e

regulators, but only in relation to relevant ADR information (see  section 306
(2) ).

303.3

The power to impose requirements under subsection (1)(a) or (b) may only be
exercised for the purpose of enabling or facilitating one or more of the
following—

303.3.a

publication of ADR information for the benefit of consumers;

303.3.b

monitoring or evaluation of the operation of the system of accreditation under
this Chapter;

303.3.c

monitoring or evaluation of the provision and quality of ADR carried out in
the United Kingdom.

303.4

It is immaterial for the purposes of subsection (3) whether the publication,
monitoring or evaluation is carried out by the Secretary of State, by a person
with functions conferred by regulations under section  307  or by any other
person acting under arrangements made with that other person by the Secretary
of State or a person with such functions.

303.5

Regulations under this section may provide for—

303.5.a

the ADR information to be provided or published;

303.5.b

the manner in which it is to be provided or published;

303.5.c

the intervals or times at which it is to be provided or published;

303.5.d

time limits for providing or publishing it.

303.6

Regulations under this section are subject to the negative procedure.

###### ADR information directions

304

304.1

The Secretary of State may give a direction to any person falling within
subsection (2)  requiring the person to provide ADR information to the
Secretary of State.

304.2

A direction may be given to—

304.2.a

an accredited ADR provider,

304.2.b

an exempt ADR provider,

304.2.c

a person (not being an accredited or exempt ADR provider) who carries out ADR
under special ADR arrangements,

304.2.d

a person who has been an accredited or exempt ADR provider or a person
mentioned in  paragraph (c) , or

304.2.e

a regulator, but only in relation to relevant ADR information (see  section
306 (2) ).

304.3

A direction may only be given—

304.3.a

for the purpose of enabling or facilitating one or more of the following
(whether done by the Secretary of State or by another person under
arrangements made with the Secretary of State)—

304.3.a.i

publication of ADR information for the benefit of consumers;

304.3.a.ii

monitoring or evaluation of the operation of the system of accreditation under
this Chapter;

304.3.a.iii

monitoring or evaluation of the provision and quality of ADR carried out in
the United Kingdom, or

304.3.b

for any other purpose connected with the exercise of the Secretary of State’s
functions under this Chapter.

304.4

A direction may provide for—

304.4.a

the ADR information to be provided;

304.4.b

the manner in which it is to be provided;

304.4.c

time limits for providing it.

304.5

A person to whom a direction is given must so far as reasonably practicable
comply with it.

304.6

The duty to comply with a direction is enforceable by the Secretary of State
in civil proceedings—

304.6.a

for an injunction,

304.6.b

for specific performance of a statutory duty under section 45 of the Court of
Session Act 1988, or

304.6.c

for any other appropriate remedy or relief.

304.7

In this section “ direction ” means a direction under this section.

###### Disclosure of ADR information by the Secretary of State

305

305.1

This section applies to any ADR information relating to ADR providers which—

305.1.a

is provided to the Secretary of State in response to regulations under
section 303  or a direction under  section 304 , or

305.1.b

is otherwise held by the Secretary of State for the purposes of any function
of the Secretary of State under this Chapter.

305.2

The Secretary of State may publish information to which this section applies
for the purpose of providing information to consumers.

305.3

The Secretary of State may disclose information to which this section applies—

305.3.a

to any Minister of the Crown, government department or devolved authority;

305.3.b

to a regulator;

305.3.c

to a public designated enforcer (see  section 151 ).

305.4

This section does not affect any power to disclose information apart from this
section.

305.5

In this section “ devolved authority ” means the Welsh Ministers, the Scottish
Ministers or a Northern Ireland Department.

###### Meaning of “ADR information” and other terms in 

306

306.1

In  sections 303  to  305  “ ADR information ” means any information about or
relating to—

306.1.a

an ADR provider,

306.1.b

ADR carried out by an ADR provider,

306.1.c

special ADR arrangements made by an ADR provider.

306.2

In those sections “ relevant ADR information ”, in relation to requirements
imposed on a regulator, means any information about or relating to—

306.2.a

ADR carried out by a relevant ADR provider,

306.2.b

special ADR arrangements made by a relevant ADR provider,

306.2.c

ADR carried out by ADR providers acting under special ADR arrangements made by
a relevant ADR provider, or

306.2.d

anything done by the regulator which directly or indirectly affects a relevant
ADR provider so far as relating to anything falling within  paragraphs (a)  to
(c) .

306.3

In  subsection (2)  “ relevant ADR provider ”, in relation to a regulator,
means an accredited or exempt ADR provider—

306.3.a

who is subject to regulation by the regulator, or

306.3.b

whose activities (as an ADR provider) relate to consumer contract disputes
involving traders acting in an area for which the regulator has responsibility
or oversight under any legislation.

306.4

In  this section —

306.4.a

a reference to information about ADR carried out by an ADR provider includes,
in the case of ADR carried out by an accredited or exempt ADR provider,
information about fees charged to consumers or traders in respect of carrying
out ADR, and

306.4.b

a reference to information about special ADR arrangements includes information
about fees charged to consumers or traders by the ADR provider who made the
arrangements.

306.5

In  this section  references to ADR carried out by an ADR provider include ADR
to be carried out by the provider.

306.6

In  this section  and  sections 303  to  305 , “ regulator ” means a person
who has responsibility for, or oversight of, an area of activity by virtue of
any legislation.

##### Involvement of other bodies in the regulation of ADR providers

###### Power to provide for other persons to have accreditation functions etc

307

307.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision for or in connection
with the conferring on another person of any function falling within
subsection (2)  so far as it is exercisable in such cases or circumstances as
may be prescribed by the regulations, in place of the corresponding function
of the Secretary of State.

307.2

The functions which may be the subject of regulations under this section are
functions corresponding to functions of the Secretary of State under the
following provisions of this Chapter as originally enacted—

      section 294 (2) (b)  (function of approving fees provisions);
section 296  (functions relating to applications for accreditation or
variation of an accreditation);           section 297  (functions relating to
determination of applications);           section 298  (functions relating to
revocation or suspension of accreditations etc);           section 299 (1)
(fees payable by accredited ADR providers), so far as relating to the function
of receiving fees;           section 302  (functions relating to enforcement
notices);           section 304  (functions relating to ADR information
directions);           section 305  (functions relating to disclosure of ADR
information).

307.3

The powers conferred by  subsection (1)  include power to make provision for
or in connection with—

307.3.a

sharing of information between any two or more relevant authorities;

307.3.b

abolishing (in whole or part) a function conferred on a person by regulations
under this section.

307.4

In  subsection (3) (a)  “ relevant authorities ” means the Secretary of State
and any persons with functions conferred by regulations under  this section .

307.5

Regulations under  this section  may amend this Chapter.

307.6

Regulations under  this section  are subject to the affirmative procedure.

##### Complaints by consumers to traders

###### Duty of trader to notify consumer of ADR arrangements etc

308

308.1

This section  applies where a trader responds to a complaint from a consumer
in respect of any matters relating to a consumer contract between them.

308.2

In  subsection (1)  “matters relating to a consumer contract” include anything
concerning—

308.2.a

the making of the contract,

308.2.b

anything done by the trader before or after making the contract,

308.2.c

any obligations of the trader under or relating to the contract, or

308.2.d

the performance by the trader of its obligations under or relating to the
contract.

308.3

The trader must, when communicating the outcome of the trader’s consideration
of the complaint to the consumer, also inform the consumer about any ADR or
other arrangement that is available if the consumer is dissatisfied with the
outcome.

308.4

In  subsection (3)  “ ADR or other arrangement ” means a scheme or
arrangement—

308.4.a

that is available to the consumer by virtue of an obligation of the trader to
participate in the scheme or arrangement imposed by—

308.4.a.i

legislation,

308.4.a.ii

terms of the consumer contract, or

308.4.a.iii

other contractual arrangements to which the trader is party, and

308.4.b

by virtue of which either or both of the following will happen if the
complaint (or any part of it) is duly pursued by the consumer—

308.4.b.i

ADR will be carried out (if or so far as the matters complained of involve a
consumer contract dispute between the parties);

308.4.b.ii

other action will be taken with a view to securing or facilitating a
resolution (if or so far as the matters complained of do not involve a
consumer contract dispute between the parties).

308.5

Section 302  (enforcement notices) applies in relation to a trader who is
contravening or has contravened the duty under  subsection (3)  as it applies
in relation to an ADR provider who is contravening or has contravened anything
mentioned in  section 302 (1) .

308.6

This section does not affect any other duty of a trader to give information to
a consumer.

##### Consequential amendments etc and transitional provision

###### Consequential amendments etc relating to this Chapter

309

Schedule 27  contains consequential amendments, repeals and revocations
relating to this Chapter.

###### Transitional provision relating to this Chapter

310

310.1

The prohibition on carrying out ADR in  section 293 (1)  does not apply to ADR
carried out by an ADR provider in relation to a consumer contract dispute
where the ADR started before the prohibition came into force.

310.2

The prohibition on charging fees to consumers in  section 294 (1)  does not
apply to ADR carried out by an ADR provider in relation to a consumer contract
dispute where the ADR started before the prohibition came into force.

310.3

For the purposes of  subsections (1)  and  (2) , the ADR is to be taken as
starting when the dispute was first referred to the ADR provider in accordance
with that provider’s rules or procedures.

310.4

The prohibition on charging fees to consumers in  section 294 (3)  does not
apply to ADR carried out by an ADR provider under special ADR arrangements
where the ADR started before the prohibition came into force.

310.5

Subsection (2)  of  section 293  applies, in the case of any special ADR
arrangements made by an ADR provider before that subsection comes into force,
as if the prohibition in it were a prohibition against the person who made the
arrangements continuing to operate them, unless that person—

310.5.a

is an exempt ADR provider whose exemption would cover making the special ADR
arrangements, or

310.5.b

is an accredited ADR provider whose accreditation would cover making the
special ADR arrangements.

310.6

But  subsection (5)  does not prevent the person from continuing to operate
the special ADR arrangements so far as relating to cases in which ADR which is
being carried out in relation to a consumer contract dispute started before
the prohibition in  section 293 (1)  came into force.

310.7

For the purposes of subsections  (4)  and  (6)  ADR is to be taken as starting
when the dispute is referred—

310.7.a

to the person who made the special ADR arrangements in accordance with the
person’s rules or procedures, or

310.7.b

to the person carrying out the ADR under the special ADR arrangements, in
accordance with the person’s rules or procedures,

whichever occurs first.

310.8

The duty in  section 308 (3)  does not apply in relation to a consumer’s
complaint if it was received by the trader before the coming into force of
section 308 .

### Miscellaneous

#### Competition in connection with motor fuel

##### Provision of information about competition in connection with motor fuel

311

311.1

The CMA may require an undertaking involved in, or connected with, the
distribution, supply or retail of motor fuel (“ U ”) to give specified
information to it where it considers that the information would assist the CMA
in—

311.1.a

assessing competition in the United Kingdom in connection with the retail of
motor fuel;

311.1.b

publishing information about competition in the United Kingdom in connection
with the retail of motor fuel;

311.1.c

making proposals, or giving information or advice, to the Secretary of State
about the need for, or the potential for, action to be taken (whether by the
Secretary of State or another person) and what that action should be for the
purposes of—

311.1.c.i

increasing competition in the United Kingdom in connection with the retail of
motor fuel;

311.1.c.ii

benefiting consumers of motor fuel;

311.1.d

assessing the effectiveness of any action taken as a result of proposals made,
or information or advice given, under  paragraph (c) .

311.2

The power conferred by  subsection (1)  is to be exercised by giving U a
notice (an “information notice”).

311.3

The CMA must include in an information notice—

311.3.a

the time at which, or the frequency with which, the information must be given
to the CMA;

311.3.b

the manner and form in which the information must be given to the CMA;

311.3.c

information about the possible consequences of not complying with the notice.

311.4

The power under this section to require U to give information to the CMA
includes the power to—

311.4.a

require U to take copies of or extracts from information;

311.4.b

require U to obtain or generate information;

311.4.c

require U to collect or retain information that they would not otherwise
collect or retain;

311.4.d

if any specified information is not given to the CMA, require U to state, to
the best of their knowledge and belief, both where that information is and why
it has not been given to the CMA.

311.5

An undertaking may not be required under this section to give the CMA a
privileged communication.

311.6

A “privileged communication” is a communication—

311.6.a

between a professional legal adviser and their client, or

311.6.b

made in connection with, or in contemplation of, legal proceedings,

which in proceedings in the High Court would be protected from disclosure on
grounds of legal professional privilege.

311.7

In the application of this section to Scotland—

311.7.a

the reference to the High Court is to be read as a reference to the Court of
Session, and

311.7.b

the reference to legal professional privilege is to be read as a reference to
the confidentiality of communications.

311.8

In this section—

      “ consumer ” has the same meaning as in Part 4 of EA 2002 (see section
183(1) of that Act);           “ motor fuel ” has the same meaning as in the
Motor Fuel (Composition and Content) Regulations 1999 ( S.I. 1999/3107 ) (see
regulation 2 of those Regulations), but as if paragraphs (c) and (d) of the
definition of that term were omitted;           “ specified ” means—
specified, or described, in the information notice, or           falling
within a category which is specified, or described, in the information notice;
“ United Kingdom ” includes a part of the United Kingdom.

311.9

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend the definition of “motor fuel”
in  subsection (8) .

311.10

Regulations under  subsection (9)  are subject to the negative procedure.

311.11

In this Chapter, “undertaking” has the same meaning it has for the purposes of
Part 1 of CA 1998 (competition: agreements, abuse of dominant position etc).

##### Penalties for failure to comply with notices under 

312

312.1

The CMA may impose a penalty on an undertaking where it considers that the
undertaking has, without reasonable excuse—

312.1.a

failed to comply with an information notice under  section 311 ;

312.1.b

destroyed, otherwise disposed of, falsified or concealed, or caused or
permitted the destruction, disposal, falsification or concealment of, any
document which the undertaking has been required to produce by an information
notice under that section;

312.1.c

given the CMA information which is false or misleading in a material
particular in connection with an information notice under that section;

312.1.d

given information which is false or misleading in a material particular to
another undertaking knowing that the information was to be used for the
purpose of giving information to the CMA in connection with an information
notice under that section.

312.2

The amount of a penalty imposed on an undertaking under this section may be
such amount as the CMA considers appropriate, provided it does not exceed the
amounts set out in subsection  (4) .

312.3

The amount of a penalty under this section must be—

312.3.a

a fixed amount,

312.3.b

an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, or

312.3.c

a combination of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a
daily rate.

312.4

The maximum amounts of a penalty that may be imposed on an undertaking are—

312.4.a

in the case of a fixed amount, an amount equal to 1% of the total value of the
undertaking’s turnover (both inside and outside the United Kingdom);

312.4.b

in the case of an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, for each day
an amount equal to 5% of the total value of the undertaking’s daily turnover
(both inside and outside the United Kingdom);

312.4.c

in the case of a combination of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by
reference to a daily rate, the amounts mentioned in  paragraph (a) , in
relation to the fixed amount, and  paragraph (b) , in relation to the amount
calculated by reference to a daily rate.

312.5

In imposing a penalty under this section by reference to a daily rate—

312.5.a

no account is to be taken of any days before the service on the undertaking
concerned of the provisional penalty notice under section 112(A1) of EA 2002
(as applied by  section 313 ), and

312.5.b

unless the CMA determines an earlier day (whether before or after the penalty
is imposed), the amount payable ceases to accumulate at the beginning of the
day on which the undertaking first complies with the requirement in question.

312.6

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision for determining the
turnover (both inside and outside the United Kingdom) of an undertaking for
the purposes of this section.

312.7

The regulations may, among other things—

312.7.a

make provision about amounts which are, or are not, to be included in an
undertaking’s turnover;

312.7.b

make provision about the date or dates by reference to which an undertaking’s
turnover is to be determined;

312.7.c

confer on the CMA the power to determine and make provision about matters
specified in the regulations (including the matters mentioned in paragraphs
(a)  and  (b) ).

312.8

Regulations under  subsection (6)  are subject to the negative procedure.

##### Procedure and appeals

313

313.1

Sections 112 (penalties: main procedural requirements), 113 (payments and
interest by instalments), section 114 (appeals) and 115 (recovery of
penalties) of EA 2002 apply in relation to a penalty imposed under  section
312  as they apply in relation to a penalty imposed under section 110(1) of
that Act.

313.2

For the purposes of this section—

313.2.a

sections 112 to 115 of EA 2002 are to be read as if references to “the
appropriate authority” were references to the CMA only;

313.2.b

section 114(5A) of EA 2002 is to be read as if the words “In the case of a
penalty imposed on a by the CMA or OFCOM,” were omitted;

313.2.c

section 114(12) of EA 2002 is to be read as if, for paragraph (b), there were
substituted—

313.2.c.b

“ the relevant guidance ” means the statement of policy which was most
recently published under  section 314  of the Digital Markets, Competition and
Consumers Act 2024 at the time of the act or omission giving rise to the
penalty.

##### Statement of policy on penalties

314

314.1

The CMA must prepare and publish a statement of policy in relation to the
exercise of powers to impose a penalty under  section 312 .

314.2

The statement must include a statement about the considerations relevant to
the determination of—

314.2.a

whether to impose a penalty under  section 312 , and

314.2.b

the nature and amount of any such penalty.

314.3

The CMA may revise its statement of policy and, where it does so, must publish
the revised statement.

314.4

In preparing or revising its statement of policy the CMA must consult—

314.4.a

the Secretary of State, and

314.4.b

such other persons as the CMA considers appropriate.

314.5

A statement of policy, or revised statement, may not be published under this
section without the approval of the Secretary of State.

314.6

Subsection (7)  applies where the CMA proposes to impose a penalty under
section 312  on an undertaking.

314.7

The CMA must have regard to the statement of policy most recently published
under this section at the time of the act or omission giving rise to the
penalty when deciding—

314.7.a

whether to impose the penalty, and

314.7.b

if so, the amount of the penalty.

##### Offences etc

315

######## Destroying or falsifying information

315.1

A person (“ P ”) commits an offence if, having been required to give
information to the CMA under  section 311 , P—

315.1.a

intentionally or recklessly destroys or otherwise disposes of it, falsifies or
conceals it, or

315.1.b

causes or permits its destruction, disposal, falsification or concealment.

######## False or misleading information

315.2

A person (“ P ”) commits an offence if—

315.2.a

P gives information to the CMA in connection with an information notice under
section 311 ,

315.2.b

the information is false or misleading in a material particular, and

315.2.c

P knows that it is or is reckless as to whether it is.

315.3

A person (“ P ”) commits an offence if P gives information to another person
which is false or misleading in a material particular and P—

315.3.a

either—

315.3.a.i

knows the information to be false or misleading in a material particular, or

315.3.a.ii

is reckless as to whether the information is false or misleading in a material
particular, and

315.3.b

knows that the information will be given to the CMA in connection with an
information notice under that section.

######## Sentences

315.4

A person guilty of an offence under this section is liable—

315.4.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to a fine;

315.4.b

on summary conviction in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding
the statutory maximum;

315.4.c

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or to a fine or to both.

######## Offences by officers of a body corporate etc

315.5

If an offence under this section committed by a body corporate is proved—

315.5.a

to have been committed with the consent or connivance of an officer of the
body corporate, or

315.5.b

to be attributable to neglect on the part of an officer of the body corporate,

the officer as well as the body corporate is guilty of the offence and liable
to be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

315.6

If the affairs of a body corporate are managed by its members,  subsection (5)
applies in relation to the acts and defaults of a member in connection with
the member’s functions of management as if the member were an officer of the
body corporate.

315.7

If an offence under this section committed by a partnership in Scotland is
proved—

315.7.a

to have been committed with the consent or connivance of a partner, or

315.7.b

to be attributable to neglect on the partner’s part,

the partner as well as the partnership is guilty of the offence and liable to
be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

315.8

In  subsection (7) , “ partner ” includes a person purporting to act as a
partner.

##### Penalties under 

316

316.1

The CMA may not impose a penalty on a person under  section 312  in relation
to an act or omission which constitutes an offence under  section 315  if the
person has, in relation to that act or omission, been found guilty of that
offence.

316.2

A person may not be found guilty of an offence under  section 315  by virtue
of an act or omission if the person has paid a penalty imposed under  section
312  in relation to that act or omission.

##### Information sharing

317

In Schedule 14 to EA 2002 (provisions about disclosure of information) at the
appropriate place insert—

      Chapter 1 of  Part 5  of the Digital Markets, Competition and Consumer
Act 2024.

##### Expiry of this Chapter

318

318.1

This Chapter, apart from  subsection (5)  of this section and  section 317 ,
expires at the end of the relevant period.

318.2

The “ relevant period ” means the period of five years beginning with the day
on which this Act is passed.

318.3

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this section to change the
definition of the “relevant period”.

318.4

Regulations under  subsection (3)  are subject to the affirmative procedure.

318.5

The expiry of this Chapter does not affect its continued operation in relation
to any information notice given under  section 311  before its expiry.

#### Provision of investigative assistance to overseas regulators

##### Provision of investigative assistance to overseas regulators

319

319.1

A relevant regulator (“ R ”) may assist an overseas regulator (“ O ”) in
accordance with the table in  subsection (2)  where—

319.1.a

O makes a request to R (see  section 320 ) for R to assist O’s carrying out of
functions which correspond or are similar to functions of R under a relevant
enactment,

319.1.b

R considers that it would be appropriate to assist O (see  section 321 ), and

319.1.c

where the request is made otherwise than under or in accordance with a
qualifying cooperation arrangement, the Secretary of State authorises R to
assist O (see  section 322 ).

319.2

The table in this subsection is—

    Where the enactment in question is— The regulator that may assist the
overseas regulator is— The regulator may assist the overseas regulator by—
Part 1 of CA 1998 (competition) the CMA exercising its powers under sections
26 to 29 of CA 1998 as if, by assisting O’s carrying out of functions which
correspond or are similar to the functions of the CMA under Part 1 of that
Act, the CMA were carrying out an investigation under section 25 of that Act
Part 3 of EA 2002 (mergers) the CMA exercising its powers under section 109 of
EA 2002 as if assisting O’s carrying out of functions which correspond or are
similar to the functions of the CMA under Part 3 of that Act were a “
permitted purpose ” for the purposes of that section Part 6 of EA 2002 (cartel
offence) the CMA exercising its powers under sections 193 and 194 of EA 2002
as if, by assisting O’s carrying out of functions which correspond or are
similar to the functions of the CMA under Part 6 of that Act, the CMA were
carrying out an investigation under section 192 of that Act Schedule 5 to CRA
2015 (investigatory powers) an enforcer for the purposes of Schedule 5 to CRA
2015 (see paragraph 2 of that Schedule) exercising the powers under Parts 3
and 4 of Schedule 5 to CRA 2015 in connection with an infringement of the law
of, or other requirement imposed in, the country or territory of O which
appears to R to make provision corresponding or similar to an enactment or
other obligation or rule of law listed in  Schedule 15  to this Act  Part 1 of
this Act (digital markets) the CMA exercising its powers under any of sections
69 ,  71  and  79  as if assisting O’s carrying out of a function which
corresponds or is similar to a digital markets function (as defined in section
118 ) were itself a digital markets function  Part 1 of this Act (digital
markets) the CMA exercising its powers under any of sections  72 ,  74  and
75  as if, by assisting O’s carrying out of any investigation which
corresponds or is similar to a digital markets investigation (as defined in
section  118 ), the CMA were carrying out a digital markets investigation

319.3

For the purposes of the exercise by R of the powers under Parts 3 and 4 of
Schedule 5 to CRA 2015 by virtue of this Chapter—

319.3.a

paragraphs 13, 19 and 20 of that Schedule are to be ignored;

319.3.b

where a power is exercisable only by an enforcer of a particular description,
the power is exercisable by R only if R is an enforcer of that description;

319.3.c

references in Part 4 of that Schedule to the enforcer’s legislation, in
relation to a domestic enforcer, are to be read in relation to R as references
to the law of, or other requirement imposed in, the country or territory of O
mentioned in the entry for that Schedule in the table in  subsection (2) .

319.4

Any reference in an enactment (other than in this Chapter) to the functions of
a relevant regulator under a relevant enactment includes a reference to those
functions as exercised by virtue of this Chapter.

319.5

In this Chapter—

      “ cooperation arrangement ” means an arrangement or agreement relating
in whole or in part to cooperation in matters relating to the subject matter
of a relevant enactment;           “ overseas regulator ” or “ O ” means a
person or body in a country or territory outside the United Kingdom which
appears to R to exercise functions of a public nature corresponding or similar
to functions of R;           “ qualifying cooperation arrangement ” means any
cooperation arrangement—         to which the United Kingdom and the country
or territory of O are parties, and           which provides for the provision
of mutual assistance as between the United Kingdom and that country or
territory, or as between R and persons or bodies in that country or territory,
in relation to matters relating to—         functions of R under a relevant
enactment, or           functions of O which correspond or are similar to
those functions;                       “ relevant enactment ” means an
enactment listed in the first column of the table in  subsection (2) ;
“ relevant regulator ” or “ R ” means a regulator listed in the second column
of the table in  subsection (2) .

##### Requests for investigative assistance

320

320.1

Subsection (2)  makes provision about requests from O for the purposes of
section 319 (1) (a) .

320.2

A request from O to R for R to assist O must—

320.2.a

be made in writing,

320.2.b

describe the matter in respect of which R’s assistance is requested, and

320.2.c

include details of any penalty or sanction that could be imposed as a result
of the carrying out by O of the functions in respect of which R’s assistance
is requested.

##### The appropriateness of providing investigative assistance

321

321.1

This subsection makes provision about how R is to consider whether it would be
appropriate to assist O for the purposes of  section 319 (1) (b) .

321.2

In considering whether it would be appropriate to assist O, R must have regard
to whether—

321.2.a

R would be able to exercise its powers under the relevant enactment concerned
in a corresponding or similar case arising in the United Kingdom;

321.2.b

the United Kingdom and the country or territory of O, or R and O, are parties
to a cooperation arrangement;

321.2.c

the matter in respect of which the assistance is requested is sufficiently
serious to justify R assisting O.

321.3

R may consider that it would not be appropriate to assist O unless O
undertakes to make such contribution as R considers appropriate towards the
cost of R doing so.

321.4

R must consider that it would not be appropriate to assist O where any of
subsections  (5)  to  (8)  apply.

321.5

This subsection applies where R considers that—

321.5.a

a person or body in the country or territory of O (whether or not O) would not
provide corresponding or substantially similar assistance to R, unless R
considers that there is an overriding public benefit to the United Kingdom in
assisting O;

321.5.b

assisting O would be contrary to the public interest.

321.6

This subsection applies where—

321.6.a

the matter to which the request relates concerns the investigation of crime or
the bringing of criminal proceedings, and

321.6.b

the request is made otherwise than under or in accordance with a qualifying
cooperation arrangement.

321.7

This subsection applies where R would not be able to disclose, under Part 9 of
EA 2002 (information), to O any information obtained by R in the course of
assisting O.

321.8

This subsection applies where—

321.8.a

the request relates to a matter in respect of which in a corresponding or
similar case arising in the United Kingdom R would not be able to exercise its
powers under the relevant enactment concerned unless R has reasonable grounds
for suspecting that there has, or may have, been a breach of the law (“the
relevant UK law”), and

321.8.b

R does not have reasonable grounds for suspecting that there has, or may have,
been a breach of the law of the country or territory of O which appears to R
to make provision corresponding or similar to the relevant UK law in question.

321.9

For the purposes of  subsection (8) (b) , R is to regard as conclusive a
certificate issued by O as to whether there has, or may have, been a breach of
the law of the country or territory of O.

##### Authorisation of the provision of investigative assistance

322

322.1

This section makes provision about how the Secretary of State authorises R to
assist O for the purposes of  section 319 (1) (c) .

322.2

The Secretary of State may authorise R to assist O either—

322.2.a

in relation to one or more specific requests for assistance, or

322.2.b

generally in respect of requests for assistance of a particular description
(including in respect of requests from particular overseas regulators).

322.3

The Secretary of State may withdraw any general authorisation given under
subsection (2) (b) .

322.4

The Secretary of State must publish—

322.4.a

any general authorisation given under  subsection (2) (b) ;

322.4.b

notice of any withdrawal of a general authorisation under  subsection (3) .

322.5

In considering whether to authorise R to assist O (whether specifically or
generally), the Secretary of State must have regard to whether—

322.5.a

O’s request for assistance is made under, or in accordance with, the terms of
an arrangement or agreement (other than a qualifying cooperation arrangement)
to which the United Kingdom is a party (and, where it is, the Secretary of
State must also have regard to the terms of the arrangement or agreement);

322.5.b

it would be more appropriate, in relation to the matter in respect of which
R’s assistance is requested, for—

322.5.b.i

any of R’s powers under the relevant enactment concerned to be exercised
solely on behalf of R (and not by virtue of this Chapter), or

322.5.b.ii

for functions to be exercised by another person or body in the United Kingdom
or in a country or territory other than the country or territory of O;

322.5.c

R assisting O would be contrary to the public interest.

322.6

In authorising R to assist O, the Secretary of State may impose conditions on
R doing so.

322.7

The conditions that may be imposed include conditions—

322.7.a

requiring R, before assisting O, to obtain an undertaking from O that any
information obtained by R in assisting O will not be used, or will only be
used, for specified purposes;

322.7.b

requiring R not to use specified powers that would otherwise be available to R
in assisting O;

322.7.c

requiring R to assist O by using specified powers available to R only in a
specified manner;

322.7.d

requiring R to assist O only in respect of specified matters.

322.8

In  subsection (7) , “ specified ” means specified in a condition imposed by
the Secretary of State under  subsection (6) .

##### Notifications in respect of requests for investigative assistance

323

323.1

R must notify the Secretary of State that R has received a request for
assistance from O where—

323.1.a

R considers that it would be appropriate for R to assist O, and

323.1.b

the Secretary of State has not given R a general authorisation to provide O
with the assistance requested (see  section 322 (2) (b) ).

323.2

But  subsection (1)  does not apply where O’s request is made under or in
accordance with a qualifying cooperation arrangement.

323.3

R must notify O as to whether R will be providing the assistance requested
and, where relevant, of any conditions imposed on that assistance (see
section 322 (6) ).

##### Guidance in connection with investigative assistance

324

324.1

The CMA must prepare and publish guidance about—

324.1.a

the making and consideration of requests for assistance under this Chapter,
and

324.1.b

the provision of assistance under this Chapter.

324.2

The CMA may at any time prepare and publish revised or new guidance.

324.3

No guidance is to be published under this section without the approval of the
Secretary of State.

324.4

In preparing guidance under this section the CMA must consult such persons as
it considers appropriate.

324.5

A relevant regulator must have regard to the guidance for the time being in
force when it is exercising functions under or in connection this Chapter.

##### Amendments to other legislation

325

Schedule 28  makes amendments to other legislation in connection with the
provision made by this Chapter.

#### Miscellaneous

##### Disclosing information overseas

326

326.1

Part 9 of EA 2002 (information) is amended as follows.

326.2

For section 243 (overseas disclosures) substitute—

########### Overseas disclosures for both overseas and domestic purposes

326.2.243A

326.2.243A.1

A public authority which holds information to which section 237 applies (“the
discloser”) may disclose that information to an overseas public authority for
the purpose of facilitating both—

326.2.243A.1.a

the exercise by the discloser of any function it has under or by virtue of
this Act or any other enactment, and

326.2.243A.1.b

the exercise by the overseas public authority of any function which it has
relating to—

326.2.243A.1.b.i

carrying out investigations in connection with the enforcement of any relevant
law by means of civil proceedings;

326.2.243A.1.b.ii

bringing civil proceedings for the enforcement of such law or the conduct of
such proceedings;

326.2.243A.1.b.iii

the investigation of crime;

326.2.243A.1.b.iv

bringing criminal proceedings or the conduct of such proceedings;

326.2.243A.1.b.v

deciding whether to start or bring to an end such investigations or
proceedings.

326.2.243A.2

Subsection (1)  does not apply to any of the following—

326.2.243A.2.a

information which is held by a person who is a private designated enforcer for
the purposes of  Chapter 3  of  Part 3  of the Digital Markets, Competition
and Consumers Act 2024 (see  section 151  of that Act);

326.2.243A.2.b

information which comes to a public authority in connection with an
investigation under Part 4 or section 174 of this Act;

326.2.243A.2.c

information which comes to a public authority in connection with an
investigation under section 11 of the Competition Act 1980;

326.2.243A.2.d

legacy information within the meaning of  subsection (5) .

326.2.243A.3

In  subsection (1) (a) , the reference to an enactment includes a reference to
an enactment contained in—

326.2.243A.3.a

an Act of the Scottish Parliament;

326.2.243A.3.b

Northern Ireland legislation;

326.2.243A.3.c

subordinate legislation.

326.2.243A.4

In  subsection (1) (b) (i) , “ relevant law ” means—

326.2.243A.4.a

this Act, any enactment specified in Schedule 14 and such subordinate
legislation as is specified by order for the purposes of section 238(1);

326.2.243A.4.b

any enactment, obligation or rule of law specified in  Schedule 15  to the
Digital Markets, Competition and Consumers Act 2024 (consumer protection
enactments);

326.2.243A.4.c

any legislation, or any obligation or rule of law in a country or territory
outside the United Kingdom which appears to the discloser to make provision
corresponding or similar to anything within paragraphs  (a)  and  (b) .

326.2.243A.5

In  subsection (2) (d) , “ legacy information ” means information which—

326.2.243A.5.a

comes to a public authority in connection with the exercise of its functions
under or by virtue of paragraphs 15 to 18 of Schedule 24 relating to
investigations under Parts 4 or 6 of the 1973 Act;

326.2.243A.5.b

came to a public authority—

326.2.243A.5.b.i

before the coming into force of this section, and

326.2.243A.5.b.ii

in connection with the exercise of its functions under or by virtue of
paragraphs 15 to 18 of Schedule 24 relating to investigations under Part 5 of
the 1973 Act;

326.2.243A.5.c

came to a public authority—

326.2.243A.5.c.i

before 1 July 2021, and

326.2.243A.5.c.ii

in connection with an investigation under Part 3 of the Enterprise Act 2002.

########### Overseas disclosures for overseas purposes only

326.2.243B

326.2.243B.1

A public authority which holds information to which section 237 applies (“the
discloser”) may disclose that information to an overseas public authority for
the purpose mentioned in  section 243A (1) (b) .

326.2.243B.2

Subsection (2)  of  section 243A  applies for the purposes of  subsection (1)
of  this section  as it applies for the purposes of  subsection (1)  of  that
section .

########### Overseas disclosures for designated cooperation arrangement purposes

326.2.243C

326.2.243C.1

A public authority which holds information to which section 237 applies (“the
discloser”) may disclose that information to an overseas public authority for
a purpose permitted under or by virtue of a designated cooperation
arrangement.

326.2.243C.2

“ Designated cooperation arrangement ” means an arrangement or agreement that
meets all of Conditions A to D.

326.2.243C.3

Condition A is that the arrangement or agreement is between—

326.2.243C.3.a

a public authority and an overseas public authority, or

326.2.243C.3.b

the United Kingdom and a country or territory.

326.2.243C.4

Condition B is that the arrangement or agreement relates to cooperation
between—

326.2.243C.4.a

the public authority and the overseas public authority, or

326.2.243C.4.b

public authorities in the United Kingdom and persons or bodies in that country
or territory,

for the purposes of facilitating the exercise of functions related to anything
mentioned in sub-paragraphs  (i)  to  (v)  of  section 243A (1) (b) .

326.2.243C.5

Condition C is that the arrangement or agreement provides for—

326.2.243C.5.a

the overseas public authority and the public authority, or

326.2.243C.5.b

a person or body in that country or territory and public authorities in the
United Kingdom,

to provide corresponding or substantially similar assistance to each other for
the purposes of facilitating the exercise of functions related to anything
mentioned in sub-paragraphs  (i)  to  (v)  of  section 243A (1) (b) .

326.2.243C.6

Condition D is that the arrangement or agreement is designated in regulations
made by the Secretary of State.

326.2.243C.7

Before designating an arrangement or agreement in regulations under
subsection (6) , the Secretary of State must have regard in particular to
whether the arrangement or agreement contains provision restricting or
preventing—

326.2.243C.7.a

the use for another purpose of information disclosed for a purpose permitted
under or by virtue of the arrangement or agreement;

326.2.243C.7.b

the further disclosure of such information.

326.2.243C.8

The Secretary of State may not designate an arrangement or agreement in
regulations under  subsection (6)  unless the Secretary of State is satisfied
that—

326.2.243C.8.a

the law and practice of the country or territory, or the country or territory
of the overseas public authority, with whom the arrangement or agreement is
with provides appropriate protection against self-incrimination in criminal
proceedings, and

326.2.243C.8.b

the law and practice of that country or territory provides appropriate
protection in relation to the storage and disclosure of confidential
information.

326.2.243C.9

For the purposes of  subsection (8) , protection is appropriate if it provides
protection in relation to the matter in question which corresponds or is
substantially similar to that so provided in any part of the United Kingdom.

326.2.243C.10

Regulations under  subsection (6)  are to be made by statutory instrument
subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of either House of
Parliament.

########### Use and further disclosure of information disclosed under sections 

326.2.243D

326.2.243D.1

Subsections  (2)  and  (3)  apply to information disclosed by virtue of
section 243A  to the extent that the disclosure was to facilitate the exercise
by the discloser of any function it has under or by virtue of this Act or any
other enactment (“the original function”) in relation to a particular matter
(“the original matter”).

326.2.243D.2

The information must not be used by the overseas public authority other than
for facilitating the exercise by the discloser of the original function in
relation to the original matter unless—

326.2.243D.2.a

the use is for the purpose of facilitating the exercise by the discloser of
any function it has under this Act or any other enactment (other than the
original function) whether or not in relation to the original matter, and

326.2.243D.2.b

the discloser consents to the use of that information for that purpose.

326.2.243D.3

The information must not be further disclosed by the overseas public authority
unless—

326.2.243D.3.a

the further disclosure is for the purpose of facilitating the exercise by the
discloser of any function it has under this Act or any other enactment
(whether or not the original function) whether or not in relation to the
original matter, and

326.2.243D.3.b

the discloser consents to the further disclosure of the information for that
purpose.

326.2.243D.4

Subsections  (5)  and  (6)  apply to information disclosed by virtue of
section  243A  or  243B  to the extent that the disclosure was to facilitate
the exercise of functions of an overseas public authority relating to anything
mentioned in sub-paragraphs  (i)  to  (v)  of  section 243A (1) (b)  (“the
original function”) in relation to a particular matter (“the original
matter”).

326.2.243D.5

The information must not be used by the overseas public authority other than
for facilitating the exercise by the authority of the original function in
relation to the original matter unless—

326.2.243D.5.a

the use is for the purpose of facilitating the exercise of a function which
the authority has relating to anything mentioned in sub-paragraphs  (i)  to
(v)  of  section 243A (1) (b)  (other than the original function) whether or
not in relation to the original matter, and

326.2.243D.5.b

the discloser consents to the use of that information for that purpose.

326.2.243D.6

The information must not be further disclosed by the overseas public authority
unless—

326.2.243D.6.a

the further disclosure is for the purpose of facilitating the exercise of any
of its functions relating to anything mentioned in sub-paragraphs  (i)  to
(v)  of  subsection (1) (b)  of  section 243A   (whether or not the original
function) whether or not in relation to the original matter, and

326.2.243D.6.b

the discloser consents to the further disclosure of the information for that
purpose.

326.2.243D.7

In deciding whether to consent to the use or further disclosure of information
for the purposes of subsection  (2) (b) ,  (3) (b) ,  (5) (b)  or  (6) (b) ,
the discloser must have regard to the considerations in  section 243F  to
which it would be required to have regard if it were deciding to disclose the
information under  243A  or  243B .

326.2.243D.8

Nothing in this section prevents information being used, or further disclosed,
by the overseas public authority if that use, or further disclosure, is
required under the law of the country or territory of the authority.

########### Directions by the Secretary of State relating to overseas disclosures under sections 

326.2.243E

326.2.243E.1

The Secretary of State may direct that a disclosure permitted under section
243A  or  243B  must not be made if the Secretary of State thinks that, in
connection with any matter in respect of which the disclosure could be made,
it is more appropriate—

326.2.243E.1.a

if any investigation is to be carried out, that it is carried out by an
authority in the United Kingdom or in another specified country or territory
(rather than by the overseas public authority);

326.2.243E.1.b

if any proceedings are to be brought, that they are brought in a court in the
United Kingdom or in another specified country or territory (rather than in
the country or territory of the overseas authority).

326.2.243E.2

In  subsection (1) , “ specified ” means specified in the direction.

326.2.243E.3

The Secretary of State must take such steps as the Secretary of State thinks
are appropriate to bring a direction under  subsection (1)  to the attention
of persons likely to be affected by it.

########### Relevant considerations relating to overseas disclosures under sections 

326.2.243F

326.2.243F.1

This section applies when a public authority is deciding whether to make a
disclosure under section  243A  or  243B .

326.2.243F.2

In deciding whether to make a disclosure under  section 243A , the public
authority must have regard in particular to the following considerations—

326.2.243F.2.a

whether the law and practice of the country or territory to whose authority
the disclosure would be made provides appropriate protection against self-
incrimination in criminal proceedings;

326.2.243F.2.b

whether the law and practice of that country or territory provides appropriate
protection in relation to the storage and disclosure of confidential
information.

326.2.243F.3

In deciding whether to make a disclosure under  section 243B , the public
authority must have regard in particular to the considerations in  subsection
(2)  and the following additional considerations—

326.2.243F.3.a

whether the matter in respect of which the disclosure is sought is
sufficiently serious to justify making the disclosure;

326.2.243F.3.b

whether the disclosure would further the aims or purposes of any convention or
treaty relating in whole or in part to cooperation in matters relating to
competition or consumer protection to which the United Kingdom and the country
or territory of the authority to whom the disclosure would be made are
parties;

326.2.243F.3.c

whether there are arrangements in place for the provision of mutual assistance
as between the United Kingdom and that country or territory to whose authority
the disclosure would be made in relation to the disclosure of information of
the kind to which section 237 applies;

326.2.243F.3.d

whether a person or body in that country or territory would assist the public
authority in a way that corresponds or is substantially similar to the
assistance that it is proposed the public authority give to the overseas
public authority by making the disclosure.

326.2.243F.4

For the purposes of this section, protection is appropriate if it provides
protection in relation to the matter in question which corresponds or is
substantially similar to that so provided in any part of the United Kingdom.

326.2.243F.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend subsections  (2)  and  (3)  so
as to—

326.2.243F.5.a

alter any consideration for the time being included in those subsections;

326.2.243F.5.b

add further considerations;

326.2.243F.5.c

remove any considerations.

326.2.243F.6

Regulations under  subsection (5)  are to be made by statutory instrument and
are subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of either House of
Parliament.

326.3

In section 244 (specified information: considerations relevant to disclosure)—

326.3.a

in subsection (2), for “information whose disclosure the authority thinks is
contrary to the public interest” substitute  “sensitive information” ;

326.3.b

in subsection (3), for the words after “(so far as practicable)” to the end of
paragraph (b) substitute  “any commercial information or private information”
.

326.4

In section 245 (offences) in subsection (2), for “243(4)” substitute  “ 243E ”
.

326.5

For section 246 substitute—

########### Interpretation

326.5.246A

In this Part—

      “ commercial information ” means information relating to any business of
an undertaking whose disclosure the public authority concerned or, for the
purposes of  section 243C  the Secretary of State, thinks might significantly
harm the undertaking’s legitimate business interests;           “ confidential
information ” means commercial information, private information or sensitive
information;           “ overseas public authority ” means a person or body in
any country or territory outside the United Kingdom which appears to the
discloser (within the meaning of any of sections  243A  to  243C ) to exercise
functions of a public nature in relation to anything mentioned in sub-
paragraphs  (i)  to  (v)  of  section 243A (1) (b) ;           “ private
information ” mean information relating to the private affairs of an
individual whose disclosure the public authority concerned, or for the
purposes of  section 243C  the Secretary of State, thinks might significantly
harm the individual’s interests;           “ sensitive information ” means
information whose disclosure the public authority concerned or, for the
purposes of  section 243C  the Secretary of State, thinks would be contrary to
the public interest;           “ subordinate legislation ” has the same
meaning as in section 21(1) of the Interpretation Act 1978 and includes an
instrument made under—         an Act of the Scottish Parliament;
Northern Ireland legislation.

326.6

In section 59 of the Companies (Audit, Investigations and Community
Enterprises) Act 2004 (information), in subsection (6)—

326.6.a

for “section 243(6)” substitute  “ section 243F (2)  and  (3) ” ;

326.6.b

for “(overseas disclosures)” substitute  “(relevant considerations relating to
overseas disclosures)” .
