### General

#### Interpretation

330

In this Act—

      “ CA 1998 ” means the Competition Act 1998;           “ CRA 2015 ” means
the Consumer Rights Act 2015;           “ EA 2002 ” means the Enterprise Act
2002;           “ ERRA 2013 ” means the Enterprise and Regulatory Reform Act
2013;           “ the CMA ” means the Competition and Markets Authority;
“ the data protection legislation ” has the same meaning as in the Data
Protection Act 2018 (see section 3 of that Act);           “ digital content ”
means data which is produced and supplied in digital form;           “
enactment ” means an enactment whenever passed or made and includes—
an enactment contained in any Order in Council, order, rules, regulations,
scheme, warrant, byelaw or other instrument made under an Act,           an
enactment contained in, or in an instrument made under, an Act of the Scottish
Parliament,           an enactment contained in, or in an instrument made
under, a Measure or Act of Senedd Cymru,           an enactment contained in,
or in an instrument made under, Northern Ireland legislation, and
any assimilated direct legislation;                 “ firm ” means any entity,
whether or not a legal person, that is not an individual and includes a body
corporate, a corporation sole and a partnership or other unincorporated
association;           “ United Kingdom national ” means—         a British
citizen, a British overseas territories citizen, a British National (Overseas)
or a British Overseas citizen;           a person who is a British subject
under the British Nationality Act 1981;           a British protected person
within the meaning of that Act;                 “ working day ” means any day
other than—         a Saturday or Sunday, or           a day that is a bank
holiday in any part of the United Kingdom under the Banking and Financial
Dealings Act 1971.

#### Data protection

331

331.1

This section applies to a duty or power to process information that is imposed
or conferred by or under any provision of this Act.

331.2

A duty or power to which this section applies does not require or authorise
the processing of information which would contravene the data protection
legislation (but the duty or power is to be taken into account in determining
whether the processing would contravene that legislation).

#### Notices

332

332.1

This section  applies in relation to a notice given to a person—

332.1.a

under this Act by the CMA, or

332.1.b

under  Part 3  by another enforcer (within the meaning of that Part).

332.2

The notice may be given by—

332.2.a

delivering it to the person,

332.2.b

leaving it at the person’s proper address,

332.2.c

sending it by post to the person at that address, or

332.2.d

sending it to the person by email to their email address.

332.3

A notice to a body corporate may be given in accordance with subsection  (2)
to any officer of that body.

332.4

A notice to a partnership may be given in accordance with subsection  (2)  to
any partner or a person who has the control or management of the partnership
business.

332.5

A notice to a firm that is not a body corporate or a partnership may be given
in accordance with subsection  (2)  to any member of the governing body of the
firm.

332.6

A person’s proper address is—

332.6.a

in a case where the person has specified an address as one at which the
person, or someone acting on the person’s behalf, will accept service of
notices or other documents, that address;

332.6.b

in any other case, the address determined in accordance with  subsection (7) .

332.7

A person’s proper address is (if  subsection (6) (a)  does not apply)—

332.7.a

in the case of a body corporate, its registered or principal office;

332.7.b

in the case of a partnership, the principal office of the partnership;

332.7.c

in the case of a firm that is not a body corporate or a partnership, the
principal office of the firm;

332.7.d

in a case where none of  paragraphs (a)  to  (c)  apply, any address at which
the CMA or other enforcer giving the notice believes, on reasonable grounds,
that the notice will come to the attention of the person.

332.8

A person’s email address is—

332.8.a

any email address published for the time being by that person as an address
for contacting that person, or

332.8.b

if there is no such published address, any email address by means of which the
CMA or other enforcer believes, on reasonable grounds, that the notice will
come to the attention of that person.

332.9

In the case of—

332.9.a

a body corporate registered outside the United Kingdom,

332.9.b

a partnership carrying on business outside the United Kingdom, or

332.9.c

any other type of firm with offices outside the United Kingdom,

references to its principal office include references to its principal office
in the United Kingdom or, if it has no principal office in the United Kingdom,
any place in the United Kingdom where it carries on business or conducts
activities.

332.10

In  this section  “ officer ”, in relation to any body corporate, means a
director, manager, secretary or other similar officer of the body.

332.11

This section  does not limit any other lawful means of giving notice.

#### Consultation

333

A duty to consult under or by virtue of this Act may be satisfied by
consultation that took place wholly or partly before the passing of this Act.

#### Financial provision

334

There is to be paid out of money provided by Parliament—

334.a

any expenses incurred by the Secretary of State or the CMA under or by virtue
of this Act, and

334.b

any increase attributable to this Act in the sums payable under any other Act
out of money so provided.

#### Minor and consequential amendments

335

Schedule 30  contains minor and consequential amendments.

#### Power to make further consequential provision

336

336.1

The appropriate authority may by regulations make provision that is
consequential on this Act or on any provision made under it.

336.2

The power to make regulations under this section includes power to amend,
repeal or revoke provision made by an enactment passed or made before the end
of the Session in which this Act is passed.

336.3

Regulations under this section are subject to the affirmative procedure if
they amend, repeal or revoke any provision of primary legislation.

336.4

Regulations under this section to which  subsection (3)  does not apply are
subject to the negative procedure.

336.5

In this section—

      “ appropriate authority ” means—         in the case of regulations
under this section that contain amendments only in relation to tax, the
Treasury;           in any other case, the Secretary of State;
“ primary legislation ” means—         an Act of Parliament (including this
Act);           an Act of the Scottish Parliament;           a Measure or Act
of Senedd Cymru;           Northern Ireland legislation.

#### Regulations

337

337.1

A power to make regulations under any provision of this Act includes power to
make—

337.1.a

consequential, supplementary, incidental, transitional or saving provision;

337.1.b

different provision for different purposes.

337.2

Regulations under this Act are to be made by statutory instrument.

337.3

Where regulations under this Act are subject to “the affirmative procedure”,
the regulations may not be made unless a draft of the statutory instrument
containing them has been laid before, and approved by a resolution of, each
House of Parliament.

337.4

Where regulations under this Act are subject to “the negative procedure”, the
statutory instrument containing them is subject to annulment in pursuance of a
resolution of either House of Parliament.

337.5

In the case of regulations under section  336  made by the Treasury, the
references in subsections (3) and (4) to each or either House of Parliament
are to be read as references to the House of Commons only.

337.6

Any provision that may be made by regulations under this Act subject to the
negative procedure may be made in regulations subject to the affirmative
procedure.

337.7

This section does not apply to regulations under  section 339 .

#### Extent

338

338.1

Subject to subsection (2), this Act extends to England and Wales, Scotland and
Northern Ireland.

338.2

Any amendment, repeal or revocation made by this Act has the same extent as
the provision amended, repealed or revoked.

#### Commencement

339

339.1

Except as provided by subsections  (2)  and  (3) , this Act comes into force
on such day as the Secretary of State may by regulations appoint.

339.2

The following provisions come into force on the day on which this Act is
passed—

339.2.a

section 130  (and  Schedule 7 );

339.2.b

this Part, other than  section 335  (and  Schedule 30 );

339.2.c

any other provision of this Act so far as it confers power to make regulations
or is otherwise necessary for enabling the exercise of such a power on or
after the day on which this Act is passed.

339.3

Section 129  (and  Schedule 6 ) come into force at the end of the period of
two months beginning with the day on which this Act is passed.

339.4

Different days may be appointed under  subsection (1)  for different purposes.

339.5

The Secretary of State may by regulations make transitional or saving
provision in connection with the coming into force of any provision of this
Act.

339.6

The power to make regulations under subsection  (5)  includes power to make
different provision for different purposes.

339.7

Regulations under this section are to be made by statutory instrument.

#### Short title

340

This Act may be cited as the Digital Markets, Competition and Consumers Act
2024.

## Schedules

  Procedure relating to commitments

Section 36

##### Application of Schedule

1

This Schedule applies for the purposes of Chapters  3  and  4  in relation to—

1.a

accepting a commitment,

1.b

accepting a variation of a commitment (a “requested variation”), or

1.c

releasing an undertaking from the requirement to comply with a commitment.

##### Procedure for accepting a commitment or requested variation

2

2.1

Before accepting a commitment or a requested variation the CMA must—

2.1.a

publish a notice under this paragraph, and

2.1.b

consider any representations made in accordance with the notice and not
withdrawn.

2.2

The notice must include—

2.2.a

the commitment or requested variation that the CMA proposes to accept,

2.2.b

the conduct requirement or, as the case may be, actual or suspected adverse
effect on competition to which the commitment or variation relates,

2.2.c

the CMA’s reasons for its proposed decision, and

2.2.d

the period within which representations may be made in relation to the
proposed commitment or requested variation.

3

3.1

Before accepting a modification of a commitment or requested variation, of
which notice has been given under paragraph  2 (1) , the CMA must—

3.1.a

publish a notice under this paragraph, and

3.1.b

consider any representations made in accordance with the notice and not
withdrawn.

3.2

The notice must include—

3.2.a

the proposed modifications,

3.2.b

the reasons for them, and

3.2.c

the period within which representations may be made in relation to them.

4

The CMA must publish notice of its decision on whether to, and the form in
which it will, accept a commitment or a requested variation as soon as
reasonably practicable.

5

The requirements of paragraphs  2  and  3  do not apply in relation to a
proposed modification which the CMA does not consider material.

##### Procedure for releasing an undertaking from a commitment

6

6.1

Before releasing an undertaking from a commitment the CMA must—

6.1.a

publish a notice under this paragraph, and

6.1.b

consider any representations made in accordance with the notice and not
withdrawn.

6.2

The notice must include—

6.2.a

that the CMA proposes to release the undertaking from the commitment,

6.2.b

the reasons for the CMA’s proposal, and

6.2.c

the period within which representations may be made in relation to the
proposal.

7

The CMA must publish a notice of its decision on whether to release an
undertaking from a commitment as soon as reasonably practicable.

  Mergers: holding of interests and rights

Section 58

##### Joint interests

1

If two or more persons each hold an interest or right jointly, each of them is
treated as holding that interest or right.

##### Joint arrangements

2

2.1

If interests or rights held by a person and interests or rights held by
another person are the subject of a joint arrangement between those persons,
each of them is treated as holding the combined interests or rights of both of
them.

2.2

A “joint arrangement” is an arrangement between the holders of interests or
rights that they will exercise all or substantially all the rights conferred
by their respective interests, or their respective rights, jointly in a way
that is pre-determined by the arrangement.

##### Interests held by nominees

3

An interest held by a person as nominee for another is to be treated as held
by the other (and not by the nominee).

##### Rights treated as held by person who controls their exercise

4

4.1

Where a person controls a right, the right is to be treated as held by that
person (and not by the person who in fact holds the right, unless that person
also controls it).

4.2

A person “controls” a right if, by virtue of any arrangement between that
person and others, the right is exercisable only—

4.2.a

by that person,

4.2.b

in accordance with that person’s directions or instructions, or

4.2.c

with that person’s consent or concurrence.

##### Rights exercisable only in certain circumstances etc

5

5.1

Rights that are exercisable by a person only in certain circumstances are to
be treated as held by the person only—

5.1.a

when the circumstances have arisen, and for so long as they continue to
obtain, or

5.1.b

when the circumstances are within the control of the person.

5.2

But rights that are exercisable by an administrator or by creditors while an
entity is in relevant insolvency proceedings are not to be regarded as held by
the administrator or creditors even while the entity is in those proceedings.

5.3

“ Relevant insolvency proceedings ” means—

5.3.a

administration within the meaning of the Insolvency Act 1986,

5.3.b

administration within the meaning of the Insolvency (Northern Ireland) Order
1989 ( S.I. 1989/2405 (N.I. 19)) , or

5.3.c

proceedings under the insolvency law of another country or territory during
which an entity’s assets and affairs are subject to the control or supervision
of a third party or creditor.

5.4

Rights that are normally exercisable but are temporarily incapable of exercise
are not for that reason to be treated as not being held.

##### Rights attached to shares held by way of security

6

Rights attached to shares held by way of security provided by a person are to
be treated as held by that person—

6.a

where apart from the right to exercise them for the purpose of preserving the
value of the security, or of realising it, the rights are exercisable only in
accordance with that person’s instructions, and

6.b

where the shares are held in connection with the granting of loans as part of
normal business activities and apart from the right to exercise them for the
purpose of preserving the value of the security, or of realising it, the
rights are exercisable only in that person’s interests.

##### Arrangements

7

7.1

In this Schedule “ arrangement ” includes—

7.1.a

any scheme, agreement or understanding, whether or not it is legally
enforceable, and

7.1.b

any convention, custom or practice of any kind.

7.2

But something does not count as an arrangement unless there is at least some
degree of stability about it (whether by its nature or terms, the time it has
been in existence or otherwise).

4

After section 47D insert—

######## Proceedings under section 47A or collective proceedings: declaratory relief

4.47DA

4.47DA.1

A declaration granted by the Tribunal in proceedings under section 47A or
collective proceedings has the same effect as a declaration granted by the
High Court.

4.47DA.2

A declarator granted by the Tribunal in proceedings under section 47A or
collective proceedings has the same effect as a declarator granted by the
Court of Session.

4.47DA.3

In deciding whether to grant a declaration in proceedings under section 47A or
collective proceedings, the Tribunal must apply the principles that the High
Court would apply in deciding whether to grant a declaration.

4.47DA.4

In deciding whether to grant a declarator in proceedings under section 47A or
collective proceedings, the Tribunal must apply the principles that the Court
of Session would apply in deciding whether to grant a declarator.

4.47DA.5

The Tribunal may grant a declaration or declarator in proceedings under
section 47A or collective proceedings whether or not any other remedy is
claimed.

Before subsection (5) insert—

2.5.4C

For the purposes of this Part, a relevant merger situation has also been
created if—

2.5.4C.a

two or more enterprises have ceased to be distinct enterprises at a time or in
circumstances falling within section 24; and

2.5.4C.b

each of the conditions mentioned in  subsections (4D)  to  (4F)  is satisfied.

2.5.4D

The condition mentioned in this subsection is that, were it not for the
enterprises concerned ceasing to be distinct enterprises, in relation to the
supply of goods or services of any description, at least 33 per cent of all
the goods or (as the case may be) services of that description which are
supplied in the United Kingdom, or in a substantial part of the United
Kingdom, would be supplied—

2.5.4D.a

by the person or persons by whom one of the enterprises concerned (“ E ”)
would be carried on, or

2.5.4D.b

to that person or those persons,

in connection with E or any other enterprise concerned with which E is under
common ownership or common control.

2.5.4E

turnover in the United Kingdom of E exceeds £350 million.

2.5.4F

enterprises concerned ceasing to be distinct enterprises, an enterprise within
subsection (4G) would satisfy one or more of the following additional
conditions—

2.5.4F.a

the enterprise would be carried on by a body of persons corporate or
unincorporate formed or recognised under the law of any part of the United
Kingdom;

2.5.4F.b

on in the United Kingdom;

2.5.4F.c

the person, or persons, by whom the enterprise would be carried on supply
goods or services to a person or persons in the United Kingdom in connection
with the enterprise.

2.5.4G

2.5.4G.a

any enterprise concerned other than—

2.5.4G.a.i

E, or

2.5.4G.a.ii

(4C)  of that section.

After subsection (3) insert—

9.4.3A

In exercising the power under subsection (1) to amend or replace the condition
mentioned in subsection  (4D)  or  (4E)  of section 23 or any condition which

new condition continues to operate by reference to the degree of commercial
strength that at least one of the enterprises concerned would have had if the
enterprises concerned had not ceased to be distinct enterprises.

7

After section 34ZC (sections 34ZA and 34ZB: supplementary) insert—

######## Fast-track reference requests

7.34ZD

7.34ZD.1

Subsection (2)  applies where the following conditions are met—

7.34ZD.1.a

arrangements or proposed arrangements might have resulted or might result in
the creation of a relevant merger situation (the “arrangements concerned”),

7.34ZD.1.b

no reference has been made under section 22 or 33 in respect of the
arrangements concerned, and

7.34ZD.1.c

the CMA has not informed the persons carrying on the enterprises concerned of
a decision that the duty to make a reference under section 22(1) or 33(1) does
not apply in respect of those arrangements.

7.34ZD.2

The persons carrying on the enterprises concerned may make a fast-track
reference request to the CMA at any time before the end of the initial period
(whether or not that period has begun).

7.34ZD.3

In this section and in  sections 34ZE  and  34ZF , “ fast-track reference
request ” means a request that the CMA makes a reference under section 22 (1A)
or 33 (1A)  in relation to the arrangements concerned.

######## Fast-track reference requests: procedure

7.34ZE

7.34ZE.1

This section applies where a fast-track reference request is made and not
withdrawn.

7.34ZE.2

Where the fast-track reference request is made before the beginning of the
initial period, the CMA may, at any time before the beginning of that period,
reject the request.

7.34ZE.3

Where the CMA has not rejected the fast-track reference request in accordance
with  subsection (2) , the CMA must, within the decision period, decide
whether to accept the request in accordance with  section 34ZF  or reject the
request.

7.34ZE.4

Where the CMA accepts or rejects a fast-track reference request, the CMA must
notify the persons carrying on the enterprises concerned that the request has
been accepted or rejected.

7.34ZE.5

In this section—

      “ decision period ” means, in relation to the arrangements concerned—
in a case where the initial period has not begun, that period, or           in
a case where the initial period has begun, the period beginning with the day
on which the fast-track reference request is made and ending at the end of the
initial period;                 “ initial period ” has the meaning given by
section 34ZA(3).

######## Acceptance by the CMA of fast-track reference requests

7.34ZF

7.34ZF.1

The CMA may accept a fast-track reference request only if the condition in
subsection (2)  or  (3)  is met.

7.34ZF.2

The condition in this subsection is that, in relation to the arrangements
concerned—

7.34ZF.2.a

the CMA believes that it is or may be the case that a relevant merger
situation has been created, and

7.34ZF.2.b

the CMA would not be prevented from making a reference under section 22(1) by
reason of section 22(3).

7.34ZF.3

The condition in this subsection is that, in relation to the arrangements
concerned—

7.34ZF.3.a

the CMA believes that it is or may be the case that, if carried into effect,
the arrangements will result in the creation of a relevant merger situation,
and

7.34ZF.3.b

the CMA would not be prevented from making a reference under section 33(1) by
reason of section 33(3).

7.34ZF.4

In deciding whether to accept a fast-track reference request under  subsection
(2)  or  (3) , the CMA must have regard, in particular, to—

7.34ZF.4.a

whether the arrangements concerned raise any consideration specified in
section 58;

7.34ZF.4.b

whether a special intervention notice (see section 59(2)) is in force in
relation to the arrangements.

7.34ZF.5

Where the CMA decides to accept a fast-track reference request the duties to
make references under sections 22(1) and 33(1) do not apply, and accordingly
the CMA may not make any reference under those provisions in respect of the
arrangements concerned (but see the duties under sections 22 (1A)  and 33 (1A)
).

  Mergers involving newspaper enterprises and foreign powers

Section 130

##### Introduction

1

In EA 2002, Part 3 (mergers) is amended as follows.

##### Prohibition on newspaper enterprise mergers involving foreign powers

2

After Chapter 3 insert—

######### Mergers involving newspaper enterprises and foreign powers

########## Intervention by the Secretary of State

2.70A

2.70A.1

The Secretary of State must give the CMA a notice (a “foreign state
intervention notice”) if the Secretary of State has reasonable grounds for
suspecting that it is or may be the case that—

2.70A.1.a

a foreign state newspaper merger situation has been created, or

2.70A.1.b

arrangements are in progress or in contemplation which, if carried into
effect, will result in the creation of a foreign state newspaper merger
situation.

2.70A.2

A foreign state intervention notice must describe the foreign state newspaper
merger situation to which it relates.

2.70A.3

For the purposes of this Chapter a foreign state newspaper merger situation
has been created where—

2.70A.3.a

as a result of two or more enterprises ceasing to be distinct, a relevant
merger situation would have been created by virtue of section 23(1) if the
modifications in  Schedule 6A  had effect,

2.70A.3.b

one of the enterprises concerned is a newspaper enterprise, and

2.70A.3.c

as a result of the enterprises ceasing to be distinct, a foreign power is able
to control or influence the policy of the person carrying on the newspaper
enterprise, or is able to control or influence that policy to a greater
extent.

2.70A.4

Schedule 6B  makes provision about the circumstances in which a foreign power
is able to control or influence the policy of a person for the purposes of
this section (and references to a foreign power being able to control or
influence the policy of a person to a greater extent are to be interpreted
accordingly).

2.70A.5

A foreign state intervention notice—

2.70A.5.a

comes into force when it is given, and

2.70A.5.b

ceases to be in force when the matter to which it relates is finally
determined under this Chapter (see  section 70F ).

########## Investigation and report by the CMA

2.70B

2.70B.1

Where the Secretary of State gives the CMA a foreign state intervention
notice, the CMA must, within such period as the Secretary of State may
require, give the Secretary of State a report in relation to the case.

2.70B.2

The report must include—

2.70B.2.a

a summary of representations relevant to the case that have been received by
the CMA, and

2.70B.2.b

a decision as to whether the CMA believes that—

2.70B.2.b.i

a foreign state newspaper merger situation has been created, or

2.70B.2.b.ii

arrangements are in progress or in contemplation which, if carried into
effect, will result in the creation of a foreign state newspaper merger
situation.

2.70B.3

The CMA must carry out such investigations as it considers appropriate for the
purposes of producing a report under this section.

2.70B.4

For the purposes of its investigation the CMA must invite representations from
the enterprises concerned in the case.

########## Intervention to prevent foreign control of a newspaper enterprise

2.70C

2.70C.1

Subsection (2)  applies where the Secretary of State has received a report
under  section 70B  stating that the CMA believes that—

2.70C.1.a

a foreign state newspaper merger situation has been created, or

2.70C.1.b

arrangements are in progress or in contemplation which, if carried into
effect, will result in the creation of a foreign state newspaper merger
situation.

2.70C.2

The Secretary of State must make an order containing such provision as the
Secretary of State considers reasonable and practicable for the purposes of
reversing or preventing the creation of the foreign state newspaper merger
situation identified in the report.

2.70C.3

An order under  subsection (2)  may contain—

2.70C.3.a

anything permitted by Schedule 8 (provision that may be contained in certain
enforcement orders), and

2.70C.3.b

such supplementary, consequential or incidental provision as the Secretary of
State considers appropriate.

2.70C.4

An order under  subsection (2) —

2.70C.4.a

comes into force at such time as is determined by or under the order, and

2.70C.4.b

may be varied or revoked by another order.

2.70C.5

Paragraph 2 of Schedule 7 (enforcement regime for public interest and special
public interest cases: order for the purposes of preventing pre-emptive
action)—

2.70C.5.a

applies in relation to a foreign state intervention notice as it applies in
relation to an intervention notice, and

2.70C.5.b

for this purpose, is to be read as if—

2.70C.5.b.i

sub-paragraph (10) were omitted;

2.70C.5.b.ii

for sub-paragraph (12), there were substituted—

2.70C.5.b.ii.12

In this paragraph “ pre-emptive action ” means action which might prejudice a
foreign state intervention notice or a report under  section 70B , or might
impede the taking of any action under this Part in relation to such a notice
or report

.

########## Other powers under this Part

2.70D

2.70D.1

Nothing in this Chapter limits the exercise of powers in relation to a foreign
state newspaper merger situation under other provisions of this Part.

2.70D.2

The powers in this Chapter may be exercised in relation to a foreign state
newspaper merger situation regardless of whether any other power under this
Part has been exercised in relation to the case.

2.70D.3

The CMA must, in considering whether to make a reference under section 22 or
33, bring to the attention of the Secretary of State any case which it
believes may be relevant to the duty in  section 70A (1) .

########## Meaning of “foreign power”

2.70E

2.70E.1

In this Chapter, “ foreign power ” means—

2.70E.1.a

the sovereign or other head of a foreign state in their public or private
capacity,

2.70E.1.b

a foreign government or part of a foreign government,

2.70E.1.c

the head or senior members of a foreign government in their private capacity,

2.70E.1.d

an agency or authority of a foreign government, or of part of a foreign
government,

2.70E.1.e

the head or senior members of an agency or authority of a foreign government,
or of part of a foreign government, in their private capacity,

2.70E.1.f

an authority responsible for administering the affairs of an area within a
foreign country or territory, or persons exercising the functions of such an
authority,

2.70E.1.g

a political party which is a governing political party of a foreign
government, or

2.70E.1.h

the officers of a political party, which is a governing political party of a
foreign government, in their private capacity.

2.70E.2

A political party is a governing political party of a foreign government if
persons holding political or official posts in the foreign government or part
of the foreign government—

2.70E.2.a

hold those posts as a result of, or in the course of, their membership of the
party, or

2.70E.2.b

in exercising the functions of those posts, are subject to the direction or
control of, or significantly influenced by, the party.

2.70E.3

In this section—

      “ foreign country or territory ” means a country or territory outside
the United Kingdom, the Channel Islands, the Isle of Man or the British
Overseas Territories;           “ foreign government ” means the government of
a foreign country or territory;           a “ government ” includes persons
exercising the functions of a government;           “ territory ” includes the
constituent territories of a federal state.

########## Other interpretation

2.70F

2.70F.1

For the purposes of this Chapter, section 44(10) is to be read as if the
definition of “newspaper” included a news publication circulating wholly or
mainly in the United Kingdom or in a part of the United Kingdom on any
periodic basis.

2.70F.2

For the purposes of this Chapter, a matter is finally determined when the
Secretary of State—

2.70F.2.a

makes an order under  section 70C (2) , or

2.70F.2.b

publishes under section 107 a report of the CMA under  section 70B  which the
Secretary of State has received and which states that the CMA has decided that
the CMA believes that—

2.70F.2.b.i

no foreign state newspaper merger situation has been created, or

2.70F.2.b.ii

no arrangements are in progress or in contemplation which, if carried into
effect would result in the creation of a foreign state newspaper merger
situation.

########## Regulations

2.70G

2.70G.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations change the meaning of—

2.70G.1.a

“foreign power”, or

2.70G.1.b

“newspaper”,

for the purposes of this Chapter.

2.70G.2

Regulations under  subsection (1) (a)  may, among other things—

2.70G.2.a

provide for a description of person to be treated as if they were not a
foreign power, and

2.70G.2.b

frame any such description by reference to—

2.70G.2.b.i

the independence of persons from other descriptions of foreign power, or

2.70G.2.b.ii

the interest which persons have in a newspaper enterprise.

2.70G.3

The Secretary of State may by regulations apply any provision made by or under
Chapter 1, with or without modifications, for the purposes of this Chapter
(including by way of amendments to the modifications in  Schedule 6A ).

2.70G.4

Regulations under this section may, among other things, make provision having
effect on or after 13 March 2024.

3

After Schedule 6 insert—

  Control or influence of a person by a foreign power

Section 70A

########### Conditions for control or influence

3.1

3.1.1

A foreign power is able to control or influence the policy of a person for the
purposes of  section 70A  if one or more of the following conditions is met.

3.1.2

Condition 1 is that the foreign power holds, directly or indirectly, any of
the shares in the person.

3.1.3

Condition 2 is that the foreign power holds, directly or indirectly, any of
the voting rights in the person.

3.1.4

Condition 3 is that the foreign power holds the right, directly or indirectly,
to appoint or remove an officer of the person.

3.1.5

Condition 4 is that the foreign power has the right or ability to direct,
control or influence to any extent, the person’s policy or activities (in
whole or in part, and whether directly or indirectly), despite not meeting
condition 1, 2 or 3.

3.1.6

Condition 5 is that—

3.1.6.a

the trustees of a trust, or the members of a partnership, unincorporated
association or other entity, that is not a legal person under the law by which
it is governed, would, if they were a foreign power, meet one or more of
conditions 1 to 4 (in their capacity as such) in relation to the person, and

3.1.6.b

the foreign power has the right or ability to direct, control or influence to
any extent the activities of that trust or entity (in whole or in part, and
whether directly or indirectly), or has any other interest in, or right over
or in relation to, the trust or entity, or any of the trustees of the trust or
the members of the entity, whether directly or indirectly.

3.2

In this Schedule, “officer”—

3.2.a

in relation to a body corporate, means a director, member of the committee of
management, chief executive, manager, secretary or other similar officer of
the body, or a person purporting to act in any such capacity;

3.2.b

in relation to a partnership, means a partner, a person purporting to act as a
partner or a person concerned in the management or control of the partnership
or who purports to act in the capacity of a person so concerned;

3.2.c

in relation to an unincorporated association other than a partnership, means a
person who is concerned in the management or control of the association or
purports to act in the capacity of a person so concerned.

########### Interpretation

############ Interpretation

3.3

This Part makes provision about the interpretation of this Schedule.

############ Joint interests

3.4

If a foreign power holds a share or right jointly with another person (whether
or not a foreign power), each of those persons is to be taken to hold that
share or right.

############ Joint arrangements

3.5

3.5.1

If shares or rights held by a foreign power and shares or rights held by
another person (whether or not a foreign power) are the subject of a joint
arrangement between those persons, each of those persons is to be taken to
hold the combined shares or rights of both persons.

3.5.2

A “joint arrangement” is an arrangement between the holders of shares (or
rights) that they will exercise all or substantially all the rights conferred
by their respective shares (or rights) jointly in a way that is pre-determined
by the arrangement.

3.5.3

For the meaning of “arrangement”, see paragraph 12.

############ Calculating shareholdings

3.6

3.6.1

In relation to a person that has a share capital, a reference to holding any
of the shares in that person is to holding any shares comprised in the issued
share capital of that person.

3.6.2

In relation to a person that does not have a share capital, a reference to
holding any of the shares in that person is to holding a right to share to any
extent in the capital or, as the case may be, profits of that person.

############ Voting rights

3.7

3.7.1

A reference to the voting rights in a person is to the rights conferred on
shareholders in respect of their shares (or, in the case of a person not
having a share capital, on members) to vote at general meetings of the person
on all or substantially all matters.

3.7.2

In relation to a person that does not have general meetings at which matters
are decided by the exercise of voting rights, a reference to exercising voting
rights in the person is to be read as a reference to exercising rights in
relation to the person that are equivalent to those of a person entitled to
exercise voting rights in a company.

3.8

In applying this Schedule, voting rights in a person held by the person itself
are to be disregarded.

############ Shares or rights held “indirectly”

3.9

3.9.1

A foreign power holds a share “indirectly” if the foreign power has any stake
in a person and that person—

3.9.1.a

holds the share in question, or

3.9.1.b

is part of a chain of persons—

3.9.1.b.i

each of which (other than the last) has any stake in the person immediately
below it in the chain, and

3.9.1.b.ii

the last of which holds the share.

3.9.2

A foreign power holds a right “indirectly” if the foreign power has any stake
in a person and that person—

3.9.2.a

holds that right, or

3.9.2.b

is part of a chain of persons—

3.9.2.b.i

each of which (other than the last) has any stake in the person immediately
below it in the chain, and

3.9.2.b.ii

the last of which holds that right.

3.9.3

For the purposes of  sub-paragraphs (1)  and  (2) , a person (“ A ”) has “any
stake” in another person (“ B ”) if—

3.9.3.a

A holds any shares or voting rights in B,

3.9.3.b

A is a member of B and has the right to appoint or remove an officer of B,

3.9.3.c

A is a member of B and controls alone, or pursuant to an agreement with other
shareholders or members, any of the voting rights in B, or

3.9.3.d

A has the right or ability to control or influence B to any extent, despite
not being within  paragraph (a) ,  (b)  or  (c) .

############ Shares held by nominees

3.10

A share held by a person as a nominee for another is to be treated as held by
the other (and not by the nominee).

############ Rights treated as held by person who is able to control their exercise

3.11

3.11.1

Where a person controls a right, the right is to be treated as held by that
person (and not by the person who in fact holds the right, unless that person
also controls it).

3.11.2

A person “controls” a right if, by virtue of any arrangement between that
person and others, the right is exercisable only—

3.11.2.a

by that person,

3.11.2.b

in accordance with that person’s directions or instructions, or

3.11.2.c

with that person’s consent or concurrence.

############ Arrangements

3.12

3.12.1

For the purposes of this Schedule, “ arrangement ” includes—

3.12.1.a

any scheme, agreement or understanding, whether or not it is legally
enforceable, and

3.12.1.b

any convention, custom or practice of any kind.

3.12.2

But something does not count as an arrangement unless there is at least some
degree of stability about it (whether by its nature or terms, the time it has
been in existence or otherwise).

############ Rights exercisable only in certain circumstances etc

3.13

3.13.1

Rights that are exercisable only in certain circumstances are to be taken into
account only—

3.13.1.a

where the circumstances have arisen, and for so long as they continue to
obtain, or

3.13.1.b

when the circumstances are within the control of the person having the rights.

3.13.2

But rights that are exercisable by an administrator or by creditors while a
person is in relevant insolvency proceedings are not to be taken into account
even while the person is in those proceedings.

3.13.3

“ Relevant insolvency proceedings ” means—

3.13.3.a

administration within the meaning of the Insolvency Act 1986,

3.13.3.b

administration within the meaning of the Insolvency (Northern Ireland) Order
1989 ( S.I. 1989/2405 (N.I. 19)) , or

3.13.3.c

proceedings under the insolvency law of another country or territory during
which a person’s assets and affairs are subject to the control or supervision
of a third party or creditor.

3.13.4

Rights that are normally exercisable but are temporarily incapable of exercise
are to continue to be taken into account.

############ Rights attached to shares held by way of security

3.14

Rights attached to shares held by way of security provided by a person are to
be treated for the purposes of this Schedule as held by that person—

3.14.a

where apart from the right to exercise them for the purpose of preserving the
value of the security, or of realising it, the rights are exercisable only in
accordance with that person’s instructions, and

3.14.b

where the shares are held in connection with the granting of loans as part of
normal business activities and apart from the right to exercise them for the
purpose of preserving the value of the security, or of realising it, the
rights are exercisable only in that person’s interests.

########### Power to amend circumstances in which there is control or influence

3.15

3.15.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision—

3.15.1.a

to change (by increasing or decreasing) the proportion of shares or rights
which a foreign power must hold in a person carrying on a newspaper
enterprise, whether directly or indirectly, in order for the foreign power to
be able to control or influence the policy of a person for the purposes of
section 70A ;

3.15.1.b

to change (by increasing or decreasing) the proportion of shares or rights
which is to be held by persons in a chain of persons for the purposes of
determining whether shares or rights are held indirectly;

3.15.1.c

about assumptions which are to be made when determining whether a foreign
power is able to control or influence the policy of a person, including
assumptions framed by reference to the ownership of shares or voting rights by
any person;

3.15.1.d

about the extent to which a foreign power needs to be able to control or
influence the policy of a person in order to control or influence that policy
for the purposes of  section 70A , including provision about a foreign power
that is already able to control or influence the policy of a person to some
extent being able to control or influence that policy to a greater extent;

3.15.1.e

to change or supplement  Part 1  of this Schedule so as to include
circumstances (for example, circumstances involving more complex structures)
that give a foreign power a level of control or influence in relation to the
policy of a person broadly similar to the level of control or influence given
by the conditions in paragraph 1;

3.15.1.f

in consequence of any provision made by virtue of  paragraph (e) , to change
or supplement  Part 2  of this Schedule so that circumstances specified in
that Part in which a person is to be regarded as holding an interest in
another person correspond to any of the conditions in paragraph 1, or would do
so but for the extent of the interest.

3.15.2

The provision that may be made under this paragraph, read with section
124(2)(a), includes—

3.15.2.a

different provision for different descriptions of foreign power, and

3.15.2.b

different provision for different persons or descriptions of person in a chain
of persons.

3.15.3

Regulations under this paragraph may, among other things—

3.15.3.a

confer a discretion on the CMA;

3.15.3.b

make provision having effect on or after 13 March 2024.

8

For section 154 (and the italic heading immediately before it) substitute—

######## Undertakings in lieu

######### Undertakings fully or partially in lieu of references or reports

8.154A

8.154A.1

This section applies where—

8.154A.1.a

no market study notice has been published under section 130A but the CMA
considers that it has the power to make a market investigation reference under
section 131 and (subject to taking action under this section) intends to make
such a reference,

8.154A.1.b

a market study notice has been published under section 130A but no market
investigation reference has been made under section 131, or

8.154A.1.c

a market investigation reference has been made under section 131 or 132 but no
report under section 136 has been published.

8.154A.2

The CMA may accept, from such persons as it considers appropriate,
undertakings to take such action as it considers appropriate for the purposes
of remedying, mitigating or preventing (to any extent)—

8.154A.2.a

any adverse effect on competition concerned, or

8.154A.2.b

any detrimental effect on customers so far as—

8.154A.2.b.i

it has resulted from the adverse effect on competition, or

8.154A.2.b.ii

it may be expected to result from the adverse effect on competition.

8.154A.3

An undertaking under this section is known as—

8.154A.3.a

an “undertaking in lieu of a reference” where it is accepted in circumstances
where this section applies by virtue of  subsection (1) (a)  or  (b) ;

8.154A.3.b

an “undertaking in lieu of a report” where it is accepted in circumstances
where this section applies by virtue of  subsection (1) (c) .

8.154A.4

The CMA may accept—

8.154A.4.a

undertakings in lieu of a reference either—

8.154A.4.a.i

instead of making a reference under section 131 (in which case the
undertakings are known as “undertakings fully in lieu of a reference”), or

8.154A.4.a.ii

in addition to making a reference under that section (in which case the
undertakings are known as “undertakings partially in lieu of a reference”);

8.154A.4.b

undertakings in lieu of a report either—

8.154A.4.b.i

instead of publishing a report under section 136 (in which case the
undertakings are known as “undertakings fully in lieu of a report”), or

8.154A.4.b.ii

in addition to publishing a report under that section (in which case the
undertakings are known as “undertakings partially in lieu of a report”).

8.154A.5

In accepting undertakings fully in lieu of a reference or undertakings fully
in lieu of a report, the CMA must, in particular, have regard to the need to
achieve as comprehensive a solution as is reasonable and practicable to—

8.154A.5.a

the adverse effect on competition concerned, and

8.154A.5.b

any detrimental effects on customers so far as resulting from the adverse
effect on competition.

8.154A.6

In accepting an undertaking under this section, the CMA may, in particular,
have regard to the effect of any action on any relevant customer benefits of
the feature or features of the market or markets concerned.

8.154A.7

Where no detrimental effect on customers has yet resulted from an adverse
effect on competition, the CMA may not accept an undertaking under this
section to remedy, mitigate or prevent a detrimental effect on customers so
far as it may be expected to result from that adverse effect on competition
unless the adverse effect on competition is also being remedied, mitigated or
prevented (whether or not by the same undertaking).

8.154A.8

An undertaking under this section—

8.154A.8.a

comes into force when accepted;

8.154A.8.b

may be varied or superseded by another undertaking;

8.154A.8.c

may be released by the CMA.

8.154A.9

The CMA must, as soon as reasonably practicable, consider any representations
received by it in relation to varying or releasing an undertaking under this
section.

4

After  section 161A  (acceptance of enforcement undertakings: Part 4)
(inserted by  paragraph 16  of  Schedule 11 ) insert—

######## Implementation trials of final orders and undertakings

######### Implementation trials: purpose and interpretation

4.161B

4.161B.1

This section and  sections 161C  to  161E  make provision in relation to the
acceptance of undertakings and making of orders by a relevant authority on a
trial basis for the purpose of assessing the effectiveness of qualifying
remedial action (and the acceptance of undertakings and making of orders on
that basis is referred to in this Part as an “ implementation trial ”).

4.161B.2

In this section and in  sections 161C  to  161E  “ relevant authority ” means
the CMA or the Secretary of State.

4.161B.3

In this Part—

      “ implementation trial measure ” means an undertaking accepted, or order
made, under  section 161C  (and references to the imposition of such a measure
are to be read as the acceptance of an undertaking or the making of an order,
as the case may be);           “ implementation trial period ” means, in
relation to an implementation trial measure, the period—         beginning
with the day on which the relevant authority begins the implementation trial,
and           ending with the last day on which the implementation trial
measure is to have effect (see  subsections (4)  and  (5) );                 “
qualifying remedial action ” means remedial action in respect of—         a
matter concerning the provision or publication of information to consumers
(whether directly or through an intermediary), or           any other matter
specified in regulations made by the Secretary of State;                 “
relevant adverse effect ” means—         where the relevant authority is the
CMA, an adverse effect on competition identified in the report mentioned in
section 138(1);           where the relevant authority is the Secretary of
State—         an adverse effect on competition identified in the report
mentioned in section 146(1);           an effect adverse to the public
interest identified in the report mentioned in section 146A(1);
“ remedial action ” means an action—         where the relevant authority is
the CMA, to be taken in accordance with section 138(2) or  section 162A (5) ;
where the relevant authority is the Secretary of State, to be taken in
accordance with section 147(2) or 147A(2) (as the case may be).

4.161B.4

The last day on which an implementation trial measure is to have effect is the
earlier of—

4.161B.4.a

the day specified under  section 161D (5) (b) (ii) , and

4.161B.4.b

the day on which action is taken under section 138(2), 147(2) or 147A(2) (as
the case may be) in relation to the relevant adverse effect which the relevant
authority considers concerns the same qualifying matter.

4.161B.5

But where—

4.161B.5.a

an implementation trial measure is imposed in accordance with this section,
and

4.161B.5.b

the CMA extends, under section 138A(3), the period within which its duty under
section 138(2) is required to be discharged in accordance with section 138A
(A3)  in relation to the measure,

the last day on which the implementation trial measure is to have effect is
the last day of that period as so extended.

######### Power to conduct implementation trials

4.161C

4.161C.1

The CMA may, in relation to a market investigation reference, begin an
implementation trial where—

4.161C.1.a

subsection (2) of section 138 applies (see subsection (1) of that section),
and

4.161C.1.b

the CMA has not taken, but is minded to take, qualifying remedial action.

4.161C.2

The Secretary of State may, in relation to a restricted PI reference or a full
PI reference, begin an implementation trial where—

4.161C.2.a

subsection (2) of section 147, or subsection (2) of 147A (as the case may be),
applies (see subsection (1) of the section in question), and

4.161C.2.b

the Secretary of State has not taken, but is minded to take, qualifying
remedial action.

4.161C.3

Subsections (1)  and  (2)  are subject to the duty to publish notices in
section 161D .

4.161C.4

The relevant authority begins an implementation trial by—

4.161C.4.a

accepting, from such persons as the relevant authority considers appropriate,
undertakings under this section to take action specified or described in the
undertakings, or

4.161C.4.b

making an order under this section,

for the purposes of assessing, during the implementation trial period, the
likely effectiveness of the qualifying remedial action.

4.161C.5

Where the relevant authority begins an implementation trial, the relevant
authority may also—

4.161C.5.a

accept, from such persons as the relevant authority considers appropriate,
undertakings under this section to take action specified or described in the
undertakings, or

4.161C.5.b

make an order under this section,

in the circumstances mentioned in subsection (6).

4.161C.6

The circumstances are that the relevant authority considers that accepting the
undertakings or making the order would be likely to contribute to, or
otherwise be of use for purposes of, remedying, mitigating or preventing,
during the implementation trial period—

4.161C.6.a

an adverse effect on competition identified in the report concerned or (as the
case may be) an effect adverse to the public interest which has resulted from,
or may be expected to result from, the features or combinations of features
mentioned;

4.161C.6.b

any detrimental effect on customers so far as it has resulted from, or may be
expected to result from, any such adverse effect on competition.

######### Implementation trials: notices

4.161D

4.161D.1

Before the relevant authority begins an implementation trial under  section
161C (4) , the relevant authority must publish—

4.161D.1.a

a provisional implementation trial notice, and

4.161D.1.b

a final implementation trial notice (but see  subsection (4) ).

4.161D.2

A provisional implementation trial notice must—

4.161D.2.a

specify each implementation trial measure the relevant authority is minded to
impose for the purposes of the implementation trial;

4.161D.2.b

specify the relevant adverse effect with which each measure is seeking to
deal;

4.161D.2.c

specify any other facts which the relevant authority considers justify the
imposition of each measure;

4.161D.2.d

specify, in relation to each measure—

4.161D.2.d.i

how the relevant authority intends to assess the likely effect of the measure,
and

4.161D.2.d.ii

the last day on which the relevant authority intends for the measure to have
effect;

4.161D.2.e

invite the making of representations by the persons on which the relevant
authority is minded to impose one or more implementation trial measure
(“implementation trial participants”) about the matters set out in the notice;

4.161D.2.f

specify the means by which, and the time by which, such representations must
be made.

4.161D.3

The time specified under  subsection (2) (f)  by which representations must be
made must be at least 15 days after the date on which the provisional
implementation trial notice is published.

4.161D.4

A relevant authority may publish a final implementation trial notice only
where—

4.161D.4.a

the relevant authority has published a provisional implementation trial notice
under  subsection (1) ,

4.161D.4.b

the time for the implementation trial participants to make representations to
the relevant authority in accordance with the notice has expired, and

4.161D.4.c

after considering such representations (if any), it appears to the relevant
authority that it is appropriate to begin an implementation trial under
section 161C (4) .

4.161D.5

A final implementation trial notice must specify—

4.161D.5.a

the implementation trial measures the relevant authority intends to impose for
the purposes of the implementation trial,

4.161D.5.b

in relation to each such measure—

4.161D.5.b.i

how the relevant authority intends to assess the likely effect of the measure,
and

4.161D.5.b.ii

the last day on which the measure is to have effect.

######### Implementation trials: supplementary

4.161E

4.161E.1

The relevant authority may not accept an undertaking from a person under
section 161C  unless it has provided the person with information about the
possible consequences of failing to comply with the undertaking.

4.161E.2

The CMA may not begin an implementation trial under  section 161C (4) —

4.161E.2.a

in respect of qualifying remedial action that would be taken in accordance
with subsection (2) of section 138, after the end of the period within which
the CMA would otherwise have been required to discharge its duty under that
subsection;

4.161E.2.b

in respect of qualifying remedial action that would be taken in accordance
with  section 162A (5) , after the end of the period mentioned in  section
162A (6) .

4.161E.3

Subsections (3), (5) and (6) of section 138 apply to action taken by the CMA
under  section 161C  as they apply to action taken by the CMA under section
138(2).

4.161E.4

Subsections (3)(b), (4), (5) and (6) of section 147 apply to action taken by
the Secretary of State under  section 161C  in relation to a restricted PI
reference as they apply to action taken by the Secretary of State under
section 147(2).

4.161E.5

Subsections (3) and (4)(b) of section 147A apply to action taken by the
Secretary of State under  section 161C  in relation to a full PI reference as
they apply to action taken by the Secretary of State under section 147A(2).

4.161E.6

Subsections (3) to (5) of section 159 apply to undertakings accepted under
section 161C  as they apply to undertakings accepted under section 159(1).

4.161E.7

Subsections (3) and (4) of section 161 apply to orders made under  section
161C  as they apply to orders made under section 161(1).

5

After section 162A (inserted by  section 139 (4) ) insert—

######## Power to vary etc undertakings and orders: implementation trials

5.162B

5.162B.1

This section applies in relation to implementation trial measures imposed in
accordance with  section 161C .

5.162B.2

The CMA must keep under review the effectiveness of the implementation trial
measures.

5.162B.3

The CMA must, in particular, from time to time consider—

5.162B.3.a

whether an implementation trial measure has been or is being complied with;

5.162B.3.b

whether an undertaking accepted under  section 161C  is no longer appropriate
and—

5.162B.3.b.i

one or more of the parties to it can be released from it; or

5.162B.3.b.ii

it needs to be varied or to be superseded by a new undertaking under that
section; and

5.162B.3.c

whether an order made under  section 161C  is no longer appropriate and needs
to be varied or revoked.

5.162B.4

The CMA must, within the implementation trial period, give the Secretary of
State such advice as it considers appropriate in relation to—

5.162B.4.a

any possible variation or release by the Secretary of State of an undertaking
accepted by the Secretary of State under  section 161C ;

5.162B.4.b

any possible new undertaking to be accepted by the Secretary of State under
that section so as to supersede another undertaking given to the Secretary of
State under that section;

5.162B.4.c

any possible variation or revocation by the Secretary of State of an order
made by the Secretary of State under that section;

5.162B.4.d

any possible undertaking to be accepted by the Secretary of State under that
section instead of an order made under that section, or any possible order to
be made by the Secretary of State under that section instead of an undertaking
accepted under that section.

5.162B.5

The relevant authority must, within the implementation trial period, take such
action as it considers appropriate in relation to—

5.162B.5.a

any possible variation or release by the relevant authority of an undertaking
accepted by it under  section 161C ;

5.162B.5.b

any possible new undertaking to be accepted by the relevant authority under
that section so as to supersede another undertaking given to it under that
section;

5.162B.5.c

any possible variation or revocation by the relevant authority of an order
made by it under that section;

5.162B.5.d

any possible undertaking to be accepted by the relevant authority under that
section instead of an order made under that section, or any possible order to
be made by the relevant authority under that section instead of an undertaking
accepted under that section.

5.162B.6

But the relevant authority may not do anything under this section that would
result in—

5.162B.6.a

the implementation trial period being extended;

5.162B.6.b

an order or undertaking made under  section 161C  being out of compliance with
any provision of that section.

5.162B.7

In this section “ relevant authority ” has the meaning given by  section 161B
(2) .

5.162B.8

Subsections (3), (5) and (6) of section 138 apply to action taken by the CMA
under this section as those subsections apply to action taken by the CMA under
section 138(2).

5.162B.9

Subsections (3)(b), (5) and (6) of section 147 apply to action taken by the
Secretary of State under this section in respect of a restricted PI reference
as those subsections apply to action taken by the Secretary of State under
section 147(2).

5.162B.10

Subsection (3) of section 147A applies to action taken by the Secretary of
State under this section in respect of a full PI reference as that subsection
applies to action taken by the Secretary of State under section 147A(2).

######### Enforcement of requirements: imposition of penalties

8.40ZE

8.40ZE.1

The CMA may impose a penalty on a person in accordance with section 40A where
the CMA considers that—

8.40ZE.1.a

the person has, without reasonable excuse, failed to comply with a requirement
imposed on the person under section 26, 26A, 27, 28, 28A or 40ZD;

8.40ZE.1.b

the person has, without reasonable excuse, obstructed an officer acting in the
exercise of the officer’s powers under section 27 or under a warrant issued
under section 28 or 28A;

8.40ZE.1.c

the person, having been required to produce a document under section 26, 27,
28 or 28A, has, without reasonable excuse—

8.40ZE.1.c.i

destroyed or otherwise disposed of, falsified or concealed the document, or

8.40ZE.1.c.ii

caused or permitted the document’s destruction, disposal, falsification or
concealment;

8.40ZE.1.d

the person has, without reasonable excuse, provided information that was false
or misleading in a material particular to the CMA in connection with any
function of the CMA under this Part;

8.40ZE.1.e

the person has, without reasonable excuse, provided information that was false
or misleading in a material particular to another person knowing that the
information was to be used for the purpose of providing information to the CMA
in connection with any function of the CMA under this Part.

8.40ZE.2

But the CMA may not proceed against a person under this section in relation to
an act or omission which constitutes an offence under any of sections 42 to 44
if the person has, by reason of that act or omission, been found guilty of
that offence.

8.40ZE.3

In deciding whether and, if so, how to proceed under subsection (1) the CMA
must have regard to the statement of policy which was most recently published
under section 40B at the time when the act or omission concerned occurred.

8.40ZE.4

In this section—

8.40ZE.4.a

the reference to the production of a document includes a reference to the
production of a legible and intelligible copy of information recorded
otherwise than in legible form;

8.40ZE.4.b

the reference to concealing a document includes a reference to destroying the
means of reproducing information recorded otherwise than in legible form.

8.40ZE.5

Sections 112 to 115 of the Enterprise Act 2002 (supplementary provisions about
penalties) apply in relation to a penalty imposed under  subsection (1)  as
they apply in relation to a penalty imposed under section 110 (1)  or  (1A)
of that Act, with the following modifications—

8.40ZE.5.a

any reference in those provisions to the appropriate authority is to be read
as a reference to the CMA only;

8.40ZE.5.b

section 114 (5A)  is to be read as if the words “In the case of a penalty
imposed on a person by the CMA or OFCOM,” were omitted;

8.40ZE.5.c

section 114(12) is to be read as if, for paragraph  (b) , there were
substituted—

8.40ZE.5.c.b

“ relevant guidance ” means the statement of policy which was most recently
published under section 40B of the 1998 Act at the time when the act or
omission concerned occurred.

9

9.1

Section 40A (penalties: failure to comply with requirements) is amended as
follows.

9.2

.

9.3

For subsection (1) substitute—

9.3.1A

A penalty imposed under  section 40ZE (1)  is to be of such amount as the CMA
considers appropriate.

9.4

In subsection (2), for the words before paragraph (a), substitute  “A penalty
imposed under  section 40ZE (1) (a)  may be—” .

9.5

After subsection (2) insert—

9.5.2A

A penalty imposed under any of  section 40ZE (1) (b)  to  (e)  must be a fixed
amount.

9.6

In subsection (3)—

9.6.a

23

After section 116 insert—

######### Intentional destruction etc of documents

23.116A

23.116A.1

A person (“ P ”) commits an offence if the person intentionally alters,
suppresses or destroys any document which P has been required to produce by a
notice under section 109.

23.116A.2

But P does not commit an offence under  subsection (1)  by reason of any act
or omission if the CMA has proceeded against P under section 110 (1)  or  (1A)
in relation to that act or omission.

23.116A.3

A person who commits an offence under  subsection (1)  is liable—

23.116A.3.a

on summary conviction, to a fine not exceeding the statutory maximum;

23.116A.3.b

on conviction on indictment, to imprisonment for a term not exceeding two
years or to a fine or to both.

23.116A.4

In this section—

23.116A.4.a

the reference to the production of a document includes a reference to the
production of a legible and intelligible copy of information recorded
otherwise than in legible form;

23.116A.4.b

the reference to suppressing a document includes a reference to destroying the
means of reproducing information recorded otherwise than in legible form.

  Civil penalties etc in connection with breaches of remedies

Section 143(2)

##### Commitments and directions under Part 1 of CA 1998 (competition)

1

In Part 1 of CA 1998 (competition), Chapter 3 (investigation and enforcement)
is amended as follows.

2

In section 31A (commitments), after subsection (2) insert—

2.2A

But the CMA may not accept commitments from a person unless it has provided
the person with information about the possible consequences of failing to
adhere to the commitments.

3

In section 31E (enforcement of commitments), after subsection (3) insert—

3.4

In deciding whether and, if so, how to proceed under this section, the CMA
must have regard to the statement of policy which was most recently published
by it under  section 35C  at the time of the failure to adhere to the
commitments.

4

In the italic heading before section 32, at the end insert  “: directions and
interim measures” .

5

In section 34 (enforcement of directions), after subsection (3) insert—

5.4

In deciding whether and, if so, how to proceed under this section, the CMA
must have regard to the statement of policy which was most recently published
by it under  section 35C  at the time of the failure to comply with the
direction.

6

After section 35 insert—

######### Civil sanctions: breaches of commitments, directions and interim measures

########## Enforcement of powers under sections 31A, 32, 33 and 35: imposition of penalties

6.35A

6.35A.1

The CMA may, in accordance with  section 35B , impose a penalty on a person—

6.35A.1.a

from whom the CMA has accepted commitments under section 31A (and who has not
been released from those commitments), or

6.35A.1.b

to whom the CMA has given a direction under section 32, 33 or 35,

where the CMA considers that the person has, without reasonable excuse, failed
to adhere to the commitments or comply with the direction.

6.35A.2

In deciding whether and, if so, how to proceed under  subsection (1)  the CMA
must have regard to the statement of policy which was most recently published
under  section 35C  at the time of the failure to adhere or comply.

########## Penalties under 

6.35B

6.35B.1

A penalty under  section 35A (1)  is to be such amount as the CMA considers
appropriate.

6.35B.2

The amount must be—

6.35B.2.a

a fixed amount,

6.35B.2.b

an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, or

6.35B.2.c

a combination of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a
daily rate.

6.35B.3

A penalty imposed under  section 35A (1)  on a person who is not an
undertaking must not—

6.35B.3.a

in the case of a fixed amount, exceed £30,000;

6.35B.3.b

in the case of an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, exceed
£15,000 per day;

6.35B.3.c

in the case of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a daily
rate, exceed such fixed amount and such amount per day.

6.35B.4

A penalty imposed under  section 35A (1)  on a person who is an undertaking
must not—

6.35B.4.a

in the case of a fixed amount, exceed 5% of the total value of the turnover of
the undertaking;

6.35B.4.b

in the case of an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, for each day
exceed 5% of the total value of the daily turnover of the undertaking;

6.35B.4.c

in the case of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a daily
rate, exceed such fixed amount and such amount per day.

6.35B.5

In imposing a penalty by reference to a daily rate—

6.35B.5.a

no account is to be taken of any days before the service on the person
concerned of the provisional penalty notice under section 112 (A1)  of the
Enterprise Act 2002 (as applied by  subsection (6) ), and

6.35B.5.b

unless the CMA determines an earlier date (whether before or after the penalty
is imposed), the amount payable ceases to accumulate at the beginning of the
day on which the person adheres to the commitments or complies with the
direction (as the case may be) referred to in  section 35A (1) .

6.35B.6

Sections 112 to 115 of the Enterprise Act 2002 apply in relation to a penalty
imposed under  section 35A (1)  as they apply in relation to a penalty imposed
under section 110 (1)  or  (1A)  of that Act, with the following
modifications—

6.35B.6.a

any reference in those provisions to the appropriate authority is to be read
as a reference to the CMA only;

6.35B.6.b

section 114 (5A)  is to be read as if the words “In the case of a penalty
imposed on a person by the CMA or OFCOM,” were omitted;

6.35B.6.c

section 114(12) is to be read as if, for paragraph (b), there were
substituted—

6.35B.6.c.b

“ relevant guidance ” means the statement of policy which was most recently
published under  section 35C  at the time when the act or omission concerned
occurred.

6.35B.7

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend subsection  (3) (a)  and  (b)
by substituting for either or both of the sums for the time being specified in
those paragraphs such other sum or sums as the Secretary of State considers
appropriate.

6.35B.8

Before making regulations under  subsection (7)  the Secretary of State must
consult—

6.35B.8.a

the CMA, and

6.35B.8.b

such other persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

6.35B.9

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision for determining the
turnover and daily turnover of an undertaking for the purposes of  subsection
(4) .

6.35B.10

Regulations under  subsection (9)  may, in particular, make provision as to—

6.35B.10.a

the amounts which are, or which are not, to be treated as comprising an
undertaking’s turnover or daily turnover;

6.35B.10.b

the date, or dates, by reference to which an undertaking’s turnover, or daily
turnover, is to be determined.

6.35B.11

Regulations under  subsection (9)  may, in particular, make provision enabling
the CMA to determine matters of a description specified in the regulations
(including any of the matters mentioned in paragraphs  (a)  and  (b)  of
subsection (10) ).

######### Statement of policy in relation to functions under sections 31E, 34 and 

########## Statement of policy in relation to functions under sections 31E, 34 and 

6.35C

6.35C.1

The CMA must prepare and publish a statement of policy in relation to the
exercise of functions under sections 31E, 34 and  35A .

6.35C.2

The statement must, in particular, include a statement about the
considerations relevant to the determination of the nature and amount of any
penalty imposed under  section 35A (1) .

6.35C.3

The CMA may revise its statement of policy and, where it does so, it must
publish the revised statement.

6.35C.4

The CMA must consult the Secretary of State and such other persons as it
considers appropriate when preparing or revising its statement of policy.

6.35C.5

If the proposed statement of policy or revision relates to a matter in respect
of which a regulator exercises concurrent jurisdiction, those consulted must
include that regulator.

6.35C.6

A statement or revised statement of policy may not be published under this
section without the approval of the Secretary of State.

  Civil sanctions: infringements of the Chapter I or II prohibitions

##### Undertakings and orders under Part 3 of EA 2002 (mergers)

7

In Part 3 of EA 2002 (mergers), Chapter 4 (enforcement) is amended as follows.

Section 89 (subject-matter of undertakings) is amended as follows.

9.2

9.3

9.3.A1

An appropriate authority may not accept an enforcement undertaking from a

9.4

After subsection (2) insert—

9.4.3

In this section, “ appropriate authority ” has the same meaning as in  section
94AA .

10

In section 94 (rights to enforce undertakings and orders), after subsection
(9) insert—

10.10

In deciding whether and, if so, how to proceed under this section, the CMA
must have regard to the statement of policy which was most recently published
by it under section 94B at the time of the failure to comply with the
undertaking or (as the case may be) order.

11

For section 94A substitute—

######### Enforcement of undertakings and orders: imposition of penalties

11.94AA

11.94AA.1

The appropriate authority may, in accordance with  section 94AB , impose a
penalty on a person—

11.94AA.1.a

from whom the authority has accepted an enforcement undertaking, or

11.94AA.1.b

to whom an enforcement order is addressed,

where the authority considers that the person has, without reasonable excuse,
failed to comply with the undertaking or order.

11.94AA.2

In this section and in  section 94AB , “ the appropriate authority ” means—

11.94AA.2.a

in relation to an enforcement undertaking or enforcement order made by the
Secretary of State under Schedule 7, the Secretary of State;

11.94AA.2.b

in relation to any other enforcement undertaking or enforcement order, the
CMA.

11.94AA.3

In deciding whether and, if so, how to proceed under  subsection (1)  the CMA
must have regard to the statement of policy which was most recently published
under section 94B at the time of the failure to comply.

######### Penalties under 

11.94AB

11.94AB.1

A penalty under  section 94AA (1)  is to be such amount as the appropriate
authority considers appropriate.

11.94AB.2

The amount must be—

11.94AB.2.a

a fixed amount,

11.94AB.2.b

an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, or

11.94AB.2.c

a combination of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a
daily rate.

11.94AB.3

A penalty imposed under  section 94AA (1)  on a person who does not own or
control an enterprise must not—

11.94AB.3.a

in the case of a fixed amount, exceed £30,000;

11.94AB.3.b

in the case of an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, exceed
£15,000 per day;

11.94AB.3.c

in the case of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a daily
rate, exceed such fixed amount and such amount per day.

11.94AB.4

A penalty imposed under  section 94AA (1)  on any other person must not—

11.94AB.4.a

in the case of a fixed amount, exceed 5% of the total value of the turnover
(both in and outside the United Kingdom) of the enterprises owned or
controlled by the person on whom it is imposed;

11.94AB.4.b

in the case of an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, for each day
exceed 5% of the total value of the daily turnover (both in and outside the
United Kingdom) of the enterprises owned or controlled by the person on whom
it is imposed;

11.94AB.4.c

in the case of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a daily
rate, exceed such fixed amount and such amount per day.

11.94AB.5

In imposing a penalty by reference to a daily rate—

11.94AB.5.a

no account is to be taken of any days before the service on the person
concerned of the provisional penalty notice under section 112 (A1)  (as
applied by  subsection (6) ), and

11.94AB.5.b

unless the CMA determines an earlier date (whether before or after the penalty
is imposed), the amount payable ceases to accumulate at the beginning of the
day on which the person complies with the enforcement undertaking or
enforcement order.

11.94AB.6

Sections 112 to 115 apply in relation to a penalty imposed under  section 94AA
(1)  as they apply in relation to a penalty imposed under section 110 (1)  or
(1A) , with the following modifications—

11.94AB.6.a

any reference in those provisions to the appropriate authority is to be read
as a reference to the appropriate authority within the meaning of this section
(see  section 94AA (2) );

11.94AB.6.b

section 114 (5A)  is to be read as if the words “or OFCOM” were omitted;

11.94AB.6.c

section 114(12) is to be read as if, for paragraph (b), there were
substituted—

11.94AB.6.c.b

“ relevant guidance ” means the statement of policy which was most recently
published under section 94B at the time when the act or omission concerned
occurred.

11.94AB.7

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend subsection  (3) (a)  and  (b)
by substituting for either or both of the sums for the time being specified in
those paragraphs such other sum or sums as the Secretary of State considers
appropriate.

11.94AB.8

Before making regulations under  subsection (7)  the Secretary of State must
consult—

11.94AB.8.a

the CMA, and

11.94AB.8.b

such other persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

11.94AB.9

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision for determining, for
the purposes of this section—

11.94AB.9.a

when an enterprise is to be treated as being controlled by a person;

11.94AB.9.b

the turnover and daily turnover (both in and outside the United Kingdom) of an
enterprise.

11.94AB.10

Regulations under  subsection (9) (b)  may, in particular, make provision as
to—

11.94AB.10.a

the amounts which are, or which are not, to be treated as comprising an
enterprise’s turnover or daily turnover;

11.94AB.10.b

the date, or dates, by reference to which an enterprise’s turnover, or daily
turnover, is to be determined.

11.94AB.11

Regulations under  subsection (9)  may, in particular, make provision enabling
the appropriate authority to determine matters of a description specified in
the regulations (including any of the matters mentioned in paragraphs  (a)
and  (b)  of  subsection (10) ).

######### Statement of policy in relation to functions under sections 167 and 

18.167C

18.167C.1

The CMA must prepare and publish a statement of policy in relation to the
exercise of functions under sections 167 and  167A .

18.167C.2

relevant to the determination of the amount of any penalty imposed under
section 167A .

18.167C.3
