publish the revised statement.

18.167C.4

The CMA must consult the Secretary of State and such other persons as it
considers appropriate when preparing or revising its statement of policy.

18.167C.5

A statement or revised statement of policy may not be published under this
section without the approval of the Secretary of State.

Article 46 of the Electricity (Northern Ireland) Order 1992 ( S.I. 1992/231

  Service and extra-territoriality of notices under CA 1998 and EA 2002

Section 144

##### Service of documents etc

1

In Part 3 of EA 2002 (mergers), in Chapter 5 (supplementary), for section 126
(service of documents) substitute—

######### Service of documents by the CMA, OFCOM or the Secretary of State

1.126

1.126.1

This section applies in relation to any document required or authorised under
this Part to be served on a person by the CMA, OFCOM or the Secretary of
State.

1.126.2

The document may be served by—

1.126.2.a

delivering it to the person,

1.126.2.b

leaving it at the person’s proper address,

1.126.2.c

sending it by post to the person at that address, or

1.126.2.d

sending it to the person by email to their email address.

1.126.3

A document may be served on a body corporate by giving it to any officer of
that body.

1.126.4

A document may be served on a partnership by giving it to any partner or a
person who has the control or management of the partnership business.

1.126.5

A document may be served on an unincorporated body or association (other than
a partnership) by giving it to any member of the governing body of the
association.

1.126.6

A person’s proper address is—

1.126.6.a

in a case where the person has specified an address as one at which the
person, or someone acting on the person’s behalf, will accept service of
documents, that address;

1.126.6.b

in any other case, the address determined in accordance with  subsection (7) .

1.126.7

A person’s “proper address” is (if  subsection (6) (a)  does not apply)—

1.126.7.a

in the case of a body corporate, its registered or principal office;

1.126.7.b

in the case of a partnership, the principal office of the partnership;

1.126.7.c

in the case of an unincorporated body or association, the principal office of
the body or association;

1.126.7.d

in a case where none of  paragraphs (a)  to  (c)  apply, any address at which
the CMA, OFCOM or the Secretary of State believes, on reasonable grounds, that
the document will come to the attention of the person.

1.126.8

A person’s email address is—

1.126.8.a

any email address published for the time being by that person as an address
for contacting that person, or

1.126.8.b

if there is no such published address, any email address by means of which the
CMA, OFCOM or the Secretary of State believes, on reasonable grounds, that the
document will come to the attention of that person.

1.126.9

In the case of—

1.126.9.a

a body corporate registered outside the United Kingdom,

1.126.9.b

a partnership carrying on business outside the United Kingdom, or

1.126.9.c

any other body with offices outside the United Kingdom,

references to its principal office include references to its principal office
in the United Kingdom or, if it has no principal office in the United Kingdom,
any place in the United Kingdom where it carries on business or conducts
activities.

1.126.10

In  this section  “ officer ”, in relation to any body corporate, means a
director, manager, secretary or other similar officer of the body.

1.126.11

This section  does not limit any other lawful means of serving a document on a
person.

2

In Part 1 of CA 1998, in Chapter 3 (investigation and enforcement), after
section 44 insert—

######### Supplementary

########## Giving of notices under Chapter 3

2.44A

Section  126  of the Enterprise Act 2002 (service of documents) applies to the
giving of notices under this Chapter as it applies to the service of documents
under Part 3 of that Act.

##### Extra-territoriality of notices under CA 1998 and EA 2002

15

In Chapter 3 of Part 1 of CA 1998 (investigation and enforcement), after
section 44A (inserted by  paragraph 2 ) insert—

######### Extra-territorial application of notices under sections 26 and 40ZD

15.44B

15.44B.1

This section applies to the exercise of the CMA’s power to give a person a
notice under section 26 or 40ZD.

15.44B.2

The power is exercisable so as to—

15.44B.2.a

give the notice to a person who is outside the United Kingdom (subject to
subsections  (3)  and  (4) );

15.44B.2.b

require the production of a specified document, or the provision of specified
information, held outside the United Kingdom.

15.44B.3

The CMA’s power to give a notice under section 26 to a person outside the
United Kingdom by virtue of  subsection (2) (a)  is exercisable only if—

15.44B.3.a

the person’s activities are being investigated as part of an investigation
under section 25, or

15.44B.3.b

the person has a UK connection.

15.44B.4

The CMA’s power to give a notice under section 40ZD to a person outside the
United Kingdom by virtue of  subsection (2) (a)  is exercisable only if—

15.44B.4.a

the person is bound by transferred EU anti-trust commitments (within the
meaning of section 40ZA), or

15.44B.4.b

the person is subject to a transferred EU anti-trust direction (within the
meaning of that section).

15.44B.5

For the purposes of  subsection (3) (b) , a person has a UK connection if the
person—

15.44B.5.a

is a United Kingdom national;

15.44B.5.b

is an individual who is habitually resident in the United Kingdom;

15.44B.5.c

is a body incorporated under the law of any part of the United Kingdom;

15.44B.5.d

carries on business in the United Kingdom.

15.44B.6

In  subsection (5) (a)  “ United Kingdom national ” means—

15.44B.6.a

a British citizen, a British overseas territories citizen, a British National
(Overseas) or a British Overseas citizen;

15.44B.6.b

a person who is a British subject under the British Nationality Act 1981;

15.44B.6.c

a British protected person within the meaning of that Act.

15.44B.7

Nothing in this section is to be taken to limit any other power of the CMA to
give a notice under section 26 or 40ZD to a person outside the United Kingdom.

16

In Chapter 5 of Part 3 of EA 2002 (mergers: supplementary: investigation
powers), after section 109A insert—

######### Extra-territorial application of notices under section 109

16.109B

16.109B.1

This section applies to the exercise of the CMA’s power to give a person a
notice under section 109(2) or (3).

16.109B.2

The power is exercisable so as to—

16.109B.2.a

give the notice to a person who is outside the United Kingdom (subject to
subsection (3) );

16.109B.2.b

require the production of documents, or the supply of information, held
outside the United Kingdom.

16.109B.3

The CMA’s power to give a notice under section 109(2) or (3) to a person
outside the United Kingdom by virtue of  subsection (2) (a)  is exercisable
only if—

16.109B.3.a

the person is, or was, part of, or involved with or carrying on, an enterprise
which has or may have ceased, or may cease, to be a distinct enterprise in
circumstances where a reference has been, or may be, made under section 22,
33, 45, 62, 62B or 68C, or a foreign state intervention notice has been given
under section 70A(1), in relation to the enterprise, or

16.109B.3.b

the person has a UK connection.

16.109B.4

For the purposes of  subsection (3) (b) , a person has a UK connection if the
person—

16.109B.4.a

is a United Kingdom national;

16.109B.4.b

is an individual who is habitually resident in the United Kingdom;

16.109B.4.c

is a body incorporated under the law of any part of the United Kingdom;

16.109B.4.d

carries on business in the United Kingdom.

16.109B.5

Nothing in this section is to be taken to limit any other power of the CMA to
give a notice under section 109(2) or (3) to a person outside the United
Kingdom.

17

In Chapter 4 of Part 4 of EA 2002 (market studies and market investigations:
supplementary: investigation powers), after section 174 insert—

######### Extra-territorial application of notices under section 174

17.174ZA

17.174ZA.1

This section applies to the exercise of the CMA’s power to give a person a
notice under section 174(4) or (5).

17.174ZA.2

The power is exercisable so as to—

17.174ZA.2.a

give the notice to a person who is outside the United Kingdom (subject to
subsection (3) );

17.174ZA.2.b

require the production of documents, or the supply of information, held
outside the United Kingdom.

17.174ZA.3

The CMA’s power to give a notice under section 174(4) or (5) to a person
outside the United Kingdom by virtue of  subsection (2) (a)  is exercisable
only if the person—

17.174ZA.3.a

is a United Kingdom national;

17.174ZA.3.b

is an individual who is habitually resident in the United Kingdom;

17.174ZA.3.c

is a body incorporated under the law of any part of the United Kingdom;

17.174ZA.3.d

carries on business in the United Kingdom.

17.174ZA.4

In  subsection (3) (a)  “ United Kingdom national ” has the same meaning as in
Part 3 (see section 129(1)).

17.174ZA.5

Nothing in this section is to be taken to limit any other power of the CMA to
give a notice under section 174(4) or (5) to a person outside the United
Kingdom.

  Orders and regulations under CA 1998 and EA 2002

Section 145

##### Orders and regulations under CA 1998

1

1.1

In Part 4 of CA 1998 (supplemental and transitional), section 71 (regulations,
orders and rules) is amended as follows.

1.2

In subsection (4)—

1.2.a

in the words before paragraph (a), for “No order is to be made” substitute
“An order made” ;

1.2.b

for the words after paragraph (e) substitute  “is subject to the affirmative
procedure” .

1.3

After subsection (4) insert—

1.3.4A

Regulations made under section  35B (7)  or 40A (7A)  are subject to the
affirmative procedure.

1.4

In subsection (5)—

1.4.a

in paragraph (a), after “(4)” insert  “or  (4A) ” ;

1.4.b

for the words after paragraph (b) substitute  “is subject to the negative
procedure” .

1.5

After subsection (5) insert—

1.5.6

Any provision that may be made by order or regulations under this Act subject
to the negative procedure may instead be made by order or regulations subject
to the affirmative procedure.

1.5.7

Where orders or regulations under this Act are subject to “the affirmative
procedure”, the orders or regulations may not be made unless a draft of the
statutory instrument containing them has been laid before, and approved by a
resolution of, each House of Parliament.

1.5.8

Where orders or regulations under this Act are subject to “the negative
procedure”, the statutory instrument containing them is subject to annulment
in pursuance of a resolution of either House of Parliament.

##### Obligations and rules of law

    Obligation or rule of law Authorised enforcers   Breach of contract for
the supply of goods, services or digital content (whether or not breach is
waived)       All public designated enforcers, other than—         the
Department of Health in Northern Ireland;           the Department for
Infrastructure in Northern Ireland;           an enforcement authority within
the meaning of section 120(15) of the Communications Act 2003 (regulation of
premium rate services);           the Maritime and Coastguard Agency;
the Office for the Traffic Commissioner;           the Secretary of State.
All private designated enforcers.       Breach of duty of care owed to
consumer under law of tort       All public designated enforcers, other than—
the Department of Health in Northern Ireland;           the Department for
Infrastructure in Northern Ireland;           an enforcement authority within
the meaning of section 120(15) of the Communications Act 2003 (regulation of
premium rate services);           the Maritime and Coastguard Agency;
the Office for the Traffic Commissioner;           the Secretary of State.
All private designated enforcers.       Breach of duty of care owed to
consumer under law of delict       All public designated enforcers, other
than—         the Department of Health in Northern Ireland;           the
Department for Infrastructure in Northern Ireland;           an enforcement
authority within the meaning of section 120(15) of the Communications Act 2003
(regulation of premium rate services);           the Maritime and Coastguard
Agency;           the Office for the Traffic Commissioner;           the
Secretary of State.                 All private designated enforcers.

1999/2083 ) All regulations (see Article 6(4) of the Consumer Rights Act 2015
(Commencement No 3, Transitional Provisions, Savings and Consequential
Amendments) Order 2015 for provision about the application of the Regulations
in connection with their revocation) 4. Other subordinate legislation Any
other subordinate legislation (not otherwise listed in this Schedule) so far
as made under an enactment so listed The entirety of the legislation.

  Investigatory powers

Section 208

##### Introductory

1

Schedule 5 to CRA 2015 (investigatory powers) is amended as follows.

##### Penalties for non-compliance with information notices

2

2.1

Paragraph 15 is amended in accordance with sub-paragraphs  (2)  and  (3) .

2.2

In sub-paragraph  (3) —

2.2.a

in the opening words for “may” substitute  “must” ;

2.2.b

after paragraph (b) insert—

2.2.b.c

the circumstances in which a monetary penalty may be payable under this Part
of this Schedule in relation to non-compliance with the notice.

2.3

After paragraph 16 insert—

########### Non-compliance with notice under paragraph 14: power of court to impose monetary penalties

2.3.16A

2.3.16A.1

This paragraph applies where—

2.3.16A.1.a

an enforcer or an officer of an enforcer has given a notice to a person (“ the
respondent ”) under paragraph 14, and

2.3.16A.1.b

the enforcer considers that the respondent has, without reasonable excuse,
failed to comply with the notice.

2.3.16A.2

The enforcer or an officer of the enforcer may make an application under this
paragraph to the court.

2.3.16A.3

If the court finds that the respondent has, without reasonable excuse, failed
to comply with the notice, the court may make an order that requires the
respondent to pay a monetary penalty to the enforcer.

2.3.16A.4

The amount of the penalty must be—

2.3.16A.4.a

a fixed amount,

2.3.16A.4.b

an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, or

2.3.16A.4.c

a combination of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a
daily rate.

2.3.16A.5

The penalty must not exceed—

2.3.16A.5.a

in the case of a fixed amount, £30,000 or, if higher, 1% of the total value of
the turnover (if any) of the respondent;

2.3.16A.5.b

in the case of an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, £15,000 per
day or, if higher, 5% of the total value of the daily turnover (if any) of the
respondent;

2.3.16A.5.c

in the case of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a daily
rate, such fixed amount and such amount per day.

2.3.16A.6

In imposing a penalty by reference to a daily rate—

2.3.16A.6.a

no account is to be taken of any days before the notification date, and

2.3.16A.6.b

unless the court determines an earlier date (whether before or after the order
imposing the penalty is made), the amount payable ceases to accumulate on the
day on which the requirements of the notice under paragraph 14 are complied
with.

2.3.16A.7

An order under this paragraph, or a notice accompanying service of the order,
must state—

2.3.16A.7.a

the amount of the penalty (including whether it is a fixed amount, an amount
calculated by reference to a daily rate or both a fixed amount and an amount
calculated by reference to a daily rate);

2.3.16A.7.b

the grounds on which the penalty is imposed together with any other factors
that the court considers justify the giving of the penalty or its amount;

2.3.16A.7.c

in the case of an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, the day on
which the amount first starts to accumulate and the day or days on which it
might cease to accumulate;

2.3.16A.7.d

how the penalty is to be paid to the enforcer;

2.3.16A.7.e

the date or dates, no earlier than the end of 28 days beginning with the date
of service of the order on the respondent, by which the penalty or (as the
case may be) different portions of it are required to be paid;

2.3.16A.7.f

that the penalty or (as the case may be) different portions of it may be paid
earlier than the date or dates by which it or they are required to be paid;

2.3.16A.7.g

that the respondent has the right to apply under sub-paragraph  (8) , and the
rights available to the respondent to appeal against the order, and the main
details of those rights.

2.3.16A.8

The respondent may, within 14 days of the date on which an order under this
paragraph is served on the respondent, apply to the court for it to specify a
different date or dates by which the penalty, or portions of it, are to be
paid.

2.3.16A.9

An application by an enforcer or officer of an enforcer under this paragraph—

2.3.16A.9.a

may be made in addition to, or instead of, an application under paragraph 16,
and

2.3.16A.9.b

where made in addition to an application under paragraph 16, may be combined
with the application under that paragraph.

2.3.16A.10

In addition to any right of appeal on a point of law, a person liable to pay a
penalty by virtue of an order under this paragraph may appeal in respect of
the amount of the penalty.

2.3.16A.11

Where an appeal is brought in respect of a penalty imposed by virtue of an
order under this paragraph, the penalty is not payable until the appeal is
determined or withdrawn, unless the court dealing with the appeal orders
otherwise.

2.3.16A.12

Sub-paragraphs (4) and (5) of paragraph 16 apply to an order under this
paragraph as they apply to an order under that paragraph.

2.3.16A.13

In the application of this paragraph to Scotland, the references in sub-
paragraphs  (7)  and  (8)  to an order being served include service of an
extract order in execution of or diligence on the order.

2.3.16A.14

In this paragraph, other than in sub-paragraph  (11) —

      “ the court ” has the same meaning as in paragraph 16;           “ the
notification date ”, in relation to an order under this paragraph, means the
date on which notice of the application for the order is given to the
respondent.

########### Non-compliance with notice under paragraph 14: powers of CMA to give provisional enforcement notice

2.3.16B

2.3.16B.1

This paragraph applies where—

2.3.16B.1.a

the CMA has given a notice to a person (“ the respondent ”) under paragraph
14, and

2.3.16B.1.b

the CMA has reasonable grounds to believe that the respondent has failed to
comply with the notice.

2.3.16B.2

The CMA may give to the respondent a notice under this paragraph (a
“provisional enforcement notice”).

2.3.16B.3

A provisional enforcement notice must—

2.3.16B.3.a

set out the grounds on which it is given, including the respondent’s acts or
omissions giving rise to the giving of the notice;

2.3.16B.3.b

specify such actions as the CMA considers appropriate to be taken by the
respondent for the purposes of securing compliance with the notice under
paragraph 14;

2.3.16B.3.c

invite the respondent to make representations to the CMA about the matters set
out in the notice;

2.3.16B.3.d

specify the means by which, and the time by which, such representations must
be made.

2.3.16B.4

The means specified under sub-paragraph  (3) (d)  for making representations
must include arrangements for them to be made orally if the respondent chooses
to make representations in that way.

2.3.16B.5

If the CMA is considering the imposition of a monetary penalty on the
respondent (see paragraph  16C ), the provisional enforcement notice must also
state—

2.3.16B.5.a

that the CMA is considering imposing a monetary penalty;

2.3.16B.5.b

the proposed amount of the penalty (including whether the penalty would be a
fixed amount, an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate or both a
fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate);

2.3.16B.5.c

any further factors (in addition to those provided under sub-paragraph  (3)
(a) ) which the CMA considers justify the imposition of the proposed penalty
and its amount or amounts.

########### Non-compliance with notice under paragraph 14: power of CMA to give final enforcement notice

2.3.16C

2.3.16C.1

This paragraph applies where—

2.3.16C.1.a

the CMA has given to the respondent a provisional enforcement notice under
paragraph 16B in respect of a notice given to the respondent under paragraph
14,

2.3.16C.1.b

the time for the respondent to make representations to the CMA in accordance
with the provisional enforcement notice has expired, and

2.3.16C.1.c

after considering such representations (if any), the CMA is satisfied that the
respondent has failed to comply with the notice given under paragraph 14.

2.3.16C.2

The CMA may by notice (a “final enforcement notice”) impose on the respondent
a requirement to do either or both of the following—

2.3.16C.2.a

a requirement to pay a monetary penalty;

2.3.16C.2.b

a requirement to comply with such directions as the CMA considers appropriate
for the purpose of securing the respondent’s compliance with the notice under
paragraph 14.

2.3.16C.3

A requirement under sub-paragraph  (2) (a)  to pay a monetary penalty may be
imposed only if the CMA is satisfied that the respondent’s failure in question
is without reasonable excuse.

2.3.16C.4

The amount of a monetary penalty must be—

2.3.16C.4.a

a fixed amount,

2.3.16C.4.b

an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, or

2.3.16C.4.c

a combination of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a
daily rate.

2.3.16C.5

The penalty must not exceed—

2.3.16C.5.a

in the case of a fixed amount, £30,000 or, if higher, 1% of the total value of
the turnover (if any) of the respondent;

2.3.16C.5.b

in the case of an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, £15,000 per
day or, if higher, 5% of the total value of the daily turnover (if any) of the
respondent;

2.3.16C.5.c

in the case of a fixed amount and an amount calculated by reference to a daily
rate, such fixed amount and such amount per day.

2.3.16C.6

In imposing a penalty by reference to a daily rate—

2.3.16C.6.a

no account is to be taken of any days before the date on which the provisional
enforcement notice mentioned in sub-paragraph  (1) (a)  was given to the
respondent, and

2.3.16C.6.b

unless the CMA determines an earlier date, the amount payable ceases to
accumulate on the day on which the requirements of the notice under paragraph
14 are complied with.

2.3.16C.7

A final enforcement notice that imposes a penalty on the respondent must
state—

2.3.16C.7.a

the amount of the penalty (including whether it is a fixed amount, an amount
calculated by reference to a daily rate or both a fixed amount and an amount
calculated by reference to a daily rate);

2.3.16C.7.b

the grounds on which the penalty is imposed together with any other factors
that the CMA considers justify the giving of the penalty or its amount;

2.3.16C.7.c

in the case of an amount calculated by reference to a daily rate, the day on
which the amount first starts to accumulate and the day or days on which it
might cease to accumulate;

2.3.16C.7.d

how the penalty is to be paid to the CMA;

2.3.16C.7.e

the date or dates, no earlier than the end of 28 days beginning with the date
of service of the notice on the respondent, by which the penalty or (as the
case may be) different portions of it are required to be paid;

2.3.16C.7.f

that the penalty or (as the case may be) different portions of it may be paid
earlier than the date or dates by which it or they are required to be paid;

2.3.16C.7.g

that the respondent has the right to apply under sub-paragraph  (8) , or to
appeal under paragraph  16D , and the main details of those rights.

2.3.16C.8

The respondent may, within 14 days of the date of service of the notice, apply
to the CMA for it to specify a different date or dates by which the penalty,
or different portions of it, are to be paid.

2.3.16C.9

In deciding whether, and if so how, to proceed under this paragraph the CMA
must have regard to the statement of policy most recently published under
paragraph  16F  at the time of the act or omission giving rise to the penalty.

2.3.16C.10

The CMA may publish a notice given under this paragraph in such manner as it
considers appropriate.

2.3.16C.11

Sections  191  to  196  of the Digital Markets, Competition and Consumers Act
2024 apply to a direction given in a notice under this paragraph as if the
direction were an enforcement direction for the purposes of those sections.

########### Appeals against final enforcement notice

2.3.16D

2.3.16D.1

A person to whom a final enforcement notice is given may appeal to the
appropriate court against—

2.3.16D.1.a

a decision to impose a monetary penalty by virtue of the notice,

2.3.16D.1.b

the nature or amount of any such penalty, or

2.3.16D.1.c

the giving of directions by virtue of the notice.

2.3.16D.2

The grounds for an appeal under sub-paragraph  (1) (a)  or  (b)  are that—

2.3.16D.2.a

the decision to impose a monetary penalty was based on an error of fact,

2.3.16D.2.b

the decision was wrong in law,

2.3.16D.2.c

the amount of the penalty is unreasonable, or

2.3.16D.2.d

the decision was unreasonable or wrong for any other reason.

2.3.16D.3

The grounds for an appeal under sub-paragraph  (1) (c)  are that—

2.3.16D.3.a

the decision to give the directions was based on an error of fact,

2.3.16D.3.b

the decision was wrong in law,

2.3.16D.3.c

the nature of the directions is unreasonable, or

2.3.16D.3.d

the decision was unreasonable or wrong for any other reason.

2.3.16D.4

On an appeal under this paragraph the appropriate court may quash, confirm or
vary the final enforcement notice.

2.3.16D.5

An appeal under this paragraph must be brought before the end of the period of
28 days beginning with the day on which the final enforcement notice was given
to the person seeking to bring the appeal.

2.3.16D.6

The appropriate court may extend the period mentioned in sub-paragraph  (5)
for bringing an appeal.

2.3.16D.7

Where an appeal is brought under this paragraph, the penalty is not payable
until the appeal is determined or withdrawn, unless the appropriate court
orders otherwise.

2.3.16D.8

In this paragraph “ the appropriate court ” means—

2.3.16D.8.a

in relation to England and Wales or Northern Ireland, the High Court, and

2.3.16D.8.b

in relation to Scotland, the Outer House of the Court of Session.

########### Recovery of penalties imposed under paragraph 

2.3.16E

2.3.16E.1

This paragraph applies where a penalty imposed by a final enforcement notice
given under paragraph  16C , or any part of such a penalty, has not been paid
by the date on which it is required to be paid and—

2.3.16E.1.a

an appeal under paragraph  16D  has not been brought before the end of the
period mentioned in sub-paragraph (5) of that paragraph, or

2.3.16E.1.b

any such appeal that was brought has been determined, withdrawn or otherwise
disposed of.

2.3.16E.2

The CMA may recover from the person on whom the penalty was imposed any of the
penalty and any interest which has not been paid.

2.3.16E.3

Any such penalty and interest may be recovered summarily (or, in Scotland,
recovered) as a civil debt by the CMA.

########### Statement of policy in relation to penalties under paragraph 

2.3.16F

2.3.16F.1

The CMA must prepare and publish a statement of policy in relation to the use
of its power to impose penalties under paragraph  16C .

2.3.16F.2

The statement must include a statement about the considerations relevant to
the determination of—

2.3.16F.2.a

whether to impose a penalty under that paragraph, and

2.3.16F.2.b

the nature and amount of any such penalty.

2.3.16F.3

The CMA may revise its statement of policy and, where it does so, must publish
the revised statement.

2.3.16F.4

In preparing or revising its statement of policy the CMA must consult—

2.3.16F.4.a

the Secretary of State, and

2.3.16F.4.b

such other persons as the CMA considers appropriate.

2.3.16F.5

A statement of policy, or revised statement, may not be published under this
paragraph without the approval of the Secretary of State.

########### Penalties imposed under paragraphs 

2.3.16G

2.3.16G.1

If the whole or any portion of a penalty is not paid by the date by which it
is required to be paid, the unpaid balance from time to time carries interest
at the statutory rate.

2.3.16G.2

Where an application has been made under paragraph  16A (8)  or  16C (8) , the
penalty is not required to be paid until the application has been determined,
withdrawn or otherwise disposed of.

2.3.16G.3

If a portion of a penalty has not been paid by the date required for it, the
enforcer to whom it is payable may, where it considers it appropriate to do
so, require so much of the penalty as has not already been paid (and is
capable of being paid immediately) to be paid immediately.

2.3.16G.4

Where on an appeal under paragraph  16D  the appropriate court substitutes a
penalty of a different nature or of a lesser amount, the court may require the
payment of interest at the statutory rate on the substituted penalty from
whatever date it considers appropriate (which may include a date before the
determination of the appeal).

2.3.16G.5

In the case of a monetary penalty imposed on a firm, the penalty is to be paid
out of the assets or funds of the firm.

2.3.16G.6

Sums received from a person towards payment of a monetary penalty must be
paid—

2.3.16G.6.a

in the case of a penalty imposed by an order of the Court of Session or the
Sheriff, into the Scottish Consolidated Fund;

2.3.16G.6.b

in the case of a penalty imposed by an order of a court in Northern Ireland,
into the Consolidated Fund of Northern Ireland;

2.3.16G.6.c

in any other case, into the Consolidated Fund of the United Kingdom.

2.3.16G.7

In this paragraph—

      “ penalty ” means a penalty imposed under paragraph  16A  or  16C ;
“ statutory rate ” means the rate for the time being specified in section 17
of the Judgments Act 1838.

########### Meaning of “turnover” for purposes of paragraphs 

2.3.16H

2.3.16H.1

References to “turnover” of a person in paragraphs  16A  and  16C  include—

2.3.16H.1.a

turnover both in and outside the United Kingdom;

2.3.16H.1.b

where the person controls another person, the turnover of that other person;

2.3.16H.1.c

where the person is controlled by another person, the turnover of that other
person.

2.3.16H.2

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

2.3.16H.2.a

make provision for determining when a person is to be treated as controlled by
another person for the purposes of sub-paragraph  (1) ;

2.3.16H.2.b

make provision for determining the turnover of a person for those purposes.

2.3.16H.3

Regulations under this paragraph may, in particular, make provision as to—

2.3.16H.3.a

the amounts which are, or which are not, to be treated as comprising a
person’s turnover or daily turnover;

2.3.16H.3.b

the date or dates by references to which a person’s turnover or daily turnover
is to be determined.

2.3.16H.4

Regulations under this paragraph may include provision enabling the court
(within the meaning of paragraph  16A ) or the CMA to determine matters of a
description specified in the regulations (including any of the matters
mentioned in paragraphs  (a)  and  (b)  of sub-paragraph (3) ).

2.3.16H.5

Regulations under this paragraph are to be made by statutory instrument.

2.3.16H.6

A statutory instrument containing regulations under this paragraph is subject
to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of either House of Parliament.

########### Power to amend amounts

2.3.16I

2.3.16I.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend the following provisions of
this Schedule for the purpose of substituting a different monetary amount for
an amount of fixed or daily penalty for the time being specified—

2.3.16I.1.a

paragraph  16A (5) (a)  and  (b) ;

2.3.16I.1.b

paragraph  16C (5) (a)  and  (b) .

2.3.16I.2

Before making regulations under this paragraph the Secretary of State must
consult such persons as the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

2.3.16I.3

Regulations under this paragraph are to be made by statutory instrument.

2.3.16I.4

Regulations under this paragraph may not be made unless a draft of the
statutory instrument containing them has been laid before, and approved by a
resolution of, each House of Parliament.

########### Miscellaneous

2.3.16J

2.3.16J.1

The CMA may not make an application under paragraph  16A  in respect of a
person’s failure to comply with a notice under paragraph 14 if the CMA has
given to the person a final enforcement notice under paragraph  16C  in
respect of that failure.

2.3.16J.2

The CMA may not give a person a final enforcement notice under paragraph  16C
in respect of a failure to comply with a notice under paragraph 14 if—

2.3.16J.2.a

the CMA has made an application under paragraph  16A  against the person in
respect of that failure, and

2.3.16J.2.b

the application has been determined by the court (within the meaning of that
paragraph).

##### Extra-territorial application in relation to notices

3

After paragraph 17 insert—

######### Extra-territorial application in relation to notices under paragraph 14

3.17A

3.17A.1

This paragraph applies to the exercise of a power of an enforcer to give a
person a notice under paragraph 14.

3.17A.2

The power is exercisable so as to—

3.17A.2.a

give the notice to a person who is outside the United Kingdom;

3.17A.2.b

require the provision of information held outside the United Kingdom.

3.17A.3

Sub-paragraph  (4)  applies where—

3.17A.3.a

an enforcer proposes to give a notice to a person outside the United Kingdom
by virtue of sub-paragraph  (2) (a) , and

3.17A.3.b

the enforcer does not consider that the person is a potential enforcement
subject.

3.17A.4

Where this sub-paragraph applies, the power to give the notice is exercisable
only if the person has a UK connection.

3.17A.5

A person has a UK connection if the person—

3.17A.5.a

is a United Kingdom national,

3.17A.5.b

is an individual who is habitually resident in the United Kingdom,

3.17A.5.c

is a firm established in the United Kingdom, or

3.17A.5.d

carries on business in the United Kingdom or by any means directs activities
in the course of carrying on a business to consumers in the United Kingdom.

3.17A.6

For the purposes of sub-paragraph  (3) (b)  a person (P) is a “ potential
enforcement subject ”, in relation to a notice given by an enforcer to P by
virtue of this paragraph, if the notice is given for the purposes of enabling
the enforcer—

3.17A.6.a

to exercise, or consider whether to exercise, a function mentioned in
paragraph 13(2), (3), (7)(a) or (9)(b) in relation to P;

3.17A.6.b

to ascertain whether P has breached any legislation mentioned in paragraph
13(4);

3.17A.6.c

to ascertain whether P has complied with, or is complying with, an injunction
or interdict mentioned in paragraph 13(7)(b);

3.17A.6.d

to determine whether to make an order of a kind mentioned in paragraph
13(9)(a) in respect of, or in relation to, P.

3.17A.7

In sub-paragraph  (5) (a)  “ United Kingdom national ” means—

3.17A.7.a

a British citizen, a British overseas territories citizen, a British National
(Overseas) or a British Overseas citizen;

3.17A.7.b

a person who is a British subject under the British Nationality Act 1981;

3.17A.7.c

a British protection person within the meaning of that Act.

3.17A.8

For the purposes of sub-paragraph (5) (c) , a firm is “established in the
United Kingdom” if—

3.17A.8.a

it is incorporated or formed under the law of a part of the United Kingdom, or

3.17A.8.b

it is administered under arrangements governed by the law of a part of the
United Kingdom.

3.17A.9

References in this paragraph to an enforcer include an officer of an enforcer.

##### Means of giving notices

4

After paragraph 17A (inserted by paragraph 3 above) insert—

######### Means of giving notice under this Part of this Schedule

4.17B

4.17B.1

This paragraph applies in relation to a notice given to a person under this
Part of this Schedule.

4.17B.2

The notice may be given by—

4.17B.2.a

delivering it to the person,

4.17B.2.b

leaving it at the person’s proper address,

4.17B.2.c

sending it by post to the person at that address, or

4.17B.2.d

sending it to the person by email to the person’s email address.

4.17B.3

A notice to a body corporate may be given in accordance with sub-paragraph
(2)  to any officer of that body.

4.17B.4

A notice to a partnership may be given in accordance with sub-paragraph  (2)
to any partner or a person who has the control or management of the
partnership business.

4.17B.5

A notice to a firm other than a body corporate or a partnership may be given
in accordance with sub-paragraph  (2)  to any member of the governing body of
the firm.

4.17B.6

A person’s proper address is—

4.17B.6.a

in a case where the person has specified an address as one at which the
person, or someone acting on the person’s behalf, will accept service of
notices or other documents, that address;

4.17B.6.b

in any other case, the address determined in accordance with sub-paragraph
(7) .

4.17B.7

A person’s proper address is (if sub-paragraph  (6) (a)  does not apply)—

4.17B.7.a

in the case of a body corporate, its registered or principal office;

4.17B.7.b

in the case of a partnership, the principal office of the partnership;

4.17B.7.c

in the case of a firm other than a body corporate or a partnership, the
principal office of the firm;

4.17B.7.d

in a case where none of paragraphs  (a)  to  (c)  apply, any address by means
of which the enforcer or officer giving the notice believes, on reasonable
grounds, that the notice will come to the attention of the person.

4.17B.8

A person’s email address is—

4.17B.8.a

any email address published for the time being by that person as an address
for contacting that person, or

4.17B.8.b

if there is no such published address, any email address by means of which the
enforcer or officer giving the notice believes, on reasonable grounds, that
the notice will come to the attention of that person.

4.17B.9

In the case of—

4.17B.9.a

a body corporate registered outside the United Kingdom,

4.17B.9.b

a partnership carrying on business outside the United Kingdom, or

4.17B.9.c

any other type of firm with offices outside the United Kingdom,

references to its principal office include references to its principal office
in the United Kingdom or, if it has no principal office in the United Kingdom,
any place in the United Kingdom where it carries on business or conducts
activities.

4.17B.10

In this paragraph “ officer ”, in relation to a body corporate, means any
director, manager, secretary or other similar officer of the body.

4.17B.11

This paragraph does not limit other lawful means of giving notice.

  Part 3 : transitional and saving provisions

Section 215

##### Interpretation

1

In  this Schedule —

      “ commencement date ” means the date on which  section 153  comes into
force;           “ continuing conduct ” means an act or omission of a person
that—         takes place before the commencement date, and           is
repeated, or continues to take place, on or after that date;                 “
enforcement action ”—         in relation to the new law, means proceedings or
other steps taken by virtue of a power conferred under the new law, and
in relation to the old law, means proceedings or other steps taken by virtue
of a power conferred under the old law;                 “ the new law ” means
Chapters 3  and  4  of  Part 3  (and any provisions of law relating to those
Chapters, including Schedule 5 to CRA 2015 as amended by this Act);
“ the old law ” means—         Part 8 of EA 2002, as that Part had effect
immediately before the commencement date, and           any provisions of law
(including in particular Schedule 5 to CRA 2015) relating to Part 8 of EA
2002, as those provisions had effect immediately before the commencement date.

##### General rules

2

2.1

The old law continues to apply—

2.1.a

in respect of conduct of a person that takes place before the commencement
date;

2.1.b

for the purposes of the taking of enforcement action relating to a breach of
an order made by, or undertaking given to, the court under the old law;

2.1.c

in a case where proceedings before a court under the old law have been started
against a person before the commencement date, for the purposes of the
continuation and completion of those proceedings (including any appeals
relating to the proceedings).

2.2

In  sub-paragraph (1) (c)  the reference to proceedings being started against
a person is a reference to an application being made against the person under
section 215 or 218ZA of EA 2002.

2.3

This paragraph is subject to—

2.3.a

paragraph 3 , which makes rules for cases involving continuing conduct, and

2.3.b

paragraph 4 , which makes rules for cases involving breach of undertakings
given to enforcers.

##### Rules applicable to continuing conduct

3

3.1

This paragraph  applies where conduct of a person is continuing conduct.

3.2

The new law applies in respect of the person’s post-commencement conduct.

3.3

The new law also applies in respect of the person’s pre-commencement conduct
for the purposes of enabling the taking of enforcement action under Chapter 3
or 4 of  Part 3  in relation to that conduct.

3.4

Where the new law applies by virtue of  sub-paragraph (3) , a requirement
under Chapter 3 or (as the case may be) Chapter 4 may be imposed on a person
in respect of the relevant infringement in relation to which the enforcement
action is taken only if a requirement of a corresponding kind could have been
imposed on the person under the old law (and accordingly a monetary penalty,
in particular, may not be imposed on the person).

3.5

In applying the new law in accordance with  this paragraph  in respect of a
person’s post-commencement conduct, regard may be had to, and findings of fact
or law may be made in respect of, the person’s pre-commencement conduct so far
as necessary or appropriate for the purposes of determining any matter that
falls to be determined in the application of the new law.

3.6

In  this paragraph —

      “ post commencement conduct ” means so much of a person’s continuing
conduct as takes place on or after the commencement date;           “ pre-
commencement conduct ” means so much of a person’s continuing conduct as takes
place before the commencement date.

##### Rules applicable to undertakings given to enforcers under the old law

4

4.1

This paragraph  applies where an enforcer has accepted an undertaking from a
person under the old law.

4.2

Enforcement action in respect of a person’s breach of the undertaking, whether
the breach takes place before, on or after the commencement date, may be taken
only under the old law.

4.3

Sub-paragraph  (4)  applies where a breach of the undertaking—

4.3.a

takes place (to any extent) on or after the commencement date, and

4.3.b

it appears to an enforcer that the act or omission comprising the breach, so
far as taking place on or after that date—

4.3.b.i

is also a commercial practice which constitutes a relevant infringement under
the new law, or

4.3.b.ii

is carried out by a person who is an accessory under the new law to such a
commercial practice.

4.4

Enforcement action in respect of the act or omission may be taken—

4.4.a

under the new law, or

4.4.b

if the act or omission would also be a domestic or Schedule 13 infringement
for the purposes of the old law, under the old law.

4.5

It is for the enforcer concerned to determine whether to take enforcement
action under the new law or the old law in accordance with sub-paragraph  (4)
.

4.6

A breach of an undertaking that first takes place before the commencement date
is to be treated for the purposes of this paragraph as also taking place on or
after that date if the act or omission comprising the breach is repeated or
continued on or after that date.

##### Information notices under Schedule 5 to CRA 2015

5

5.1

The amendments made by  paragraph 2 (3)  of  Schedule 17  (which insert new
paragraphs  16A  to  16J  into Schedule 5 to CRA 2015) have effect only in
relation to an information notice given on or after the commencement date.

5.2

In  sub-paragraph (1)  “ information notice ” means a notice given under
paragraph 14 of Schedule 5 to CRA 2015.

##### Further provision

6

Nothing in  this Schedule  limits the power under  section 339 (5)  to make
further transitional and saving provision in connection with the coming into
force of the new law.

  Commercial practices which are in all circumstances considered unfair

Section 225

1

Claiming to be a signatory to a code of conduct when the trader is not.

2

Claiming that a code of conduct has an endorsement from a public or private
body which it does not have.

3

Displaying a trust mark, quality mark or equivalent without having obtained
the necessary authorisation.

4

Claiming that a trader, a trader’s commercial practice, or a product has been
approved, endorsed or authorised by a public or private body when—

4.a

the claim is false, or

4.b

the terms of the approval, endorsement or authorisation have not been, or are
not being, complied with.

5

5.1

Making an invitation to purchase products at a specified price where—

5.1.a

the trader has reasonable grounds for believing that it will not be possible
for the trader to offer those products, or equivalent products, for supply at
that price, in reasonable quantities, for a reasonable period of time (or to
procure another trader to do so), and

5.1.b

the trader does not disclose that fact.

5.2

In sub-paragraph  (1) , the references to reasonable quantities and a
reasonable period of time are references to what is reasonable having regard
to—

5.2.a

the nature of the product,

5.2.b

the extent of advertising for the product, and

5.2.c

the price offered for the product.

6

Making an invitation to purchase products at a specified price and then—

6.a

refusing to show the advertised item to consumers,

6.b

refusing to take orders for it or deliver it within a reasonable time, or

6.c

demonstrating a defective sample of it,

with the intention of promoting a different product.

7

Falsely stating that a product will only be available for a limited time, or
that it will only be available on particular terms for a limited time, in
order to elicit an immediate decision and deprive consumers of sufficient
opportunity or time to make an informed choice.

8

Undertaking to provide an after-sales service to consumers and then making
such service available only in a language which is different to the language
used in communication with the consumer for, or prior to, the transaction
without clearly disclosing this to the consumer before the consumer committed
to the transaction.

9

Falsely claiming or creating the false impression that an after-sales service
is available, including falsely claiming that it is available in, or
accessible from, any particular country or location.

10

Stating or otherwise creating the impression that a product can be legally
sold when it cannot.

11

Presenting rights given to consumers by law as a distinctive feature of the
trader’s offer.

12

Using editorial content in the media to promote a product where a trader has
paid for the promotion without making that clear in the content or by images
or sounds clearly identifiable by the consumer.

13

13.1

Submitting, or commissioning another person to submit or write—

13.1.a

a fake consumer review, or

13.1.b

a consumer review that conceals the fact it has been incentivised.

13.2

Publishing consumer reviews, or consumer review information, in a misleading
way.

13.3

Publishing consumer reviews, or consumer review information, without taking
such reasonable and proportionate steps as are necessary for the purposes of—

13.3.a

preventing the publication of—

13.3.a.i

fake consumer reviews,

13.3.a.ii

consumer reviews that conceal the fact they have been incentivised, or

13.3.a.iii

consumer review information that is false or misleading, and

13.3.b

removing any such reviews or information from publication.

13.4

Offering services to traders—

13.4.a

for the doing of anything covered by sub-paragraph (1) or (2);

13.4.b

for the facilitating of anything covered by sub-paragraph (1) or (2) to be
done.

13.5

For the purposes of this paragraph—

13.5.a

“ consumer review ” means a review of a product, a trader or any other matter
relevant to a transactional decision;

13.5.b

“ fake consumer review ” means a consumer review that purports to be, but is
not, based on a person’s genuine experience;

13.5.c

a consumer review conceals the fact it has been incentivised if—

13.5.c.i

a person has been commissioned to submit or write the review, and

13.5.c.ii

that fact is not made apparent (whether through the contents of the review or
otherwise);

13.5.d

“ consumer review information ” means information that is derived from, or is
influenced by, consumer reviews;

13.5.e

a person “submits” a review or information if they supply it with a view to
publication;

13.5.f

“ writing ” includes creating by any means;

13.5.g

“ commissioning ” includes incentivising by any means (and “commissioned” is
to be read accordingly);

13.5.h

“ publishing ” includes disseminating, or otherwise making available, by any
means;

13.5.i

publishing in a “ misleading way ” includes (for example)—

13.5.i.i

failing to publish, or removing from publication, negative consumer reviews
whilst publishing positive ones (or vice versa);

13.5.i.ii

giving greater prominence to positive consumer reviews over negative ones (or
vice versa);

13.5.i.iii

omitting information that is relevant to the circumstances in which a consumer
review has been written (including that a person has been commissioned to
write the review).

14

Making a materially inaccurate claim concerning the nature and extent of the
risk to the personal security or safety of the consumer, a member of the
consumer’s family or anyone living in the consumer’s home, if the consumer
does not purchase the product.

15

Promoting a product similar to a product made by a particular manufacturer in
such a manner as deliberately to mislead the consumer into believing that the
product is made by that same manufacturer when it is not.

16

16.1

Establishing, operating or promoting a pyramid promotional scheme.

16.2

In sub-paragraph  (1) , a pyramid promotional scheme means a scheme where a
consumer gives consideration for the opportunity to receive compensation that
is derived primarily from the introduction of other consumers into the scheme
rather than from the supply or consumption of products.

17

Claiming that the trader is about to cease trading or move premises when the
trader is not.

18

Claiming that products are able to facilitate winning in games of chance.

19

19.1

Falsely claiming that a product is able to—

19.1.a

prevent or treat disease or a malformation,

19.1.b

restore, correct or modify a physiological function, or

19.1.c

modify a person’s appearance.

19.2

For the purposes of sub-paragraph  (1) , “ disease ” includes any injury,
ailment or adverse condition, whether of body or mind.

20

Providing (including passing on) materially inaccurate information about
market conditions or about the availability of the product with the intention
of inducing the consumer to acquire the product under conditions that are less
favourable than normal market conditions.

21

Claiming to offer a competition or prize promotion without awarding the prizes
described or a reasonable equivalent.

22

Creating the false impression that the consumer has already won, will win, or
will on doing a particular act win, a prize or other equivalent benefit, when
in fact either—

22.a

there is no prize or other equivalent benefit, or

22.b

taking any action in relation to claiming the prize or other equivalent
benefit requires the consumer to pay money or incur a cost.

23

Describing a product as “gratis”, “free”, “without charge” or similar if the
consumer has to pay anything other than the unavoidable cost of responding to
the commercial practice and collecting or paying for delivery of the item.

24

Including in marketing material an invoice or similar document seeking payment
which gives the consumer the impression that the consumer has already ordered
the marketed product when the consumer has not.

25

Falsely claiming or creating the false impression that the trader is not
acting for purposes relating to the trader’s business or falsely representing
oneself as a consumer.

26

Creating the impression that the consumer cannot leave the premises until a
contract is formed.

27

Ignoring a request from a consumer to leave or not return to the consumer’s
home except in circumstances and to the extent justified to enforce a
contractual obligation.

28

Making persistent and unwanted solicitations by any means, other than by
attending at the consumer’s home, except in circumstances and to the extent
justified to enforce a contractual obligation.

29

Requiring a consumer who wishes to claim on an insurance policy to produce
documents which could not reasonably be considered relevant as to whether the
claim was valid, or failing systematically to respond to correspondence, in
order to dissuade a consumer from exercising the consumer’s contractual
rights.

30

Including in an advertisement a direct appeal to children to buy advertised
products or persuade their parents or other adults to buy advertised products
for them.

31

Supplying products to a consumer that have not been requested by the consumer
and demanding that the consumer—

31.a

pays for the products,

31.b

returns the products, or

31.c

safely stores the products.

32

Explicitly telling a consumer that if the consumer does not buy the product,
the trader’s job or livelihood will be at risk.
